母鸡 (mǔjī) does indeed mean "hen."  However, be aware of its slang usage, particularly mimicking Cantonese, where it can humorously mean "I don't know" (唔知). This usage is informal and might not be understood by everyone.

~
大米

大米 (dàmǐ) refers specifically to uncooked, husked rice.  Cooked rice is generally referred to as 米饭 (mǐfàn) or just 饭 (fàn).

~
职工

职工 (zhígōng) is a more formal term encompassing both staff and workers within an organization.  It can refer to both blue-collar and white-collar employees and often appears in official contexts.

~
免得

免得 (miǎnde) is used to express the purpose of avoiding something negative.  It's similar to "so as not to" or "lest" in English.  It often follows a suggestion or command.

~
互动

互动 (hùdòng) implies a reciprocal exchange or interaction, often between people.  It suggests a two-way flow of communication or action, not just a one-sided influence.

~
网址

网址 (wǎngzhǐ) is a general term for a web address or URL.  It can refer to any type of website, not just specific kinds.

~
新人

新人 (xīnrén) can have several meanings depending on context. While it can mean "newcomer," it's also frequently used to refer to newlyweds, especially the bride.

~
此刻

此刻 (cǐkè) emphasizes the present moment, often with a sense of immediacy.  It's a more formal and emphatic way of saying "now" than 现在 (xiànzài).

~
国民

国民 (guómín) refers to citizens of a nation, emphasizing their legal status and relationship to the state.  It's a more formal term than 人民 (rénmín), which is a more general term for "the people."

~
时

时 (shí) can be polysemous, meaning "time," "hour," "season," "o'clock." Pay attention to context for disambiguation.  It's also a surname (Shí).

~
福利

福利 (fúlì) generally refers to benefits provided by an employer or the government, often beyond basic salary.  These could include things like health insurance, retirement plans, or subsidized housing.

~
回信

回信 (huíxìn) is a reply letter, either written or in some cases email.  It emphasizes the act of replying to a previous communication.

~
一点点

一点点 (yīdiǎndiǎn) means "a little bit." Repeating "一点" emphasizes the smallness of the quantity.

~
截至

截至 (jiézì) indicates a point in time up to which something is counted or valid. It often appears in official reports or announcements.

~
发怒

发怒 (fānù) implies a more intense anger than simply being upset.  It suggests a visible display of anger, like yelling or losing one's temper.

~
闭幕

闭幕 (bìmù) is typically used for formal events like conferences, meetings, or exhibitions.  It implies a formal closing ceremony or announcement.

~
名义

名义 (míngyì) refers to something done in name only, often without real authority or substance. It can also refer to the stated purpose or pretext for something.

~
泡

泡 (pào) has a wide range of meanings.  It can refer to bubbles, soaking, or even picking someone up (romantically). Context is crucial for understanding its intended meaning.  Also, be aware of its less polite usage referring to urine or feces.

~
村

村 (cūn) specifically refers to a village or hamlet, usually in a rural setting. It's distinct from 城市 (chéngshì), which means "city."

~
特
When used as an adverb, 特 is usually placed before an adjective, and means "especially" or "particularly". It cannot be used before a verb.

When used as an adjective, 特 means "special" or "unique".

~
英勇
A synonym is 英雄 (yīngxióng). However, 英雄 is usually used to describe a *person*, while 英勇 is usually used to describe an *action*.

~
午睡
There is no difference between the use of 午睡 in Chinese and nap/siesta in English.

~
忽略
There is not much difference between 忽略 (hūlüè) and 忽视 (hūshì). If anything, 忽略 is slightly more colloquial than 忽视.

~
报警
There is no difference between the use of 报警 in Chinese and "call the police" or "report sth to the police" in English.

~
若
This word is usually used in the written register.  It's more colloquial counterpart is "如果" (rúguǒ).

~
办学
There is no difference between the use of 办学 in Chinese and "run a school" in English.

~
避
When used to mean "avoid", 避 is usually placed immediately before the thing being avoided.

~
医学
There is no difference between the use of 医学 in Chinese and "medical science" or "medicine" in English.

~
排名
There is no difference between the use of 排名 in Chinese and "rank" or "ranking" in English.

~
见
In addition to its literal meaning of "to see", 见 also appears in many common compounds verbs where the meaning can be non-obvious. Here are a few:

* 意见 (yìjiàn) - opinion, view
* 看见 (kànjiàn) - to see (something visible)
* 听见 (tīngjiàn) - to hear
* 见面 (jiànmiàn) - to meet up with (someone)

~
再说
再说 can mean both “besides” and “we’ll talk about it later”. The meaning is usually clear from context. If 再说 appears at the beginning of a sentence, and there is a previous sentence providing reasons for something, then the meaning is usually "besides". If 再说 appears at the end of a sentence, the meaning is usually "we'll talk about it later".

~
科技
There is no difference between the use of 科技 in Chinese and "science and technology" in English.

~
航空
There is no difference between the use of 航空 in Chinese and "aviation" in English.

~
usb
There is no difference between the use of usb in Chinese and "USB" in English.

~
放下
放下 (fàngxià) means to physically “put down” or “lay down” something. It can also have the extended meaning of to “let go of” something emotionally.

~
全国
There is no difference between the use of 全国 in Chinese and "nationwide" in English.

~
邮票
There is no difference between the use of 邮票 in Chinese and "(postage) stamp" in English.

~
儿女
The primary meaning of 儿女 (érnǚ) is “sons and daughters; children.”  Less commonly, it can also refer to “a young man and a young woman (in love).” The intended meaning is usually clear from context.

~
无关
There is no difference between the use of 无关 in Chinese and "unrelated" or "having nothing to do with" in English.  无关 is often used in the phrase 无关紧要 (wúguān jǐnyào), which means "unimportant" or "insignificant".

~
圆珠笔
There is no difference between the use of 圆珠笔 in Chinese and "ballpoint pen" in English.

~
闭
闭 (bì) can be translated as "to close" or "to shut." It is typically used for things that open and close, such as eyes, doors, or mouths.  It shouldn't be used to refer to closing something like a shop, a road, or an account.

~
胡子
胡子 (húzi) can refer to both "beard" and "mustache". If you need to be specific, use the words 鬍鬚 (húxū) for mustache and 山羊鬍 (shānyánghú) for beard.

~
迷信
迷信 (míxìn) is similar in meaning to "superstition" in English. It can be used as a noun or a verb. It often carries a negative connotation, suggesting blind faith or belief without evidence.

~
之外
之外 (zhīwài) means "outside of" or "except for." It usually follows a noun or pronoun.  A near synonym is 以外 (yǐwài), although 之外 is slightly more formal.

~
昏
昏 (hūn) has two main meanings. It can mean “faint; lose consciousness,” or it can refer to the time of day, “dusk; twilight.” The meaning is usually clear from context.

~
各个
各个 (gège) means "each" or "every" and emphasizes individuality. It implies looking at things one by one.  各个 is more specific than 每 (měi), which simply means "every".

~
华语
华语 (huáyǔ) refers specifically to the Chinese language, encompassing all its varieties. It is often used in formal settings or when emphasizing the unity of the Chinese language across different regions.

~
请教
请教 (qǐngjiào) is a polite way to ask for advice or guidance from someone with more expertise. It is more formal and respectful than simply asking a question.

~
大都
大都 (dàdū) has two meanings.  The first, and more common one is "for the most part" or "mostly".  The second, and less common one is the historical name for Beijing.

~
悬
悬 (xuán) has two main meanings: one concrete and one abstract. It can refer to the physical act of "hanging" or "suspending" something. Additionally, it can refer to a state of uncertainty or anxiety, as in a "cliffhanger" or an unresolved problem.

~
走私
走私 (zǒusī) refers to the illegal transportation of goods across borders, often to avoid taxes or import restrictions.  The closest English equivalent is "smuggle".

~
上衣
上衣 (shàngyī) generally refers to any upper garment, including shirts, jackets, coats, and sweaters. A more specific word for jacket is 夹克 (jiākè), while a more specific word for coat is 大衣 (dàyī).

~
风
风 (fēng) can mean either “wind” (the natural phenomenon) or “style; custom; manner”. Its specific meaning is often clear from context.

~
轮子
轮子 (lúnzi) primarily means "wheel". It can also be used to derogatorily refer to a Falun Gong practitioner.

~
面向
面向 (miànxiàng) is typically used to describe the direction something faces or the intended audience of something.

~
侄女
There is no difference between the use of 侄女 in Chinese and "niece" in English.

~
没用
没用 (méiyòng) is an adjective that means "useless." It can also be used as a standalone phrase expressing frustration or disappointment.  A more colloquial, and slightly stronger, way of expressing the same idea is "没鸟用" (méiniǎoyòng), although this is generally only used in informal spoken Chinese.


~
之内
之内 (zhīnèi) means "within" or "inside" and is often used with a timeframe or a physical boundary.  A near synonym is 以内 (yǐnèi), although 之内 is slightly more formal.

~
操作
Can be a noun or a verb.


~
心脏病
There is no difference between the use of 心脏病 in Chinese and Heart Disease in English.


~
缩小
Can be used as a verb or an adjective.


~
震惊
Can be a verb, adjective, or noun.


~
中外
There is no difference between the use of 中外 in Chinese and "at home and abroad" in English.


~
犯
犯 (fàn) has a wide range of meanings related to transgression, from minor mistakes to serious crimes.  Here's a breakdown:

* **To commit (a crime/mistake/error):** This is the most common usage.  犯错误 (fàn cuòwù) means "to make a mistake," and 犯罪 (fànzuì) means "to commit a crime."
* **To violate (a law/rule):**  犯规 (fàn guī) means "to break the rules."
* **To offend:**  You can use 犯 with words like 上 (shàng - superior) to indicate offending someone, e.g., 犯上 (fàn shàng).
* **To have a recurrence (of illness/bad habit):** For example, 老毛病又犯了 (lǎo máobìng yòu fàn le) means "The old problem/illness has recurred."
* **Criminal/crime:** While less common, 犯 can also be used as a noun meaning "criminal" or "crime."

The specific meaning often depends on the context and the word it's used with.


~
混合
Can be a verb, adjective or noun.


~
替代
Can be a verb or a noun.


~
回来
回来 is specifically about returning to a place considered "home" or a familiar place.  If you are simply going back to a place you were previously, then you would use 回去 (huíqù).  For example, after visiting a friend, you would say 我回去了 (wǒ huíqù le).


~
梅花
梅花 (méihuā) has a few meanings:

1. **Plum blossom:** This is the most common meaning.
2. **Wintersweet:** This is a slightly different flower but still translates as plum blossom.
3. **Clubs (card game):**  In card games, 梅花 represents the suit of clubs.

The context will usually make the intended meaning clear.


~
应
应 (yīng) has a wide range of meanings and uses.  Here's a breakdown:

* **Should/Ought to/Must:** This is a common modal verb expressing obligation or duty.
* **To answer/respond:**  This can refer to answering a question, responding to a call, or reacting to a situation.
* **To agree/promise:**  应 can indicate agreement or consent.
* **To comply with/deal with:**  This usage often appears in formal contexts.

The specific meaning depends heavily on context. Pay attention to the surrounding words and the overall sentence structure.


~
愁
愁 (chóu) is primarily a verb meaning "to worry" or "to be anxious."  It can also be used as a noun meaning "worry" or "anxiety." Unlike 担心 (dānxīn), which implies concern for a specific outcome, 愁 is more of a general feeling of unease and sadness.


~
办
Besides meaning "to do," 办 (bàn) also carries the nuance of "to manage," "to handle," "to run," "to set up," or "to take care of."  It implies taking action to resolve or organize something.  For example, you might use it in the context of organizing an event, handling a problem, or setting up a business.


~
开头
开头 (kāitóu) can function as both a noun and a verb. As a noun, it means "beginning" or "start." As a verb, it means "to begin" or "to start."


~
血管
There is no difference between the use of 血管 in Chinese and "blood vessel" in English.


~
骑车
骑车 (qíchē) generally refers to riding a bicycle. If you want to specify a motorbike or motorcycle, you should say 骑摩托车 (qí mótuōchē).


~
隔开
隔开 (gékāi) emphasizes the result of being separated, highlighting the state of being apart.  Another similar word is 分开 (fēnkāi) which emphasizes the process of separating, highlighting the action of dividing or splitting.


~
上课
上课 (shàngkè) can mean both "to attend class" (as a student) and "to go to teach a class" (as a teacher). The context will usually make the meaning clear.


~
收回
收回 (shōuhuí) implies retrieving something that was previously given out or belongs to you, while 拿回 (náhuí) simply means taking something back and doesn't necessarily imply ownership or prior giving.


~
以后
以后 (yǐhòu) specifically refers to a time *after* a certain point.  If you are speaking of something happening at a *later* time within a given timeframe, you would use 过后 (guòhòu).


~
差异
差异 (chāyì) highlights the *differences* between things, whereas 区别 (qūbié) emphasizes the *distinction* between things.  While often interchangeable, 差异 suggests more of a quantitative difference (e.g., in size, degree), whereas 区别 focuses more on qualitative difference (e.g., in nature, type).


~
干吗
干吗 (gànmá) is a colloquial way of saying "why?"  It's more informal than 为什么 (wèishénme).


~
没事儿
没事儿 (méishìr) is a versatile expression with several meanings:

* **It's okay/You're welcome:** Used as a response to "thank you."
* **It's nothing/Never mind:** Used to downplay something.
* **I'm fine:** Used to indicate well-being.
* **To have free time:**  没事儿 can also mean having nothing to do.

The context will usually make the intended meaning clear.


~
随意
随意 (suíyì) suggests a relaxed and informal atmosphere, granting freedom of choice or action without strict rules or constraints.  It's closer to "as you wish" or "feel free."  On the other hand, 随便 (suíbiàn) implies a more casual and perhaps even careless approach, where one doesn't give much thought or consideration to their actions.  It can sometimes carry a slightly negative connotation, suggesting a lack of seriousness or respect.


~
宝石
There is no difference between the use of 宝石 in Chinese and gemstone in English.


~
多年
多年 (duōnián) implies a long period of time, usually several years or even decades.  It emphasizes the duration and often has a sense of history or continuity associated with it.  好几年 (hǎo jǐ nián) means "several years" or "quite a few years" and is more specific about the duration being more than a couple of years but less than a very extended period.


~
薯条
There is no difference between the use of 薯条 in Chinese and French Fries in English.


~
前进
前进 (qiánjìn) implies moving forward towards a specific goal or destination, often with determination and effort.  It carries a more active and purposeful connotation than simply moving forward.  向前走 (xiàng qián zǒu) simply means to walk forward and lacks the same sense of purpose or progress.


~
有人
有人 (yǒurén) can mean "someone," "there's someone," "anyone," or "occupied" (as in a restroom).  The meaning depends entirely on context.


~
级
级 (jí) is a versatile word indicating levels, ranks, grades, or degrees. It can also refer to steps (of stairs).  The specific meaning depends heavily on context.


~
特有
特有 (tèyǒu) refers to something unique or specific to a particular place, group, or thing. It highlights the distinctiveness and exclusiveness of a characteristic.  特别 (tèbié) means "special" or "particularly" and emphasizes something unusual or noteworthy, but it doesn't necessarily imply exclusivity.


~
宏大
宏大 (hóngdà) is usually used to describe physical size, scale, or scope. 伟大 (wěidà) can describe both physical and abstract greatness, including achievements, character, or impact.


~
同
同 (tóng) has a very wide range of meaning. Be careful not to confuse its role as a noun (meaning alleyway) and its other, more common usage as an adjective.


~
中奖
中奖 (zhòngjiǎng) specifically refers to winning a prize in a lottery, raffle, or similar contest involving chance.  获奖 (huòjiǎng) refers to winning an award or prize in a competition or contest based on skill, merit, or achievement.


~
队长
There is no difference between the use of 队长 in Chinese and team leader/captain in English.


~
店
店 (diàn) is a general term for "shop" or "store."  If you want to specify a particular type of shop, you would usually add a word before 店, such as 书店 (shūdiàn - bookstore), 饭店 ( fàndiàn - restaurant), or 咖啡店 (kāfēi diàn - coffee shop).


~
节假日
节假日 (jiéjiàrì) refers to both traditional festivals (like Spring Festival or Mid-Autumn Festival) and public holidays (like National Day or Labor Day).


~
宫
宫 (gōng) has a few distinct meanings:

1. **Palace:**  This is the most common meaning, referring to the residence of an emperor or other royalty.
2. **Temple:** Can refer to a place of worship, often Taoist or Buddhist.
3. **Uterus:**  In a medical context, 宫 refers to the uterus.
4. **(Archaic) Castration:** This is a less common and archaic meaning.

The context will usually make the intended meaning clear.


~
名牌儿
名牌儿 (míngpáir) can refer to both a "famous brand" and a "name tag/nameplate." The context will clarify the intended meaning.


~
毛笔
There is no difference between the use of 毛笔 in Chinese and "writing brush" in English.

~
挨
挨着 (āizhe) means next to. It emphasizes physical proximity.  It can often be translated as "close to" or "right next to". For example, 他挨着我坐 (tā āizhe wǒ zuò) means "He sat right next to me."


~
产业
产业 (chǎnyè) refers to a large-scale economic activity or all the assets of a company, including both tangible assets (like factories, equipment, and raw materials) and intangible assets (like brand recognition, patents, and copyrights). It's broader than just a single product or factory.

~
偏
When 偏 (piān) means "stubbornly" or "contrary to expectations," it often implies that something happened despite efforts to prevent it or that someone insisted on doing something against advice.  It can often be followed by 要 (yào) or 就 (jiù) to emphasize the unexpected or contrary nature of the action.  For example,  他偏要这样做 (tā piān yào zhèyàng zuò) means "He insisted on doing it this way (despite being told otherwise)."

~
救命
As an interjection, 救命 (jiùmìng) is equivalent to "Help!" or "Save me!"  It is used in emergencies.  It doesn't necessarily mean someone's life is in danger, just that they're in serious trouble and need assistance.

~
主持人
主持人 (zhǔchí rén) can refer to a host in any context, not just TV or radio.  It can be used for the host of a party, event, or even a meeting.

~
池子
池子 (chízi) is a more colloquial term than 泳池 (yóngchí) for a swimming pool.  泳池 is more formal and often used in official contexts like signs or announcements.

~
各位
各位 (gèwèi) is a formal and respectful way to address a group of people.  It's often used in speeches, announcements, or formal meetings.

~
日夜
日夜 (rìyè) emphasizes continuous activity without rest, while the more straightforward term 整天 (zhěng tiān), meaning "all day long," can refer to a single day.

~
从中
从中 (cóngzhōng) emphasizes obtaining something *from within* a larger context, like gaining experience from a situation or deriving profit from a business.  It suggests an active involvement or extraction, rather than simply being near something.

~
冷气
冷气 (lěngqì) is the common term for air conditioning in Taiwan and some Southern Chinese dialects, but in Mainland China, the standard term is 空调 (kōngtiáo).

~
收藏
收藏 (shōucáng) implies a deliberate and organized approach to collecting, often with an element of value or appreciation.  It's more than just gathering things randomly.

~
夺
夺 (duó) often implies taking something by force or against someone's will. It emphasizes a struggle or competition to gain possession.

~
债
债 (zhài) can also encompass non-monetary debts, such as favors owed or obligations to others. This broader sense of indebtedness is often referred to as 人情债 (rénqíng zhài) - "debt of gratitude" or "social debt."

~
打
打 (dǎ) has a very wide range of uses.  It's not always about physical striking. It can be used for making phone calls (打电话 dǎ diànhuà), playing games (打牌 dǎ pái), or even expressing time durations (打一个小时 dǎ yī ge xiǎoshí - "for one hour").

~
投
投 (tóu) often implies putting something into or onto a target, often with a specific purpose or intention.  It's more directed than just throwing something randomly.

~
加热
加热 (jiārè) is commonly used when talking about cooking or warming up food.  It can also be used for industrial processes involving heat, but for warming a room, the term 取暖 (qǔnuǎn) is more appropriate.

~
支撑
支撑 (zhīchēng) suggests providing essential support to prevent something from collapsing or failing. It's a more critical kind of support than just helping something stay upright.  It implies bearing a significant load or responsibility.

~
领取
领取 (lǐngqǔ) often involves formally receiving something, often official documents, salaries, or prizes.  It emphasizes the process of officially obtaining something to which one is entitled.

~
采购
采购 (cǎigòu) is used specifically for purchasing supplies or goods for a business or organization.  It's not typically used for personal shopping.

~
雄伟
雄伟 (xióngwěi) is typically used to describe grand and imposing structures or natural landscapes, such as mountains or buildings.  It emphasizes magnificence and scale.

~
金融
金融 (jīnróng) encompasses a broader range of financial activities, including banking, investment, insurance, and other financial services.  It refers to the entire system of managing money and investments.

~
书店
书店 (shūdiàn) is often used for stores selling new books.  If the store primarily sells used books, it's more accurately described as 旧书店 (jiùshūdiàn).

~
患者
患者 (huànzhě) is a more formal and medical term for a patient.  病人 (bìngrén) is more commonly used in everyday conversation.

~
工夫
工夫 (gōngfu) can also refer to skill, expertise, or effort put into something, especially in the context of martial arts or crafts.  It can also mean "time" but is becoming less common.

~
完了
完了 (wánle) can also be used to express alarm or despair, similar to "Oh no!" or "I'm doomed!".  It doesn't always mean something is finished in a neutral sense.

~
采纳
采纳 (cǎinà) is a more formal term for accepting a suggestion, proposal, or plan.  It suggests careful consideration and approval by someone in authority.

~
录
录 (lù) has multiple meanings.  It can refer to recording, copying, writing down, carving, or even hitting. Be sure to pay attention to the context and surrounding words.

~
提交
提交 (tíjiāo) suggests formally presenting something for review or approval.  It implies a hierarchical relationship where one party submits something to a higher authority.

~
船只
船只 (chuánzhī) is a more formal and collective term for ships or boats.  It's often used in official contexts or when referring to a group of vessels.

~
凡是
凡是 (fánshì) emphasizes inclusivity and generality.  It means "all" or "every" without exception. It is often followed by 都 (dōu - "all") to further emphasize the all-encompassing nature of the statement. For example, 凡是努力的人都会成功 (fánshì nǔlì de rén dōu huì chénggōng) - "All those who work hard will succeed."

~
融合
融合 (rónghé) suggests a blending or merging of different elements into a harmonious whole.  It emphasizes the seamless integration of the parts.

~
再次
再次 (zàicì) is a more formal way to say "once again" or "once more".  It's commonly used in official announcements or formal writing.

~
股
股 (gǔ) can be a classifier for various things.  It classifies long, thin, flexible objects (like ropes, rivers), smells/smoke (a whiff), groups of people (gangs, bands), and bursts of energy/emotion (a surge of anger).

~
一番
一番 (yīfān) often means "a spell of" or "a period of," indicating a duration of time spent doing something.  It can also be used as a measure word for actions or experiences.  For instance, 一番努力 (yīfān nǔlì) means "a spell of hard work."

~
增长
增长 (zēngzhǎng) often refers to an increase in quantity, size, or intensity over time.  It's a more gradual and continuous increase than a sudden jump.

~
查看
查看 (chá kàn) emphasizes careful and thorough examination or inspection to understand something's condition or details. It is more than simply looking over something superficially.


~
公众
公众 (gōngzhòng) refers to the general public or the people as a whole.  It emphasizes the collective nature of the group, rather than individual citizens.

~
量
量 (liàng) can function as both a verb and a noun. As a noun, it means "quantity" or "amount". As a verb, it means "to measure" or "to estimate". It also serves as an abbreviation for 量词 (liàngcí) - measure words/classifiers.

~
聘请
聘请 (pìnqǐng) is generally used for hiring professionals or experts for a specific task or position.  It's more formal and implies a higher level of skill or expertise than just hiring someone for a regular job.

~
后头
后头 (hòutou) can also mean "later" or "in the future"  It's a more colloquial way to say 以后 (yǐhòu).

~
fu
This represents two different words. One is the character 副 (fù), which means "vice," "deputy," "assistant," etc. The other is the character 服 (fú), which means "clothes" or "to serve." Be careful to distinguish these by context.

~
热量
In the context of food, this translates to "calories." Otherwise, it just means "heat."

~
区域
This can refer to any area, but is more commonly used to refer to a large, vaguely defined area.

~
仍
This word has the same meaning and usage as 还 (hái), except 仍 is slightly more formal.

~
乘
This has many meanings, but most commonly means "to ride" something. Note that this word is usually used for larger vehicles, like cars, buses, ships, etc. For smaller vehicles like bicycles, the word to use is usually  骑 (qí).

~
将近
This has the same meaning as 差不多 (chàbuduō), but 将近 is more formal.

~
排行榜
There is no difference between the use of 排行榜 in Chinese and Leaderboard in English.

~
高大
Although this literally means tall and big, it is more commonly used to describe buildings or other inanimate objects that are large and imposing. For tall people, the word 高 (gāo) is usually sufficient.

~
心疼
This has two main meanings. One is to love someone dearly. The other is to feel sorry for someone. The specific meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
作
This has many meanings. When used as a verb, it can be translated as "to do," "to make," or "to write." When used as a noun, it can be translated as "work," "composition," or "deed." The specific meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
毫升
There is no difference between the use of 毫升 in Chinese and milliliter in English.

~
平坦
This word implies more than just being flat. It usually describes a vast, open expanse of flat land, and has positive connotations.

~
卷
This word is usually used for something rolled up, especially a scroll or something similar.

~
商场
This has two main meanings. One is "mall," while the other is "business world." Context makes the meaning clear.

~
冒
The most common meaning is "to risk," but this character has many others. It is usually apparent from the context.


~
支援
This means to support someone, usually by giving them material assistance like money, weapons, or other supplies.

~
外科
There is no difference between the use of 外科 in Chinese and surgery in English.

~
没想到
This is just like "didn't expect" in English.

~
蒙
This has many meanings. It's most common meaning is to cover. If you see this character, it's best to look it up in a dictionary and pick the definition which fits the context best.

~
车票
This can refer to a ticket for any kind of transportation, not just buses and trains.

~
不停
This has two meanings. One is "without stop," which is usually used for continuous motion. The other is "incessant," which describes something which occurs very frequently.

~
舞
This means to dance, but is usually used for more formal dances. For casual dancing, the word 跳舞 (tiàowǔ) is more common.

~
损害
This can be both physical and non-physical.

~
棉
There is no difference between the use of 棉 in Chinese and cotton in English.

~
两边
This means "both sides," but is usually used in the physical sense, as in "both sides of the street."

~
空儿
This has the same meaning as 空 (kōng), but is much more colloquial.

~
超越
This is just like "surpass" or "exceed" in English.

~
露
This has many meanings, but the most common is to reveal something, usually unintentionally.

~
预测
This has the same meaning as 预报 (yùbào), but 预测 is usually used for scientific or technical forecasts.

~
分行
This means "branch," and is usually used in the banking or financial context.

~
心里
This has the same meaning as 心 (xīn), but is slightly more colloquial.

~
牌
This has many meanings. The most common is a signboard or a brand. It can also refer to cards, mahjong tiles, or other similar objects.

~
夜间
This means "nighttime," but can refer to any time during the night.

~
汉字
There is no difference between the use of 汉字 in Chinese and Chinese character in English.

~
打击
This can mean a physical blow or a metaphorical one. It often implies something harmful or destructive.

~
金
This has many meanings, but most commonly refers to gold, money, or something of high quality or prestige.

~
不同
This means "different." There is no difference between the use of 不同 in Chinese and different in English.

~
左
This word usually means "left." It is also used in a few idioms.

~
适用
This is just like "applicable" or "suitable" in English.

~
夺取
This means to seize or capture something, but often implies a struggle or competition to obtain it.

~
价
价 (jià) can also mean "valence" in chemistry.

~
弯曲
Note that 弯曲 is more often used to describe physical objects like roads or wires.  For more abstract things, such as a "crooked/corrupt deal", the word 歪曲 (wāiqū) - to distort or misrepresent - is usually more appropriate.

~
变动
变动 carries a neutral connotation, simply indicating change.  For negative connotations like unwanted change or disruption, use words like 波动 (bōdòng fluctuation) or 动荡 (dòngdàng turbulence).

~
奶
奶 (nǎi) can refer to milk from any animal, not just a cow. For cow's milk specifically, you'd say 牛奶 (niúnǎi).  It can also be used as a term of address for a woman who has breastfed someone, similar to "wet nurse" or "milk mother."

~
发病
发病 refers specifically to the onset of a disease. It's not used for getting injured.

~
短片
While 短片 can refer to short videos in general, it often specifically implies a short film with a narrative structure, as opposed to just a clip.

~
一路
一路平安 (yílù píng'ān) is a common farewell, meaning "have a safe journey." 一路 can also be used with other words to describe the journey, such as 一路顺风 (yílù shùnfēng) - "bon voyage" (literally "may the wind be with you").

~
刺
刺 can also mean to irritate or stimulate (e.g., a smell 刺鼻 - cìbí - stings the nose). As a noun, it also means "thorn" or "prickle".

~
利
利 is often used in binomes related to pros and cons, like 利弊 (lìbì - advantages and disadvantages), or 福利 (fúlì - welfare; benefits).

~
晚安
晚安 is only used for "good night." It's not a general evening greeting like "good evening."

~
规划
规划 implies a more long-term, comprehensive plan, unlike 计划 (jìhuà), which can be for shorter-term or more specific tasks.

~
绿化
绿化 specifically refers to adding greenery, like plants and trees.  For making something literally green in color, use 涂绿 (tú lǜ).

~
四处
四处 emphasizes scattered or dispersed action, going in multiple directions.  到处 (dàochù) simply means everywhere.

~
慌
慌 describes a temporary state of panic.  For a more long-term or deep-seated fear, use 害怕 (hàipà).

~
轮椅
Be mindful of politeness when discussing disabilities.  Using 轮椅使用者 (lúnyǐ shǐyòng zhě) - wheelchair user - is generally preferred to directly labeling someone.

~
流动
流动 describes a continuous movement, like a river.  For single movements from one place to another, use 移动 (yídòng).

~
非得
非得 is more colloquial than 必须 (bìxū) and expresses a stronger sense of compulsion, often with a hint of stubbornness.

~
下去
下去 can also imply continuing a current action, similar to "go on" or "keep going."

~
剧场
剧场 is specifically a building for theatrical performances.  电影院 (diànyǐngyuàn) is the word for a movie theater.

~
扩展
扩展 emphasizes increasing the scope or scale of something.  扩大 (kuòdà) focuses on increasing size or quantity.

~
睡
睡 can also be used in the sense of "to stay overnight," as in 我想睡你家 (wǒ xiǎng shuì nǐ jiā) - "I'd like to stay at your place tonight."

~
大致
大致 focuses on the general idea, not precise details.  大概 (dàgài) is similar but can also refer to probability ("probably").

~
潮流
潮流 emphasizes fashion or popular trends.  趋势 (qūshì) is more general and can refer to any trend.

~
篮球
Besides the ball itself, 篮球 can also mean the sport of basketball.

~
早饭
早饭 is the most common word for breakfast. 早餐 (zǎocān) is more formal.

~
漫长
漫长 highlights the subjective experience of time feeling long, due to boredom or difficulty.  长 (cháng) simply means long in duration.

~
于
于 is a formal preposition with multiple uses. It is not interchangeable with 在 (zài).  For basic location, stick to 在.

~
考
考 can also refer to a deceased father.

~
年前
年前 can mean either "years ago" or "before the New Year," depending on context.

~
院子
院子 can also refer to a walled compound containing multiple buildings.

~
正义
正义 is a more abstract concept of justice.  公正 (gōngzhèng) refers to fairness in a specific situation.

~
电话
打电话 (dǎ diànhuà) means "to make a phone call."

~
指责
指责 implies strong criticism or blame.  批评 (pīpíng) is more general and can be constructive.

~
不利
不利 describes something as being disadvantageous or harmful. It does not directly translate to "unlucky."

~
不再
不再 emphasizes that something *used* to happen but *no longer* does.  没再 (méi zài) simply means it hasn't happened again.

~
有效
有效 implies that something produces the desired result.  有用 (yǒuyòng) simply means useful or helpful.

~
新郎
新娘 (xīnniáng) is the word for "bride."

~
戏
戏 has many meanings related to performance, playfulness, and tricks.  It's a component of many words like 游戏 (yóuxì - game) and 玩戏 (wánnòng - to play around).

~
这样
这样 is often used at the beginning of a sentence to introduce a conclusion or suggestion.


~
答
答 is the more formal and literary word for "to answer." 回答 (huídá) is more common in everyday conversation.

~
成品
成品 (chéngpǐn) refers to a product that has completed the manufacturing process and is ready for sale or use.  It emphasizes the state of being *fully completed and ready*.  While it can often overlap with "finished product," there's a subtle difference.  Think of "finished product" as simply meaning the product is no longer being worked on, while 成品 emphasizes its readiness for the next stage, whether that's sale, distribution, or further processing.  A cake that has just come out of the oven might be a "finished product" but not yet a 成品 until it's cooled, iced, and ready to be served.

~
手里
手里 (shǒulǐ) literally means "in hand."  Figuratively, it implies having something under control, possession, or responsibility.  It's often used to describe having tasks, resources, or information at one's disposal.  For example,  "我手里有很多工作" (wǒ shǒulǐ yǒu hěn duō gōngzuò) means "I have a lot of work on my hands."  手里 also conveys a sense of immediacy and availability, unlike other phrases like "掌握" (zhǎngwò - to grasp, control) which imply a more firm and long-term hold.

~
线
线 (xiàn) has numerous meanings related to long, thin objects or connections. Be mindful of its context-dependent interpretations.  When referring to physical objects like thread, string, or wire, 线 emphasizes their thin, flexible nature.  When referring to lines, routes, or connections, it implies a path or channel.  As a classifier, it is used for things that are long, thin and flexible, such as a ray of light or a stream of water. It's crucial to pay attention to the surrounding words to determine the precise meaning of 线 in a given sentence. Additionally, the "tier" ranking of Chinese cities is colloquial and not an official designation.

~
漩儿
The 儿 (er) suffix indicates a diminutive and affectionate meaning. So 漩儿 is not just a swirl, but a *little* swirl.  This word is colloquial.

~
硌
硌 is often used with the verb 得 (dé).  For example, 这块石头硌得我的脚疼死了 (zhè kuài shítóu gè de wǒ de jiǎo téng sǐ le) - This stone is hurting my foot so much.

~
书呆
书呆 (shūdāi) has more of a negative connotation compared to English words like "nerdy" and carries the implication that the person is socially inept because of their excessive focus on books.  A close but more neutral word is 书虫 (shūchóng), "bookworm."

~
概率
概率 is the more formal and technical term for probability, commonly used in academic or scientific contexts.  A more colloquial equivalent is  几率 (jīlǜ).

~
缝纫
缝纫 is a more formal and less common way to say "sewing" compared to the simpler and more frequently used word 缝 (féng).

~
睡袋
睡袋 is indeed "sleeping bag," but specifically emphasizes the bag itself.  If you're talking about the activity of using a sleeping bag, you might say 睡在睡袋里 (shuì zài shuìdài lǐ), which means "to sleep in a sleeping bag."

~
耳塞
耳塞 can refer to both earplugs *and* earphones.  Context is usually enough to determine the intended meaning.  If you need to specify, use 防噪音耳塞 (fángzàoyīn ěrsāi) for "noise-canceling earplugs" or  耳机 (ěrjī) for "earphones" or "headphones."

~
反腐
反腐 is a shortened form of 反腐败 (fǎnfǔbài), so it directly relates to the word 腐败.  It's a politically charged term frequently used in official contexts.

~
螃蟹
The measure word 只 (zhī) is typically used for crabs.

~
语法格
语法格 is a linguistic term.  While it translates to "grammatical case," be aware that Chinese does not have grammatical cases in the same way that languages like Latin or Russian do.

~
潲
潲 (xiào) has a strong regional association. It's particularly common in Southern Mandarin dialects and might not be universally understood. Standard Mandarin uses  瓢泼大雨 (piáopō dàyǔ) for "downpouring rain."

~
腐败
腐败 can refer to both literal rotting and metaphorical corruption.  It’s important to pay attention to the context.

~
剥
剥 has a wide range of uses.  It doesn’t simply mean "to peel." It can also refer to removing an outer layer from something, whether it's skin, shell, or even moving beads on an abacus.

~
刺绣
刺绣 can be both a noun and a verb. It means both the *act* of embroidering and the *embroidery* itself.

~
蹭饭
蹭饭 carries a slightly negative connotation, suggesting that someone is taking advantage of another's generosity.  It's often used humorously or self-deprecatingly.

~
帐篷
The two measure words for tent, 顶 (dǐng) and 座 (zuò), are used in slightly different ways.  顶 emphasizes the tent as a single unit, while 座 is more often used when discussing multiple tents or a tent as a structure, similar to how you would say "a building."

~
随和
随和 describes someone agreeable and easy to get along with.

~
特产
特产 refers to local specialties or products unique to a specific region.

~
捷克语
捷克语 is specifically the Czech *language*. If you want to refer to something related to the Czech Republic more generally, use 捷克 (Jiékè).

~
大白天
大白天 emphasizes that something is happening in broad daylight, often with a connotation of surprise or disbelief that it occurred at such a time.

~
红楼梦
红楼梦 is one of the Four Great Classical Novels of Chinese literature.  Its English translations are typically titled "Dream of the Red Chamber" or "A Dream of Red Mansions."

~
密度
密度 is often used in scientific contexts. It can also be used metaphorically to refer to the concentration of something, such as population density.

~
蛤蜊
Note the pronunciation of this word: gé lí.

~
章鱼
The more common name for octopus is 八爪鱼 (bā zhuǎ yú) literally, "eight-legged fish".

~
发呆
发呆 suggests being in a daze or staring blankly into space, often due to daydreaming or being lost in thought.  It can have a slightly negative connotation, implying a lack of focus.

~
开胃
开胃 can be used literally and figuratively. It literally means “to open the stomach,” but more commonly refers to “whetting the appetite.” Figuratively, 开胃 means to amuse oneself at someone’s expense.

~
山丘
山丘 refers to small hills, emphasizing their gentle slopes.

~
走廊
走廊 refers to a passageway, corridor, or hallway.  It can be indoors or outdoors.

~
刺眼
刺眼 is specifically used for light that is too bright and hurts the eyes.

~
T恤
No additional notes.

No additional notes.

~
篮球队
No additional notes.

~
一楼
In China, this means the ground floor. Note that this differs from American English usage.

迪士尼
Can refer to the company, Walt Disney himself, or anything Disney-related.

对了
Used as an interjection to introduce a new thought or topic that has just come to mind. Similar to "by the way" or "oh, that's right".

No additional notes.

~
判
Can mean "to judge", "to decide", "to sentence" (in a legal context), or "to differentiate".

~
到时候
Means "when the time comes" or "at that time". Often used to refer to a future event.

~
曹励嘉
No additional notes.

~
痛
Describes a sharper, more intense, and often sudden pain.  疼 is used for a milder, duller, and more persistent ache.

~
中国菜
No additional notes.

~
敲字
A more vivid and descriptive way to say "to type," emphasizing the action of striking the keys.  打字 is the more common and general term.

~
粉丝
Has two main meanings: (1) a type of noodle made from mung bean starch, and (2) a fan or enthusiast of someone or something.  Context usually clarifies which meaning is intended.

~
成年人
There is no difference between the use of 成年人 in Chinese and "adult" in English.

~
拿去
The difference between 拿去 (ná qù) and 带去 (dài qù) is subtle and often confusing for learners. Both verbs involve taking something to a place, but the key difference lies in the location of the speaker.  拿去 is used when the speaker is *at the destination* and someone is bringing the object *to them*.  带去 is used when the speaker is going somewhere and taking something along *with them*.  For example, a child is bringing a toy to their mother in the living room. The mother can say "把玩具拿来(ná lái)". On the other hand, if the mother takes her child to school, then she will 带 her child 去 学校 (dài tā qù xuéxiào).

~
冬令时
Remember that China only has one time zone. So even though 冬令时 exists as a word, it is in fact not used at all. For the entire year, China follows Beijing time.

~
中世纪
There is no difference between the use of 中世纪 in Chinese and "Middle Ages" or "medieval" in English.

~
年末
年末 (niánmò) refers to the end of the year, typically the period from December to the very end of the year. It has a similar meaning to 年底 (niándǐ), but 年底 can also refer to the end of a fiscal year, not just the calendar year. If you are just referring to the calendar year, 年末 and 年底 have the same meaning.

~
兽医
There is no difference between the use of 兽医 in Chinese and "veterinarian" in English.

~
连帽衫
There is no difference between the use of 连帽衫 in Chinese and "hoodie" in English.

~
说废话
There is no difference between the use of 说废话 in Chinese and "talk nonsense" in English.

~
生日卡
There is no difference between the use of 生日卡 in Chinese and "birthday card" in English.

~
车来了
车来了 (chē láile) is a versatile phrase used to announce the arrival of various forms of transportation, not just buses.  It can refer to taxis, trains, subways, or any other vehicle someone might be waiting for. The specific type of vehicle is usually understood from the context.

~
炒蔬菜
There is no difference between the use of 炒蔬菜 in Chinese and "fried vegetables" in English.

~
一条鱼
There is no difference between the use of 一条鱼 in Chinese and "a fish" in English.

~
动漫
动漫 (dòngmàn) encompasses both animation and comics. While sometimes used interchangeably with 动画 (dònghuà - animation), 动漫 often specifically refers to Japanese animation and manga.

~
西柚
There is no difference between the use of 西柚 in Chinese and "grapefruit" in English.

~
蓝莓
There is no difference between the use of 蓝莓 in Chinese and "blueberry" in English.

~
母语
There is no difference between the use of 母语 in Chinese and "native language" in English.

~
简体字
There is no difference between the use of 简体字 in Chinese and "simplified Chinese character" in English.

~
通勤
There is no difference between the use of 通勤 in Chinese and "commute" in English.

~
萝卜
Specifically, 萝卜 (luóbo) usually refers to the daikon radish (Raphanus sativus var. longipinnatus).  While it can sometimes refer to other radish varieties, daikon is the most common meaning.

~
躲猫猫
There is no difference between the use of 躲猫猫 in Chinese and "hide and seek" in English.

~
阴暗
阴暗 (yīn'àn) carries both literal and figurative meanings.  Literally, it describes a dimly lit or dark place. Figuratively, it can describe something gloomy, depressing, or even sinister.

~
杏仁糊
There is no difference between the use of 杏仁糊 in Chinese and "almond paste" in English.

~
一支笔
There is no difference between the use of 一支笔 in Chinese and "a pen" in English.

~
躲起来
There is no difference between the use of 躲起来 in Chinese and "hide oneself up" in English.

~
幻灯片
There is no difference between the use of 幻灯片 in Chinese and "slide" in English.

~
极端
There is no difference between the use of 极端 in Chinese and "extreme" in English.

~
症状
There is no difference between the use of 症状 in Chinese and "symptom" in English.

~
红肉橙
There is no difference between the use of 红肉橙 in Chinese and "cara cara" in English.

~
旧金山
There is no difference between the use of 旧金山 in Chinese and "San Francisco" in English.

~
软化
There is no difference between the use of 软化 in Chinese and "soften" in English.

~
等等
等等 (děngděng) has two main meanings.  It can mean "et cetera" or "and so on" when listing things. It can also mean "wait a moment" or "hold on," often used in spoken Chinese. The meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
为她想
为她想 (wèi tā xiǎng) emphasizes considering someone else's needs or perspective. It goes beyond simply "thinking about" someone; it suggests actively considering their well-being and making decisions with their interests in mind.

~
冷漠
冷漠 (lěngmò) describes a state of emotional detachment and indifference, often implying a lack of empathy or concern for others. It can describe a person's demeanor or their attitude towards a specific situation or person.

~
不舒服
不舒服 (bù shūfu) is a broad term for feeling unwell, either physically or emotionally. It can range from mild discomfort to more serious illness. If you are feeling significantly ill, you should use a more specific term.

~
燕麦粥
There is no difference between the use of 燕麦粥 in Chinese and "oatmeal" or "porridge" in English.

~
时区
There is no difference between the use of 时区 in Chinese and "time zone" in English.

~
段落
段落 (duànluò) can refer to a paragraph in writing or a distinct period or phase in a larger process or timeframe.

~
做完
做完 (zuò wán) emphasizes completing a task fully. It implies not only finishing the action but also ensuring its completion to a satisfactory degree.

~
说谎
There is no difference between the use of 说谎 in Chinese and "to lie" in English.

~
伴侣
伴侣 (bànlǚ) typically refers to a romantic partner, especially a spouse or long-term partner. It can also be used more broadly to mean "companion," but the romantic connotation is most common.

~
亲情
A more formal way to say this is 亲属关系 (qīnshǔ guānxi).

~
北方人
There is no single definition of where "Northern China" is.  For example, people in Jiangsu might call people in Shandong "Northerners".

~
月末
This means "at the end of the month". A related word is 月底 (yuèdǐ), which also means "at the end of the month". However, 月末 has more of an emphasis of "the final days of the month".  For example, if an event is happening on the 28th, 29th, 30th or 31st of the month, it's more natural to use 月末.

~
种菜
Note that the second character is pronounced with the fourth tone here.

~
有面子
The opposite of this is 丢面子 (diū miànzi), which means "lose face".  You can also say 很有面子 to emphasize the degree to which one gains face. Note that the meaning of 面子 is much broader than the literal English translation, "face".

~
一场雪
This is a poetic way to refer to an instance of snowfall.  More colloquially, one would say 下雪 (xià xuě).

~
接电话
The literal translation of this is "receive a phone call". This is a very common and perfectly acceptable way of saying "answer the phone".  Other more colloquial ways include 听电话 (tīng diànhuà).

~
大堂
This is a rather formal term for "lobby".  Other words for "lobby" include 门厅 (méntīng) and 前厅 (qiántīng).

~
攀岩
Another word for rock climbing is 岩石攀登 (yánshí pāndēng), which is more formal and technical.

~
百分比
A more colloquial equivalent is 百分率 (bǎifēnlǜ).

~
备份
This word is both a noun and a verb.

~
歌单
The prevalence of streaming music services has increased the usage of this word dramatically.

~
戴口罩
Note that this word uses 戴, not 带.

~
益虫
The opposite of this is 害虫 (hài chóng).

~
会议室
A similar word is 会议厅 (huìyì tīng), which usually refers to a larger meeting space.

~
卡农
卡农 is a transliteration of "canon".  卡农 can also refer to other types of canons, such as canons in literature or art.


~
杨红
This is a common Chinese name.

~
前男友
The female equivalent is 前女友 (qián nǚyǒu).

~
屁股
This word can be considered vulgar and should be used with care.  A more polite synonym is 臀部 (túnbù).

~
在一起
This is the most common and natural way to express "be in a romantic relationship". Be aware that it also has other meanings, including "together" in general. The context will generally make this clear.

~
卫衣
This is a relatively new word that has become popular in recent years. It encompasses various types of sweatshirts, hoodies, and sweaters.

~
好胜
This word carries a slightly negative connotation. It implies an excessive desire to win, even if it means being overly competitive or aggressive.  If you wish to describe someone who likes winning but is not overly aggressive, you can use the words 求胜心切 (qiúshèngxīnqiè) or 竞争意识强 (jìngzhēng yìshí qiáng).

~
一顿饭
This is the most standard way of saying "a meal". In some dialects, 一餐饭 (yī cān fàn) can also be used.

~
弓
Although 弓 can be used as a verb, it is usually used as a noun.  When used as a verb, it is usually paired with another word, e.g., 弓着背 (gōngzhe bèi) means to hunch one's back.


~
华氏度
The more common way to describe temperatures is Celsius (摄氏度 - shèshìdù). However, Fahrenheit can still be encountered in some scientific or technical contexts.


~
两年后
Similarly, you can say "two years ago" as 两年前 (liǎng nián qián)

~
泰国
The demonym for Thailand is 泰国人 (Tài guó rén).

~
杏仁膏
You could also just say almond paste.

~
住宅区
This is a more formal way to say residential area.  A more colloquial way is 小区 (xiǎoqū).

~
柚子
In southern China, this word usually refers to the pomelo, but in northern China it might refer to the grapefruit.


~
猜灯谜
This is a traditional activity during the Lantern Festival (元宵节 - Yuánxiāojié), which marks the end of the Chinese New Year celebrations.

~
涩
This word can be used to describe the taste of unripe fruit, but also for other unpleasant tastes like bitterness or astringency. Figuratively, it can refer to something that is awkward, uncomfortable, or difficult to understand, such as a social situation or a piece of writing.

~
农历
The lunar calendar is used to determine traditional Chinese festivals.  However, most day-to-day scheduling in China follows the Gregorian calendar.

~
休息室
In most contexts this word refers to a small room used for short breaks in workplaces or public areas. Another meaning is a room in a funeral home where family view the deceased's body.

~
一条蛇
Be careful of the tones when saying this phrase, since the tone of 一 changes depending on the tone that follows. Here, 一 is pronounced with the second tone.

~
过新年
This term is very versatile, covering everything from the few days just before New Years to the entire New Years period.  In China this could be referring to the Lunar New Year, or the Western New Year.


~
打屁股
This is the most common way to say "spank".  It is often used as a light-hearted way to describe a mild punishment, especially for children.  However, in more formal or serious contexts, 体罚 (tǐfá) is used.

~
圣诞节
Christmas is not a traditional Chinese holiday, but it has become increasingly popular in recent years, especially among young people in urban areas.

~
排除法
This term is generally used in problem-solving or reasoning situations, where you eliminate unlikely options to arrive at the correct solution.


~
王蕴宏	
No notes.

~
量词	
A useful way to think about 量词 is that they specify the *shape* of the noun. So, for example, we use 枝 (zhī) for long, thin objects like pens and guns. We use 张 (zhāng) for flat objects like paper and tables.  This can help in memorizing which 量词 goes with which noun.

~
藏起来	
The difference between 藏 (cáng) and 躲 (duǒ) is that 藏 is for hiding *things*, while 躲 is for hiding *oneself*.

~
害虫	
No notes.

~
拿来	
The 来 here indicates motion *towards* the speaker. The opposite is 拿去 (ná qù). Note that these phrases are more colloquial than other ways of expressing "bring" and "take," such as 带 (dài).

~
软柿子	
This is a useful idiom for learners to know, as it is quite common and has no direct English equivalent.

~
有美感	
No notes.

~
专注

做好	
做好 means to *complete* something *well*. 做完 (zuò wán) just means to complete it.

场 (chǎng) is the measure word for events like rain, snow, wind, movies, etc.

一节课	
节 (jié) is the measure word for classes, lessons, train carriages, and other segmented things.

暖心

~
叶子华

~
教科书

~
买菜	
菜 (cài) here specifically refers to food, groceries, or ingredients, *not* dishes.

~
新历	
No notes.

~
广萝丽	
No notes.

~
煎鸡蛋
This literally translates to "fried egg", but it typically refers to a sunny-side up egg.  If you want to specify other kinds of fried eggs, you can say "荷包蛋" (hébāodàn) for sunny-side up, "双面煎蛋" (shuāngmiàn jiāndàn) for over easy/medium/hard.

~
迸发
While 迸发 (bèngfā) can describe a literal bursting, it's more commonly used metaphorically to describe a sudden surge of emotions, creativity, or energy.  Think of it as something bursting forth from within. For example, "热情迸发" (rèqíng bèngfā) means "bursting with enthusiasm."

~
好笑
Be careful with the tone.  好笑 (hǎoxiào) means funny.  If you say 好笑 (hàoxiào) with a falling tone, it means laughable in a *bad* way – ridiculous or absurd.

~
糖果
While 糖果 (tángguǒ) generally refers to sweets or candy, it leans more towards individually wrapped candies or small treats. If you're talking about dessert in general, use 甜点 (tiándiǎn).

~
西班牙
No special notes.

~
膝盖
The internet slang meaning "to kneel down in admiration" is very common online, so be aware of this usage. You might see it used with the phrase “跪了” (guì le).

~
草莓
Be aware of the slang meaning "hickey".  It's common in Taiwan and increasingly used in mainland China as well.

~
幸福感
This word emphasizes the *feeling* of happiness, rather than happiness as a state of being.  It's more like a sense of well-being or contentment.

~
坏了
The colloquial uses are important to note. 坏了 can be used as an exclamation similar to "Shoot!" "Gosh!" or "Oh no!" The suffix use, 坏了,  expresses something to the utmost degree, usually negative. For example, 忙坏了 means "extremely busy".

~
商业区
While this can refer to a downtown area, it more specifically refers to a district with a concentration of businesses, which may or may not be in the city center.

~
从商
This implies a longer-term engagement in business, rather than a single transaction.  It often suggests a career in business.

~
浪漫的
The concept of romance in Chinese culture can be slightly different from Western cultures. While 浪漫的 (làngmàn de) can describe romantic love, it also encompasses a broader sense of dreaminess, sentimentality, and a focus on creating a special atmosphere.

~
释迦果
No special notes.

~
素食
This can refer to both the food itself and the practice of eating a vegetarian diet.

~
一家人
This emphasizes the unity and closeness of a family. It can also be used figuratively to refer to a group of close friends or colleagues.

~
比萨饼
While 比萨饼 is the more formal and complete term, 比萨 (bǐsà) is more common in everyday conversation.

~
东亚
No special notes.

~
富人
This term can sometimes carry a slightly negative connotation, especially in contexts discussing wealth disparity.

~
感恩节
No special notes.

~
有意义
This emphasizes the presence of meaning or significance.  It suggests that something is worthwhile, important, or has a deeper purpose.

~
门把

~

~
爱说话
This can be neutral or slightly negative, depending on context. It can mean "talkative," but also "chatty" or even "gossipy."

~

~
棺材
Be mindful of the cultural sensitivity surrounding death and funerals in Chinese culture.  Avoid using this word casually.

~
印度菜
No special notes.

~
本地
This refers to the immediate locality or area, as opposed to somewhere further away.

~
吐实
This implies confessing or revealing a hidden truth, often reluctantly or under pressure.

~
好好儿
The 儿 (er) adds a colloquial and softening effect to the word.  It emphasizes the sincerity and good intentions of the speaker.

~
虚假
This emphasizes the artificiality or lack of authenticity of something.

~
降落伞

~

~

This emphasizes the monetary loss or compensation aspect.

~
说漏嘴

你身边

~
龚美丽

~
加湿器

~
诶
This interjection has a wide range of uses and its meaning is highly dependent on context and tone.

~
五星
In addition to "five-star" and the five planets, 五星 can also refer to the Five-starred Red Flag, the national flag of the People's Republic of China.

~
王一然	
No notes.

~
Eva

~
蒸鸡蛋

~
听不懂	
No notes.

~
手臂	
While 手臂 can refer to the whole arm, it more often refers to the part of the arm from the shoulder to the elbow, i.e. the upper arm.  If you want to refer to the whole arm, the word 胳膊 (gēbo) is more appropriate.

~
市中心

~
瑞典

~

~
给你看

~

~
坏习惯

~
爱玩	
This can mean "like to play," but depending on context, can also have a negative connotation of being frivolous or irresponsible.  For example, if you say someone 爱玩, it can sometimes imply that they are not serious about their studies or work.

~
一棵树	
No notes.

~
国旗

~
箭	
No notes.

~
灯笼

~
荒凉

~
腥	
No notes.

~
X以上	
Be aware that 以上 is inclusive, i.e., it means "greater than or equal to X."  If you want to specify "strictly greater than X," you would say 超过 X (chāoguò X) or 大于 X (dàyú X).

This can refer to a fire alarm (the device), but it also refers to a fire emergency itself.

~

~

~
臊	
The meaning of "smell of urine" is usually only applied to children.

~

Note that 流量 most commonly refers to cellular data usage.

~
