~
一把刀	
No notes.

~
疫情
疫情 is more accurately translated as "epidemic situation".  While it can refer to the epidemic itself, it often encompasses the broader context, including the government's response, public health measures, and the overall impact on society.

~
熟成
When referring to fruit, this word means that it's perfectly ripe, at the peak of its flavor and ready to eat.  It's a more specific and positive term than just saying the fruit is "ripe."

~
冰雕节
The most famous 冰雕节 is held in Harbin (哈尔滨), and if you use this term, people will likely assume you're talking about the Harbin Ice Festival.

~
孔明灯
Be mindful of local regulations regarding 孔明灯 as they pose a fire hazard and are banned in some areas.

~
闪婚
This word often carries a slightly negative or skeptical connotation, suggesting that the marriage might be impulsive and not well-considered.

~
大腿
While 大腿 primarily means "thigh," it can also be used colloquially to refer to someone powerful or influential who offers support or protection, similar to the English idiom "having a strong backing."

~
洗手液
洗手液 is generally liquid soap.  If you need to specify the foaming type, you can say 泡沫洗手液 (pàomò xǐshǒuyè).

~
咨询室
This term can be used for a variety of consultation rooms, from psychological counseling to academic advising.  The specific type of consultation is usually clarified through context or additional modifiers.

~
不可能
除了“impossible”以外，不可能 also means "no way!" or "I can't!" as an exclamation of disbelief or refusal.

~
一群人
一群人 is a general term, but if the group is organized or has a shared purpose, a more specific term like 团队 (tuánduì, "team") or  组织 (zǔzhī, "organization") might be more appropriate.

~
说真话
This phrase emphasizes the act of telling the truth, often implying that it's difficult or risky to do so.

~
南方人
The definition of "south" in China can be relative. Someone from Hunan might be considered a 南方人 to someone from Beijing, but a 北方人 (northerner) to someone from Guangdong.

~
办公楼
While both 座 and 栋 can be used as measure words for 办公楼, 座 is generally used for smaller office buildings, while 栋 is more common for larger, multi-story buildings.

~
浴袍
In China, 浴袍 are commonly provided in hotels and spas, but not always worn at home as frequently as in some Western cultures.

~
我睡了
This phrase is more accurately translated to "I'm going to sleep now" and signifies an intention to go to sleep imminently.

~
同义词
Note that true synonyms are rare, and 同义词 often refers to words with similar but not identical meanings.

~
哈尔滨
Harbin is known for its cold winters and Russian influence, which is reflected in its architecture and culture.

~
沈朗天
This is likely a transliteration of a foreign name, probably "Elliot Sanborn."

~
抓马
"抓马" originates from the transliteration of the English word "drama." While it can simply mean "drama" in a general sense, it often refers specifically to interpersonal conflict, gossip, or sensational events.

~
赚钱
This term often carries a connotation of actively seeking ways to make money, possibly through business or investment, rather than simply earning a salary.

~
烦躁
烦躁 describes a state of both irritability and restlessness, a combination of being annoyed and unable to sit still.

~
繁体字
繁体字 are used in Taiwan, Hong Kong, and Macau.  While generally understood by mainland Chinese speakers, they are not commonly used in mainland China.

~
一个梗
This term is relatively new, reflecting the increasing influence of internet culture.  It often refers to inside jokes, catchphrases, or humorous images that circulate online.

~
混乱的
混乱的 can describe both physical disorder and a state of mental confusion.

~
在街上
Be aware that 街上 (on the street) is more commonly used in China than its English equivalent. One might say 在街上 instead of 在公园 or 在银行 while having the same intended meaning as the english translations of these phrases (in the park and in/at the bank respectively).


~
噩梦
While 噩梦 specifically refers to a bad dream that causes fear or distress, it can also be used metaphorically to describe a very unpleasant or difficult situation.

~
看不懂
This can refer to not understanding written text, spoken language, or even a situation or someone's behavior.

~
着迷
着迷 implies a strong and sometimes excessive fascination or obsession with something.

~
长裤
长裤 is a general term for trousers or pants, regardless of the material or style.

~
小偷
Beware of pickpockets in crowded areas, especially tourist attractions.

~
橙子
橙子 can refer to various types of oranges, including mandarins and tangerines.

~
纳粹
This term carries strong negative connotations due to the historical atrocities committed by the Nazis.

~
旗子
The type of flag is usually specified with a modifier, such as 国旗 (guóqí, national flag) or 校旗 (xiàoqí, school flag).

~
背心
背心 can refer to different types of sleeveless garments, including tank tops, vests, and undershirts.  Context usually clarifies the specific type.

~
总统
Although 总统 technically can refer to the president of any organization, it is almost exclusively used to refer to the president of a country. If you want to talk about the president of a company, you should use 总裁 (zǒngcái).

~
空气
The word 空气 can also be used figuratively to refer to a general mood or atmosphere, e.g.  学习空气 (xuéxí kōngqì) "learning atmosphere."  It is similar to the English word "vibe."  Another figurative use relates to a person's perceived social standing or "face." In this context, it can describe a puffed-up sense of self-importance: 他太好空气了 (tā tài hào kōngqì le)  "He’s got such an inflated ego!"


~
笨
笨 (bèn) carries a slightly stronger negative connotation than words like "clumsy" or "foolish." It's closer to "stupid" but can also suggest a lack of practical skills. It's generally not used as a lighthearted tease.

~
抱
Aside from the meanings given above, 抱 (bào) also describes holding an attitude or belief: 抱有希望 (bàoyǒu xīwàng) - to hold onto hope.

~
秘密
秘密 can be an adjective ("secret") or a noun ("a secret").  As a noun, it can be followed by a 的 clause. For example,  秘密的武器 (mìmì de wǔqì) "Secret weapon."  Notice this is 的 and not 地, as the word is acting as a noun and not an adjective here.

~
依然
依然 (yīrán) emphasizes continuity despite change, similar to "still" or "as before." However, it has a more formal and literary tone.  A more common and versatile equivalent is 还是 (háishì).

~
抬
抬 (tái) specifically implies lifting something heavy or cumbersome, often requiring two or more people.  For lifting lighter objects, use 拿 (ná) or 提 (tí).

~
期待
This word is somewhat formal (书面). A more colloquial way to say "look forward to" is "盼着" (pànzhe).

~
科学
科学 (kēxué) can function as both a noun and an adjective.  As an adjective, it can mean "scientific" or "rational," indicating a logical and systematic approach.

~
节省
This can be a verb or adjective. As a verb, it suggests the active effort of saving or conserving something such as money, time, or resources. As an adjective, 节省 describes someone who is frugal or economical.  It sometimes carries a connotation of being stingy.

~
亲爱
亲爱 (qīn'ài) is generally used as a term of endearment in written language, like in letters. In spoken Chinese, it sounds a bit overly formal or dramatic.  More common spoken equivalents include  亲爱的 (qīn'ài de) followed by a name or term of relationship, or simply using terms like 宝贝 (bǎobèi) - "baby," or  老公 (lǎogōng) - "husband,"老婆 (lǎopo) - "wife."

~
脾气
脾气 (píqi) often refers to a negative temper or disposition.  If you want to speak of temperament in a more general or positive way, use 性格 (xìnggé).


~
完全
完全 (wánquán) carries a sense of thoroughness and completeness.  It is more emphatic than  都 (dōu).


~
掉
掉 (diào) is often used as a complement following other verbs, indicating completion or separation, a resultative complement.  For example,  吃掉 (chīdiào) - to eat up completely,  忘掉 (wàngdiào) - to completely forget.


~
盘子
Although it can refer to a tray, 盘子 (pánzi) more commonly means a plate or dish used for serving food.

~
重量
重量 is the noun "weight". The associated verb is  称重 (chēngzhòng) - to weigh.

~
吸收
吸收 (xīshōu) can mean to absorb both physically (like a sponge) and metaphorically (like absorbing information or ideas).

~
尽快
尽快 is very formal. A more colloquial alternative is  快点儿 (kuài diǎnr).

~
本来
本来 (běnlái) is often used to emphasize a prior plan or expectation that has changed or been disrupted.  It can also mean "originally," "at first," "supposed to," or "should have."

~
辣
辣 (là) refers to the spicy heat of foods, primarily from chili peppers.  If you are sensitive to spicy foods, you can ask for your dish to be 不辣 (bù là) - not spicy, or 微辣 (wēi là) - slightly spicy.


~
师傅
师傅 (shīfu) is a versatile term of respect for skilled workers, such as drivers, chefs, plumbers, etc. It can also be used to address strangers, particularly men of an older generation.

~
召开
召开 (zhàokāi) is specifically used for formally organized meetings or conferences, such as a congress or board meeting. For more informal gatherings, use  举行 (jǔxíng) or 举办 (jǔbàn).

~
单独
单独 (dāndú) stresses being alone and separate from others.  It differs from  自己 (zìjǐ) which means "oneself" or "by oneself" and doesn't necessarily imply solitude.

~
合同
合同 (hétóng) is a legally binding agreement, a formal contract. For more casual agreements, use 协议 (xiéyì).

~
无所谓
无所谓 (wúsuǒwèi)  can also express that something is trivial or inconsequential, not just indifference. It can also mean something like "whatever" in English.

~
付款
付款 (fùkuǎn) refers specifically to the action of paying money. The noun for payment itself is  付款额 (fùkuǎn'é)  or just 款 (kuǎn).

~
动画片
动画片 (dònghuàpiàn) specifically refers to animated movies or cartoons. For animation in general, use 动画 (dònghuà).

~
趟
趟 (tàng) as a measure word usually goes with verbs of motion like  走 (zǒu), 跑 (pǎo), and 去 (qù).  It emphasizes the completion of a round trip.

~
考虑
考虑 (kǎolǜ) suggests a more thorough and deliberate process of thinking something over, often involving weighing pros and cons.  For simpler thinking, use 想 (xiǎng).


~
成功
成功 (chénggōng) is both a verb and a noun. It often pairs with 失败 (shībài) - to fail, to create an contrasting pair: 成功或失败 (chénggōng huò shībài) - success or failure.


~
小伙子
小伙子 (xiǎohuǒzi) is specifically used for young, often unmarried, men.  It has a slightly informal and often playful tone.


~
地位
地位 (dìwèi) denotes social standing, rank, or position within a hierarchy. It can also represent an abstract place or position in a broader context, like historical significance or importance in a field.


~
获得
获得 (huòdé) implies gaining something through effort or achievement, like obtaining a degree, a prize, or recognition.  For simply receiving something, use 收到 (shōudào) or 得到 (dédào).

~
长途
长途 (chángtú) is generally paired with words suggesting travel or communication:  长途电话 (chángtú diànhuà) - long-distance call, 长途旅行 (chángtú lǚxíng) - long-distance travel.

~
袜子
袜子 (wàzi) always occurs in pairs. Therefore, although you could theoretically count a single sock, you would never use the measure word 只 (zhī), which denotes single items. Instead, you always use 双 (shuāng) or 对 (duì), which emphasize pairs.

~
投资
投资 (tóuzī) is both a noun and a verb, translating to "investment" and "to invest."  It usually refers to financial investment. For investment in terms of effort or time, use other verbs like 投入 (tóurù).

~
失败
失败 (shībài) suggests a lack of success in achieving a specific goal, often implying a setback or defeat.  It has a stronger negative connotation than simply not succeeding.


~
得
得 (děi/de) has several meanings, and in certain cases can be pronounced děi or de. When it means "must" or "have to", it's pronounced děi. When it functions as a possessive marker (like 's in English) or as a structural particle linking a verb/adjective to a resultative or descriptive complement, it's pronounced de. Pay attention to context to discern the correct pronunciation and meaning.


~
避免
避免 (bìmiǎn) implies taking proactive steps to prevent something undesirable from happening.  It differs from  防止 (fángzhǐ) which focuses on general preventative measures rather than specific avoidance.

~
抄
抄 (chāo) has several meanings and can also describe taking a shortcut or folding one's arms, but its usage as "to copy" or related meanings are by far the most frequent and useful for learners.

~
针对
The difference between 针对 and 对 is subtle. 针对 suggests a more purposeful and direct action or focus. It often implies a specific problem or issue is being addressed, or a particular group is being targeted.  对 is more general and can be used in a wider range of situations where something is simply directed at or towards something else.  Think of 针对 as "specifically targeting" and 对 as "towards" or "at."

~
橡皮
Note, if you want to be specific that you're talking about an eraser (and not just rubber) you should add 擦 (cā - to rub, to wipe) in front, i.e. 橡皮擦.

~
模型
模型 can refer to both a physical model (like a scale model of a building) or an abstract model (like a statistical model).

~
乘坐
This word is more formal than 坐.

~
扩大
This word is generally used to describe increasing physical size or scope.  It's less commonly used for abstract concepts. For increasing influence or power, 扩张 (kuòzhāng) might be more appropriate.

~
也许
Perhaps is a bit more formal than maybe.

~
提
Be careful with the tones. 提一提 (tí yī tí - to mention) and 提一题 (tí yī tí - to carry a question) are easily confused.  Also, 提 is used as a verb, but not a noun. To make it into a noun (a handle) use 提手 (tíshǒu)

~
熟练
This implies a high degree of skill and fluency acquired through practice. It's stronger than just "familiar" with something.

~
具备
This implies not just having something, but having it as a necessary quality or characteristic.  It often describes meeting certain requirements or qualifications.

~
开水
Specifically means boiling or recently boiled water, suitable for making tea, etc.  It does *not* refer to any hot water in general.

~
大型
This emphasizes scale and complexity, often involving significant resources and organization.  It's more than just "big."

~
随手
This describes an action done casually, without much effort, often while doing something else.  It often has a connotation of convenience or thoughtlessness.

~
讲座
More formal and academic than just a talk or speech.

~
邀请
More formal than just asking someone to do something. It implies a certain level of formality and courtesy.

~
未必
This is stronger than "maybe not."  It often implies doubt or skepticism about a certain possibility.

~
于是
Indicates a direct consequence or result of a preceding action or event.

~
积累
This emphasizes gradual accumulation over time.

~
在于
Indicates where the key aspect or essence of something lies.  Similar to saying "lies in" or "depends on."

~
弱
Can be used to describe physical weakness, a weak argument, or a less developed skill. Context is important.

~
抱歉
More formal than 对不起.

~
得意
Be careful – this can have a negative connotation of being arrogant or conceited.

~
下载
Specifically refers to downloading digital files.

~
骨头
Besides meaning "bone," it can also refer to character or strength of will.

~
培养
Implies careful and sustained effort in developing or nurturing something or someone.

~
原谅
More formal and serious than just excusing a small mistake.

~
以为
Often implies a mistaken assumption.

~
交际
More formal and structured than just chatting.

~
挺
As an adverb, 挺 (tǐng) means "very" or "quite."  It's colloquial and usually used before adjectives, often suggesting a pleasant surprise.

~
反映
In the context of reporting or making something known, it carries a more formal tone than other verbs like 说 or 告诉, and often implies a problem or issue being raised to a higher authority.

~
厕所
A more direct and less euphemistic term than 洗手间 (xǐshǒujiān - washroom).

~
脱
Can be used both literally (taking off clothes) and figuratively (escaping a difficult situation).

~
按照
A related word is 根据 (gēnjù). In general, 根据 emphasizes the rationale or justification for something, especially a law or regulation. It is more about the state of the world and less about the speaker's actions or opinions. On the other hand, 按照 highlights the specific process or protocol being followed. In other words, 根据 is more about the basis, while 按照 is more about the manner of implementation.

Contexts: 根据 is usually used with rules, e.g. 规定 (guīdìng), 法律 (fǎlǜ) etc. On the other hand, 按照 is usually used with requests or directions, e.g. 要求 (yāoqiú), 说法 (shuōfǎ), etc.

Finally, a different related word is 依照 (yīzhào). This has the same meaning as 根据, but is used more in the written register.


~
燃烧
More dramatic and intense than just "burning."  Often used for large fires or passionate emotions.

~
诗
Refers specifically to poetry as a literary form.

~
座
As a classifier, 座 is used for large, immovable objects like mountains, buildings, bridges, etc.

~
广播
Can refer to both the act of broadcasting and the content being broadcast.

~
延长
Implies making something longer in time or space.

~
精彩
Implies a high level of skill, artistry, or excitement.

~
无数
Emphasizes a vast, uncountable quantity.

~
烦
Can mean to be bothered or annoyed, but also to trouble someone with a request.  The context is crucial.

~
报名
Can be used with 参加 (cānjiā, to participate) to form the phrase 报名参加, meaning "to register to participate in".  For example, 我报名参加了比赛 (wǒ bàomíng cānjiā le bǐsài) - I registered to participate in the competition.

~
存
The meanings "to exist", "to survive", and "to store" are all quite common and important. Note also the very common phrases 储存 (chǔcún, to store; storage) and 存在 (cúnzài, to exist; existence).

~
礼拜天
More formal than 星期天 (xīngqítiān).  Also, unlike 星期天, 礼拜天 cannot be used for days of the week other than Sunday.

~
矿泉水
While both 瓶 (píng) and 杯 (bēi) are measure words for 矿泉水, 瓶 is far more common. 杯 is more appropriate for a single serving poured into a drinking glass.

~
小吃
Often used in the plural, 小吃 (xiǎochī) refers to snacks or small dishes, especially those unique to a particular region.  家 (jiā) as a measure word here is most common in the context of counting establishments selling snacks.

~
治疗
Often used with other words to create more specific medical terms.  For instance, 治疗方法 (zhìliáo fāngfǎ) means "treatment method", and 接受治疗 (jiēshòu zhìliáo) means "to undergo treatment".

~
管理
Covers a broad range of managerial activities.  Can refer to managing people, resources, or even information.

~
餐厅
The measure word 家 (jiā) is more commonly used for smaller restaurants, while 间 (jiān) is more common for larger restaurants and rooms in general.

~
占线
Specifically refers to a phone line being busy.  For other situations where something is occupied, use other words like 忙 (máng) or 被占用 (bèi zhànyòng).

~
最好
While often translated as "had better", 最好 carries a slightly softer tone of advice or suggestion. It does not have the same force of obligation as "must" or "should".

~
甚至
Often used to introduce an extreme example to further emphasize a point. It indicates a surprising or unexpected extent.

~
态度
Can describe a general disposition towards something or someone.  It often carries a connotation of the emotion or feeling displayed.

~
由
When used to mean "by" indicating the agent performing an action, it often carries a slightly more formal tone than other options like 被 (bèi) or 让 (ràng).

~
记者
Often used in compounds like 新闻记者 (xīnwén jìzhě) - news reporter, or 体育记者 (tǐyù jìzhě) - sports reporter.

~
熟悉
Implies a deeper understanding than simply knowing something.  It suggests familiarity through experience or close contact.

~
往往
Indicates a high probability or frequency of something happening, often based on past experience or observation.

~
说不定
Expresses uncertainty and possibility. It often implies a hopeful or optimistic outlook on the uncertain situation.

~
卫生间
A more polite and formal term for bathroom/toilet than other terms like 厕所 (cèsuǒ).

~
后悔
Usually implies a sense of self-blame or remorse for a past action or decision.

~
透明
The figurative meaning, "transparent; open to scrutiny," emphasizes honesty and openness, often in the context of organizational practices or governmental affairs.

~
官
Used alone, can have somewhat negative connotations, similar to "bureaucrat" or "officialdom" in English. More often appears in compounds referring to different ranks.

~
神话
Can refer to both the body of myths of a culture and a single myth or legendary story.

~
台
The different meanings of 台 can seem unrelated, but they all share the underlying meaning of something elevated, prominent, or supporting something else.

~
打针
The focus is on the act of injecting, regardless of who is receiving the injection.  Both giving and receiving injections are encompassed by this term.

~
逐步
Highlights the gradual and steady nature of a process.  Suggests progress in stages or increments.

~
经典
Implies something timeless and influential. It's often used to describe works of art, literature, or film that have enduring value.

~
之
Often found in classical Chinese texts and some formal contexts today.  Be aware that its use can make your language sound artificial in modern conversations.

~
热闹
Focuses on the atmosphere of noise and excitement. It can describe places, events, or even people.

~
专心
Implies a high degree of focus and concentration. It suggests putting all of one's attention on a single task.

~
赢
Can also be used figuratively to describe gaining an advantage or succeeding in a non-competitive situation.

~
哪怕
Used to express a strong sense of determination or resolve, even in the face of adversity or unfavorable conditions.

~
降落
Used not just for aircraft but can also refer to things like parachutes, birds, or even snowflakes descending to the ground.

~
普遍
Suggests something common and widespread, often across a large area or population.

~
耐心
Can be used both as a noun (patience) and an adjective (patient).  The context will usually make the intended meaning clear.

~
顺便
Highlights the convenience and lack of extra effort involved in doing something while already engaged in another activity.

~
俩
A colloquial contraction of 两个 (liǎng ge), "two." It is generally used for people or things that are closely related or considered a pair.

~
纪律
Often used in contexts related to rules, behavior, and maintaining order, especially within an organization or group.

~
倒
Has a very wide range of meanings and uses. Pay close attention to context to determine its specific meaning.  The "contrary to expectation" usage is particularly important.

~
老婆
While a common term for "wife," 老婆 (lǎopo) can be considered informal.  More formal terms include 妻子 (qīzi) or 太太 (tàitai), depending on context.

~
规模
Describes the size and extent of something, often referring to projects, organizations, or events.  It emphasizes the overall magnitude.

~
取
The meanings "to get" and "to fetch" are slightly less common than the meanings "to take" and "to choose".  When used in the sense of "to choose", there is sometimes the connotation of selecting a good or auspicious option (e.g., picking a lucky number, choosing an auspicious date for a wedding).

~
使用
Can be used as a noun or a verb.

~
脏
Note that this word can be read as either zāng (dirty) or zàng (internal organs). However, in spoken Mandarin, it is more common to say  内脏 (nèizàng) for internal organs.

~
促进
This has the connotation of "actively" promoting something, sometimes behind the scenes, in the sense of lobbying or working towards change.  It's not merely stating one's agreement with something.

~
逐渐
This means gradually but specifically with the sense of a continuing trend.

~
调皮
While this can be translated as "naughty", it sometimes carries a less negative connotation in Chinese than "naughty" does in English. It can sometimes suggest playful misbehavior rather than deliberate wrongdoing.  It is often used to describe children or pets.

~
并且
This emphasizes the addition of information to what has already been said. It's stronger than simply saying "and".  It introduces a further point, often a stronger or more significant one.

~
细节
This isn't always used in the same way as "details" in English. In Chinese, it can refer to smaller points, often practical ones, that need to be addressed, especially within a plan or arrangement.

~
销售
This can be a noun or a verb.

~
浪漫
This word is usually used to describe a person, an event or atmosphere, rather than an object. Saying something like "a romantic flower" (浪漫的花) sounds unusual in Chinese.

~
挂
The meaning "to hang up" (the phone) is now archaic. It's better to use 挂断 (guàduàn) for this meaning. The slang meanings (to kill, to fail etc) are very informal and best avoided.

~
出生
This is more often used when speaking *about* someone else being born. If you want to say *where* you were born, then it's better to use 出生于 (chūshēng yú). For example:

我出生于北京。(wǒ chūshēng yú běijīng) = I was born in Beijing.


~
污染
This emphasizes the negative effects of pollution, not just the presence of pollutants.

~
凉快
This implies a pleasant coolness, a refreshing temperature. It doesn't describe something that's simply "not hot".

~
西瓜
The measure word 颗 (kē) is preferred. 个 is also acceptable, but less common.


~
迫切
This describes something that needs immediate attention and action.  It suggests a sense of urgency and importance.

~
剩
When used as a verb, it takes the following structure:

Subject + 还 + 剩 + Object

~
流传
This word describes the spreading of stories, rumors, traditions, and legends. It isn't typically used for the spread of things like diseases.

~
戴
For hats, you can also use the word 帽子 (màozi). Otherwise, the usage of 戴 is just like "wear" in English, for accessories like jewelry and scarves.


~
厉害
This word has a very broad meaning. It can be either positive or negative, and the meaning must often be determined from context.  It generally expresses a strong impression or impact.

~
难道
This is used rhetorically in questions to express disbelief or disapproval.  It expects a negative answer or agreement with the speaker's implied assertion.

~
急忙
This word describes hurried actions prompted by a sense of urgency or the need to be somewhere quickly.

~
圆
This can also be used to describe a situation being perfectly resolved, or a lie being seamless and believable.

~
桥
Be sure to use the correct measure word (座 zuò).

~
推
This word has many meanings. The meanings "to cut" and "massage" use the alternative pronunciation (tuī).

~
营业
This can be used as a noun or a verb.

~
礼貌
This can be used as a noun or an adjective.

~
台阶
This can also mean giving someone a way out of an embarrassing situation, a way to save face.  It is often used as 给…台阶下 (gěi… táijiē xià), meaning "to give someone a way out", or "to let someone off the hook".

~
地址
Be sure to use the correct measure word (个 gè).

~
沉默
This suggests a deliberate withholding of speech, often due to sadness, anger, or disapproval.  It isn't merely being quiet.

~
缺少
This is a more formal way to say "lack of".

~
冲
This word has many meanings and several pronunciations. The pronunciation (chōng) is most common in the meanings listed above.

~
肚子
Be sure to use the correct measure word (个 gè).

~
继续
This word can be used as either an adverb or a verb.

~
预订
This is very similar to the English word "pre-order".


~
皮肤
Be sure to use the correct measure word (层 céng or 块 kuài).

~
意见
Be sure to use the correct measure word (点 diǎn or 条 tiáo).

~
哪
Be careful not to confuse this word with 那 (nà, "that"). Although they are pronounced similarly, they have very different meanings.

~
阳光
The "transparent, open to scrutiny" meaning usually refers to actions, behavior or processes, rather than people.

~
立即
This implies a more immediate action than 马上 (mǎshàng).  It emphasizes doing something without any delay.

~
大概
When expressing probability, 大概 is interchangeable with 也许 (yěxǔ) and 可能 (kěnéng). All three are adverbs and thus modify verbs. However, if you want to modify a noun, then use 大概 + 的. For example, "It's probably John" is "大概是约翰" while "It's probably John's" is "大概是约翰的".


~
护士
A common colloquialism is 护士小姐.


~
激动
激动 can also mean "to agitate". Note that it has a slightly more formal connotation than "excited" in English.


~
信心
信心 is typically used with 对. E.g., 我对我的未来很有信心 (I'm very confident about my future).


~
篇
When referring to articles, 篇 is now the most common measure word.


~
重
As a character, 重 has two pronunciations:
* zhòng: weight; heavy; serious
* chóng: again; repeat


~
的确
的确 is more formal than 真的.


~
系
系 has many meanings, but the following two are particularly worth noting.
* To tie: e.g., 系鞋带
* Department (in a university): e.g., 数学系


~
操场
This can also refer to a parade ground.


~
财产
This can also refer to a personal belonging of special sentimental value.


~
接着
This word has two meanings:
* to catch: e.g., 把球接住 (catch the ball)
* to continue: e.g., 接下来的时间我要读书 (I'm going to read in the time to come)


~
由于
由于 is slightly more formal than 因为.


~
加油站
A colloquial term for this is 加油店.


~
保护
保护 is used for concrete, tangible objects, while 保卫 (bǎowèi) is used for abstract things like ideas and rights.


~
伤心
This is best translated as heartbroken.


~
商务
商务 is usually used as an attributive adjective, as in 商务英语 (business English) or 商务旅行 (business trip).


~
果实
果实 may also metaphorically refer to the result or outcome of an effort, in a similar way to how "fruit" is used metaphorically in English.


~
赚
This means to *profit from*, and doesn't necessarily mean that someone else was tricked. You can use it to talk about making money at a job.


~
承受
This is quite close in meaning to 忍受 (rěnshòu), but 承受 implies that one is being subjected to an external force or pressure, whereas 忍受 suggests that one is actively enduring or tolerating something unpleasant or difficult. In short, 承受 is passive and 忍受 is active.


~
迷路
It is also possible to say 走迷路了 (zǒu mílù le).


~
规则
This implies an official, codified rule.


~
力气
This word is usually used in the negative: 没有力气 (méiyǒu lìqì).


~
房东
The female equivalent is 房东太太 (fángdōng tàitai).


~
拉
拉 can also mean "to play a stringed instrument."


~
包子
小笼包 is a small steamed bun, typically filled with pork.


~
大楼
大楼 and 楼 (lóu) refer to a multistory building, while 房屋 (fángwū) and 房子 (fángzi) refer to houses and small buildings.


~
区别
This is very close in meaning to 差别 (chābié), but 区别 emphasizes the features that make things different, whereas 差别 emphasizes the extent or degree of difference between things.


~
利息
The person who receives the interest is called 收益人 (shōuyìrén).


~
出色
This word is similar to 优秀 (yōuxiù), but 出色 is more often used in everyday situations.


~
一律
一律 is formal and often used in rules and regulations.


~
仍然
仍然 is more formal than 还.


~
学问
学问 can also refer to a specific field of study, as in 语言学问 (linguistics).


~
聚会
A more casual word is just 会 (huì), but be careful, because this also means "to meet."


~
信息
信息 can also refer to signals transmitted over a network.


~
比如
For single-word examples, use 比方说 (bǐfāngshuō).


~
教训
教训 can also mean "to teach someone a lesson," similar to "to punish" or "to discipline".


~
坚持
坚持 can also mean "to adhere to," which implies sticking to a certain principle or ideology.


~
消化
It's usually used with 不好 or 好.


~
之后
之后 is used *after* a noun or noun phrase. It cannot be used by itself.

~
假 (jiǎ)
When used in the context of "fake", 假 (jiǎ) can be combined with other characters to create words like 假货 (jiǎhuò) - counterfeit goods, 假冒 (jiǎmào) - to counterfeit, and 假装 (jiǎzhuāng) - to pretend.  The word 假掰 (gēibāi), while containing the character 假, is Taiwanese slang.

~
前途 (qiántú)
前途 (qiántú) carries a more positive connotation than just "future." It emphasizes a bright or promising future, often related to career or personal development.  A similar word, 未来 (wèilái), is more general and neutral in tone.

~
中介 (zhōngjiè)
中介 (zhōngjiè) typically refers to a third-party agent or agency facilitating transactions, particularly in real estate or other business dealings.  It's often used with 公司 (gōngsī) to form 中介公司 (zhōngjiè gōngsī), meaning "intermediary company" or "agency."

~
规定 (guīdìng)
规定 (guīdìng) implies a formally established rule or regulation. It carries more weight and authority than simply saying "rule."  A less formal word would be 规则 (guīzé).

~
如今 (rújīn)
如今 (rújīn) emphasizes a change from the past to the present. It's similar to "nowadays" but suggests a contrast with how things were before.  It's more formal than 現在 (xiànzài) and carries a slightly literary tone.

~
够 (gòu)
够 (gòu) can be tricky because it functions as both an adjective and a verb. As an adjective, it means "enough." As a verb, it means "to reach" or "to be sufficient."  Pay attention to the sentence structure to determine its role.  The "really" meaning only applies before adjectives.

~
圈 (quān)
圈 (quān) has various meanings, but the most common ones relate to a circular shape or an enclosed area.  When referring to a group of people, 圈子 (quānzǐ) is more appropriate, meaning "circle" or "clique."

~
激烈 (jīliè)
激烈 (jīliè) describes intense competition, fighting, or emotions.  It can also be used to describe pain, in which case it means "acute" or "severe."

~
失业 (shīyè)
失业 (shīyè) refers specifically to involuntary job loss.  It doesn't apply to someone quitting their job voluntarily.

~
刚 (gāng)
刚 (gāng) can be confusing because it has so many meanings.  Pay close attention to context.  The most common usage is to indicate something that just happened.

~
形势 (xíngshì)
形势 (xíngshì) refers to a general situation, often political or economic, and implies the direction in which things are developing.  It's more formal and broader than 情况 (qíngkuàng), which refers to a specific situation.

~
连 (lián)
连 (lián) has several functions. As a conjunction, it means "even." As an adverb, it means "continuously" or "in succession."  It can also be a verb meaning "to connect" or "to join."

~
概括 (gàikuò)
概括 (gàikuò) suggests summarizing the main points while omitting details.  It's more concise than 总结 (zǒngjié), which implies a more comprehensive summary.

~
幽默 (yōumò)
幽默 (yōumò) refers to a quality of being funny or witty, or to something that possesses this quality.  It's both a noun and an adjective.

~
效率 (xiàolǜ)
效率 (xiàolǜ) emphasizes the rate at which work is done or the effectiveness of a process.  提高效率 (tígāo xiàolǜ) means "to improve efficiency."

~
竟然 (jìngrán)
竟然 (jìngrán) expresses surprise or disbelief at an unexpected event.  It carries a stronger sense of surprise than 意外 (yìwài).

~
老公 (lǎogōng)
老公 (lǎogōng) is an informal term for "husband."  The formal term is 丈夫 (zhàngfu).  Be aware of the potential for misinterpretation as "eunuch" in certain dialects or historical contexts.

~
种类 (zhǒnglèi)
种类 (zhǒnglèi) refers to different categories within a broader group.  It's similar to "type" or "kind" but often implies a more scientific or systematic classification.

~
内科 (nèikē)
内科 (nèikē) refers to the branch of medicine dealing with internal organs and non-surgical treatments.  It contrasts with 外科 (wàikē), which means "surgery."

~
愉快 (yúkuài)
愉快 (yúkuài) describes a feeling of happiness and pleasure.  It's more formal and less common in everyday conversation than 开心 (kāixīn).

~
主意 (zhǔyi)
主意 (zhǔyi) can be a plan, idea, or decision.  It often implies a course of action or a settled opinion.  拿主意 (ná zhǔyi) means "to make a decision."

~
尤其 (yóuqí)
尤其 (yóuqí) emphasizes a particular item or aspect within a larger group.  It's similar to "especially" but often follows a more general statement.

~
登机牌 (dēngjīpái)
登机牌 (dēngjīpái) is specifically a boarding pass for an airplane.  It's not used for other forms of transportation.

~
发展 (fāzhǎn)
发展 (fāzhǎn) can be both a noun and a verb. As a noun, it means "development" or "growth." As a verb, it means "to develop" or "to grow."

~
争论 (zhēnglùn)
争论 (zhēnglùn) implies a more formal and reasoned argument or debate, often over a significant issue.  It's more serious than 吵架 (chǎojià), which means "to quarrel."

~
复制 (fùzhì)
复制 (fùzhì) means to make an exact copy of something.  It can refer to physical objects or digital information.

~
可怜 (kělián)
可怜 (kělián) can mean both "pitiful" and "to pity."  The meaning depends on the context.

~
看望 (kànwàng)
看望 (kànwàng) implies visiting someone out of concern or care, often someone who is sick or elderly.  It's more specific than just "visiting."

~
任何 (rènhé)
任何 (rènhé) emphasizes "any" without exception.  It's often used in negative sentences or with questions.

~
过程 (guòchéng)
过程 (guòchéng) refers to the steps or stages involved in a process.  It emphasizes the duration and development of something.

~
距离 (jùlí)
距离 (jùlí) refers to physical distance or a gap between two things.  It can also refer to a difference in opinion or feeling.

~
期间 (qījiān)
期间 (qījiān) refers to a specific period of time during which something happens.  It's often used with a preceding time phrase.

~
叶子 (yèzi)
叶子 (yèzi) generally refers to a leaf of a plant. Be aware of its slang meaning of marijuana.

~
划 (huá/huà)
The pronunciation and meaning of 划 (huá/huà) vary depending on the context. As huá, it can mean "to row," "to paddle," or "worthwhile." As huà, it means "to draw a line," "to delimit," or "to transfer."

~
难受 (nánshòu)
难受 (nánshòu) describes physical or emotional discomfort. It can range from mild unease to severe pain or distress.

~
进行 (jìnxíng)
进行 (jìnxíng) emphasizes the ongoing nature of an activity or process.  It often implies a structured or planned activity.

~
信封 (xìnfēng)
信封 (xìnfēng) is specifically an envelope for letters or documents.

~
豆腐 (dòufu)
豆腐 (dòufu) refers specifically to tofu, a food made from soybeans.

~
陆续 (lùxù)
陆续 (lùxù) indicates a series of events happening one after another, often over an extended period.

~
影子 (yǐngzi)
影子 (yǐngzi) can refer to a literal shadow or a figurative one, such as a hint, trace, or influence.

~
战争
战争 can be used as both a noun and a verb.  As a noun, it means "war."  As a verb, it means "to wage war" or "to make war." For example, 不要战争 (bùyào zhànzhēng) means "don't wage war."

~
特殊
特殊 (tèshū) carries a stronger connotation than just "special."  It often implies unusualness, distinctiveness, or even peculiarity.  Think of it as meaning "exceptional" or "unique."  It's not used for things that are merely slightly different.

~
指挥
指挥 can mean "to conduct" in the musical sense, but it can also mean "to command" or "to direct" in a more general sense, often in a military context or for large-scale operations.

~
改善
改善 usually refers to making a situation better or improving some condition, rather than repairing a broken object. The object of 改善 is generally an ongoing process or a less tangible entity.

~
色彩
Besides literal color, 色彩 can also refer to the "flavor" or "character" of something in a figurative sense, such as the distinctive style of a piece of writing.

~
维修
维修 emphasizes the act of maintaining something in good working order through regular checks and repairs, as opposed to just fixing something that is broken. It often refers to the upkeep of equipment, machinery or infrastructure.

~
语言
While both 门 (mén) and 种 (zhǒng) are measure words for language, 门 is more commonly used, especially when referring to languages as subjects of study.

~
逛
逛 describes leisurely strolling or wandering with no specific destination in mind, or with the implicit purpose of looking around. It is different from 去 (qù) which indicates going to a specific place.

~
呀
呀 (ya) is typically used at the end of a sentence after a vowel, often in exclamatory expressions of surprise, realization, or emphasis.  It's similar to 啊 (a), but used specifically after vowels.

~
售货员
Although 个 (gè) is given as the measure word, 位 (wèi) is generally considered more polite and respectful when referring to a salesperson.

~
以
以 (yǐ) has many different usages, so context is essential for understanding its meaning.  It does not have a single, easily defined English equivalent.  Pay close attention to how it's used in different sentences.

~
描写
描写 implies a vivid and detailed description, often creating a picture with words.  It goes beyond simply stating facts and aims to create an image or impression in the reader's mind.

~
顺利
顺利 describes something proceeding without difficulty or obstacles.  It often implies ease and success in completing a task or reaching a goal.

~
事先
事先 specifically means "beforehand" or "in advance of" a particular event or action.  It emphasizes the preparation or planning done before something happens.

~
实在
实在 has a wide range of meanings, from "really" and "truly" to "honest" and "dependable."  The meaning depends heavily on context.  It can describe both the nature of things (real, true) and the character of people (honest, down-to-earth).

~
速度
速度 refers to the rate at which something moves or progresses, emphasizing the distance covered over time.  It's a more formal and technical term than 快慢 (kuài màn).

~
懒
懒 (lǎn) carries a negative connotation, often implying unwillingness to work or exert effort.  It goes beyond simply being relaxed or inactive.

~
闪电
闪电 usually refers to the flash of light produced by lightning, whereas 雷 (léi) refers to the sound of thunder.

~
平方
平方 specifically refers to "square" in the mathematical sense (e.g., square meter, square root).  For a physical square shape, 正方形 (zhèngfāngxíng) is more appropriate.

~
详细
详细 emphasizes a high level of detail and thoroughness.  It implies more than just providing basic information and often includes specific facts and figures.

~
光临
光临 is a very formal and respectful way to say someone has graced a place with their presence.  It's often used in business settings or formal announcements.

~
与
与 (yǔ) is generally more formal than 和 (hé) when used to mean "and."  It also has other meanings such as "to give" or "to be involved in," so context is key.

~
行
行 (xíng/háng) has numerous meanings and is pronounced differently depending on the meaning and context. It is important to discern the intended meaning through context.

~
担任
担任 emphasizes taking on the responsibilities of a role or position, often one that carries some importance or authority.

~
小说
小说 usually refers to longer works of fiction, like novels.  For shorter stories, 故事 (gùshi) is more appropriate.

~
出席
出席 implies formal participation in a meeting, ceremony, or other organized event.  It is more formal than 参加 (cānjiā).

~
美丽
美丽 usually describes visual beauty, often of a refined and elegant kind.  It's more formal and poetic than 漂亮 (piàoliang).

~
盒子
盒子 is a general term for a box or container.  More specific words exist for different types of boxes (e.g., 箱子 xiāngzi for a chest or suitcase).

~
翻译
翻译 covers both translation of written text and interpretation of spoken language, although 口译 (kǒuyì) is more specifically used for interpretation.

~
京剧
京剧 is a specific type of Chinese opera originating in Beijing.  It has distinctive characteristics, including elaborate costumes, makeup, and singing styles.

~
导致
导致 emphasizes a cause-and-effect relationship, where one action or event directly leads to another, often with a negative connotation.

~
其次
其次 indicates the next item in a sequence or list, usually after the most important point has been made. It’s more formal than 然后 (ránhòu).

~
尽力
尽力 emphasizes making one's best effort, regardless of the outcome.  It suggests putting in all possible effort to achieve something.

~
堵车
堵车 specifically refers to traffic congestion or a traffic jam.  It's distinct from other transportation delays.

~
无
无 (wú) is more formal and literary than 没有 (méiyǒu) when used to mean "not have" or "there is no."

~
一再
一再 emphasizes repeated occurrences of something, often with a sense of persistence or insistence.

~
担心
担心 implies anxiety or concern about something that might happen in the future. It suggests a feeling of unease or apprehension.

~
相同
相同 highlights the similarities between two or more things, often implying that they are exactly alike.

~
倍
倍 indicates a multiple or factor of increase. It indicates a proportional relationship between quantities.

~
爱护
爱护 implies cherishing and protecting something or someone, often with a sense of care and responsibility.  It’s more profound than simply liking something.

~
粮食
粮食 is typically used to refer to staple food crops, especially grains like rice, wheat, and corn.  It's less commonly used for other food items.  Think of it more as "grains" or "staple crops" than "food" in general.

~
满
满 (mǎn) can mean "full" in the physical sense (e.g., a full glass) or in the sense of a time period being complete (e.g., a full year). It can also mean "satisfied" or "content."  As a verb, it means "to fill" or "to reach the limit." Be aware that 满 also exists as a surname (Mǎn) and refers to the Manchu ethnic group. Context is crucial to distinguish these meanings.

~
县
县 (xiàn) is generally translated as "county," but its size and administrative level can vary depending on the specific context within China. It's smaller than a city (市, shì) but larger than a township (乡, xiāng).

~
网站
No special notes.

~
盖 (gài)
When 盖 means "to build," it specifically refers to constructing a roof or covering a structure.  It doesn't mean "to build" in the general sense.  For general building, use 建造 (jiànzào) or 建设 (jiànshè).  Also, pay attention to the tone change when 盖 (gě) is used as a noun meaning a lid or top.

~
动作 (dòngzuò)
As a noun, this refers to a physical movement or action.  As a verb, it means "to move" or "to act," often implying some kind of deliberate action or gesture.

~
尽管
尽管 (jǐnguǎn) is used in the following structure:

尽管…，(可是 / 但是 +) Subj. (还是)…

Aside from that, its usage is just like "despite" or "although" in English.

~
对于 (duìyú)
对于 is a preposition meaning "regarding," "concerning," or "with respect to." It's more formal than 关于 (guānyú) and is often used in written Chinese.  It introduces the topic or object of a discussion or consideration.

~
疑问 (yíwèn)
疑问 refers to a question or doubt about something. It carries a stronger sense of uncertainty or questioning than simply asking a question (问题, wèntí).

~
分布 (fēnbù)
分布 is typically used to describe the distribution of things over a geographical area, or the distribution of data in statistics.

~
方案 (fāng'àn)
方案 specifically refers to a detailed and concrete plan for a specific project or task. It’s more formal and detailed than 计划 (jìhuà), which can refer to a more general plan.

~
些 (xiē)
些 is used after a number or demonstrative pronoun to indicate an approximate quantity. It suggests a relatively small and indefinite amount.

~
养成 (yǎngchéng)
养成 emphasizes the process of developing a habit or cultivating a skill over time. It highlights the gradual and continuous nature of the development.

~
感情 (gǎnqíng)
感情 can refer to a broad range of emotions, from simple feelings to deep affections or sentiments.  It can also refer specifically to romantic feelings.  The context will usually make the specific meaning clear.

~
常识 (chángshí)
常识 refers to basic knowledge and understanding that is generally accepted within a culture or society.  It's similar to "common sense."

~
摸 (mō)
摸 implies touching or feeling something to explore its texture, shape, or temperature. It can also mean to grope or to steal by stealthily touching.

~
活泼 (huópō)
活泼 describes someone lively, energetic, and cheerful.  It's often used to describe children or young people.

~
气候 (qìhòu)
气候 refers to long-term weather patterns in a particular region, not just the current weather conditions (天气, tiānqì).  It can also be used figuratively to describe the prevailing atmosphere or conditions in a particular environment or situation.

~
方 (fāng)
方 has many meanings. Pay close attention to context.  As a noun, it can mean "square," "direction," "side," "party," "place," "method," or "prescription." As an adjective, it can mean "upright" or "honest."  As an adverb, it can mean "just when" or "only or just." It's also a classifier for square objects and an abbreviation for square or cubic meters.

~
父亲 (fùqīn)
No special notes.

~
酸 (suān)
酸 can refer to both the physical sensation of sourness and emotional feelings like sadness, grief, or jealousy. It can also describe someone who is pedantic or impractical.

~
可见 (kějiàn)
可见 is an adverb meaning "it can be seen that" or "it is evident that."  It's used to introduce a conclusion or inference based on previously stated information.

~
垃圾桶 (lājītǒng)
No special notes.

~
种 (zhǒng)
种 is both a noun (seed, species, kind, type) and a verb (to plant, to grow, to cultivate). As a classifier, it's used for types, kinds, and sorts of things.

~
几乎 (jīhū)
几乎 means "almost" or "nearly," but it implies a closer approximation than 差一点 (chà yīdiǎn), which means "almost" in the sense of "nearly but not quite."

~
举办 (jǔbàn)
举办 means "to hold" or "to organize" an event, usually a large or formal one.

~
香 (xiāng)
香 can describe pleasant smells (fragrant, aromatic) or pleasant tastes (savory, appetizing).  It can also refer to incense or joss sticks.

~
羽毛球 (yǔmáoqiú)
This refers to both the sport of badminton and the shuttlecock used in the game.

分手 (fēnshǒu)

~
一致 (yízhì)
一致 emphasizes agreement and uniformity of opinion or action.

~
以及 (yǐjí)
以及 is a conjunction meaning "as well as" or "and."  It's more formal than 和 (hé) and is typically used to connect items of a similar nature.

~
本科 (běnkē)
本科 refers specifically to undergraduate education.

~
极 (jí)
极 can act as an adjective (extreme, utmost), a noun (pole, limit), or an adverb (extremely).  Its meaning depends heavily on context.

~
作用 (zuòyòng)
作用 can mean "effect," "influence," "function," or "role."  It can also be used as a suffix similar to "-ation" or "-tion" in English.

~
零食 (língshí)
零食 refers to snacks or treats eaten between meals.

~
接受 (jiēshòu)
接受 implies a willingness to take or receive something offered. It often suggests a more formal or considered acceptance than simply taking something.

~
云 (yún)
Remember that 云 also has a classical meaning of “to say,” is short for Yunnan province, and is a surname.  These meanings are much rarer than the primary meaning of “cloud.”

~
培训 (péixùn)
培训 refers to structured training or instruction aimed at improving skills or knowledge in a specific area.  It often implies a more formal and organized process than simply learning something.

~
吃惊 (chījīng)
吃惊 describes the feeling of surprise or amazement, often with a slight connotation of shock or disbelief.

~
要是
The word 要是 (yàoshi) is indeed used to mean "if," particularly in spoken Mandarin. However, there are some important distinctions and usage notes to keep in mind:

Colloquial Nature: 要是 is primarily used in informal settings and spoken conversations. In more formal written contexts, other "if" words like 如果 (rúguǒ) or 假如 (jiǎrú) are generally preferred.

Implication of Uncertainty: 要是 carries a slight implication of uncertainty or hypotheticality.  It's often used to introduce a condition that the speaker is not entirely sure will happen, or to discuss a hypothetical scenario.

Conditional Clauses:  要是 introduces the conditional clause (the "if" part) in a sentence. The consequence clause (the "then" part) can be introduced by 就 (jiù), which implies a direct consequence, or other conjunctions like 那 (nà), 那么 (nàme), or even without an explicit conjunction.

~
实际
实际 (shíjì) can indeed translate to "reality," "practice," "practical," "realistic," "real," and "actual." However, there are nuances in its usage that might not be obvious:

Emphasis on Groundedness: 实际 often emphasizes what is grounded in reality, as opposed to theory or ideals.  It carries a sense of pragmatism or what is truly feasible.

Contrast with Theory: It's frequently used to contrast with theory or expectations. For example, 实际情况 (shíjì qíngkuàng) means "actual situation" and often implies a difference from what was planned or anticipated.

实际 vs. 现实: While both 实际 and 现实 (xiànshí) can mean "reality," 实际 tends to focus on the practical aspects of reality, whereas 现实 has a broader scope, encompassing both the tangible and intangible aspects of real life.

Adjective Use: When used as an adjective, 实际 can mean "practical" or "realistic." For instance, 实际经验 (shíjì jīngyàn) translates to "practical experience."

Adverb Use: As an adverb, 实际 can mean "actually" or "in fact," similar to 实际上 (shíjì shang).


~
骗
骗 (piàn) primarily means "to deceive" or "to cheat." The meaning "to get on (a horse etc) by swinging one leg over" is archaic and rarely used.  It is best to avoid this usage to prevent confusion.

~
工资
While both 个 (gè) and 份 (fèn) can be used as measure words for 工资 (gōngzī, "wages; pay"), 份 is generally preferred.  份 suggests a regular payment or a portion, making it more suitable for salaries or wages. 个 is less specific and can be used for counting instances of receiving wages.

~
总结
总结 (zǒngjié) can be used as both a verb and a noun. As a noun, referring to a "summary" or "conclusion," the measure word 个 (gè) is common but not mandatory. Using 个 emphasizes the summary as a discrete item.  It can also be used without a measure word, especially when the context is clear.

~
抓紧
抓紧 (zhuājǐn) is often used to convey urgency. It implies "to seize (an opportunity)" or "to not waste time." Think of it as "hurry up" or "do something quickly" rather than simply "pay close attention to."

~
玉米
While the measure word 粒 (lì) can be used for individual kernels of corn, it's rarely used in everyday conversation. For corn on the cob or corn as a dish, use 根 (gēn) or no measure word at all.

~
趋势
趋势 (qūshì) implies a developing direction or a general movement, often used in formal contexts to describe social, economic, or political trends. It is different from 倾向 (qīngxiàng, "tendency"), which suggests a leaning or inclination toward something specific.

~
晒
晒 (shài) has a wide range of meanings related to exposure, primarily to the sun.  Be mindful of the context to discern the intended meaning.  While the online "sharing" meaning exists, ensure the context supports it, as it's not always synonymous with "to share" in general.

~
共同
共同 (gòngtóng) emphasizes shared qualities or actions.  It suggests something done or possessed together by multiple parties, highlighting the collaborative or collective aspect.

~
毛
毛 (máo) has numerous meanings, so context is crucial. When referring to currency, it represents one-tenth of a yuan (角/jiǎo). The meaning "nervous/scared" is colloquial and often combined with other words, like 毛毛的 (máomao de), to describe a feeling of unease or anxiety.

~
咳嗽
咳嗽 (késòu) refers to coughing due to illness or irritation.  For coughing to clear the throat, other terms like 清嗓子 (qīng sǎngzi) are more appropriate.

~
宝贵
宝贵 (bǎoguì) is more often used for abstract things like time, experience, or advice.  For valuable physical objects, other terms like 贵重 (guìzhòng) are more common.

~
空
空 (kōng) has several meanings.  It's important to distinguish between its use as an adjective ("empty," "vacant") and as a noun ("space," "air," "sky").  As a verb, it means "to empty."

~
从此
从此 (cóngcǐ) highlights a turning point or a significant event that marks the beginning of a new state. It emphasizes the lasting effect of the previous event.

~
肯定
肯定 (kěndìng) can be an adverb ("definitely," "certainly"), an adjective ("positive," "affirmative"), or a verb ("to affirm," "to approve").  Be aware of these different usages and how they affect sentence structure.

~
浪费
浪费 (làngfèi) can apply to tangible resources like money, food, or time, as well as intangible ones like opportunities or talent.  It often carries a negative connotation of carelessness or extravagance.

~
彻底
彻底 (chèdǐ) emphasizes completeness and leaving nothing undone. It often implies going to the root of a problem or making a fundamental change.

~
抽烟
抽烟 (chōuyān) is specifically for smoking tobacco. For other substances, use 吸 (xī), e.g., 吸毒 (xīdú, "to take drugs").

~
省
省 (shěng) has numerous meanings depending on the tone and context. As a verb (pronounced shěng), it means "to save" or "to omit."  As a noun (pronounced shěng), it refers to a province. The bound form meanings are less commonly used in modern Mandarin.

~
任务
任务 (rènwu) implies a specific assigned duty or responsibility, often within a larger project or goal.  It carries a more formal connotation than just "task" or "job."

~
交
交 (jiāo) has multiple meanings.  The most common meanings are "to hand over" and "to make friends."  Context is essential for accurate interpretation.

~
结构
结构 (jiégòu) refers to the way parts are arranged or organized to form a whole. It can be used for physical objects, systems, or even abstract concepts.

~
来不及
来不及 (láibují) emphasizes the lack of time to complete an action before a deadline or consequence.  It implies that the action is now impossible due to time constraints.

~
巧克力
While 块 (kuài) is a common measure word for chocolate, it's mainly used for solid pieces. For other forms like liquid chocolate or chocolate powder, different measure words may be more appropriate.

~
作为
作为 (zuòwéi) can be a noun ("conduct," "deed"), a verb ("to act as"), or a conjunction ("as," "in the capacity of"). Pay attention to sentence structure to determine its role.

~
道歉
道歉 (dàoqiàn) implies admitting fault and expressing regret. It's more formal than simply saying "sorry."

~
各
各 (gè) emphasizes individuality within a group.  It highlights the distinctness of each member or element.

~
厘米
厘米 (límǐ) is the standard term for "centimeter" in mainland China.

~
许多
许多 (xǔduō) implies a large but indefinite quantity.  It's less precise than specific numbers and more formal than 很 多 (hěn duō).

~
只好
只好 (zhǐhǎo) indicates a lack of better alternatives, often due to unfavorable circumstances.  It expresses a sense of resignation or compulsion.

~
毕业
毕业 (bìyè) marks the completion of a course of study. It signifies the formal ending of an educational program.

~
发烧
发烧 (fāshāo) specifically refers to having a fever due to illness.  It shouldn't be used for other types of heat or high temperatures.

~
缓解
缓解 (huǎnjiě) implies a temporary lessening of severity, not a complete cure or solution.  It suggests making something more bearable or manageable.

~
围巾
围巾 (wéijīn) usually refers to a longer scarf worn around the neck for warmth.  For shorter, decorative scarves, other terms might be more appropriate.

~
议论
议论 (yìlùn) often carries a connotation of critical discussion or debate, sometimes implying gossip or speculation.

~
国籍
国籍 (guójí) is a legal status, not simply ethnicity or place of birth.  It indicates citizenship in a particular country.

~
实用
实用 (shíyòng) emphasizes functionality and practicality over aesthetics or other considerations. It suggests something designed for real-world use.

~
最初
最初 (zuìchū) emphasizes the very beginning or earliest stage of something. It highlights the initial point in a process or timeline.

~
出差
出差 (chūchāi) refers specifically to business trips, usually involving travel away from one's regular workplace.  It implies a temporary work assignment in a different location.

~
传真
Can be both a noun and a verb.

~
构成
A relatively formal (书面) word.  More colloquial equivalents include 组成 (zǔchéng) and 形成 (xíngchéng).

~
复印
Can be both a noun and a verb.

~
心理
This word is often used in the pattern 心理 + Adj., meaning "psychologically + Adj."  For example, 心理健康 (xīnlǐ jiànkāng) means "mentally healthy".

~
摇
When used to mean "to row", specifically refers to rowing a small boat with oars, unlike 划 (huá), which can be used for rowing larger boats or using paddles.

~
咱们
This word is primarily used in northern dialects. The standard word for "we/us" inclusive of the speaker and listener is 我们 (wǒmen).

~
妻子
More formal than 老婆 (lǎopo) or 太太 (tàitai).

~
紧张
Meaning "scarce" or "in short supply," 紧张 is often used in a commercial context, e.g., supplies, funds, etc.

~
照
The usage meaning "as before" is often seen in phrases like 照旧 (zhàojiù) - "as before; as usual".

~
阿姨
Commonly used to address any woman of one's parents' generation, not just one's actual aunt.

~
网球
Can mean both "tennis" and "tennis ball". Context will usually disambiguate.

~
海洋
Sometimes used metaphorically to represent a vast amount of something.

~
积极
The "proactive" meaning carries a stronger connotation of taking initiative and being assertive than the English word.

~
节
Has many meanings.  Pay attention to context.

~
列车
Specifically refers to trains, unlike 车 (chē) which can mean any vehicle.

~
指
The meaning "(of hair) to stand on end" is usually used in the context of being frightened.

~
大夫
In modern Chinese, primarily means "doctor".  The older meaning of "senior official" is archaic.

~
手术
Can also be used as a verb, meaning "to operate (surgically)".

~
根据
A related word is 按照 (ànzhào). In general, 根据 emphasizes the rationale or justification for something, especially a law or regulation. It is more about the state of the world and less about the speaker's actions or opinions. On the other hand, 按照 highlights the specific process or protocol being followed. In other words, 根据 is more about the basis, while 按照 is more about the manner of implementation.

Contexts: 根据 is usually used with rules, e.g. 规定 (guīdìng), 法律 (fǎlǜ) etc. On the other hand, 按照 is usually used with requests or directions, e.g. 要求 (yāoqiú), 说法 (shuōfǎ), etc.

Finally, a different related word is 依照 (yīzhào). This has the same meaning as 根据, but is used more in the written register.


~
猜
Often used with the complement 对 (duì), as in 猜对 (cāi duì) - "to guess correctly".

~
尝
The meaning "ever" or "once" is literary and less common in modern spoken Chinese.

~
面试
Can be both a noun and a verb.

~
部分
Often used with the preposition 当中 (dāngzhōng) to mean "among these" or "within this".

~
确认
Has a stronger connotation of certainty than the English "confirm".

~
改变
Implies a more significant change than 变化 (biànhuà).

~
说明
Can refer to both an explanation/illustration and the act of explaining/illustrating.

~
公元
Used before a year in the Common Era (CE), equivalent to A.D.

~
浓
Can describe a wide variety of things, not just liquids, including fog, emotions, etc.

~
理发
Can refer to both getting a haircut and giving a haircut.

~
温度
Generally refers to air temperature unless otherwise specified.

~
沙发
Its internet slang usage of referring to the first reply originates from its pronunciation being similar to the English word "sofa", and is also related to the phrase "沙发土豆" (shāfā tǔdòu) "couch potato."

~
马虎
Implies negligence or carelessness leading to errors, rather than just general sloppiness.

~
牙膏
Usually comes in a tube (管 - guǎn), hence the common measure word.

~
非
Has a wide range of meanings. Pay close attention to context.

~
充分
Often used in official or formal contexts.

~
脑袋
While literally meaning "head," 脑袋 can also be used figuratively to refer to one's mind or intellect.

~
对话
Can refer to both the act of conversing and the content of the conversation.

~
单纯
Can sometimes be negative, implying naivety or lack of experience.

~
度过
Typically used for periods of time, like holidays or difficult phases.

~
宝贝
Can be used as a term of endearment, but can also be sarcastic, referring to someone spoiled or incompetent.

~
问候
While 问候 can technically mean "to make offensive reference to (somebody dear to the person to whom one is speaking)," this meaning is extremely vulgar and should be avoided at all costs.  It's the equivalent of cursing someone out in English.

~
赞成
The meaning "to assist" is archaic and should not be used in modern Chinese.

~
正常
正常 is usually used predicatively.  If you want to use it attributively, then 通常 is a better choice.

~
究竟
究竟 is usually used in questions. It adds emphasis to the question, implying a desire to get to the bottom of the matter or to finally understand something. It can also appear in statements to mean “after all,” implying a reason or explanation for a situation.

~
其中
其中 implies a selection from a larger group.  The appropriate English translation might be "among them" rather than simply "among".

~
所有
所有 (suǒyǒu) means "all" when used before a noun. But when it's used as a verb after a noun, it means "to own" or "to possess." The pronunciation shifts slightly to (suǒ yǒu).

~
摆
While 摆 can mean "pendulum," it is more often used in the sense of "to put; to place; to arrange." For pendulum, use 摆锤 (bǎichuí).

~
家具
家具 is always plural.  Don't say "一个家具."

~
手工
手工 can also refer to something made by hand, as in 手工皂 (shǒugōngzào) - handmade soap.

~
禁止
禁止 is a stronger and more formal word than 不许. 禁止 is often seen in official notices and implies legal consequences.  不许 is more common in everyday speech and often used by parents to children.

~
迟到
迟到 always implies arriving late to a scheduled event or appointment. It's not used for general lateness.

~
严重
严重 is more formal than 厉害 when describing the severity of something.  严重 is better used in written contexts.

~
办事
办事 can also mean "to get things done" or "to be effective," often carrying a slightly negative connotation of using connections or unconventional methods.

~
合格
合格 simply means meeting the minimum standard. It doesn't necessarily imply excellence.

~
秒
秒 can be colloquially used as an adjective to mean "instant" or "in a flash," often paired with other words to create phrases like 秒懂 (miǎodǒng) - to understand instantly.

~
背景
The usage relating to powerful backers is often subtle and implied rather than explicitly stated.  It can also refer to someone's family background.

~
感谢
感谢 is more formal than 谢谢.

~
减肥
减肥 focuses specifically on weight loss, while 瘦身 (shòushēn) has a broader meaning of improving overall body shape and fitness.

~
刺激
刺激 can have both positive and negative connotations.  It can mean a positive stimulation or a negative irritation. Context is essential to understanding the intended meaning.

~
难免
难免 implies that something is difficult but not impossible to avoid.  It expresses a higher probability than  可能.

~
使
使 often introduces a clause, meaning "to cause" or "to make."  It's more formal than 让.

~
土地
土地 can have a spiritual meaning in the context of one's homeland or ancestral land, not just the physical land.

~
业余
业余 emphasizes activities done outside of one's profession, often for hobbies or personal interest.

~
果汁
果汁 almost always refers to 100% fruit juice.  If it is a mixed drink, other words will be used.

~
回忆
回忆 can be both a noun and a verb.

~
转告
转告 implies passing a message indirectly through a third party, not directly to the intended recipient.

~
输
输 in the context of entering a password emphasizes the physical act of typing or inputting.

~
阅读
阅读 implies a focused and intentional act of reading, not just casual glancing.

~
麻烦
As a verb, 麻烦 is often used as a polite way to ask someone for a favor, acknowledging the potential inconvenience.

~
奖金
奖金 specifically refers to monetary bonuses or awards, while 奖励 (jiǎnglì) is a broader term for rewards, which can include non-monetary forms of recognition.

~
设施
设施 always refers to physical infrastructure or equipment.

~
重新
重新 implies starting something over from the beginning, after a previous attempt or process has been completed or abandoned.

~
饼干
The specific type of 饼干 being referred to (biscuit, cracker, or cookie) depends on the context and regional variations in Chinese usage.

~
即使
即使 sets up a hypothetical situation, while 虽然 (suīrán) describes a factual one.

~
数码
数码 usually refers to digital technology or information represented in digital form.

~
引起
引起 suggests a causal relationship, often leading to negative consequences or reactions.

~
潮湿
潮湿 implies an unpleasant level of dampness, often associated with mold or mildew.

~
观众
观众 typically refers to a large group of people watching a performance or event, while 听众 (tīngzhòng) is used for listeners of a speech or audio broadcast.

~
互联网
互联网 is synonymous with the internet, but it sometimes carries a more formal connotation in Chinese.  More colloquially, people just say 网络 (wǎngluò).

~
稍微
Can be placed before or after the subject, but usually before.

~
来得及
The opposite of 来不及 (láibují). Note that these phrases are different from English, as they focus on the time it takes to get ready, not on being on time or late once you get there. For example, even if you arrive on time but rushed to get ready, you might still say 来不及. Also, both words can be used transitively or intransitively.

~
零钱
Can also refer to pocket money or allowance.

~
密码
Generally refers to a password for electronic devices or online accounts.

~
青春
Often used to describe the period of adolescence and young adulthood, a time of vitality, energy, and potential. It carries a strong emotional connotation of nostalgia and longing for a time of innocence and possibility.

~
辩论
The object of the debate is typically introduced by the preposition 关于 (guānyú) or 对 (duì).

~
忽视
Often collocates with words like 问题 (wèntí, problem) or 重要性 (zhòngyàoxìng, importance) to emphasize the failure to recognize or address something significant.

~
字母
When referring to initials, it is often used in the plural form 字母缩写 (zìmǔ suōxiě).

~
切
Tut! can be used by itself as an interjection and as such is rather informal and colloquial

~
想象
Can be followed by a clause introduced by a conjunction like that, how, etc.

~
十分
Can be used before adjectives to indicate a high degree. In this usage, it is similar to 很 (hěn) but emphasizes a higher degree of intensity.

~
丰富
Often used to describe experiences, knowledge, or resources, emphasizing their variety and abundance.

~
进口
When referring to the action of importing, the preposition 从 (cóng) is often used to indicate the origin of the imported goods.

~
普通话
Often abbreviated as "Putonghua." It is based on the Beijing dialect and serves as the official language of China.

~
符合
Can be followed by a noun or a clause. It is commonly used in formal contexts, such as official documents or academic writing.

~
反而
Often used in conjunction with a previous clause or sentence that sets up a contrasting situation.

~
无论
Followed by a question word or phrase (e.g., 什么, 谁, 多长时间) and usually paired with 也 (yě) or 都 (dōu) to emphasize the inclusiveness of the condition.

~
按时
Used to emphasize punctuality and adherence to schedules.

~
填空
Commonly used in educational settings to refer to exercises where students fill in missing information.

~
陆地
Contrasts with 海洋 (hǎiyáng, ocean) or 水域 (shuǐyù, waters). It often refers to the solid ground of a continent or island.

~
允许
Often used in formal contexts, such as laws or regulations, to indicate official permission.

~
乒乓球
When referring to the sport itself, the word is often shortened to 乒乓 (pīngpāng).

~
登记
Often used in official contexts, such as registering for a hotel, a flight, or a government service.

~
排列
Implies a systematic arrangement of items in a specific sequence or order.

~
宽
Can be used metaphorically to describe a person's open-mindedness or tolerance.

~
总理
Refers to the head of government in many countries.

~
总之
Used to summarize or conclude a discussion or argument.

~
糖
Can refer to various types of sugar or sweet substances.

~
左右
When used to mean "approximately," it follows the number it modifies.

~
打扰
A polite expression used to excuse oneself for interrupting or inconveniencing someone.

~
生意
Can also refer to the general state of business or commercial activity.

~
梦想
Often followed by a clause introduced by the preposition "of" or "about."

~
受不了
Expresses a strong feeling of intolerance or inability to cope with something.

~
承认
Often implies accepting the truth or validity of something previously denied or disputed.

~
举
Can be used metaphorically to indicate presenting examples or evidence to support a point.

~
苦
Can also refer to bitterness in taste or to hardship and suffering.

~
根
Often used metaphorically to refer to the foundation or origin of something.

~
广告
Can refer to various forms of advertising, including print, television, radio, and online ads.

~
附近
Often followed by a location or landmark to indicate proximity.

~
能干
Often used to describe someone who is skilled and efficient in their work.

~
因此
A related word is 所以 (suǒyǐ). 因此 is more formal than 所以.  Thus 因此 is more appropriate for formal writing, such as academic papers or official documents.  所以 is more common in everyday conversation and informal writing.  There is no difference in meaning.

~
保证
This word can mean "to guarantee" or "to ensure".  However, when it means "to ensure", it takes on a slightly different grammatical role. In this case, you would say something like:

我保证完成任务 (wǒ bǎozhèng wánchéng rènwu) - I guarantee I will complete the mission.

~
敌人
While 敌人 (dírén) technically means "enemy," its usage is much broader in Chinese than "enemy" is in English. It can refer to opponents in games, rivals in business, or even just something one is struggling with, such as 减肥的敌人 (jiǎnféi de dírén) - the enemy of weight loss (i.e., things that make it hard to lose weight).

~
空间 (space)
空间 can be a tricky word because it encompasses both physical and abstract space.  When referring to a physical space or room, you could also use 地方 (dìfang). When referring to outer space, you can also use 太空 (tàikōng) or 宇宙 (yǔzhòu). When referring to abstract space like headroom or margin you can use 余地 (yúdì).


~
丢
The meanings of 丢 (diū) – "to lose" and "to throw" – while seemingly disparate, share the core idea of something becoming separated from its owner or original location.  This connection might be helpful in remembering both meanings.  When it means "to throw" it's similar to "to toss" in English, i.e. casually throwing something away.


~
伞
伞 (sǎn) can sometimes be seen written as 伞 (sǎn).  These are just variant characters and there is no difference in meaning.

~
活动 (activity; to move about)
As a noun, 活动 (huódòng) refers to a planned event or organized activity, similar to "event" or "function" in English.  It does not usually refer to a hobby.  A hobby would be 爱好 (àihào).

~
同时
同时 (tóngshí) as an adverb means "at the same time".  As a conjunction, however, it translates to "meanwhile" or "at the same time". For example:

我做饭，你同时可以打扫卫生。(Wǒ zuò fàn, nǐ tóngshí kěyǐ dǎsǎo wèishēng.)  I'll cook, and meanwhile you can clean.


~
航班
航班 (hángbān) specifically refers to scheduled commercial flights. It wouldn't be used for a private plane or chartered flight.


~
理想
理想 (lǐxiǎng) is a word commonly misunderstood by English speakers. In English, we have the word "ideal" which is synonymous with "perfect". However, in Chinese, the word 理想 usually means something one strives for, sometimes unrealistically. It can mean "ideal" as an adjective, but only in certain contexts. 理想 can also be used as a noun meaning "ideal" or "dream".

~
成为
成为 (chéngwéi) emphasizes the process of transformation or reaching a certain status. 成为 highlights the change from one state to another.  A related word is 变成 (biànchéng) which focuses on the end result.

~
样子
样子 (yàngzi) can encompass a wide range of meanings beyond just physical appearance. It can refer to someone's demeanor, the state or condition of something, or even a general semblance or likeness.


~
及格
及格 (jígé) only refers to barely passing a test or exam.  It doesn't mean to pass with flying colors or to excel.  The more generic word for "pass" is 通过 (tōngguò).


~
穷
穷 (qióng) can mean "poor" in the financial sense, or it can more broadly mean exhausted or depleted.


~
着 (aspect particle)
The aspect particle 着 (zhe) indicates an ongoing action or state. This can sometimes be tricky for learners because its presence or absence subtly alters the meaning of a sentence. Be mindful of these nuances. For example:

我看电视 (wǒ kàn diànshì) - I watch TV (in general)
我看着电视 (wǒ kànzhe diànshì) - I'm watching TV (right now)


~
辛苦
辛苦 (xīnkǔ) can be used to both describe something as arduous or tiring, and to thank someone for their hard work or effort.  For example:

这份工作很辛苦 (zhè fèn gōngzuò hěn xīnkǔ) - This job is very hard.
你辛苦了 (nǐ xīnkǔ le) - Thank you for your hard work.

~
作者
作者 (zuòzhě) refers specifically to the author of a written work, not a creator in general.


~
锻炼
锻炼 (duànliàn) implies a continuous and purposeful effort to improve or strengthen, whether it's one's physical fitness or a specific skill.


~
情景
情景 (qíngjǐng) combines the elements of emotion (情 qíng) and scene (景 jǐng) to create a vivid depiction of a particular moment or situation.


~
临时
临时 (línshí) carries the connotation of something being unplanned or hastily arranged due to unforeseen circumstances.


~
主题
主题 (zhǔtí) represents the central idea or message being conveyed, whether in a piece of writing, a discussion, or a work of art.


~
阶段
阶段 (jiēduàn) highlights a distinct period within a larger process, marked by specific characteristics or milestones.


~
民族
民族 (mínzú) refers to a group of people sharing a common culture, history, and often language, similar to "ethnic group" in English.  It's not the same as 国籍 (guójí) which means nationality.


~
促使
促使 (cùshǐ) emphasizes the catalyst or driving force that leads to a particular action or outcome.


~
全部
全部 (quánbù) emphasizes totality, encompassing every single part or element within a given scope.


~
片面
片面 (piànmiàn) suggests a perspective that is incomplete or biased, lacking a comprehensive understanding of all relevant factors.


~
饺子
饺子 (jiǎozi) are a staple food in China, often eaten during festivals and special occasions, and can be prepared in countless ways with diverse fillings.


~
承担
承担 (chéngdān) implies taking on a responsibility, burden, or task, often with a sense of duty or obligation.


~
举行
举行 (jǔxíng) is used for formal events or ceremonies, and carries a sense of official organization and significance.


~
烤鸭
烤鸭 (kǎoyā), a renowned Beijing dish, is known for its crispy skin and tender meat, often served with pancakes and sweet bean sauce.


~
毛巾
毛巾 (máojīn) specifically refers to a towel used for wiping the body or face, rather than a dishcloth or other cleaning cloth.


~
场
场 (chǎng) as a measure word can be tricky. It's used for a variety of situations, including games, performances, and even arguments.


~
研究
研究 (yánjiū) implies a systematic and in-depth investigation or exploration of a particular subject, often with the aim of gaining new knowledge or understanding.


~
不得不
不得不 (bùdébù) expresses a sense of compulsion or lack of choice in a given situation, emphasizing the inevitability of the action being taken.


~
千万
千万 (qiānwàn) can be both a numeral (ten million) and an intensifier meaning "absolutely must" or "be sure to," emphasizing the importance of the following action.


~
阳台
阳台 (yángtái) is an open-air platform attached to a building, offering a space for relaxation and outdoor activities.


~
沉
沉 (chén) can describe a physical sinking or a metaphorical deepening of an emotion or thought.


~
顺序
顺序 (shùnxù) emphasizes the arrangement of things in a specific order, following a logical or chronological progression.


~
征求
征求 (zhēngqiú) implies actively seeking opinions or feedback, usually from a wider audience or group, with the intention of gathering information or gaining consensus.


~
名片
