名片 (míngpiàn) is a small card containing essential contact information, commonly exchanged in professional or formal settings.

~
而
The word 而 (ér) is a conjunction that can be tricky for learners because it has several different meanings and usages. Here are some key points to remember:

1. **Connecting clauses with a contrastive or adversative relationship:** This is the most common usage of 而, similar to "but" or "yet" in English.  It implies a contrast or opposition between the two clauses.  For example: 他很努力，而没有成功 (Tā hěn nǔlì, ér méiyǒu chénggōng) - He worked hard, but didn't succeed.

2. **Connecting clauses with a sequential or consequential relationship:**  In this case, 而 can mean "and so" or "and then."  It indicates that the second clause follows naturally from the first.  For example:  天气很冷，而我穿了很多衣服 (Tiānqì hěn lěng, ér wǒ chuān le hěn duō yīfu) - The weather was cold, and so I wore a lot of clothes.

3. **Connecting verbs or adjectives:**  而 can be used to link two verbs or adjectives, often highlighting a contrast or difference.  For example:  这个问题既复杂而又有意义 (Zhège wèntí jì fùzá ér yòu yǒuyìyì) - This question is both complex and meaningful.

4. **Indicating a change of state:**  而 can show a transition or change in a situation. For example:  雨停而云散 (Yǔ tíng ér yún sàn) - The rain stopped and the clouds dispersed.

5. **Formal usage:**  而 is more common in formal or written Chinese.  In spoken Chinese, other conjunctions like 可是 (kěshì) or 但是 (dànshì) are often used instead for the adversative meaning.

A key difference between 而 and other conjunctions like 但是 (dànshì) is that 而 emphasizes the connection between two clauses, while 但是 emphasizes the contrast.  Consider the difference between these two sentences:

* 他很努力，而没有成功 (Tā hěn nǔlì, ér méiyǒu chénggōng) - He worked hard, but didn't succeed. (Focus is on the connection between effort and lack of success)
* 他很努力，但是没有成功 (Tā hěn nǔlì, dànshì méiyǒu chénggōng) - He worked hard, but didn't succeed. (Focus is on the contrast between effort and outcome)

~
日记
When talking about keeping a diary, the associated verb is 写 (xiě - to write), so you would say 写日记 (xiě rìjì).

~
刀
Measure words:
A single knife is usually measured with the measure word 把 (bǎ).  A set of knives might be counted with 套 (tào) meaning "set."  刀 can also be used as a measure word itself, referring to cuts or stabs with a knife, e.g., 一刀 (yīdāo) - one cut/stab.

Colloquial usage:
In certain dialects, 刀 (dāo) can be slang for a dollar (influenced by the similar-sounding word "dollar" in English).

~
底
底 (dǐ) can be tricky.  In addition to the meanings listed, pay close attention to its grammatical function as a possessive particle.  In this case, it's equivalent to 的 (de) but has a more literary or classical feel.  You'll see it in phrases like 年底 (niándǐ - end of the year) or 月底 (yuèdǐ - end of the month), where it indicates possession (the end "of" the year/month).

~
个别
个别 (gèbié) is often misused by learners to mean "a few." While it can sometimes imply a small number, it primarily emphasizes the *distinctness* or *separateness* of the individuals or items being referred to. A more accurate translation would be "individual," "separate," or "a few exceptional cases."  Avoid using it when you simply mean "a few."

~
地球
地球 is the standard and universal term for "Earth."

~
想念
想念 (xiǎngniàn) carries a stronger emotional weight than simply thinking of someone. It implies missing them and longing for their presence.

~
打扮
打扮 (dǎbàn) includes a wider range of actions than simply dressing up. It encompasses all aspects of making oneself look presentable, including hair styling, makeup, and accessories.  It carries a connotation of putting effort into one's appearance.

~
长江
While 长江 (Cháng Jiāng) is typically translated as "Yangtze River," be aware that 长江 literally means "Long River."  This name is more commonly used within China.

~
困
困 (kùn) can mean both "sleepy" and "trapped/surrounded." Pay attention to context to discern the intended meaning.  When meaning "sleepy", it is similar to 困了 (kùn le).

~
目的
目的 (mùdì) is more formal than other words for purpose or goal, like  目标 (mùbiāo).

~
淡
淡 (dàn) is much broader than just "light in color". It is also used for tastes, like coffee, or even for feelings or relationships between people.

~
陪
陪 (péi) implies spending time with someone, often to prevent them from feeling lonely or bored.  It emphasizes the companionship aspect of being together.

~
孙子
孙子 (sūnzǐ) is also the name of the famous Chinese general and author of "The Art of War."

~
固定
固定 (gùdìng) implies something is fixed *permanently* or *regularly*. It's stronger than simply saying something is in a fixed position temporarily.

~
收获
收获 (shōuhuò) is not limited to agricultural harvests. It can refer to gains or achievements in any area of life, including personal growth, career, or relationships.

~
首先
首先 (shǒuxiān) is more formal than other ways of saying "first," such as  先 (xiān).

~
精力
精力 (jīnglì) refers specifically to mental or physical energy, not energy in other forms like electricity.

~
项
项 (xiàng) as a classifier is very versatile.  It is used for items in a list, terms in a contract, events in a competition, or academic projects. It implies a distinct and separate unit within a larger group.

~
植物
植物 (zhíwù) encompasses all plant life, not just flowers or trees.


~
停
停 (tíng) implies a temporary cessation of movement or activity.

~
弹钢琴
弹钢琴 (tán gāngqín) specifically refers to playing the piano, not any other keyboard instrument.

~
士兵
士兵 (shìbīng) is a more general term than other words for military personnel, like 军人 (jūnrén - military person).

~
火
火 (huǒ) has many meanings beyond "fire."  Be aware of its colloquial usage to mean "popular" or "hot" (trendy), similar to the English slang usage.  Also, watch for its use in traditional Chinese medicine to describe internal heat or inflammation.

~
标志
标志 (biāozhì) can function as both a noun and a verb.  As a noun, it translates to "sign," "symbol," "logo," or "mark." As a verb, it means "to mark," "to symbolize," or "to indicate."

~
不要紧
不要紧 (búyàojǐn) has a wide range of meanings related to "not serious" or "it doesn't matter." It can be used to downplay the severity of a situation, reassure someone, or express that something is unimportant.  The specific nuance depends heavily on context.

~
酒吧
While 酒吧 (jiǔbā) generally refers to a bar or pub, it can sometimes encompass other similar establishments like nightclubs or lounges, especially in casual conversation.

~
公里
公里 (gōnglǐ) is the standard term for "kilometer" in Chinese.  Be sure to pronounce the "gōng" clearly, as it can sometimes be misheard as "gōngjīn" (公斤), which means "kilogram."

~
增加
增加 (zēngjiā) specifically refers to an increase in quantity or number. It doesn't describe an increase in quality or intensity. For those cases, you would use other words like 提高 (tígāo) or 加强 (jiāqiáng).

~
综合
综合 (zōnghé) can be both an adjective and a verb. As an adjective, it describes something "comprehensive" or "composite." As a verb, it means "to sum up," "to integrate," or "to synthesize."

~
平均
平均 (píngjūn) is often used with the preposition 每 (měi), meaning "every," to express "on average," as in 每人平均 (měirén píngjūn) - "on average per person."

~
扔
扔 (rēng) generally implies a casual or forceful throw, not a gentle toss.  For a more gentle throw, you might use 丢 (diū) or 投 (tóu).

~
座位
While the most common measure word for 座位 (zuòwèi) is 个 (gè), 位 (wèi) is also used, especially in more formal contexts or when showing politeness.

~
重点
重点 (zhòngdiǎn) acts as both a noun ("important point," "focus") and a verb ("to focus on," "to emphasize").  As a noun, it often appears in phrases like 重点项目 (zhòngdiǎn xiàngmù) - "key project."

~
万一
万一 (wànyī) is always used in hypothetical situations, introducing a low-probability but potentially serious event.  It's often followed by a statement outlining a contingency plan or precautionary measure.

~
反对
反对 (fǎnduì) expresses strong opposition or disagreement.  For milder disagreement, you might use different words like 不赞成 (bù zànchéng) - "to disapprove of" or 有异议 (yǒu yìyì) - "to have objections."

~
女士
女士 (nǚshì) is a polite and formal way to address a woman.  It's equivalent to "Ms." or "Madam" in English.  Avoid using it for young girls.

~
打扫
打扫 (dǎsǎo) usually refers to cleaning or sweeping a physical space, like a room or a street.  For cleaning oneself, you would use other verbs like 洗 (xǐ) or 清洗 (qīngxǐ).

~
或许
或许 (huòxǔ) expresses a slightly higher degree of probability than 也许 (yěxǔ) - "perhaps." Both are interchangeable in many situations, though.

~
演出
演出 (yǎnchū) refers to a public performance, often artistic in nature.  It can be a play, concert, or other show.

~
恐怕
恐怕 (kǒngpà) expresses a polite and indirect way of saying "I'm afraid that..." It can also indicate a degree of uncertainty or apprehension.

~
份
份 (fèn) is a versatile measure word, often used for portions, shares, or copies of things.  It's not usually used for countable objects.

~
赶
赶 (gǎn) has a wide range of meanings related to "hurrying," "catching up," or "driving (something) forward." The specific meaning depends heavily on the context.

~
富
富 (fù) refers to wealth or abundance.  It can describe both material wealth and abundance in other areas, like natural resources or talent.

~
老虎
Remember to use the correct measure word 只 (zhī) when referring to tigers.

~
利益
利益 (lìyì) encompasses both "interest" and "benefit," often implying a material or practical advantage.

~
干杯
干杯 (gānbēi) is the standard toast in Chinese, equivalent to "Cheers!" It literally means "dry cup," suggesting finishing the drink in one go.

~
良好
良好 (liánghǎo) describes a generally good or favorable situation, condition, or quality.

~
节约
节约 (jiéyuē) emphasizes conserving resources or being frugal, not necessarily being cheap.

~
包裹
包裹 (bāoguǒ) can refer to both the act of wrapping something and the resulting package or parcel.

~
勺子
勺子 (sháozi) refers to a spoon, ladle, or scoop, usually for serving food.  The specific meaning can depend on the context or the size and shape of the utensil.

~
眼镜
眼镜 (yǎnjìng) is the general term for glasses or spectacles.  Remember to use the measure word 副 (fù).

~
大使馆
大使馆 (dàshǐguǎn) refers to an embassy.

~
留
While 留 (liú) has the general meaning of "to leave" or "to stay,"  it often specifically refers to leaving behind a message, an object, or a lasting impression.

~
再三
再三 (zàisān) emphasizes repeated actions or requests, often implying persistence or insistence.

~
到处
到处 (dàochù) indicates a wide area or many different places. It emphasizes being scattered or spread out.

~
其余
其余 (qíyú) refers to the remaining part or the rest of something, often after a portion has been removed or dealt with.

~
从来
从来 (cónglái) is tricky because its meaning changes depending on whether the sentence is positive or negative. In affirmative sentences, it means "always," but in negative sentences, it means "never."

~
加班
加班 (jiābān) means both "overtime work" and "to work overtime."  It's often used with the verb 上 (shàng) as in 上加班 (shàng jiābān) - "to work overtime."

~
偶尔
偶尔 (ǒu'ěr) describes something that happens infrequently or occasionally.

~
地点
地点 (dìdiǎn) refers to a specific place or location.

~
不管
不管 (bùguǎn) means "regardless of" or "no matter."  It introduces a condition that doesn't affect the outcome or action that follows.

~
叔叔
叔叔 (shūshu) refers specifically to a younger brother of one's father.  It's often used as a general term of address for a man of a similar age to one's father, showing respect and familiarity.

~
可是
可是 (kěshì) is a conjunction that introduces a contrast or objection, similar to "but" or "however" in English. It can also be used for emphasis, like "indeed" or "certainly."

~
棒
When used to mean "great", it is best translated as "awesome" or "fantastic". It's quite informal.  It can also be reduplicated as 棒棒 (bàngbàng).  This is usually used to encourage children.

~
棵
This measure word is generally for plants which have a trunk.  So, it's fine for trees and cabbages, but not for flowers or grass.

~
运气
A useful phrase is "运气好" (yùnqi hǎo) meaning "good luck". Similarly, "运气不好" (yùnqi bù hǎo) means "bad luck".

~
减少
This word emphasizes the *amount* of the decrease, in contrast to 降低 (jiàngdī), which emphasizes the *level* of the resulting value.  For example, we would use 减少 to talk about how much pollution has gone down, and 降低 to talk about the current level of pollution.

~
收入
The related word, "收入囊中" (shōurù nángzhōng), meaning "to pocket," is frequently used in colloquial Chinese.

~
客厅
In mainland China, this is the main room in a house where guests are received and entertained. However, in Hong Kong and Taiwan, this word refers to a bathroom/restroom.

~
擦
As a verb, this word usually means to wipe *lightly*.  It suggests gentleness and superficiality.  For more serious wiping or scrubbing, use 닦 (dā).

~
措施
This word usually refers to concrete and specific actions taken to achieve a goal.  For broader or less tangible steps, consider using 方法 (fāngfǎ) or 办法 (bànfǎ).

~
页
When referring to web pages, the correct term is "网页" (wǎngyè).

~
尾巴
The term "尾巴狼" (wěiba láng) refers to a playboy or womanizer, similar to a "wolf" in English slang.

~
受到
This word implies a passive reception of something, often something positive but not always.  In contrast, 得到 (dédào) suggests active acquisition or achievement, typically of something desirable.

~
随便
When used before a verb, it often carries a sense of casualness or carelessness. However, when used as a response to a question, it can mean "as you like" or "whatever you want," indicating deference to the other person's wishes.

~
阻止
阻止 means to prevent something from *starting* or *continuing*.  If something has already happened, then it cannot be 阻止-ed.  Instead, you might use 阻碍 (zǔ'ài), which means to hinder or impede progress that's already underway.

~
过分
This adjective is generally stronger than "excessive" and carries a negative connotation. It often implies crossing a line or being unreasonable.

~
顾客
This word is a more formal and respectful term than simply saying "客人" (kèrén) for customer.

~
汤
This character can also refer to hot water, as in "热水汤" (rèshuǐ tāng), emphasizing its temperature.

~
微笑
A common collocation is "微微一笑" (wēiwēi yīxiào), meaning to smile slightly or faintly.

~
着火
This signifies the *state* of being on fire. In contrast, 起火 (qǐhuǒ) refers to the *act* of something catching fire.

~
位于
This is typically used for more formal or official contexts, such as describing the geographical location of a city or building. For everyday conversations, "在" (zài) is more common.

~
简历
It's crucial to tailor your 简历 to the specific job you're applying for.  A generic 简历 is less likely to be successful.

~
参考
When used before another noun, it functions like an adjective meaning "for reference" or "reference …."

~
主席
This title is most commonly associated with political leadership, such as the Chairman of the Communist Party or the Chairman of a country. For less formal meetings, "主持人" (zhǔchí rén), meaning "host" or "moderator," is more appropriate.

~
缩短
The focus is on the *duration*.  "缩小" (suōxiǎo) would be to reduce the *size*.

~
商量
This suggests a more collaborative and equal discussion than 讨论 (tǎolùn), which can imply a more formal or one-sided presentation of ideas.

~
亲密
This can describe relationships between family members, close friends, or romantic partners.  Avoid using it for casual acquaintances.

~
参与
This implies more active involvement than 参加 (cānjiā).

~
表扬
This term is typically used for commending someone publicly or formally.  For more casual praise, use 称赞 (chēngzàn).

~
号码
Be mindful of tone changes: 号码 (hàomǎ) vs. 好吗 (hǎoma).

~
此外
This phrase is more formal and literary than "还有" (háiyǒu).

~
发挥
This implies making full use of something's potential or inherent qualities.

~
寻找
This implies a more deliberate and thorough search than simply "找" (zhǎo).

~
阵
It's a useful measure word for events of short duration.

~
光
光 can also mean "smooth" or "bald".

~
错误
The difference between 错误 (cuòwù) and 差错 (chācuò) is that 错误 tends to emphasize moral failing while 差错 emphasizes minor errors or miscalculations in routine actions.

~
现金
In China, mobile payments are widely used.  Cash is less common now than in most Western countries.

~
遍
Remember that 遍 is a measure word for actions, not nouns.

~
试卷
Remember to bring all necessary materials for the 试卷, like pens and erasers.

~
钥匙
Related phrase: "丢了钥匙" (diūle yàoshi) means "lost the keys."

~
参观
Implies a more formal and organized visit than simply "看" (kàn).

~
移动
When referring to mobile phones, the correct term is "手机" (shǒujī).

~
程序
Can also mean "sequence" or "order," such as in "按程序做" (àn chéngxù zuò) - "to do things in order/according to the procedure."

~
好像
This word is usually used for subjective impressions.  For more objective situations where something "appears to be," 看起来 (kàn qǐ lái) is more suitable.

~
舒适
A more formal synonym is 舒服 (shūfu).

~
总共
This word emphasizes the final sum after adding things up.  一共 (yígòng) is more general and can be used even if no explicit adding has occurred.

~
却
This word is placed *before* the verb or adjective it modifies.  For example, "He is small but strong" would be "他个子小却很强壮 (Tā gèzi xiǎo què hěn qiángzhuàng)."

~
尺子
The most common measure word for 尺子 is indeed 把 (bǎ).

~
镜子
面 (miàn) is the more common measure word for 镜子.

~
极其
极其 is more formal than 非常 (fēicháng) or 很 (hěn).

~
葡萄
The most common measure word for 葡萄 is 串 (chuàn), meaning "bunch."  颗 (kē) can be used for individual grapes.

~
关闭
关闭 is more formal than 关 (guān).  It often implies a more complete or permanent closure, especially for businesses, computer systems, or official functions.

~
法院
The measure word for 法院 is 家 (jiā) or 所 (suǒ), not 个.

~
塑料袋
个 (gè) is the most common measure word.

~
羡慕
This word carries a connotation of wishing one had what the other person has.  欣赏 (xīnshǎng) is a better choice for simply admiring someone's qualities without envy.

~
待遇
This word encompasses not just salary, but also benefits, perks, and overall how someone is treated in their position.

~
不仅
Remember the structure 不仅..., 也/而且....  也 (yě) is used in simpler constructions, while 而且 (érqiě) is used in more complex sentences.

~
失望
Be mindful of the difference between 失望 (shīwàng) which describes the *feeling* of disappointment and 让人失望 (ràng rén shīwàng), meaning *to disappoint someone*.

~
祝贺
个 is not a typical measure word for 祝贺.  You could use 句 (jù) if referring to a spoken congratulation.  It's also common to use it without a measure word at all.

~
感兴趣
The preposition used with this phrase is 对 (duì) –  对...感兴趣 (duì...gǎn xìngqù).

~
地方
地方 can refer to a general area, a specific location, or even a point in an argument. Context is crucial.

~
邮局
家 (jiā) is the more appropriate measure word.

~
支持
支持 can be abstract, such as supporting an idea.  拥护 (yōnghù) implies stronger, more active support, often for a political figure or cause.

~
性别
While both terms refer to distinctions between male and female, 性别 is broader, encompassing social and cultural aspects alongside biological ones.  性 (xìng) primarily refers to the biological aspect.

~
充电器
The measure word is 个 (gè).

~
是否
是否 is more formal than simply using a question with 吗 (ma).

~
西红柿
个 (gè) is the more common measure word in northern China.

~
导游
导游 can refer to both the person (tour guide) and the activity (to conduct a tour).  It can also refer to a guidebook.

~
矮
矮 is the opposite of 高 (gāo).  It is generally used for people and objects, while 低 (dī) is used for things closer to the ground.

~
密切
密切 suggests a very close connection, often with strategic or political implications.  亲密 (qīnmì) is more appropriate for personal relationships.

~
放暑假
This describes the *state* of being on summer vacation.  If you want to say "to go on summer vacation," use 去放暑假 (qù fàng shǔjià).

~
例如
例如 introduces examples that are part of a larger category, implying there are other examples.  比如 (bǐrú) introduces examples that are more representative.

~
奋斗
奋斗 suggests a continuous, strenuous effort towards a long-term goal.  努力 (nǔlì) implies general hard work.

~
降低
降低 usually describes lowering something abstract like prices, temperature, or risk.  减少 (jiǎnshǎo) is for decreasing the quantity of something.

~
翻
Among its many meanings, 翻 also means "to browse" or "to leaf through," as in flipping through pages.

~
词语
词语 is a broader term encompassing various linguistic units, including words, phrases, and expressions. 词 (cí) refers specifically to individual words.

~
身材
身材 usually describes the overall shape and proportions of a person's body, rather than just height and weight.  体型 (tǐxíng) refers more specifically to body type.

~
收拾
收拾 implies putting things away tidily or dealing with a problem effectively.  整理 (zhěnglǐ) focuses more on organizing and arranging things.

~
修理
修理 is typically used for fixing machinery or equipment.  修 (xiū) is a more general term that can also be used for repairing buildings, roads, or relationships.

~
母亲
妈妈 (māma) is the more common and informal term.

~
说服
说服 means to successfully persuade someone.  劝 (quàn) is the act of trying to persuade, regardless of the outcome.

~
挑战
挑战 implies a direct confrontation or competition.  考验 (kǎoyàn) refers more to a test or trial of one's abilities.

~
醒
Can be used transitively (to wake someone up) or intransitively (to wake up).

~
深
Aside from the literal meaning of "deep", 深 can also have the figurative meaning of "late" (e.g. 深夜 - late at night), or "deep" in the sense of advanced or profound knowledge.

~
集合
The most common meanings of 集合 are:
1. (Intransitive) To gather/assemble (people).
2. (Transitive) To summon/muster (troops, courage, strength, etc.)
3. (Noun) A set (mathematics) or a collection

~
厚
Aside from literally meaning "thick", 厚 can mean:
1. Kind or generous (e.g. 厚待 - to treat someone well)
2. Rich or strong in flavor
3. To favor or stress (e.g. 厚此薄彼 - to favor one and discriminate against the other).


~
季节
Usually used to refer to a longer period of time, like a season, rather than just a specific time or date.

~
称赞
More formal than other words for praise, like 表扬 (biǎoyáng) or 夸奖 (kuājiǎng).


~
纷纷
Can be tricky to translate into English, meaning something along the lines of "one after another; in succession" in some cases, or meaning "numerous and confused; pell-mell" in others. Context and collocation are key to understanding its usage.

~
啊
Pronunciation and tone changes significantly based on the proceeding word, so listen to examples in context to get a feel for this. It also has several different uses and meanings depending on context, which aren't always obvious to beginners.

~
散步
More leisurely than other words for walking. Implies strolling for pleasure or relaxation, not just walking from point A to point B.

~
首都
Always refers to a capital *city*. The word for capital as in money/assets is 资本 (zīběn).

~
儿童
Refers to children in general, or a child, rather than a specific child. A more specific way to say child is 孩子 (háizi).


~
正好
Covers a broader range of meanings than "just" or "just in time" in English. Can also convey "just right", "coincidentally", or "fortunately".

~
到底
Used to emphasize finality or certainty, often in questions seeking a definitive answer.


~
功夫
When meaning kung-fu, usually uses the full two characters 功夫. The single character 功 is typically used for "merit, achievement".


~
帅
Meaning "handsome" is mostly used for men, and is somewhat colloquial. A more formal term for men is 英俊 (yīngjùn).


~
破
Has a wide range of meanings, and context is necessary to determine whether it signifies something broken, damaged, or a breakthrough or victory over something negative.


~
风俗
Refers to customs and traditions in general, often of a particular region or group. Don't confuse with the words for habit (习惯 - xíguàn) or manners (礼貌 - lǐmào).


~
整理
Implies a more thorough and organized approach than just tidying up. Often involves putting things in a systematic or logical order.


~
兄弟
Although it refers to brothers literally, it is also sometimes used colloquially to show friendship or close relationships with other men.


~
仔细
Means careful or thorough with close attention to details, whereas 小心 (xiǎoxīn) is more about avoiding mistakes or being cautious in action.


~
帽子
Figuratively refers to labels. Can be any label, positive, negative, or neutral.


~
内
Often used in formal contexts and in written Chinese, though it has a counterpart, 裡 (li), which is used more in spoken language.


~
同情
A stronger emotion than just pity. Suggests understanding and sharing someone's feelings, often accompanied by a desire to help.


~
随着
Implies a closer, more direct relationship between the two things described than just happening at the same time. One thing follows or changes according to the other.

~
预习
More structured and comprehensive than just previewing or glancing at a lesson. Involves active reading and preparation for upcoming content.


~
另外
Means more than just the equivalent of "in addition", and can also carry the nuance of indicating something separate, distinct, or an alternative. Can also begin a sentence, which "in addition" cannot.


~
黄金
Aside from the literal meaning of gold, this can also figuratively refer to golden times, prime times, or opportunities.


~
提供
Implies the provision of something substantial or necessary, like resources, support, or information, while other words for give, such as 给 (gěi), can be used more generally.


~
轻易
Has a connotation of doing something without enough thought or effort, possibly leading to a negative outcome. The antonym is 慎重 (shènzhòng).


~
不然
Used in various ways to mean "if not; otherwise; or else; no". Can also be used in rhetorical questions.


~
粗心
Usually used to describe carelessness which leads to a bad or undesired outcome.


~
好
Extremely versatile, meaning different things depending on context. Can be used to describe easy/good to do, a close relationship, affirmation, or completion. Also used in greetings. Pay close attention to pronunciation and tone to discern meaning.


~
演讲
More formal and structured than 说话 (shuōhuà) or 讲话 (jiǎnghuà). Often refers to a prepared speech on a specific topic, especially for public or ceremonial purposes.

~
义务
More formal than other words for duty. Relates to social responsibilities or moral obligations.


~
统一
Not just "to unify", but also carries the meaning "united" or "consistent". Also means "7-Eleven".


~
神秘
Can describe things that are intentionally kept secret or just naturally unknown.  Not always negative, can also imply intrigue or fascination.


~
只要
Important to consider the word order of the clause that follows. The thing desired comes after 只要, and then followed by 就 (jiù) or 便 (biàn).


~
胳膊
Specifically means the arm from shoulder to wrist. 手臂 (shǒubì) is a broader term encompassing the entire arm including the hand.


~
顶
Very versatile. Aside from the definitions given above, it is also used as a measure word for hats and objects on top of things.


~
干
Extremely versatile. Pay close attention to context, pronunciation, and tone to discern which meaning is being used. In the spoken language, it's typically the fourth tone (gàn), but when it's a verb and the object is a monosyllabic word, it changes to the neutral tone.

~
危险
危险 can be used as both a noun and an adjective.  As a noun, it means "danger".  As an adjective, it means "dangerous".  For example,  "很危险" (hěn wēixiǎn) means "very dangerous". "那很危险" (nà hěn wēixiǎn) means “That’s very dangerous” or "That's dangerous".

~
着急
着急 is typically used to describe the feeling of anxiety or urgency *from the speaker's perspective*.  You wouldn't typically use it to describe someone else's anxiety unless you're empathizing with them.  To describe someone else as anxious, you'd more likely use 担心 (dānxīn) or 焦虑 (jiāolǜ).  Also, 着急 implies a sense of impatience or being in a hurry.

~
材料
While 材料 can refer to physical materials, it can also mean "data" or even figuratively refer to a person with potential ("he's good material"). Context is key to understanding the intended meaning.

~
冷静
As a verb, 冷静 (lěngjìng) means "to calm down". As an adjective, it describes someone who is "calm, cool-headed, or dispassionate."  Be aware of its less common meaning: "deserted" or "quiet" when describing a place.

~
景色
景色 is a more poetic or literary term for scenery, often used to describe beautiful or impressive natural views.  风景 (fēngjǐng) is a more general term for scenery, encompassing both natural and man-made views.

~
似的
似的 (shìde) adds a sense of uncertainty or approximation. It softens the comparison, suggesting "kind of like" or "seems as if" rather than a direct equivalence. For example, "他跑得像风似的" (tā pǎo de xiàng fēng shìde) means "He runs like the wind" with a more figurative and less literal nuance than just using 像 (xiàng).

~
心情
心情 refers specifically to one's mood or emotional state. It's different from 心情 (xīnqíng), which can refer to mentality, feelings, or interest.

~
单调
单调 (dāndiào) implies a sense of boredom or tediousness due to lack of variety.  It's stronger than simply "simple" and carries a negative connotation.

~
勇敢
勇敢 (yǒnggǎn) emphasizes having courage in the face of fear or danger. It is more about overcoming fear than simply being bold.

~
暂时
暂时 (zánshí) always implies a temporary state of affairs. It's often used with the implication that the situation will change in the future.

~
呼吸
呼吸 (hūxī) is both a noun and a verb, meaning "breath" or "breathing" and "to breathe," respectively.

~
刷牙
刷牙 (shuāyá) specifically refers to brushing one's teeth, not brushing anything else.

~
味道
味道 can refer to both taste and smell, especially in some dialects.  It can also have a figurative meaning, like "a hint of..." or "a sense of..."

~
大约
大约 (dàyuē) is closer to "approximately" or "about" than "probably."  While it can suggest probability, its primary meaning is an estimation of quantity or time.

~
运用
运用 (yùnyòng) suggests skillful or practical application of knowledge or skills, not simply using something.

~
事物
事物 (shìwù) refers to things in a general, abstract sense, often in philosophical or academic contexts.  东西 (dōngxi) is a more common and concrete word for "things" or "objects."

~
死
死 (sǐ) has many colloquial uses beyond its literal meaning of "to die." It can be used as an intensifier, like "extremely" or "damned," or to describe something as impassable or inflexible.

~
勇气
勇气 (yǒngqì) is the inner strength to face fear or danger, similar to 勇敢, but more focused on the mental aspect of courage.

~
估计
估计 (gūjì) is closer to "to reckon" or "to think" in colloquial usage, often implying a less precise estimation than 计算 (jìsuàn) which is to "calculate."

~
街道
街道 (jiēdào) can refer to both a street and an administrative district, similar to a subdistrict or residential area.

~
谈
谈 (tán) covers a wide range of verbal communication, from casual chatting to formal discussions or negotiations.

~
答案
答案 (dá'àn) specifically refers to the correct answer to a question or problem.  It's not a general synonym for "reply" or "response."

~
免费
免费 (miǎnfèi) means "free of charge" or complimentary.

~
短信
短信 (duǎnxìn) is short for 短消息 (duǎn xiāoxi), specifically referring to text messages or SMS.

~
轻
轻 (qīng) has many meanings, including "light" (in weight), "easy," "gentle," "soft," but also "reckless," "unimportant," and "to disparage." Context is essential.

~
数字
数字 (shùzì) can refer to numerals, digits, numbers, figures, or amounts.  It can also refer to digital technology.

~
警察
警察 (jǐngchá) refers to police in general or a police officer specifically.

~
汗
Besides its literal meaning "sweat", 汗 (hàn) is internet slang used as an interjection expressing speechlessness, similar to "OMG".

~
光盘
光盘 (guāngpán) can refer to various optical discs, including CDs, DVDs, and CD-ROMs.

~
冰箱
冰箱 (bīngxiāng) is the general term for a refrigerator.

~
乱
乱 (luàn) describes a state of disorder or confusion, but it can also refer to upheaval, riots, or even illicit sexual relations.

~
天真
天真 (tiānzhēn) implies a childlike innocence that can sometimes be seen as naive or foolish.

~
梦
梦 (mèng) can be a noun or a verb.

~
幼儿园
幼儿园 (yòu'éryuán) is equivalent to "kindergarten" or "nursery school."

~
租
租 (zū) can mean both "to rent" and "to rent out," as well as "rent" (the payment itself) and "land tax."

~
开玩笑
开玩笑 (kāi wánxiào) means "to joke" or "to make fun of." It can also be used to tell someone they are not being serious, even if the comment being made is not humorous. For example, in English, “You must be joking!”

~
原料
原料 (yuánliào) specifically refers to raw materials used in production.

~
伙伴
伙伴 (huǒbàn) suggests a close working relationship, often involving shared goals or activities.  It's more than just a casual friend.

~
产品
产品 (chǎnpǐn) refers to manufactured goods or products, typically the result of some production process.

~
结论
The difference between 结论 and 结果 (jiéguǒ) can be tricky. 结论 refers to a reasoned judgment or inference, often reached after careful consideration or investigation. It implies a more definitive and conclusive statement, often based on evidence or logical deduction. In contrast, 结果 simply means the outcome or result of an event or process. It doesn't necessarily involve the same level of reasoned judgment as 结论.


~
迅速
迅速 (xùnsù) is a more formal and literary way to express "fast". It emphasizes not just speed, but also efficiency and decisiveness in action.  More colloquial options for "fast" include 快 (kuài) or  飞快 (fēikuài), the latter specifically suggesting "as fast as flying," which is more descriptive and informal.


~
内部
内部 (nèibù) refers to the "inside" or "interior" of something, both concrete and abstract objects. It emphasizes the inner workings, members, or structure of a system or organization, often implying a sense of exclusivity or privacy.  里边 (lǐbiān), also meaning "inside", is more general and often used for physical locations, like "inside the house." 内部 means "internal" and can be used in formal settings as well as informal settings.


~
弄 (nòng)
弄 (nòng) is a very versatile verb, encompassing a broad range of actions related to handling, manipulating, or dealing with something. It is very colloquial. Its ambiguity can make it difficult to translate directly into English, so understanding its usage depends heavily on context.  For learners, it's crucial to pay attention to the specific context to grasp the intended meaning.  Often, words like "do," "manage," "handle," "mess with," or "fix" are suitable English equivalents.

~
吃亏
This word has quite a wide semantic range, covering situations from minor inconveniences to significant losses. It can describe being taken advantage of financially, suffering a setback in a competition, or simply experiencing an unfortunate event.  The severity is often determined by context.  It often carries a connotation of being naive or easily tricked.

~
形状
A similar word is "形态" (xíngtài), which is usually more abstract and refers to the overall form, including intangible aspects. 形状 typically refers to the physical outline or appearance.

~
某
Note that when 某 is used before a measure word such as 个, 位, or 种, it is pronounced mǒu. Otherwise, it is pronounced mou.

~
播放
This term usually refers to pre-recorded audio or video content. For live broadcasts, use "直播" (zhíbō).

~
暗
The meanings related to "darkness" and those related to "secrecy/hiddenness" are distinct and should be considered different words. Be careful not to confuse them.  The tone changes between the two meanings.

~
与其
与其 is always followed by 不如 (bùrú) in this structure, and the whole phrase expresses a preference for the second action.

~
时代
时代 refers to a longer period with significant characteristics, while "时期" (shíqī) refers to a shorter, more specific period.

~
机器
The measure word depends on the type of machine. 台 is for larger machines, 部 is for electronic devices, and 个 is a more general measure word.

~
假装
This word sometimes has a slightly negative connotation of deception.  For a more neutral way to express pretense, consider using "装作" (zhuāngzuò).

~
课程
"课" (kè) refers to a single class session, while 课程 refers to the overall course of study.

~
人员
人员 is a collective term.  For specific professions, use a more precise term like 老师 (lǎoshī) for teachers,  医生 (yīshēng) for doctors, etc.

~
相对
As an adjective, 相对 means “relative”. As a verb, it means “to resist, to oppose”.

~
繁荣
This term usually refers to economic prosperity, and less frequently to cultural flourishing.

~
内科
This term refers to the medical specialty of internal medicine.  Don't confuse it with "外科" (wàikē), which is surgery.

~
地理
地理 can refer to both the academic subject and the physical terrain of a place.

~
开幕式
Pay attention to the tone change on the fourth character from the verb "开" (kāi) to the noun suffix "式" (shì).

~
尽量
This emphasizes making an effort, but doesn't guarantee success.  It's closer to "try one's best" than "definitely".

~
乖
The meanings of "obedient" and "contrary to reason" seem contradictory but reflect different usages. Be mindful of context.

~
夜
“夜” (yè) usually refers to the period after dark, while “晚上” (wǎnshang) is a broader term for the evening, which may include daylight hours.

~
证件
This word refers to official documents that prove identity or qualifications. Don't confuse it with "文件" (wénjiàn), which refers to general documents.

~
批
This word has several distinct meanings. Pay close attention to context to determine the intended meaning.

~
时刻
时刻 refers to a precise point in time, while 时间 (shíjiān) refers to a duration or period of time.

~
钓
This word refers specifically to fishing with a rod, line, and hook.  For other methods of fishing, use other words like "捕鱼" (bǔyú).

~
至于
This introduces a new topic or aspect of a topic, often with a slight implication of "regarding" or "with respect to".

~
服装
服装 is a general term, while "衣服" (yīfu) is more colloquial.

~
锅
The measure word depends on the type of pot. 口 is generally used for woks and pots with openings, while 只 is used for other pot-like containers.

~
模仿
模仿 implies an attempt to replicate something closely, while “学习” (xuéxí) focuses on learning from something.

~
双方
This emphasizes the distinctness of the two parties involved.  For a more general "both", consider using "两个" (liǎng ge) or "两者" (liǎng zhě).

~
疯狂
This can be used both positively and negatively, depending on the context. It can describe exciting enthusiasm as well as dangerous recklessness.

~
集中
This can refer to both physical gathering and mental focus.

~
成长
This emphasizes a gradual process of development, often used to describe personal or intellectual growth.

~
地道
The meaning of "authentic" or "genuine" generally applies to language, food, or cultural practices.

~
始终
This emphasizes continuity and lack of change throughout the entire duration.

~
有利
This often implies an advantage in a competitive situation.

~
洒
This can be intentional or accidental.

~
斜
This emphasizes a deviation from the vertical or horizontal, often at an angle.

~
羽毛球
This word can refer to the sport of badminton, a shuttlecock, or a badminton racket.  Context is needed to distinguish.

~
采取
This indicates a deliberate choice of action, often in response to a problem or situation.

~
传播
This can refer to the spread of information, ideas, or diseases.  Context will usually clarify.

~
个性
个性 highlights the unique characteristics of a person, while 性格 (xìnggé) refers to their general character or temperament.

~
发愁
A more formal way to say this is 担忧 (dānyōu).

~
和平
Note that 和平 can also mean the Heping District of Shenyang city or Heping/Hoping Township in Taichung County, Taiwan.

~
提问
A more formal synonym is 质问 (zhìwèn). 提问 usually suggests a neutral inquiry seeking information, while 质问 carries a more challenging or accusatory tone, often implying doubt or disapproval of something.

~
爱心
爱心 can refer to a heart shape (symbol ♥).

~
恨
恨 has two main meanings. One is "to hate," and the other is "to regret."  Be aware of the context to distinguish between these two meanings.  For regret, you could also use 后悔 (hòuhuǐ) which is less ambiguous.

~
踩
踩 can also mean "to downvote" in online contexts.

~
劳动
劳动 is more formal than 工作 (gōngzuò) and can also be used as an adjective.

~
客户
Formal, and more business-like.  A more casual way to say "customer" is 顾客 (gùkè).

~
接触
接触 has a wide range of meanings related to "touching" both physically and metaphorically, such as making contact with someone, coming into contact with an idea, or being exposed to something new.

~
灰
灰 can be used as an adjective to describe feeling discouraged or dejected.

~
傻
More childish than other similar words like 笨 (bèn) or 愚蠢 (yúchǔn).  Often used playfully or affectionately.

~
随时
随时 has two distinct but related meanings.  It can mean "at any time" as well as "at the right time; whenever necessary".  Context is key to understanding which meaning is intended.

~
差距
差距 emphasizes the measurable difference or gap between things, often in terms of quantity, quality, or progress.  A related word is 差别 (chābié) which refers to general differences or distinctions between things, focusing on their distinguishing features or characteristics rather than a quantifiable gap.

~
妨碍
More formal than 打扰 (dǎrǎo).  It implies a more serious or significant obstruction.

~
广大
广大 is typically used to describe physical areas (vast) or large groups of people (numerous). It's not used for individual objects.

~
盖
盖 can be a noun meaning lid or cover. As a verb it can be to cover, conceal or build (like build a house).

~
王子
王子 specifically refers to the son of a king.  For other male royalty, different terms are used (e.g., 皇子 for the son of an emperor).

~
当心
A synonym is 小心 (xiǎoxīn), which is arguably more common.  They can be used interchangeably.

~
要不
要不 can introduce a suggestion or alternative, similar to "how about...?" or "otherwise." It can also express a mild warning or threat, similar to "or else."

~
孝顺
孝顺 describes being filial and showing respect and obedience to one's parents and elders.  This is a culturally significant concept in Chinese society.

~
志愿者
This is more formal than 义工 (yìgōng) although either word will be understood.

~
感激
感激 is stronger than 感谢 (gǎnxiè). It expresses deep gratitude and appreciation, often for significant help or kindness.

~
乙
Besides the usual meaning of second in order, 乙 also appears in legal contexts.  It refers to the “Party B” in a contract, usually contrasted with 甲 (jiǎ), meaning "Party A".  It's also a radical in Chinese characters.

~
游览
游览 implies a leisurely visit or sightseeing tour, often to scenic or historical places.  A related word is 参观 (cānguān), but this implies observing or visiting a specific place with a particular aim, often educational or cultural.

~
救
救 can mean to save a life, but also to help or assist in a more general sense.

~
连忙
连忙 emphasizes a quick and immediate reaction to something, often out of urgency or surprise.  A related word is 赶紧 (gǎnjǐn), which also implies a quick action but often with a sense of eagerness or proactiveness.

~
复制
复制 implies creating an exact copy or duplicate of something.  A related word is 抄袭 (chāoxí), which has the negative connotation of copying someone else's work and presenting it as one's own.

~
届
届 is a classifier for events, meetings, elections, sporting fixtures, and even graduating classes (e.g., "Class of 2023").

~
皮鞋
Specifically refers to leather shoes as opposed to other kinds of shoes.

~
灾害
This refers to large scale calamities and disasters and might sound odd when describing minor mishaps.

~
苗条
苗条 is generally used to describe women.  While you can use it for men, it might sound a bit unusual or even have a slightly negative connotation.  Using other words like  瘦 (shòu) or  清瘦 (qīngshòu) might be more appropriate for men.

~
状况
状况 suggests the overall state or condition of something. 情况 (qíngkuàng) is more general and can refer to any circumstance.

~
成果
成果 suggests a positive result or accomplishment, often the product of effort or work. 结果 (jiéguǒ) is more neutral and simply refers to an outcome.

~
补充
补充 emphasizes adding something to make it complete or sufficient. 添加 (tiānjiā) means to simply add something, without necessarily implying completion or sufficiency.

~
伟大
伟大 is a very strong word, reserved for truly exceptional people or achievements.  It's not used casually.

~
制作
制作 suggests the process of creating or producing something, often involving skill or craftsmanship. 做 (zuò) is more general and can refer to any kind of making or doing.

~
聪明
Generally positive.  A more negative word that implies trickiness or slyness is 狡猾 (jiǎohuá).

~
金属
金属 refers specifically to metals.  Other materials have other specific terms.

~
争论
争论 emphasizes a back-and-forth argument or debate. 讨论 (tǎolùn) suggests a more cooperative and less confrontational discussion.

~
平等
平等 highlights the concept of equality and fairness. 公平 (gōngpíng) implies justice and impartiality in treatment or distribution.

~
灰心
The more formal, written version of this word is 泄气 (xièqì).

~
欠
欠 is often used in the structure 欠 + adj. It means to not reach a certain level of desirability in terms of quality, capability etc. For example:

我的中文还欠好。
This means "my level of Chinese is not good enough". Note that this is a self-deprecating phrase and you cannot use it to criticize someone else.

~
展览
This word can be used as a noun or as a verb.

~
脖子
There are three words with more or less the same meaning: 脖子 (bózi), 颈 (jǐng) and 颈部 (jǐngbù). 脖子 is the common spoken word. 颈 and 颈部 are the medical or technical terms. 颈部 is the most formal and means "cervical region".

~
艰苦
This has a similar meaning to 辛苦 (xīnkǔ). However, 艰苦 refers to hardships over a longer time period, whereas 辛苦 can refer to just a temporary difficulty.

~
挂号
This is now somewhat of a dated word, as in modern times you can often register (at a hospital) using a smartphone app.

~
胸
If this refers to part of one's anatomy, then its measure word is 部 (bù).

~
观念
This has more or less the same meaning as the English word "concept", but it is only ever used in the plural.

~
唉
This is similar to "oh dear" in English.

~
柜台
This has more or less the same meaning as the English words "counter" and "front desk".

~
测验
A more colloquial version of this word is simply 考试 (kǎoshì).

~
手续
The measure word is usually either 道 or 套. A "套手续" means a complete set of formalities.

~
地区
As indicated by the given definition, this is not necessarily an official administrative region. It can just be a vaguely defined geographical area.

~
日期
This word refers to the date of something, not the day itself. The word for the day itself is simply called "日" (rì).

~
娶
This is the male perspective word for marriage. The female counterpart is 嫁 (jià).

~
太太
When this word is used on its own, it can also mean "your wife" or "his wife".

~
报道
A similar word is 报告 (bàogào). 报道 means "to report something on the news". 报告 means "to report something to one's superiors".

~
面对
This word means to physically face something. It does not have the same metaphorical meanings as "face" in English.

~
念
This word means "to miss someone" or "to think about someone you're not with". A similar word is 想 (xiǎng). The word 念 is usually used in more literary contexts.

~
克
The second meaning (to be able to, to overcome) has similar meaning to both 克服 (kèfú) and 战胜 (zhànshèng). 克服 implies that some undesirable part of yourself is being restrained, e.g. 克服困难. 战胜 implies that there's an external opponent which needs to be overcome, e.g. 战胜敌人. 克 is in between these two, but perhaps slightly more similar to 克服 than to 战胜.

~
不见得
This is a relatively colloquial word, similar to 不一定.

~
幅
This measure word is generally used for artistic pieces like paintings and calligraphy. However, recently some people have started using it for online images as well, although technically speaking this is incorrect usage.

~
以及
This is quite formal. A less formal equivalent is simply "和" (hé).

~
遵守
This is a somewhat formal word. A related word is 尊守 (zūnshǒu). The two words have basically the same meaning, but the first is more common in PRC, whereas the second is more common in Taiwan.

~
押金
This word can also be written as "押金".

~
处理
This has various meanings, including: to punish; to deal with a situation; and to sell things at a reduced price.

~
猴子
This word is often used to refer to "clever but naughty children". It can be also be used in this metaphorical sense even when speaking about adults.

~
空闲
This can refer to free time, a vacant room, or an unused piece of equipment.

~
受伤
This is mainly used to describe physical injuries. Mental harm is more accurately described as "心灵受伤" (xīnlíng shòushāng).

~
个人
When used as a pronoun on its own, it means "me".

~
充满
This emphasizes a container being completely full to the point of overflowing.

~
称呼
There are two closely related words: 称呼 (chēnghu) and 称号 (chēnghào). 称呼 is the more general word, simply meaning "form of address". 称号 means a more official title, e.g. "chairman".

~
因而
This word is quite formal.

~
驾驶
This is the general term for operating any type of vehicle, including cars, boats and airplanes. The equivalent of the English word "drive" is 开车 (kāichē), but this is only for cars.

~
具体
This word is similar to the English words "concrete", "specific", and "detailed". A similar word is 详细 (xiángxì), but this emphasizes that many small details are provided, whereas 具体 simply means that something is not vague or abstract.

~
丑
This word can also be used to describe undesirable non-physical things, e.g. "ugly behavior".

~
追
This word has the meaning of "retroactively" or "posthumously" only in certain set phrases, such as "追认" and "追封".

~
日常
This word implies something is normal or usual, e.g. 日常生活. It does *not* imply something happens every single day.

~
尤其
This word is similar to "especially" in English. A related word is 特别 (tèbié). 尤其 emphasizes a certain item in a list over all the other items. 特别 usually just singles something out as special without comparing it with anything else.

~
样式
Often used together with 款式 (kuǎnshì). 款式 is more about the overall design or model, while 样式 is about the specific style, including things like color and size.  You can think of 款式 as being at a higher level than 样式.

~
花生
Be careful of the tones! 花 (huā, first tone) means flower, while 花 (huà, fourth tone) is spend money. 生 (shēng, first tone) means life, give birth, etc., while 生 (shèng, fourth tone) is an adjective meaning uncooked, unfamiliar, etc.

~
中介
中介 can be both a noun and a verb.  As a noun, it means "intermediary," "agent" or "agency."  As a verb, it means "to mediate."

~
飘
Note that the meaning "complacent" or "frivolous" is somewhat rare and literary. You probably won't hear it used that way often in modern speech.

~
威胁
This word has negative connotations.  Don't use it in neutral contexts.

~
淘气
Mostly used to describe children.

~
射
All the meanings of 射 come from the idea of something being propelled outward. The meaning "allude to" is literary.

~
中心
Be careful of the tones! 中 (zhōng, first tone) means middle, center, hit the mark, while 中 (zhòng, fourth tone) is used for many words including "kind," "seed," "race," and "hit with a weapon or object."

~
火柴
Remember that when counting 火柴, the measure word 根 (gēn) is for individual matches, while 盒 (hé) is for boxes of matches.

~
英雄
This word is quite formal.  A more colloquial word is 好汉 (hǎohàn).

~
整个
整个 can be used before or after a measure word, and both usages are valid. The pre-measure-word usage is more colloquial.

~
本质
本质 is often used in conjunction with 上 (shàng, on, above), i.e., 本质上.

~
骂
The related word 骂人 (màrén) has the same meaning.

~
预防
预防 means to *prevent* something from happening before it happens.  Don't confuse it with 预防针 (yùfángzhēn), which is an inoculation/vaccination *against* a disease.

~
推广
推广 is about expanding the scope of something's influence or usage, such as promoting a product or spreading an idea or practice. It suggests making something more widespread.

~
闻
The meaning "to smell" or "to sniff at" is pronounced wén (second tone). All other meanings are pronounced wén (fourth tone).

~
年纪
This word is usually used for older people. For children or young adults, you would usually say  年龄 (niánlíng).

~
去世
This is a respectful way to say someone has died, typically used for older people or those deserving respect. For less formal situations or younger individuals, 死亡 (sǐwáng) or other more colloquial terms might be appropriate.

~
耽误
耽误 implies a negative consequence or loss due to the delay.

~
通常
通常 suggests something happens most of the time but not always.  It's synonymous with 一般 (yībān).

~
糊涂
糊涂 is usually used for people, to describe their mental state.

~
仿佛
Often used with 好像 (hǎoxiàng). When using 仿佛, there is usually uncertainty about whether the apparent resemblance is accurate.

~
人物
This word has multiple meanings, depending on context. When referring to a person, it often emphasizes their social standing or significance.

~
中秋节
中秋节 is celebrated on the 15th day of the 8th lunar month, a time when the moon is considered to be at its fullest and brightest.  Traditional customs include eating mooncakes and gazing at the moon.

~
耳环
Be careful of the tones!  环 (huán, second tone) is a ring or loop.  On the other hand, 环 (huàn, fourth tone) means to surround or encircle.

~
智慧
This word often refers to deep understanding and insight, not just factual knowledge.

~
拍
This word has many meanings, all based on the basic concept of applying pressure with a flat object.

~
现实
Can be both a noun and an adjective.

~
命令
命令 implies an authoritative command that must be obeyed, usually from a superior to a subordinate.

~
胆小鬼
This is a derogatory term.  Use with caution.

~
嫁
Only use 嫁 for women. The equivalent for men is 娶 (qǔ).

~
群
Used for living things that gather together, including humans.

~
劝
劝 often suggests trying to get someone to change their mind or actions.

~
写作
写作 is the more formal way to say "to write" and usually refers to the composition of text.  A more colloquial synonym is 写 (xiě).

~
不得了
不得了 implies something serious, significant, or extraordinary, often with negative connotations but sometimes positive, especially when expressing excitement or surprise.

~
被子
Measure word is 床 (chuáng), referring to the bed the quilt is used on, not the quilt itself.

~
哎
哎 (āi) has many meanings and uses. It can express surprise, disappointment, or agreement, be used to call someone, or simply as a filler word. The specific meaning is determined by context and intonation.

~
建设
建设 is a broad term, often used for infrastructure projects or other development efforts, with a focus on creating something new.

~
失眠
This term refers to difficulty falling asleep or staying asleep. It can be temporary or chronic.

~
恶劣
This word has strongly negative connotations. Avoid using it in neutral contexts.

~
桃
桃 can also refer to the color peach, similar to 粉红色 (fěn hóng sè).

~
提纲
The use of 提纲 (tígāng) is just like "outline" in English.  提纲 is often used to describe the main points of a speech, presentation, or academic essay.  提纲 (tígāng) is often used in conjunction with挈领 (qièlǐng) to form the idiom 提纲挈领 (tígāng qièlǐng), which means "to summarize the main points."

~
利润
There is no difference between 利润 in Chinese and "profit" in English.

~
目前
目前 (mùqián) is more formal than 現在 (xiànzài).

~
涨
When referring to prices or rivers swelling, there's no difference between 涨 (zhǎng) and the English equivalent.  However, 涨 can also refer to one's face becoming red due to anger or embarrassment.  For example, 他的脸涨得通红 (Tā de liǎn zhǎng dé tōnghóng) means "His face turned bright red."

~
公主
There is no difference between 公主 (gōngzhǔ) in Chinese and "princess" in English.

~
周到
周到 (zhōudào) emphasizes attentiveness to detail and ensuring everything is taken care of, often in the context of hospitality or service.  It goes beyond simple consideration and suggests a high level of care and anticipation of needs.

~
相关
相关 (xiāngguān) is more formal than 有关 (yǒuguān).

~
兑换
兑换 (duìhuàn) implies a formal exchange, often involving currencies or vouchers.  It's not typically used for casual swaps or trades.

~
等于
等于 (děngyú) can also be used metaphorically to mean "tantamount to" or "equivalent to" (in a figurative sense). For instance, 沉默等于同意 (chénmò děngyú tóngyì) means "Silence is equivalent to agreement."

~
木头
Calling someone 木头 (mùtóu) is a lighthearted way of teasing them for being slow or unresponsive, like calling someone a "blockhead". It is not generally offensive, especially when joking around with friends. Note that it is informal, colloquial and casual, and therefore should be reserved for informal and casual contexts.


~
批准
批准 (pīzhǔn) is typically used for formal approvals by authorities, governments, or organizations. It has a more official connotation than 同意 (tóngyì).

~
汽油
汽油 (qìyóu) is simply the standard term for gasoline in Chinese.

~
布
布 (bù) primarily means "cloth."  Its other meanings, "to declare/announce/spread/make known," are less common in modern usage.

~
递
递 (dì) is the general word for "to hand over."  The progressive meaning is mainly seen in set phrases like 递增 (dìzēng - progressively increase) or 递减 (dìjiǎn - progressively decrease).

~
碰
碰 (pèng) can also mean "to run into" someone unexpectedly or "to encounter" a problem.  It doesn't always imply a physical collision.

~
亮
亮 (liàng) can also be used as a verb meaning "to reveal" or "to display," as in 亮出你的证件 (liàng chū nǐ de zhèngjiàn) - "Show your ID."

~
配合
配合 (pèihé) often carries the sense of collaboration towards a common goal.  It can be used in a wide range of contexts, from teamwork in a project to the synergy between different parts of a machine.

~
合影
合影 (héyǐng) specifically refers to a group photo, not just any photograph.

~
煤炭
煤炭 (méitàn) refers specifically to coal as a fuel source. It is not usually used metaphorically.

~
滴
滴 (dī) can also be used as a measure word for small quantities of liquid, like a drop.

~
工人
工人 (gōngrén) generally refers to blue-collar workers, laborers, or factory workers. It may not be suitable for white-collar professionals.

~
赶紧
赶紧 (gǎnjǐn) expresses a sense of urgency, like "hurry up!" or "do it quickly!"

~
盆
盆 (pén) can have various meanings depending on context, from a basin for washing to a flower pot. The specific meaning is usually clear from context.

~
抓
抓 (zhuā) can also have a more abstract meaning of "to grasp" or "to seize," as in 抓住机会 (zhuā zhù jīhuì) - "to seize the opportunity."

~
主人
主人 (zhǔrén) also means "owner" in a more general sense and "host".

~
核心
核心 (héxīn) can be used metaphorically to describe the most important part or central idea of something.

~
眉毛
眉毛 (méimao) - there is no notable difference compared to "eyebrow" in English.

~
简直
简直 (jiǎnzhí) is used for emphasis, similar to "simply" or "really."  It often expresses surprise or disbelief.

~
时差
时差 (shíchā) can also refer to "jet lag," the fatigue and disorientation caused by crossing multiple time zones.

~
记忆
记忆 (jìyì) can be used as both a noun (memory) and a verb (to remember).

~
优惠
优惠 (yōuhuì) often refers to discounts or special offers, especially in a commercial context.

~
多余
多余 (duōyú) can also have a slightly negative connotation, implying something is not only unnecessary but also burdensome or in the way.

~
平衡
平衡 (pínghéng) can also be used metaphorically to describe a state of harmony or stability in various aspects of life, not just physical balance.

~
集体
集体 (jítǐ) emphasizes the group as a whole, often in a collaborative or unified context.

~
摄影
摄影 (shèyǐng) encompasses both still photography and cinematography (shooting movies).

~
疼爱
疼爱 (téng'ài) specifically denotes love combined with care and tenderness, often used for familial affection.

~
居然
居然 (jūrán) expresses surprise or disbelief, often with a negative connotation, suggesting something unexpected or even unwelcome has happened.

~
政治
政治 (zhèngzhì) can also be used as an adjective meaning "political."

~
丝绸
丝绸 (sīchóu) refers specifically to silk fabrics, not just silk in general.

~
病毒
No additional notes.

~
球迷
A more general word for "fan" (of anything, not just sports) is 粉丝 (fěnsī).  While 球迷 is specifically for sports fans, 粉丝 can be used for fans of movies, music, celebrities, etc.  It literally means "powdered silk," referring to how closely fans follow their idols.

~
甲
While 甲 can mean "first," it's usually used in more formal or technical contexts, like rankings or contracts.  For everyday use, 第一 (dì yī) is more common.  Also, note that when referring to nails (fingernails or toenails), 指甲 (zhǐjia) is used for fingernails and 脚趾甲 (jiǎozhǐjia) is used for toenails.

~
账户
This can refer to any type of account, not just bank accounts.  It includes online accounts, email accounts, social media accounts, etc.  For specifically a bank account, you can use 银行账户 (yínháng zhànghù).

~
宾馆
This word usually refers to a larger, more formal hotel, as opposed to smaller guesthouses or inns.  For a smaller lodging, you might use 招待所 (zhāodàisuǒ) or 旅馆 (lǚguǎn).

~
命运
No additional notes.

~
表面
Besides its literal meaning of "surface," 表面 can also be used figuratively to mean "superficial" or "outward appearance."  For example, 表面上他很平静 (biǎomiànshang tā hěn píngjìng) means "On the surface, he seems calm."

~
舍不得
This word implies a strong emotional attachment, making it difficult to part with something or someone. It goes beyond simple reluctance.  You might use it when talking about a beloved childhood toy or a close friend moving away.

~
落后
This word carries a negative connotation, implying inferiority or being outdated. It's often used in the context of economic or technological development.

~
保留
When used in the context of "having reservations," it implies doubt or uncertainty rather than a definite disagreement.

~
可见
This is an adverb used to draw a conclusion based on preceding evidence.  It's similar to "therefore," "thus," or "evidently" in English.

~
询问
This is a more formal way of saying "to ask" or "to inquire."  For casual conversations, 问 (wèn) is sufficient.

~
海关
No additional notes.

~
墙 (slang)
In the slang context of blocking websites, "被墙" (bèi qiáng) is the passive form, meaning "to be blocked by the Great Firewall." The active form, "墙" (qiáng), although less common, can also be used, meaning "to block (a website)."

~
闯
This word emphasizes a forceful or reckless action, often involving overcoming obstacles or difficulties.

~
培训
This word implies a more formal and structured training process, often involving professional development or skill acquisition.

~
热烈
This describes a high degree of enthusiasm or passion, often expressed openly and with excitement.

~
发抖
This can be due to cold, fear, or excitement.  The context will usually make the reason clear.

~
必要
This word emphasizes something essential or indispensable for achieving a particular goal or purpose.

~
反复
The meaning of 反复 changes depending on context.  Make sure to pay attention to the surrounding words to understand if it refers to repetition, instability, or the recurrence of an illness.

~
尊敬
This expresses a deep sense of respect and admiration, often towards elders or superiors.

~
划 (huá, to row) vs. 划 (huà, to draw/delimit)
Be aware of the different pronunciations and meanings. 划 (huá) means "to row" or "to paddle", and also carries the meaning of "profitable" or "worthwhile". On the other hand, 划 (huà) is used for drawing lines, delimiting boundaries, or planning.

~
到达
This is a more formal way to say "to arrive."  到 (dào) is more commonly used in everyday conversation.

~
惭愧
This conveys a feeling of shame or guilt for having done something wrong or falling short of expectations.

~
牛仔裤
No additional notes.

~
借口
This word carries a negative connotation, implying that the excuse is insincere or fabricated.

~
不耐烦
This describes a state of impatience and irritation, often due to delays or interruptions.

~
道理
This can refer to a logical principle, a moral justification, or simply the way things are.  It encompasses a broad range of meanings related to reason and understanding.

~
讽刺
This can range from gentle teasing to harsh criticism, depending on the context and intent.

~
滑
The meaning of 滑 (huá) can vary depending on the context. It can refer to the physical act of slipping, the texture of a surface being smooth, or someone being cunning or deceitful.

~
废话
This dismissive term suggests that the words spoken are meaningless, irrelevant, or even annoying.

~
前途
This refers to someone's future prospects, especially in terms of career or personal development.

~
迎接
This implies actively going out to meet or receive someone or something, often with a sense of anticipation or preparation.

~
舅舅
No additional notes.

~
资格
This refers to the official right or permission to do something, often based on qualifications or experience.

~
目录
No additional notes.

~
彼此
This emphasizes mutuality or reciprocity between two or more parties.

~
拥抱
This refers to a warm and affectionate embrace, often conveying comfort, support, or love.

~
挡
This verb emphasizes obstructing or hindering something. It can also mean "to shift gears (in a vehicle)". The simplified character 挡 is more commonly used than the traditional form 擋.

~
砍
While 砍 usually refers to chopping or cutting down, it can also colloquially mean to drastically reduce a price or to remove someone from a list or group.

~
应付
This word has a negative connotation, implying that the speaker is dealing with something perfunctorily or insincerely, or that they are barely managing to cope.

~
指导
A more colloquial synonym is 指点 (zhǐdiǎn).

~
造成
This is a very formal way of saying "to cause." More colloquial words include 引起 (yǐnqǐ) and 导致 (dǎozhì).

~
难怪
This word can stand alone as an interjection, or it can be followed by a clause explaining the reason for the surprise. For example:

难怪！ (No wonder!)

难怪他今天看起来很累。(No wonder he looks tired today.)

~
凭
This word has many meanings. As a preposition, it means "on the basis of" or "by means of." It also has the idiomatic meaning "no matter (how, what, etc.)" when placed before a question word, e.g., 凭什么 (píng shénme) "no matter what; why on earth."

~
光明
This word has the figurative meaning of "bright prospects."

~
奇迹
This word has the figurative meaning of an impressive achievement that was unexpected.

~
披
This word emphasizes the draping or covering aspect, often with loose or flowing material. For example, 披着毯子 (pī zhe tǎnzi) "wrapped in a blanket."

~
大象
Unlike English, the Chinese word for elephant contains the explicit meaning "big."

~
制度
Note that this word only refers to systems of rules or practices. It does not include electronic or mechanical systems.

~
强调
This word has a stronger emphasis than just simply "to mention." It implies that the speaker is giving special importance or weight to something.

~
思想
This word encompasses both individual thoughts and broader ideologies. It can refer to a specific idea or a whole system of beliefs.

~
一致
When used to describe opinions or views, 一致 emphasizes the lack of disagreement or conflict. It doesn't necessarily mean everyone actively agrees, but rather that there is no opposition.

~
编辑
This can be both a noun and a verb.

~
教材
This refers specifically to materials used for structured learning, like textbooks or workbooks.

~
如今
如今 is more formal than 現在 (xiànzài).

~
能源
This term broadly refers to any source of power or energy.

~
鼠标
This is a relatively recent word, coined for the computer mouse. It literally translates to "hand mouse."

~
烂
This word can have both positive and negative connotations depending on the context. For food, it describes a desirable softness or tenderness. However, for other objects, it usually means "rotten" or "worn out."

~
掌握
This word goes beyond simply knowing something. It implies a deep understanding and the ability to apply that knowledge effectively. It's often used for skills or information.

~
亿
Be careful not to confuse this with 10,000 (万, wàn).

~
合理
This word signifies that something is appropriate, justifiable, or makes sense according to logic or reason.

~
日子
This word can refer to a specific date, but also to the general passage of time in one's life.

~
圈
圈 can be used as a verb meaning to encircle or enclose. It's also a measure word for circular or loop-like things.

~
烫
Besides the literal meaning of "hot," 烫 is also used for hair perming.

~
可怜
This word can mean both "pitiful" and "to pity." The specific meaning is determined by the context.

~
着凉
The most common structure is probably "V + 着凉了", e.g. "我游泳游着凉了" (wǒ yóuyǒng yóu zhe liáng le).

~
流泪
This is a formal way of saying "cry" and more specifically implies tears coming out rather than just the expression of sadness or making sound. A more colloquial way is 哭 (kū).

~
麦克风
This is a loanword from "microphone." The Chinese pronunciation closely mimics the English pronunciation.

~
扶
This word depicts a specific action of providing physical support to someone or something, usually to help them stand or walk.

~
化学
This refers to the science of chemistry, but can also be used as an adjective for "chemical."

~
鲜艳
This word emphasizes brightness and vividness of color, often implying a lively or eye-catching appearance.

~
兔子
There is no difference in usage between 兔子 and "rabbit" in English.


~
悲观
The opposite of 悲观 is 乐观 (lèguān, optimistic).

~
如何
如何 is slightly more formal than 怎么样 (zěnmeyàng, how).

~
输出
This word can be used both literally (e.g., exporting goods) and figuratively (e.g., outputting data).

~
拦
The most common structure is "Subj. + 拦 + Obj. + Location", e.g. "我在门口拦他"(wǒ zài ménkǒu lán tā).

~
规矩
规矩 has a wide range of meanings related to rules, customs, and proper behavior. It can refer to formal regulations as well as informal social conventions.

~
招待
This word implies a welcoming and hospitable treatment of guests or customers. It is more formal than 请客 (qǐngkè).

~
醉
This is the adjective form; the verb form is 喝醉 (hē zuì).

~
冻
For the meaning of "to feel very cold", a more common synonym is 寒冷 (hánlěng).

~
冷淡
When referring to a person's attitude, 冷淡 suggests indifference or aloofness, rather than outright hostility.  It implies a lack of warmth and enthusiasm.

~
胶水
This word is usually used to refer to clear-drying glue, and is less often used to refer to white glue.

~
油炸
油炸 is usually translated as "deep fry", but technically it encompasses both deep frying and pan frying.  If you want to be specific that something is deep-fried, you can say "深度油炸" (shēndù yóuzhá).

~
梨
梨 can also be used as a surname.

~
业务
When used to refer to one's work or area of expertise, 业务 can often be translated as "line of work" or "area of expertise."

~
消极
消极 behavior is not necessarily malicious. It can also describe a lack of initiative or motivation, or a general pessimism or negativity.

~
预报
预报 emphasizes the act of predicting or forecasting. A related word is 预测 (yùcè), which carries the nuance of conjecture or estimation based on data analysis.

~
生长
Be careful to use the correct pronunciation when referring to growing up (zhǎng dà) versus growing plants, hair, etc. (shēng zhǎng)

~
太极拳
This term refers to the full set of movements and principles of Tai Chi Chuan. If you are simply referring to the slow, flowing movements, you can use the more general term 太极 (tàijí).

~
逗
The colloquial usage of 逗 to mean "funny" is primarily used in northern China.  In other regions, 好笑 (hǎoxiào) or 有趣 (yǒuqù) are more common.

~
强烈
强烈 describes something forceful, intense, or extreme.  It can refer to emotions, desires, sensations, or even physical phenomena like light or sound.  It differs from other words for "strong" like 强大 (qiángdà), which denotes power or strength, or 坚强 (jiānqiáng), which describes resilience or fortitude.

~
军事
军事 is often used as an adjective, directly modifying a noun. e.g. 军事基地 (jūnshì jīdì) - military base; 军事力量 (jūnshì lìliàng) - military force

~
挥
揮 has many meanings, but is perhaps most commonly used in metaphorical phrases such as 揮手告别 (huīshǒu gàobié) - to wave goodbye and 揮之不去 (huīzhībùqù) - lingering; unforgettable.

~
滚
The usage of 滚 to mean "get lost!" is extremely rude and should be avoided unless you intend to be offensive.

~
分配
分配 implies a systematic and organized distribution of resources or tasks according to a plan or criteria.

~
背包
Don't get confused with 书包 (shūbāo), which is a schoolbag.

~
英俊
英俊 is typically used to describe male attractiveness.  The female equivalent is 美丽 (měilì) or 漂亮 (piàoliang).

~
国庆节
国庆节 refers specifically to the National Day of the People's Republic of China. Other countries have their own 国庆节, so be sure to clarify if there is any ambiguity.

~
比例
比例 refers to a quantitative relationship between two or more things, usually expressed as a ratio or percentage.

~
广场
广场 can refer to squares of any size, from small neighborhood squares to large city squares like Tiananmen Square.

~
歪
歪 is an adjective and does not mean "to sprain" in standard Mandarin. The meaning of "to sprain" is dialectal.

~
签
The character 签 has multiple pronunciations with different meanings. Be mindful of the context to determine the correct pronunciation.

~
甩
甩 emphasizes a forceful and decisive throwing motion, often with the intention of getting rid of something.

~
因素
因素 implies a contributing element or a cause that influences an outcome. It's often used in more formal contexts.

~
领导
Be aware of the different measure words used for 领导: 位 (wèi) is generally more respectful, while 个 (gè) is more neutral.

~
接近
接近 implies a nearness in space, time, or degree. It suggests that something is almost, but not quite, reaching a certain point.

~
拼音
While 拼音 is generally used to refer to the romanization system for Mandarin Chinese, it can also broadly refer to any phonetic transcription system.

~
照常
照常 implies adherence to a regular schedule or routine, despite any potential disruptions.

~
射击
射击 is usually used to refer to shooting with a gun.

~
寂寞
寂寞 describes a deep, emotional loneliness or isolation.  It differs from other words for "lonely," such as 孤独 (gūdú), which implies more of a physical or social isolation.

~
修改
修改 implies making relatively minor changes or corrections to something that already exists, like a document or a piece of code.

~
显示
显示 refers to making something visible or apparent, often through a visual display.

~
组合
组合 can be both a verb and a noun.  As a verb, it emphasizes the act of combining elements.  As a noun, it refers to the resulting combination or group.

~
超级
超级 is a very common prefix and is more flexible in its use than English "super-".

~
盼望
盼望 emphasizes a strong feeling of anticipation and hope for something positive to happen.  It carries a more emotional weight than 期待 (qīdài).

~
资金
资金 specifically refers to monetary resources, especially those used for investment or business operations.

~
打交道
打交道 implies ongoing interactions or dealings with someone or something, often in a professional or business context.

~
自私
自私 carries a strong negative connotation. It implies a disregard for the needs and feelings of others.

~
善于
善于 highlights a specific skill or talent.  It is often used with verbs or verb phrases that describe the particular area of expertise.

~
挣
挣 (zhèng) is often used interchangeably with 赚 (zhuàn) to mean "to earn money." However, there's a subtle difference. 挣 emphasizes the effort and labor involved in earning money, while 赚 focuses more on the profit or gain.  Think of 挣 as "to work for" and 赚 as "to profit from."

~
睁
睁 (zhēng) specifically refers to opening one's eyes.  For opening other things, like a door or a window, use 打开 (dǎkāi) or 开 (kāi).

~
委屈
委屈 (wěiqu) has a stronger connotation of "feeling wronged" or "suffering injustice" than simply feeling sad.  It implies that someone has been treated unfairly.

~
古典
古典 (gǔdiǎn) refers specifically to classical art, literature, or music, particularly from ancient Greece and Rome, or traditional Chinese styles.  It doesn't mean "old" in a general sense.

~
分手
分手 (fēnshǒu) primarily means "to break up" in a romantic context.  For other types of separations, use other verbs like 离开 (líkāi) or 分开 (fēnkāi).

~
全面
全面 (quánmiàn) emphasizes completeness and covering all aspects.  It's often used in formal contexts to describe something comprehensive or thorough.

~
煮
煮 (zhǔ) is a general term for cooking in boiling water.  More specific terms exist for other cooking methods, like frying (炒 chǎo), steaming (蒸 zhēng), or baking (烤 kǎo).

~
窄
窄 (zhǎi) can mean "narrow-minded" figuratively, but it's more commonly used to describe physical narrowness.

~
自从
自从 (zìcóng) is always followed by a time phrase indicating the starting point of an action or state.

~
狮子
Besides meaning "lion," 狮子 (shīzi) can also refer to the Shihtzu dog breed or the Leo astrological sign.  Context is key to understanding the intended meaning.

~
表明
表明 (biǎomíng) means "to make clear" or "to indicate." It's often used in formal writing or speeches.

~
秩序
秩序 (zhìxù) refers to an organized and regulated state, often in a social or public context.

~
姥姥
姥姥 (lǎolao) is a colloquial term for maternal grandmother, primarily used in northern China.  奶奶 (nǎinai) is the more common term.

~
决心
决心 (juéxīn) can be both a noun ("determination") and a verb ("to be determined").  As a verb, it often takes the form 下决心 (xià juéxīn), meaning "to make up one's mind."

~
罚款
罚款 (fákuǎn) refers specifically to a monetary penalty.

~
壶
壶 (hú) is a classifier for liquids contained in pots or bottles.

~
鼓舞
鼓舞 (gǔwǔ) emphasizes inspiring and motivating others.

~
省略
省略 (shěnglüè) is commonly used in grammar and writing to describe omitting words or phrases.

~
宿舍 and 卧室
宿舍 (sùshè) refers to a dormitory room or shared living space. 卧室 (wòshì) specifically means "bedroom."

~
平常
平常 (píngcháng) can mean both "ordinary" and "usually."

~
嗯
嗯 (ēn, ng, ń) has several pronunciations and meanings depending on the tone and context. It can be an affirmative response, a sound of agreement, or a noncommittal grunt.

~
犹豫
犹豫 (yóuyù) implies hesitation due to uncertainty or indecision.

~
不如
不如 (bùrú) can be used for comparison ("not as good as") or to suggest an alternative ("it would be better to").

~
姑姑
姑姑 (gūgu) refers to one's father's sister.

~
遗憾
遗憾 (yíhàn) implies a sense of disappointment or regret over something that didn't happen or wasn't as expected.

~
咨询
咨询 (zīxún) implies seeking professional or expert advice.

~
摔倒
摔倒 (shuāidǎo) specifically means to fall to the ground.

~
硬件
硬件 (yìngjiàn) refers to computer hardware.

~
建立
建立 (jiànlì) implies creating something new or establishing a foundation.

~
形式
形式 (xíngshì) refers to the outward appearance or form of something, often contrasting with the content or substance.

~
部门
部门 (bùmén) refers to a division or section of an organization.

~
痒
