痒 (yǎng) can be both a physical sensation (itching) and a figurative one (eagerness to do something).

~
书架
书架 (shūjià) specifically refers to a bookshelf.

~
浏览
浏览 (liúlǎn) implies skimming or quickly looking through something, like a website or a document.

~
蛋糕
蛋糕 is typically measured using 块 (kuài), but can also be measured with 个 (gè)

~
搜索
搜索 (sōusuǒ) implies a thorough search.

~
嘉宾
嘉宾 (jiābīn) refers to a distinguished or honored guest, often at a formal event.

~
传染
传染 (chuánrǎn) refers to the spread of infectious diseases.

~
优美
优美 (yōuměi) describes something graceful, elegant, and aesthetically pleasing, often related to art, music, or literature.

~
宣布
A similar word is 宣告 (xuāngào).  宣布 is more general and can be used for any kind of announcement, big or small, formal or informal. 宣告 is more formal and often used for important or official pronouncements, declarations, or proclamations.  It often implies a sense of finality or authority.

~
电台
While this can refer to a transmitter-receiver, it most commonly refers to a radio station.

~
妇女
This term refers to a married woman, and is sometimes considered a bit dated.  A more neutral term is 女性 (nǚxìng).

~
姑娘
姑娘 originally referred to unmarried young women. However, in modern usage, it has broadened to include any young woman, regardless of marital status. In some northern dialects, 姑娘 is a general term for women. It's also used as a polite form of address for young women, similar to "miss" or "young lady" in English.  However, it can feel somewhat old-fashioned to younger generations in urban areas.  It carries less potential for misinterpretation in rural areas or when used by older generations.

~
嗓子
While the primary meaning of 嗓子 is “throat,” it's very commonly used to refer to one's voice, particularly in the context of singing or speaking. For example,  好嗓子 (hǎo sǎngzi) means "a good voice."

~
商品
This refers specifically to commercially available goods or merchandise, not just any item.

~
拐弯
拐弯 literally means "to turn a corner," but it can also figuratively mean "a new direction," especially in the context of changing one's life or career path.

~
出示
This emphasizes the act of taking something out and presenting it for inspection, often in a formal context like showing identification or a document.

~
竹子
Note the various measure words depending on the form of bamboo being referenced.  棵 is used for the whole bamboo plant. 支 is for a stalk or branch of bamboo, and 根 is for a piece or length of bamboo.

~
组成
This implies that parts come together to form a whole.  It's not the same as 建立 (jiànlì) which means to establish or found something new.

~
决赛
This specifically refers to the final round of a competition, not just any important match.

~
灰尘
灰尘 specifically refers to dust, while 灰 (huī) can mean ash or dust.

~
升
Be aware of the multiple meanings and pronunciations of this character.

~
除非
This word sets up a necessary condition.  The structure is 除非...才....  The first clause is the only condition under which the second clause can happen.

~
执照
This refers to an official license or permit issued by an authority.

~
破坏
This carries a stronger connotation of damage or destruction than 打破 (dǎ pò), which simply means "to break."

~
粗糙
When referring to a person's manner or behavior, 粗糙 implies rudeness or lack of refinement.

~
喜剧
Remember the measure word for 喜剧 is 部 or 出.

~
逃
逃 usually suggests fleeing from a dangerous or unpleasant situation.  It's more intense than just leaving or going away.

~
损失
损失 specifically refers to loss or damage of material possessions, resources, or economic value.  It's not typically used for emotional loss or grief.

~
接待
This typically refers to the formal reception of guests, visitors, or clients in a professional or official capacity.

~
饮料
This word specifically refers to all kinds of beverages, unlike 水 (shuǐ), which just means water.

~
用途
This refers to the purpose or function of something, not just how it's used.

~
牙齿
Note the measure word is 颗, not 个.

~
除夕
This specifically refers to Lunar New Year’s Eve, not New Year’s Eve in general.

~
叉子
Remember the measure word is 把.

~
催
This implies repeated urging or prompting, often with a sense of impatience.

~
体会
体会 emphasizes understanding something deeply through personal experience, often involving reflection and internalization.

~
平安
This conveys a sense of overall well-being, safety, and peace.  It's a common greeting, especially during holidays.

~
吸取
This often refers to absorbing knowledge, lessons, or insights, but it can also refer to physical absorption.

~
创造
This emphasizes the creation of something entirely new or original.  It's more significant than just making or producing something.

~
生动
This implies a vividness and liveliness that captures attention and interest.

~
实话
This emphasizes that something is the truth, often implying that it might be unpleasant or difficult to hear.

~
蛇
Remember the measure word is 条.

~
基本
This word indicates something fundamental or essential, forming the basis of something else.

~
输入
This can refer to both importing goods and inputting data into a computer.

~
紫
This refers to a range of purplish colors, from violet to a deep reddish-purple.

~
人事
This word has several meanings, from personnel matters to the complexities of human relationships, and even a euphemism for sexuality.  Pay attention to context.

~
交往
This implies ongoing interaction and connection with others, often with a sense of mutual exchange or relationship building.  It's broader than just meeting or talking to someone.

~
逃避
This emphasizes avoiding something unpleasant or challenging, often with a sense of guilt or irresponsibility.  It's stronger than just avoiding something.

~
则
The most common meaning of 则 is simply "then" in Classical Chinese.  It's often paired with "若" (ruò, "if").  For example, 若…则… (ruò...zé...) means "if...then...".  In modern Chinese, it's mostly seen as a measure word for writings or articles (e.g., 一篇文章 (yī piān wénzhāng) - one article).

~
亲切
This describes a feeling of warmth, closeness, and familiarity, often implying a sense of care and concern.  It's stronger than just being friendly (友好 - yǒuhǎo). It suggests a deeper bond, like between family members or close friends.

~
企业
Remember the measure word for 企业 is 家 (jiā).  This measure word is commonly used for establishments like companies, restaurants, and hotels.

~
干燥
干燥 can be used for both concrete dryness (like dry weather or soil) and abstract dryness (like a dull or boring presentation).  Be mindful of the context.

~
连续
This emphasizes an uninterrupted sequence.  Don't confuse it with 继续 (jìxù), which means to continue something that may have been paused.

~
自愿
This highlights the willingness and initiative of the actor.  It's often used to contrast with 被迫 (bèipò) - forced, or compulsory.

~
地震
Just a note: 地震 can also be used as a verb, meaning "to have an earthquake."

~
主张
主张 implies actively promoting and supporting a particular viewpoint.  It's stronger than simply having an opinion (意见 - yìjiàn).

~
爱惜
This suggests cherishing something and treating it with care to prevent damage or loss.  It's a deeper feeling than just liking something.

~
缺乏
缺乏 implies a deficiency or shortage of something essential.  It's stronger than simply not having something (没有 - méiyǒu).

~
赶快
This emphasizes urgency.  It's stronger than  快 (kuài) alone.

~
婚姻
Remember the measure words for 婚姻 are 桩 (zhuāng) and 次 (cì). 桩 is used for counting instances of marriage, while 次 counts the number of times someone has been married.

~
豆腐
A useful phrase to know is “吃豆腐” (chī dòufu) -  to flirt with or take advantage of someone (usually a woman), often through inappropriate touching or suggestive remarks.  It doesn't literally mean “to eat tofu.”

~
雾
Pay attention to the measure words: 场 (cháng) is used for a period of fog, while 阵 (zhèn) refers to a burst or instance of fog.

~
称
称 has many meanings. Be aware of its polysemy. As a verb, it can mean "to weigh" or "to call."  It can also function as a noun meaning “name” or “appellation.”  It’s related to, but distinct from, 秤 (chèng), which specifically means "scale."

~
抢
抢 implies a forceful or hasty taking of something.  It often involves competition or a sense of urgency.

~
假设
This is used for hypothetical situations and conjectures.  It's more formal than  如果 (rúguǒ) - "if."

~
中旬
Specifically refers to days 11-20 of the month.

~
领域
This refers to a specific area of expertise, study, or activity.  It's more specialized than  范围 (fànwéi) - scope or range.

~
发明
发明 refers to creating something entirely new.  Don't confuse it with 发现 (fāxiàn) - to discover.

~
打喷嚏
Remember to use the verb 打 (dǎ) with 喷嚏 (pēntì).

~
属于
This denotes belonging to a group, category, or owner.  It can also indicate possession.

~
成分
This can refer to both the physical components of something and a person's social background or status.

~
后背
This specifically refers to the back of the body.  It's more specific than  后面 (hòumiàn) - behind.

~
高跟鞋
Just a note:  鞋 (xié) is always plural when referring to a pair of shoes.

~
小气
This can refer to both stinginess with money and a narrow-minded or petty attitude.

~
疑问
疑问 signifies uncertainty or doubt requiring clarification.  It’s a noun form, distinct from the verb  怀疑 (huáiyí) - to suspect.

~
种类
This refers to a distinct type or category within a larger group.  It emphasizes the differences between groups.

~
抽屉
Often used metaphorically.  For example, 把这件事放在抽屉里 (bǎ zhè jiàn shì fàng zài chōutì lǐ) - "to put this matter aside."

~
保险
This word functions as both a noun (insurance) and a verb (to insure) and an adjective (safe, secure, bound to).

~
巧妙
This implies ingenuity and skillfulness.  It's more than just clever (聪明 - cōngmíng).

~
屋子
This term is more colloquial and intimate than  房子 (fángzi), which is a more general term for house or building.

~
形势
形势 refers to the overall state of affairs or the current situation, often with implications for future developments.  It's more dynamic than  情况 (qíngkuàng) - situation or circumstance.

~
朗读
This refers to reading aloud clearly and expressively, often with attention to pronunciation and intonation. It's different from simply reading aloud.

~
鼻子
Besides its literal meaning, 鼻子 can also mean "sense of smell."  It’s also used in idioms, like  碰鼻子 (pèng bízi) - to run into trouble.

~
清淡
Regarding food, this describes a light, mild flavor.  It can also describe slack business sales.

~
握手
This is both a literal and figurative expression.  Figuratively, it can mean "to make peace" or "to reach an agreement."

~
制造
制造 implies producing something tangible, often on a large scale.  It's different from  做 (zuò) - to make or do.

~
虚心
This describes a humble and open-minded attitude receptive to learning and feedback.  It's an important quality in Confucian thought.

~
办理
This is often used in formal contexts, such as handling official procedures or business transactions. It carries a more formal tone than 做 (zuò) or 办 (bàn).

~
上当
上当 is usually followed by 了.

~
吓
吓 can be used as a verb, in which case it is usually followed by a complement like 一跳 (yītiào, to give a jump) or 一大跳 (yī dà tiào, to give a big jump). It can also be used as an interjection, in which case it can stand alone, but is sometimes followed by 人 (rén, people).

~
剪刀
A similar word is 剪子 (jiǎnzi). There is no difference in meaning, but 剪刀 is more common in the north of China, whereas 剪子 is more common in the south.

~
魅力
魅力 describes a more intrinsic, natural kind of attractiveness, while 迷人 (mírén) refers to something or someone that actively attracts attention and admiration. For example, a charismatic leader might be said to have 魅力, while a flashy sports car or an enchanting performer might be described as 迷人.

~
否认
否认 emphasizes the act of contradicting or rejecting a statement or accusation, often with a formal or official tone. On the other hand, 不承认 (bùchéngrèn) focuses on the lack of acknowledgement or acceptance of something, which can be due to various reasons, including ignorance or unwillingness to admit.

~
蹲
蹲 is usually used with some sort of location following. For instance, 蹲在家里 (dūn zài jiālǐ), or 蹲在办公室 (dūn zài bàngōngshì).

~
恭喜
恭喜 is often paired with 发财 (fācái), especially during Chinese New Year. Together, they form the expression 恭喜发财 (gōngxǐfācái), which means "Congratulations and be prosperous."  On its own, 恭喜 is often used for congratulating someone on a happy event like a wedding, birth, or promotion.

~
唯一
A similar word is 独一无二 (dúyīwú'èr). Both words emphasize singularity and exclusivity. However, 唯一 is often used in formal contexts to describe something that is essential or indispensable. On the other hand, 独一无二 conveys a stronger sense of uniqueness and irreplaceability, often used to describe something or someone truly special or exceptional.

~
佩服
佩服 is quite formal. A more colloquial way to express admiration is 挺佩服的 (tǐng pèifú de).

~
瞎
瞎 is a very versatile word with diverse usages. When combined with verbs like 说 (shuō), 想 (xiǎng), or 搞 (gǎo), it often conveys a sense of groundlessness or recklessness. For example, 瞎说 (xiāshuō) means to talk nonsense, 瞎想 (xiāxiǎng) means to let one's imagination run wild, and 瞎搞 (xiāgǎo) means to mess around or act foolishly.

~
月饼
Different fillings exist depending on the region of China. In Beijing, the most common fillings are red bean paste and lotus seed paste. In the south of China, egg yolks are often placed in the middle.

~
随身
随身 is usually used with the word 携带 (xiédài) or some equivalent expression. It might be combined, for instance with a bag of some sort, such as 随身小包 (suíshēn xiǎobāo, small personal bag).

~
抽象
抽象 is typically associated with concepts or ideas removed from concrete reality.  On the other hand, 概括 (gàikuò) refers to a more general summary or synthesis of information, without necessarily losing its connection to the concrete.  Consider 抽象 as dealing with the realm of pure thought, while 概括 helps to organize and simplify existing knowledge.

~
香肠
香肠 comes in many varieties in China, including 腊肠 (làcháng, preserved sausage), which is a dried, cured sausage often enjoyed during Chinese New Year, and 血肠 (xuěcháng, blood sausage), a type of sausage made with animal blood.

~
喊
喊 usually suggests a loud, forceful vocalization aimed at attracting attention or conveying urgency. It carries a stronger sense of urgency or alarm compared to 叫 (jiào), which is a more general term for calling out or making a sound.

~
实验
Although 次 (cì) is the given measure word, 个 (gè) is also very commonly used.

~
吹
吹 has a wide range of meanings, some of which are idiomatic, such as 吹牛 (chuīniú, to brag or boast), which literally means "to blow a cow".

~
外公
In some parts of China, the term used might be 姥爷 (lǎoye).

~
成立
成立 typically refers to the establishment of something substantial or enduring, like an organization, company, or theory. On the other hand, 建立 (jiànlì) has a broader scope, encompassing the creation or construction of things that can be both concrete or abstract, like buildings, relationships, or systems.

~
岛屿
A similar word is 海岛 (hǎidǎo). 岛屿 is the more formal term, while 海岛 is more colloquial.  Another word is 群岛 (qúndǎo, archipelago).

~
庆祝
庆祝 usually implies public or shared rejoicing and often involves ceremonies, rituals, or other forms of communal expression.  On the other hand, 庆贺 (qìnghè) is more formal and traditional, often associated with official events or significant life milestones.

~
撞
撞 often implies a forceful or accidental impact, whereas 碰 (pèng) describes a lighter or more incidental contact.  Another word, 击 (jī), specifically refers to hitting or striking something forcefully and intentionally.

~
确定
确定 emphasizes the state of being firmly established or decided, while 决定 (juédìng) highlights the act of making a decision or setting a course of action.  For example, 确定日期 means "the date is fixed", while 决定日期 means "to decide on a date."

~
干脆
干脆 can be used as an adjective, meaning direct and to the point. Or it can be used as an adverb, indicating that one might as well take a certain course of action.

~
瞧
瞧 carries a sense of casual observation, often implying a quick or cursory glance.  It's more informal and less intense than 看 (kàn), which is a general term for looking or watching.

~
空间
空间 is more associated with physical or measurable extents, while 余地 (yúdì) focuses on the availability of freedom or flexibility within certain limitations.  For example, 空间 might describe the area of a room, while 余地 refers to room for negotiation or compromise.

~
答应
答应 indicates a positive response to a request or demand, often involving a commitment or obligation.  On the other hand, 回答 (huídá) is a more general term for providing a response, not necessarily affirmative, to a question or inquiry.

~
刻苦
刻苦 suggests diligent and persistent effort, often involving self-discipline and hardship.  It is somewhat formal. More colloquial expressions include 努力 (nǔlì) and hard-working, although they lack the nuance of overcoming hardship conveyed by 刻苦.

~
完美
完美 suggests an ideal state free from flaws or imperfections.  On the other hand, 完善 (wánshàn) focuses on the state of being complete or comprehensive, often involving the gradual improvement or refinement of something.

~
诚恳
诚恳 conveys a sincere and earnest attitude, often expressed through open and honest communication.  On the other hand, 真诚 (zhēnchéng) refers to a more fundamental quality of genuineness and authenticity, without necessarily implying an outward expression of earnestness.

~
模特
模特 comes from the English word "model."  It is typically used to refer to fashion models.

~
行人
行人 is the general term for pedestrians in China.  路过的人 (lùguò de rén), which literally translates to "people passing by," can be more descriptive and specific to those who happen to be passing by at a particular moment.

~
锁
锁 has a literary meaning of "old" in classical Chinese. In modern standard Chinese, this character is used with the pronunciation suǒ. But there is still a word 老锁 (lǎosuǒ), which refers to an old lock.

~
改进
改进 suggests making incremental changes or enhancements to something existing, while 改善 (gǎishàn) refers to making broader or more substantial improvements, often to conditions or circumstances.

~
鼓掌
鼓掌 can also be pronounced gǔzhǎng, although this is uncommon.

~
炒
炒 has various meanings. In cooking, it means to stir-fry. In finance, it means to speculate or hype up. In employment, it can mean to fire someone.

~
捐
The word 捐款 (juānkuǎn) specifically refers to making a monetary donation, often for charitable causes.

~
恋爱
恋爱 is typically used to describe romantic relationships.  On the other hand, 爱情 (àiqíng) is a broader and more abstract concept of love, encompassing romantic, familial, or platonic forms.

~
翅膀
翅膀 describes a bird's wing, while 翅膀 is a general word referring to something that extends off to the side of a main body. It can also metaphorically refer to somebody's assistant.

~
夹子
Different kinds of 夹子 include: 晒衣夹 (shàiyī jiā, clothespin) and 文件夹 (wénjiàn jiā, file folder).

~
推荐
Can be used as a noun or a verb.  When used as a noun, it means "recommendation". When used as a verb, it means "to recommend".


~
车厢
Remember that 节 is pronounced in the second tone (jié) when used as a measure word, but in the first tone (jiē) in other contexts.


~
玻璃
The slang use of 玻璃 to mean "male homosexual" is considered derogatory.


~
愿望
愿望 is a more formal way to express "wish" than 心愿 (xīnyuàn). 心愿 carries a more personal and heartfelt connotation.


~
玩具
There's no major difference between 玩具 (wánjù) and the English word "toy."


~
沙滩
The measure word 片 (piàn) is used for 沙滩 (shātān) because it emphasizes the expansive, flat nature of a beach.


~
声调
Be mindful of the tones themselves when pronouncing this word!  声 (shēng) is first tone, and 调 (diào) is fourth tone. 声调 refers specifically to the tones in tonal languages like Mandarin Chinese.


~
推辞
推辞 (tuīcí) implies politeness and tact in declining. It suggests offering an excuse or explanation, unlike simply refusing.  It's more formal than other ways of saying no.


~
完善
完善 (wánshàn) describes something complete and well-developed, often referring to systems or processes. It implies a high level of refinement and functionality.


~
告别
告别 (gàobié) is a more formal and sometimes more permanent way of saying goodbye than 再见 (zàijiàn). It can carry the weight of a final farewell.


~
悠久
悠久 (yōujiǔ) is typically used to describe abstract things like history, traditions, or culture, not physical objects. It emphasizes a long and continuous duration.


~
影子
The figurative meanings of 影子 (yǐngzi) – "hint," "indication," "influence" – often carry a slightly negative or suspicious connotation, suggesting something hidden or lurking.


~
以来
以来 (yǐlái) is used to indicate the period from a certain point in the past up to the present.  The structure is "[time] 以来".


~
迟早
迟早 (chízǎo) carries a sense of inevitability. It means something *will* happen, it's just a matter of when.


~
恢复
恢复 (huīfù) implies a return to a previous state, whether it be health, order, or a former practice.


~
方
方 (fāng) has a wide range of meanings and uses, making it important to pay attention to context.


~
印刷
印刷 (yìnshuā) usually refers to the mechanical process of printing, not handwriting or other forms of reproduction.


~
等待
等待 (děngdài) is more formal than 等 (děng).


~
重复
This entry seems to have a mistake. 重复 (chóngfù) means "to repeat" and is not a variant of itself.


~
戒
戒 (jiè) has multiple meanings, ranging from "to quit" a habit to "a ring" or "Buddhist monastic discipline."  Context is crucial.  The "quit" meaning is often seen in compounds like 戒烟 (jièyān) – to quit smoking.


~
血
While 血 (xuè) can be pronounced xiě colloquially, the standard pronunciation is xuè.


~
宁可
宁可 (nìngkě) expresses a preference for one option, even if it involves some disadvantage, over another option that might seem better on the surface.


~
车库
车库 (chēkù) refers specifically to a garage for cars, not other vehicles.


~
坚强
坚强 (jiānqiáng) describes mental and emotional strength, resilience in the face of adversity.


~
操心
操心 (cāoxīn) means "to worry about" and usually implies excessive worrying.


~
搞
搞 (gǎo) is a very versatile verb, but it's often used informally.  Be careful not to overuse it in formal contexts.


~
对手
对手 (duìshǒu) can refer to any kind of opponent, from a sports rival to a business competitor.


~
结实
结实 (jiēshi) can describe both physical sturdiness and a well-built physique.


~
派
派 (pài) can be tricky because it has several distinct meanings and pronunciations (pài and pāi). Be aware of the context.


~
名牌
名牌 (míngpái) can refer to a famous brand or a name tag/nameplate.  The meaning is usually clear from context.


~
至今
至今 (zhìjīn) highlights the continuing state of something from the past up to the present moment.


~
时期
时期 (shíqī) refers to a particular time period characterized by certain events or conditions.


~
晕
晕 (yūn) can describe the physical sensation of dizziness or a halo around the sun or moon. It can also mean feeling confused or overwhelmed, like "I'm dizzy with all this information".


~
感想
感想 (gǎnxiǎng) are thoughts and feelings based on personal experiences, often implying deeper reflection than simply thoughts.


~
活跃
活跃 (huóyuè) suggests energetic and enthusiastic participation or a lively atmosphere.


~
谈判
谈判 (tánpàn) implies a formal discussion between parties, often with conflicting interests, aimed at reaching an agreement.


~
轻视
轻视 (qīngshì) implies looking down on someone or something, considering them unimportant or inferior.


~
必然
必然 (bìrán) expresses certainty and inevitability, often due to logical or natural laws.


~
报到
报到 (bàodào) refers specifically to the act of reporting one's arrival, often for official purposes like starting a new job or checking into a hotel or conference.


~
急诊
急诊 (jízhěn) refers to emergency medical treatment, often in a dedicated emergency room setting.

~
均匀
Can be used to describe the distribution of something across a surface or within a volume. For example, you can say that the salt is 均匀地分布在汤里 (jūnyúnde fēnbù zài tāng lǐ) - "the salt is evenly distributed in the soup".

~
支
The measure word 支 (zhī) is a versatile classifier in Chinese, used for a variety of long, thin objects.  While commonly used for pens and guns, it also classifies other items like cigarettes, flowers (with stems), and even songs or musical pieces.

~
各自
各自 (gèzì) emphasizes individuality and separate actions within a group.  Think of it as highlighting that each member is doing something independently or has their own distinct role.

~
狡猾
狡猾 (jiǎohuá) carries a stronger negative connotation than "crafty" or "cunning" sometimes do in English. It often implies deceit and underhanded tactics.

~
退
退 (tuì) covers a wide range of "backward" movements, from physical retreat in battle to returning a purchased item.  It emphasizes the act of moving away or giving something back.

~
西装
西装 (xīzhuāng) specifically refers to Western-style suits, not just any Western clothing.  It's often used in formal settings or business contexts.

~
组
组 (zǔ) can refer to a group of people working together as a team, similar to "team" or "group" in English.  It also applies to sets or series of things, like batteries or a collection of items.

~
工厂
工厂 (gōngchǎng) refers to a factory or manufacturing plant, usually on a larger scale than a workshop or small production facility.

~
装饰
装饰 (zhuāngshì) can function as both a verb (to decorate) and a noun (decoration).  It encompasses both the act of decorating and the decorative elements themselves.

~
摩托车
摩托车 (mótuōchē) is a general term for motorcycles and motorbikes, including scooters and mopeds.  It's derived from "motor" and "cycle," reflecting the vehicle's nature.

~
嫩
嫩 (nèn) has various meanings, including "tender" (for food), "light" (for colors), and "inexperienced" (for people).  Its usage depends on the context.

~
绳子
绳子 (shéngzi) can refer to cords, strings, or ropes of various materials and thicknesses. It's a general term for flexible, linear materials used for tying or binding.

~
展开
展开 (zhǎnkāi) can be used figuratively, such as launching a project or initiative.  It implies a spreading out or unfolding of activities or plans.

~
突出
突出 (tūchū) describes something that stands out or is prominent, both physically and figuratively. It can refer to a protruding object or an outstanding achievement.

~
失业
失业 (shīyè) refers to the state of being unemployed or the act of losing one's job. It specifically relates to employment status.

~
杀
杀 (shā) can be used figuratively in certain contexts, like "杀价" (shājià), meaning "to haggle" or "to bargain." It implies a forceful or aggressive approach.

~
期间
期间 (qījiān) refers to a specific period or duration of time, often associated with an event or activity. It signifies a block of time within which something occurs.

~
娱乐
娱乐 (yúlè) encompasses a wide range of leisure activities, from entertainment and amusement to hobbies and recreational pursuits.

~
老板
老板 (lǎobǎn) is a general term for "boss" or "owner," often used in a business context. It can also be used respectfully to address someone older or in a position of authority.

~
根本
根本 (gēnběn) is often used for emphasis in negative sentences, meaning "absolutely not" or "not at all." It strengthens the negation and conveys a sense of certainty.

~
纪录
纪录 (jìlù) is the preferred term for "record" in Taiwan, except when used as a verb meaning "to record," where 记录 (jìlù) is used.  Be mindful of this regional difference.

~
报社
报社 (bàoshè) specifically refers to a newspaper company or news organization, not just the physical newspaper itself.

~
悄悄
悄悄 (qiāoqiāo) describes actions or sounds that are quiet and subtle, often implying secrecy or stealth. It emphasizes the low volume and discreet nature.

~
实现
实现 (shíxiàn) suggests making something real or concrete, often referring to achieving goals, fulfilling dreams, or bringing about desired outcomes.

~
本领
本领 (běnlǐng) refers to a specific skill or ability, often acquired through training or practice. It emphasizes competence and proficiency in a particular area.

~
珍惜
珍惜 (zhēnxī) implies a deep appreciation and value for something, often something rare or precious. It suggests cherishing and safeguarding something important.

~
捡
捡 (jiǎn) focuses on picking up something that has been dropped or discarded. It implies selecting and retrieving specific items.

~
钢铁
钢铁 (gāngtiě) refers to steel as a material, encompassing both iron and steel alloys. It's a broad term for ferrous metals used in construction and manufacturing.

~
出版
出版 (chūbǎn) refers specifically to the process of producing and distributing printed materials, like books, magazines, and newspapers.

~
耳朵
Aside from its primary meaning of "ear," 耳朵 (ěrduo) can also refer to handles on objects like cups, due to their similar shape and function.

~
堆
堆 (duī) can refer to both the action of piling things up and the resulting pile or heap itself. It suggests an unorganized or loosely arranged collection of items.

~
断
断 (duàn) has a range of meanings, including "to break," "to cut off," and "to judge." It can also be used for emphasis in negative sentences, similar to 根本 (gēnběn).

~
所
所 (suǒ) introduces relative clauses and passive voice constructions. It acts as a link between the clause and the noun it modifies, similar to relative pronouns in English.

~
戏剧
戏剧 (xìjù) encompasses various forms of theatrical performance, including drama, plays, and opera.  It refers to the art form itself, rather than a specific production.

~
常识
常识 (chángshí) refers to general knowledge and common sense, the basic understanding of everyday concepts and social norms.

~
宠物
宠物 (chǒngwù) refers to animals kept as companions, not just domesticated animals in general.  It implies a close relationship between the animal and its owner.

~
追求
追求 (zhuīqiú) suggests persistent effort in seeking or pursuing something, often a goal, ideal, or romantic interest. It implies dedication and determination.

~
歇
歇 (xiē) emphasizes taking a break or resting to recover from exertion. It suggests pausing an activity to regain energy or composure.

~
发言
发言 (fāyán) specifically refers to making a formal speech or statement, often in a public setting.  It implies a prepared or official address.

~
初级
初级 (chūjí) denotes a beginner or introductory level, often used in educational or skill-based contexts. It signifies the starting point of a learning process.

~
优势
A related word is 好处 (hǎochù). 好处 is more general and can refer to any kind of benefit or advantage, while 优势 specifically refers to a superior position or condition relative to others.  优势 often implies competition or comparison.  Think of 优势 as "competitive advantage".

~
信号
When referring to a phone signal, the measure word is 格 (gé).  For example, "My phone has one bar of signal" would be 我的手机只有一格信号 (wǒ de shǒujī zhǐyǒu yī gé xìnhào).

~
胜利
Besides 胜利 (shènglì), another word for "victory" is 成功 (chénggōng).  成功 is more general and can refer to success in any endeavor, while 胜利 specifically refers to winning a competition or battle.

~
零食
Often used with the verb 吃 (chī) - to eat.  For example,  吃零食 (chī língshí) means "to eat snacks."

~
彩虹
The most common way to refer to a rainbow is simply 彩虹, not 一道彩虹.  一道 emphasizes the shape or the appearance of a single, complete arc of a rainbow.

~
绕
绕 is often used in the sense of "to go around" or "to bypass." For giving directions in driving, however, 拐弯 (guǎiwān) is better.

~
公布
公布 is often used for official announcements, often by the government.  A more general word for "announce" is 宣布 (xuānbù).

~
无奈
无奈 describes a feeling of powerlessness or resignation in the face of a difficult situation. It carries a sense of acceptance of the undesirable situation, unlike words like 难受 (nánshòu - uncomfortable) or 痛苦 (tòngkǔ - painful), which express stronger negative emotions.

~
作品
Be careful not to confuse this word with 工作 (gōngzuò - work, job).

~
勤奋
Often used to describe students or employees, this word implies consistent hard work and dedication over time.

~
格外
格外 intensifies the adjective or verb it modifies. It emphasizes a degree beyond the usual or expected.

~
怪不得
This is an informal expression.  怪不得 is often followed by an explanation for a previously puzzling situation.

~
手套
The measure word 双 (shuāng) is more common than 只 (zhī) when referring to gloves in pairs. 只 is typically used when talking about a single glove.

~
宴会
This word evokes a more formal and grand occasion than simply a meal or party.  It often involves a large number of guests, elaborate food, and sometimes entertainment.

~
撕
The object of 撕 is usually something thin and flat like paper or cloth.  For tearing thicker or more substantial materials, other verbs like 扯 (chě - to rip) might be more appropriate.

~
吵
吵 can be both intransitive (to quarrel) and transitive (to disturb by making noise).  For example, 他们一直在吵架 (tāmen yīzhí zài chǎojià) - They kept quarreling, versus  别吵我! (bié chǎo wǒ!) - Don't disturb me!  The meanings are related, but slightly different.

~
汇率
Often paired with verbs like 升高 (shēnggāo - to rise) or 降低 (jiàngdī - to lower) to describe fluctuations.

~
模糊
Can be used both literally (e.g., a blurred image) and figuratively (e.g., a vague memory).

~
纪念
Can be both a verb (to commemorate) and a noun (souvenir, memento). The meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
陆续
Describes a sequential arrival or occurrence of things, not necessarily in a strictly ordered manner, but one after another.

~
面积
Refers specifically to the size of a surface or area.  Do not confuse this with 面子 (miànzi - face, reputation).

~
经营
Implies the management and operation of a business or enterprise, including aspects of planning, strategy, and financial management.  More complicated than just making something.

~
鞭炮
The sound of exploding firecrackers is often described with the onomatopoeia 噼里啪啦 (pīlipālā).

~
整体
Emphasizes wholeness and unity, considering something as a complete system rather than individual parts.

~
人类
This word can carry a connotation of human civilization and collective progress.

~
行动
Has a broader meaning than just physical movement. It can also refer to taking action, conducting operations, or behavior in general.

~
长辈
Shows respect for older people. Using this term demonstrates good manners in Chinese culture.

~
蜜蜂
Often associated with honey and beekeeping.

~
赔偿
Specifically refers to compensating for loss or damage, often financial.  More formal than other words for repaying money.

~
元旦
Marks the beginning of the Gregorian calendar year. Distinct from the traditional Chinese New Year (春节 - chūnjié).

~
装
This word has many meanings.  Pay attention to the context to determine the intended meaning.

~
干活儿
The 儿 (er) suffix adds a colloquial and informal tone.

~
激烈
Describes a high degree of intensity or vehemence.  Often used in contexts of competition, conflict, or debate.

~
紧急
Implies a need for immediate action or attention.  Often used in situations of danger or crisis.

~
软件
Refers specifically to computer software.  Don't confuse it with 硬件 (yìngjiàn - hardware).

~
胡说
Implies speaking carelessly, without regard for truth or accuracy.  Carries a negative connotation.

~
单元
Can refer to a unit within a larger structure, like a chapter in a book, a unit of measurement, or an entrance in a building.  Context is key.

~
看望
Implies visiting someone to check on their well-being, especially if they are sick or elderly.  More caring than just visiting.

~
吻
More formal and literary than 亲 (qīn - to kiss).

~
高档
Used to describe high-quality, expensive goods or services.  Often associated with luxury or prestige.

~
占
Can also mean to account for a certain proportion. For example, 人口占 13% (rénkǒu zhàn 13%) means "the population accounts for 13%".

~
归纳
When used to mean "induction" (as a method of deduction in logic), this is somewhat formal (书面).

~
反正
This word can also be used at the end of a sentence, where it has a similar meaning to "总之" (zǒngzhī), i.e., "in short" or "in conclusion".

~
天空
There is no difference between the use of 天空 in Chinese and Sky in English.

~
补贴
There is no difference between the use of 补贴 in Chinese and Subsidy in English.

~
管子
This can also refer to any hollow cylindrical object.

~
危害
There is no difference between the use of 危害 in Chinese and Jeopardize in English.

~
摸
There is no difference between the use of 摸 in Chinese and Touch in English.


~
雷
As a verb, this means to "shock" or "stun" someone (often with an unexpected plot detail).


~
倒霉
There is no difference between the use of 倒霉 in Chinese and Have bad luck in English.

~
利用
There is no difference between the use of 利用 in Chinese and Make use of in English.

~
效率
There is no difference between the use of 效率 in Chinese and Efficiency in English.

~
醋
There is no difference between the use of 醋 in Chinese and Vinegar in English. Note the second meaning, though.

~
自觉
There is no difference between the use of 自觉 in Chinese and Conscientious in English.

~
据说
There is no difference between the use of 据说 in Chinese and It is said that in English.

~
范围
There is no difference between the use of 范围 in Chinese and Range in English.

~
瘦
There is no difference between the use of 瘦 in Chinese and Thin in English.

~
克服
There is no difference between the use of 克服 in Chinese and Overcome in English.

~
豪华
There is no difference between the use of 豪华 in Chinese and Luxurious in English.

~
扇子
There is no difference between the use of 扇子 in Chinese and Fan in English.

~
文字
There is no difference between the use of 文字 in Chinese and Written language in English.

~
话题
There is no difference between the use of 话题 in Chinese and Topic in English.

~
满足
There is no difference between the use of 满足 in Chinese and Satisfied in English.

~
标点
There is no difference between the use of 标点 in Chinese and Punctuation in English.

~
开放
There is no difference between the use of 开放 in Chinese and Open in English. Note the other meanings, though.

~
贡献
There is no difference between the use of 贡献 in Chinese and Contribute in English.

~
肩膀
There is no difference between the use of 肩膀 in Chinese and Shoulder in English.

~
亲自
There is no difference between the use of 亲自 in Chinese and Personally in English.

~
颗
颗 is also sometimes used as a measure word for relatively small, roundish items.

~
重大
There is no difference between the use of 重大 in Chinese and Major in English.

~
直
直 is used to indicate continuous motion. This is similar to how 一直 (yīzhí) is used, except that 直 must be placed *before* the verb.


~
勿
This word is extremely formal and archaic. It is almost never used in modern spoken Chinese.

~
助手
There is no difference between the use of 助手 in Chinese and Assistant in English.

~
心脏
There is no difference between the use of 心脏 in Chinese and Heart in English.

~
匹
匹 is also sometimes used as a measure word for relatively thin, flat items.

~
冠军
There is no difference between the use of 冠军 in Chinese and Champion in English.

~
物质
There is no difference between the use of 物质 in Chinese and Material in English. Note the other meaning, though.

~
安装
There is no difference between the use of 安装 in Chinese and Install in English.

~
把握
This can also refer to a "grasp" of something in the metaphorical sense, meaning to have a strong understanding or mastery of a particular subject or skill.  For example, 我对这门学科很有把握 (wǒ duì zhè mén xuékē hěn yǒu bǎwò) means "I have a strong grasp of this subject."


~
主任
There is no difference between the use of 主任 in Chinese and Director in English.

~
忽然
A similar word is 突然 (tūrán). 忽然 emphasizes the unexpectedness of an event, while 突然 emphasizes the abruptness or suddenness of the change.  忽然 often describes a feeling or realization, while 突然 describes an objective event.

~
青
When referring to the color, 青 is closer to cyan than to green or blue. It is a color between green and blue.

~
伸
伸 is usually used with a complement, e.g. 伸手 (shēnshǒu), 伸腿 (shēntuǐ), 伸长 (shēncháng), 伸出 (shēnchū), etc.

~
语气
语气 can also be translated as "tone of voice".

~
主持
主持 can also refer to emceeing an event.

~
结合
结合 is often used with "actual" (实际 shíjì).

~
团
Although 团 can be translated as "dumpling", in practice it's never used that way. It's always used to mean round, lump, ball, etc.

~
成就
As a verb, 成就 is more formal than "achieve". It is also somewhat archaic.

~
桔子
桔子 and 橘子 are interchangeable.

~
买卖
Although normally translated as "buy and sell", it often just means "business" or "to do business".

~
毛病
毛病 is rarely used to refer to physical ailments. It's most commonly used to describe a personal defect, character flaw, or something that is unsatisfactory.

~
冰激凌
冰淇淋 (bīngqílín) is a more common way to say "ice cream".

~
组织
组织 as a verb is sometimes used colloquially to mean to "arrange something for someone", where the word "arrange" would be translated as 安排 (ānpái) in standard usage.

~
从前
从前 is used almost exclusively when telling fairy tales or children's stories.

~
相当
相当 is more commonly used to mean "equivalent to" or "quite/fairly". The other meanings are less frequent.

~
抱怨
It might help learners to know that 抱怨 is composed of the characters 抱 (bào) meaning "to hold; to embrace; to hug" and 怨 (yuàn) meaning "resentment; complaint; to blame."

~
发表
发表 is typically used for formal announcements or publications in academic or professional contexts. For expressing personal opinions or sharing information casually, other verbs like 说 (shuō, to say), 分享 (fēnxiǎng, to share), or 表达 (biǎodá, to express) are more appropriate.

~
相似
A similar word is 相像 (xiāngxìang), which often means to resemble or look like. The two words can often be used interchangeably, but 相似 emphasizes having shared characteristics or qualities, while 相像 specifically refers to visual resemblance.

~
正
正 can also be used to emphasize that something is happening right now, e.g. 正吃饭 (zhèng chīfàn) means "(I'm) in the middle of eating dinner."

~
胃口
胃口 is also used metaphorically to mean "interest", e.g. 对…没有胃口 (duì … méiyǒu wèikǒu) means "not have an appetite/taste for".

~
方案
方案 generally refers to a comprehensive and detailed action plan, usually for something complicated or large-scale. 计划 (jìhuà) is a more general term for any kind of plan.

~
分布
分布 emphasizes the arrangement or spread of something over an area or among a group.  散布 (sànbù) means simply to scatter or spread out.

~
功能
功能 emphasizes inherent capabilities or intrinsic functions of something, rather than what something can actively do.  作用 (zuòyòng) is a more general term for function or role, and it can describe the effect or influence something has on another thing.  It also refers to a benefit.

~
美术
美术 refers to the visual arts, particularly painting, drawing, and sculpture. 艺术 (yìshù) is a broader term encompassing all art forms, including music, literature, theater, etc.

~
温柔
While 温柔 can be used for both men and women, it is much more common for women. The best translation when describing a man is "gentle".  Other synonyms to 温柔 include 柔和 (róuhé), which emphasizes calmness and softness, and 温和 (wēnhé), which means mild or moderate.

~
明星
When referring to a movie or TV star, the more common word is 影星 (yǐngxīng).

~
坦率
坦率 implies honesty and directness, potentially even to the point of bluntness or lack of tact.  直率 (zhíshuài) has similar meaning.  真诚 (zhēnchéng) emphasizes sincerity and genuineness, and it carries a more positive connotation.

~
幻想
幻想 carries a slightly negative connotation, implying unrealistic or impractical dreams.  梦想 (mèngxiǎng) is a more positive term for dreams and aspirations.

~
人口
人口 can also refer to a specific demographic or a group of people.

~
形成
形成 implies a gradual process of development or evolution.  构成 (gòuchéng) means "to constitute" or "to compose."

~
明确
明确 emphasizes clarity and precision, leaving no room for ambiguity. 清楚 (qīngchu) is more general term for clear or understandable.

~
用功
用功 focuses on diligence and effort in studying.  努力 (nǔlì) is a more general term for making an effort in any endeavor.

~
使劲儿
It might be helpful for learners to know that 使劲儿 (shǐjìnr) can be translated as "to put forth one's strength" or "to make a determined effort."

~
夏令营
There is no difference between 夏令营 in Chinese and "summer camp" in English.

~
概括
概括 focuses on summarizing the main points.  总结 (zǒngjié) implies a more comprehensive review and analysis.

~
转变
转变 suggests a fundamental shift in direction or nature.  改变 (gǎibiàn) is a more general term for change.

~
键盘
There is no difference between 键盘 in Chinese and "keyboard" in English.

~
从而
从而 emphasizes the consequential relationship between two clauses, often indicating a cause-and-effect relationship. 因此 (yīncǐ) is more general term meaning "therefore" or "thus".

~
运输
运输 specifically refers to the transportation of goods or materials.  交通 (jiāotōng) is a broader term encompassing all forms of transportation, including passenger travel.

~
实践
实践 emphasizes the application of theory or ideas in real-world situations.  练习 (liànxí) means "to practice" or "exercise".

~
私人

This can mean "private", but also can mean something like "personal connections" (关系).

~
农村

A related word is 乡村 (xiāngcūn).  Both refer to rural areas. However, 农村 emphasizes the agricultural aspect of the countryside, while 乡村 focuses more on the rustic charm and idyllic scenery.  Think "farmland" vs. "village".  In official contexts, 农村 might be used when discussing agricultural policies or rural development.

~
坚决

坚决 is often used together with verbs related to decisions or actions, such as 支持 (zhīchí - support), 反对 (fǎnduì - oppose), 执行 (zhíxíng - implement), and 保卫 (bǎowèi - defend). This emphasizes the unwavering nature of the action.  For example, 坚决支持 means to resolutely support.

~
册

册 is typically used for books that are thin or part of a series. For larger, single-volume books, 本 (běn) is more common.

~
巨大

巨大 is often used to describe physical size or scale, while other synonyms like 庞大 (páng dà) can also describe large, complex systems or organizations. 巨大的 can also imply a sense of enormity or immensity, sometimes with a negative connotation.

~
套

As a measure word, 套 is used for sets or collections of things. Be aware that 套 also has several other meanings as a verb.

~
偷

Be aware that 偷看 (tōu kàn) means "to peek" or "to glimpse".  偷听 (tōu tīng) means "to eavesdrop".

~
总算

总算 emphasizes the difficulty or delay in achieving something.  It often implies relief or satisfaction that something finally happened.

~
湿润

This word can be used figuratively.  For example, 湿润的眼睛 can mean tearful eyes.

~
毕竟

毕竟 suggests an undeniable truth or reason that explains a situation. It emphasizes the underlying cause or logic behind something.

~
银

银 can refer to money (especially in older texts).  Specifically, 银子 (yínzi) is a colloquial way to say "money".

~
饮食

饮食 is a formal word, used in contexts like healthcare, nutrition, or formal writing.  More common words are 吃饭 (chīfàn) or 吃东西 (chī dōngxi).

~
国王

This word refers specifically to a king.  A more general word for "monarch" is 君主 (jūnzhǔ).  女皇 (nǚhuáng) is "empress" or "queen".

~
平

平 can also be used to describe a tone in Mandarin Chinese. The first tone is called 平声.

~
匆忙

This emphasizes doing something quickly due to time constraints, which may lead to mistakes.  A related word is 仓促 (cāngcù). This word emphasizes the lack of preparation and the resulting negative consequences. It implies a sense of being rushed and unprepared, which often leads to a poor outcome.

~
呆

As an adjective, this can also be used to describe someone who is slow to react.

~
多亏

This is usually used in positive situations, expressing gratitude for someone's help or a fortunate event.

~
开发

This can refer to developing software, real estate, or any other product or resource.

~
设备

This refers to the physical equipment or machinery used in a particular setting, such as a factory, laboratory, or office.

~
违反

违反 is usually used with laws, rules, or agreements.  For social norms or customs, 违背 (wéibèi) is more appropriate.

~
土豆

In Taiwan, 土豆 means "peanut."  In mainland China, 花生 is "peanut" and 土豆 is "potato".

~
概念

概念 can refer to abstract ideas, general notions, or the basic understanding of something.

~
铃

铃 is a smaller bell than 钟 (zhōng). Think "doorbell" rather than "church bell".

~
热爱

This describes a deep and passionate love for something, often used for ideals, causes, or hobbies.

~
食物

食物 is a general term for all kinds of food.  食品 (shípǐn) also refers to food but is more commonly used for processed or packaged foods.

~
活泼

This is typically used to describe children or young animals, implying cheerful energy and playfulness.

~
体贴

This is often used to describe actions or gestures that demonstrate care and concern for another person's well-being.

~
岸

岸 is usually a natural shore, while 边 (biān) can be any edge.

~
救护车

救护车 is used for medical emergencies.  消防车 (xiāofángchē) is a fire engine.

~
劳驾

This is a polite way to get someone's attention, especially when asking for help or directions.

~
传说

传说 implies that the story may not be entirely true or verifiable, based on popular belief.

~
行为

行为 refers to observable actions, often implying a pattern of behavior.  举动 (jǔdòng) refers to a single, specific action.

~
何必

何必 questions the necessity or value of an action, often implying that it's unnecessary or not worth the effort.

~
时髦

时髦 specifically refers to being fashionable in a trendy or stylish way.

~
零件

零件 refers to smaller components or parts of a machine or device.  部件 (bùjiàn) refers to larger components or modules.

~
慌张

慌张 emphasizes the inner feeling of panic or anxiety.  惊慌 (jīnghuāng) suggests a more visible reaction to a sudden shock or surprise.

~
灵活

灵活 suggests adaptability and quick thinking, suitable for both physical and mental dexterity.

~
洞

洞 emphasizes the depth and hollowness of an opening, while 孔 (kǒng) suggests a smaller hole, often xuyên through something.

~
馒头

This is white and plain.  包子 (bāozi) are filled buns.

~
小麦

This refers to the wheat plant itself. 面粉 (miànfěn) is wheat flour.

~
休闲
Can be used as an adjective ("leisurely") or a noun ("leisure time").  As an adjective, it can describe an activity (e.g., 休闲活动, "leisure activities") or a lifestyle (e.g., 休闲生活, "leisurely lifestyle").

~
谨慎
Often collocates with words like  小心 (xiǎoxīn, "careful") and 认真 (rènzhēn, "serious, conscientious") to emphasize a cautious and meticulous approach.

~
幽默
Can describe a person (幽默的人, "a humorous person"), a story (幽默的故事, "a humorous story"), or a style of expression (幽默的表达方式, "a humorous way of expression").  Note that 幽默 itself is not a verb; use  表现幽默 (biǎoxiàn yōumò) to express "to display humor".

~
自动
As an adjective, it means "automatic."  As an adverb, it means "voluntarily" or "of one's own accord." The meaning is usually clear from context.  For "voluntarily," you can also use 主动 (zhǔdòng).

~
龙
Highly symbolic in Chinese culture, representing power, good fortune, and imperial authority.  Has many idiomatic uses (e.g., 龙飞凤舞 lóngfēifèngwǔ, "vigorous strokes of calligraphy").

~
片
A versatile measure word. Pay close attention to the context to determine the specific nuance. For example, 一片面包 (yī piàn miànbāo) means "a slice of bread," while 一片欢呼 (yī piàn huānhū) means "a burst of cheers."

~
哈
The onomatopoeia for laughter can be reduplicated as 哈哈 (hāhā) or even further for greater emphasis.  The slang meaning of "to be infatuated with" is relatively modern and more common online.

~
象征
Often used with the preposition  代表 (dàibiǎo, "to represent, to stand for").  For example,  鸽子象征和平 (gēzi xiàngzhēng hépíng), "The dove symbolizes peace."

~
生产
Be aware of the two distinct meanings: "to produce/manufacture" and "to give birth." Context is key.

~
文明
Can refer to both a specific civilization (e.g.,  古埃及文明, "ancient Egyptian civilization") and the general concept of civilized behavior (e.g.,  讲文明懂礼貌, "to be civilized and have good manners").

~
顿
As a measure word, it emphasizes the discrete nature of the action or event, often unpleasant ones.

~
贷款
Distinguish between  贷款 (dàikuǎn, "to provide a loan") and  借款 (jièkuǎn, "to take out a loan").

~
姿势
Can be physical, as in  保持正确的姿势 (bǎochí zhèngquè de zīshì, "maintain correct posture"), or figurative, as in  摆姿势 (bǎi zīshì, "to strike a pose, to put on airs").

~
立刻
Essentially interchangeable with  马上 (mǎshàng, "immediately").

~
蔬菜
A general term.  Specific vegetables are usually referred to with their individual names.

~
学历
Focuses on the formal credentials achieved, like degrees or diplomas.  For broader learning experience, use  学习经历 (xuéxí jīnglì, "learning experience").

~
自豪
Often used with the preposition  为 (wèi, "for, because of"). For example, 我为我的祖国感到自豪 (wǒ wèi wǒ de zǔguó gǎndào zìháo), "I am proud of my country."

~
总裁
A high-ranking executive title.  The precise equivalent in English depends on the specific company structure, but it generally denotes a top-level leader.

~
糟糕
Expresses a stronger sense of misfortune or unpleasantness than simply "bad."

~
显得
Used to describe appearances or impressions. It often indicates something that may not be entirely true or factual.  For example, 她显得有点紧张 (tā xiǎnde yǒudiǎn jǐnzhāng), "She seems a little nervous."

~
象棋
Refers specifically to Chinese chess, distinct from international chess (国际象棋 guójì xiàngqí).

~
傍晚
Refers to the time just before nightfall, dusk.

~
便
Highly versatile.  As a stand-alone word, it's usually an adverb indicating convenience or ease.  It can also function as a conjunction similar to  就 (jiù), meaning "then" or "in that case."  Be aware of its different tones and meanings when part of compound words.

~
大厦
Usually refers to large, imposing buildings, often commercial or office spaces.

~
退休
Implies a formal withdrawal from the workforce, typically associated with age or length of service.

~
轮流
Often used with  做 (zuò, "to do") to indicate taking turns doing something.

~
人民币
The official currency of China.  The abbreviation RMB is commonly used internationally.

~
请求
More formal and polite than  要 (yào, "to want") or  想 (xiǎng, "to want, to think").

~
日用品
Encompasses a wide range of everyday items, from toiletries to cleaning supplies.

~
改革
Implies significant change, often systemic or institutional.

~
艰巨
Emphasizes the difficulty and demanding nature of a task.

~
项链
Typically worn around the neck as jewelry.

~
池塘
Smaller than a lake (湖 hú). Often artificial or found within gardens.

~
碎
Has both literal and figurative meanings. For example, 玻璃碎了 (bōli suì le), "The glass broke," and  心都碎了 (xīn dōu suì le), "My heart is broken."

~
朵
Primarily used as a measure word for flowers and clouds.

~
往返
Specifically refers to a round trip, going somewhere and returning.

~
昆虫
A general term for insects.

~
打听
Implies actively seeking information, often by asking multiple people.

~
频道
Refers to a specific frequency or band used for broadcasting, or a designated channel on television.

~
青少年
Refers to the age group between childhood and adulthood.  The exact age range varies depending on context, but it generally covers teenagers and young adults.

~
骗子
Adding "老" (lǎo) before 骗子 (piànzi) emphasizes the cunning and experience of the swindler, implying they are a habitual con artist.  It carries a stronger negative connotation than 骗子 alone.  Think of it like calling someone a "con man" or "hustler" in English.

~
靠
As a verb, besides the meanings you provided, 靠 can also mean "to rely on" or "to depend on," similar to 依靠 (yīkào), but less formal.  For example,  "我靠父母" (wǒ kào fùmǔ) means "I rely on my parents."  As an interjection, "靠 (kào)" is a common, somewhat vulgar expression of frustration or disbelief, similar to "damn" or "shit" in English.  Be careful where you use it!

~
调整
调整 suggests a fine-tuning or minor alteration to improve something or make it more suitable. It implies a deliberate and methodical process of adjustment.

~
浇
When used in the context of emotions, 浇 can mean "to dampen" or "to quell." For example, 浇灭热情 (jiāo miè rèqíng) means "to dampen enthusiasm."  Also, note the specific usage with concrete:  浇水泥 (jiāo shuǐní) - "to pour concrete."

~
幸亏
This word implies that something bad could have happened, but didn't, due to some fortunate circumstance.  It often carries a sense of relief.

~
诊断
诊断 is a formal and technical term used in medical contexts.  It implies a professional assessment leading to a conclusion about a patient's condition.

~
真实
真实 emphasizes the veracity and accuracy of something, often in contrast to falsehood or illusion.  It often suggests objectivity and evidence-based truth.  It can often be interchangeable with 真正 (zhēnzhèng), but 真实 emphasizes the factuality of something while 真正 points out something's genuineness or authenticity.

~
从事
This word is often used to describe professions or careers, indicating a sustained involvement in a particular field.  For example, "从事教育工作" (cóngshì jiàoyù gōngzuò) means "to work in education." It is a formal way of saying one's occupation.

~
导演
导演 can be used metaphorically to describe someone who orchestrates or masterminds a situation or event.

~
分别
分别 also functions as an adverb meaning "respectively" or "severally".  For example, "他们分别去了北京和上海" (tāmen fēnbié qù le Běijīng hé Shànghǎi) means "They went to Beijing and Shanghai respectively."

~
启发
启发 emphasizes the process of sparking understanding or insight. It suggests that the learning is self-directed, triggered by an external stimulus.

~
肥皂
肥皂 is the general term for "soap."  香皂 (xiāngzào) specifically refers to scented soap.

~
辣椒
辣椒 can refer to both chili peppers and chili powder.

~
猪
Calling someone 猪 (zhū) can be a mild insult, implying they are lazy, dirty, or gluttonous.

~
作文
作文 specifically refers to essays written as school assignments.

~
本科
本科 is used in contrast to 研究生 (yánjiūshēng) "graduate student/studies."

~
吨
Be aware that a metric ton (吨, dūn) is equivalent to 1,000 kilograms, while an imperial/US ton is approximately 907 kilograms.

~
提倡
提倡 suggests actively promoting or advocating for a specific idea or practice.  It often implies trying to persuade others to adopt a certain behavior or viewpoint.

~
隔壁
隔壁 can also mean "neighbor."

~
制定
制定 emphasizes the process of creating rules, plans, or policies through careful consideration and discussion.

~
贸易
贸易 is a broad term encompassing all forms of commercial exchange, both domestic and international.

~
趁
趁 is often followed by the opportunity or time being taken advantage of, e.g., 趁热吃 (chèn rè chī) - "eat while it's hot."

~
俱乐部
俱乐部 covers various types of clubs, from sports clubs to social clubs.

~
外交
外交 can also be used as an adjective, meaning "diplomatic," such as 外交关系 (wàijiāo guānxì) - "diplomatic relations."

~
温暖
Beyond physical warmth, 温暖 can also describe emotional warmth, kindness, or a feeling of comfort.

~
产生
产生 implies a process of something coming into existence, often as a result of other factors. It is commonly used in more formal or technical contexts.

~
酱油
Different varieties of soy sauce exist, such as 生抽 (shēngchōu, light soy sauce) and 老抽 (lǎochōu, dark soy sauce), which are used for different purposes in cooking.

~
记录
记录 can also refer to a best performance or highest score in a competition.

~
果然
果然 is used to confirm a prior expectation or prediction.  It expresses the idea that something turned out as anticipated.

~
躲藏
躲藏 emphasizes actively trying to remain hidden or concealed, often out of fear or to avoid detection.

~
臭
When used with certain nouns, 臭 can have a less negative connotation. For example, 臭豆腐 (chòu dòufu, stinky tofu) is a popular snack. The character can also express something done severely or ruthlessly. E.g. 臭骂一顿 (chòu mà yī dùn) To scold someone ruthlessly.

~
围绕
围绕 can be used both literally and figuratively. For example, "卫星围绕地球旋转" (wèixīng wéirào dìqiú xuánzhuǎn) - "The satellite revolves around the Earth," and "讨论围绕着这个问题展开" (tǎolùn wéirào zhe zhège wèntí zhǎnkāi) - "The discussion revolved around this issue."

~
媒体
媒体 can be used both generally, encompassing all forms of media, or more specifically to refer to news media.

~
光滑
光滑 emphasizes a perfectly smooth surface, often with a sheen or gloss.

~
招手
招手 implies beckoning someone to come closer or calling a taxi.

~
联合
联合 highlights the act of joining forces or working together for a common purpose, often involving multiple parties.

~
首
首 is a measure word for songs and poems.  It emphasizes the completeness of a piece of work.

~
逻辑
逻辑 refers to the principles of reasoning and argumentation, emphasizing clear and structured thinking.

~
丝毫
丝毫 is usually used in negative contexts to emphasize a complete lack of something.  For example, "丝毫没有改变" (sīháo méiyǒu gǎibiàn) - "not the slightest change."

~
风险
风险 refers to the possibility of loss or harm, often in financial or business contexts. It highlights the potential negative consequences of an action or decision.

朝 (cháo) /morning/

When referring to "morning," 朝 is somewhat literary.  More common ways to say "morning" include 早上 (zǎoshang) or 上午 (shàngwǔ).  Note that 早 (zǎo) on its own can also mean "morning."

~
舱
Sometimes used interchangeably with 船舱 (chuáncāng).  While both refer to compartments on a ship, 舱 is more general, referring to any enclosed space, whereas 船舱 specifically refers to cabins for passengers or crew.

~
溅
Similar to  泼 (pō), but 溅 implies smaller droplets and less forceful splashing.  Think "splash" versus "pour".

~
丸
This character can refer to small, round objects of various types. Context is crucial.  药丸 (yàowán) means "pill", 肉丸 (ròuwán) means "meatball", and so on.

~
守护
More formal and literary than 保护 (bǎohù).  守护 carries a stronger sense of dedication and duty.

~
趴
While the primary meaning is "to lie on one's stomach," 趴在桌子上 (pā zài zhuōzi shang) means to lean forward, resting on a desktop. Note the usage with "在".  The Taiwanese percentage meaning is slang and unlikely to be encountered in mainland China.

~
优越
Often carries a negative connotation of arrogance or looking down on others.  Be mindful of the context.

~
钙
Remember to pronounce the fourth tone correctly.  It's a common mistake to say it in the third tone.

~
魔鬼
While 魔鬼 is the general translation for "devil,"  恶魔 (èmó) is sometimes used and can be more sinister.

~
条约
Remember the classifier 个 (gè).

~
陷害
Stronger than 诬陷 (wūxiàn), implying more elaborate scheming and more severe consequences.

~
要点
Often appears in the plural form 要点们 (yàodiǎnmen) when referring to multiple key points.

~
共和国
Usually refers to the People's Republic of China (中华人民共和国 - Zhōnghuá Rénmín Gònghéguó).

~
殴打
Implies physical violence, whereas 打 (dǎ) can have broader meanings, including hitting in sports or games.

~
万分
Can mean both "extremely" and "one ten-thousandth."  Context is essential for understanding the intended meaning.

~
申报
Has a more official and formal connotation than 报道 (bàodào) when referring to reporting information.

~
断绝
Implies a complete and irreversible break.

~
款待
More formal and elaborate than 招待 (zhāodài), implying a higher level of hospitality.

~
撇
The meaning shifts depending on the context.  It can mean to cast aside or to execute a specific calligraphy stroke.

~
事项
Refers to a specific item or task within a larger project or process.

~
散布
Often used with negative connotations, such as spreading rumors or misinformation.

~
请帖
More formal than 请柬 (qǐngjiǎn), often used for weddings or significant events.

~
诉讼
A formal legal term.

~
化肥
Specifically refers to chemical fertilizers.

~
机密
Implies a higher level of secrecy than 秘密 (mìmì).

~
拨
Has many meanings.  Pay attention to the context to discern the correct interpretation.

~
哺乳
Specifically refers to breastfeeding, not bottle-feeding.

~
冒充
Implies deception for personal gain.

~
别墅
Refers to a luxurious, detached house, often used as a second home or vacation property.

~
刹车
Can be used as both a verb and a noun.

~
岳母
Specifically refers to one's wife's mother.

~
挽回
Implies retrieving something lost or damaged, such as a relationship or reputation.

~
混浊
Describes a liquid state.

~
烹饪
More formal than 做饭 (zuòfàn).

~
反之
Used to introduce a contrasting statement or idea.

~
天生
Often used to describe innate qualities or talents.

~
郑重
Emphasizes seriousness and formality.

~
风气
Refers to prevailing social customs or trends.

~
出神
Describes a state of being completely absorbed in thought.

~
苍白
Often used metaphorically to describe a weak argument or unconvincing explanation.

~
气魄
Refers to a grand or impressive scale or scope, often used to describe a person's demeanor or a project's ambition.

~
昂贵
Close synonyms include 贵 (guì) and 高昂 (gāo'áng). 贵 is the most general and common word for "expensive". 昂贵 (ángguì) is more formal and emphasizes a high price. 高昂 (gāo'áng) is also formal and is often used to describe abstract things like morale or aspirations.


~
清晰
清晰 (qīngxī) is more formal than 清楚 (qīngchu). 清晰 is usually used to describe physical things like images or sounds, as well as abstract concepts like ideas or memories. 清楚 is usually used to describe more concrete things like situations and facts, as well as something being easy to see/hear.


~
统治
A synonym is 执政 (zhízhèng), but this specifically refers to being in power or in office, whereas 统治 (tǒngzhì) means "to rule" and can also be used for past rulers who are no longer in office.


~
水龙头
Nothing special to mention.


~
愚昧
More formal than other words with a similar meaning like  笨 (bèn) or  傻 (shǎ).


~
分泌
Nothing special to mention.


~
逝世
Formal and respectful way of saying 死 (sǐ). Mostly used for important or famous people.


~
忠实
Can be translated as "faithful", "loyal", or "true".  It can be used to describe people, animals, or even translations.


~
事务
Be aware that 事物 (shìwù) with a fourth tone means "thing" or "object".


~
操劳
More formal than  辛苦 (xīnkǔ).


~
深沉
Nothing special to mention.


~
俯视
Nothing special to mention.


~
储蓄
Note the distinct meanings of 储蓄 (chǔxù) versus 节约 (jiéyuē). 储蓄 specifically refers to saving money, typically in a bank. 节约 means to economize or conserve more generally, whether it's money, resources, or energy. You 节约 electricity, but you 储蓄 money.


~
启程
Formal. A more colloquial equivalent is 出发 (chūfā).


~
遥远
Nothing special to mention.


~
可行
Nothing special to mention.


~
得力
Often used to describe assistants or subordinates who are competent and helpful.


~
烘
烘 (hōng) is often seen in specific contexts. For baking, 烤 (kǎo) is more common. 烘干 (hōnggān) means "to dry".


~
堆积
Nothing special to mention.


~
巢穴
Nothing special to mention.


~
骚扰
Nothing special to mention.


~
条理
Nothing special to mention.


~
迟钝
Nothing special to mention.


~
践踏
Often used figuratively to mean violating or disregarding something, like someone's feelings or the law.


~
辩解
Nothing special to mention.


~
上游
When referring to rivers, note the difference between 上游 (shàngyóu), which refers to the upper reaches or the area upstream, and 源头 (yuántóu), which means "source" or "headwaters."


~
案例
Nothing special to mention.


~
徘徊
The meaning of fluctuating is less common.


~
矿产
Nothing special to mention.


~
取缔
取缔 (qǔdì) implies a more forceful and complete suppression or prohibition, often by law enforcement, compared to other words like 禁止 (jìnzhǐ), which simply means "to forbid".


~
谅解
More formal than  理解 (lǐjiě).


~
舰艇
Nothing special to mention.


~
托运
Nothing special to mention.


~
古董
Nothing special to mention.


~
恨不得
This phrase expresses a strong desire, to the point of impatience or frustration.


~
演习
Nothing special to mention.


~
搀
The various meanings are not related.


~
推理
Nothing special to mention.


~
上瘾
Nothing special to mention.


~
凝聚
Can be used both literally (like water condensing) and figuratively (like consolidating strength or power).

~
务必
务必 (wùbì) carries a stronger sense of urgency or importance than other ways of expressing "must" or "need to," such as  必须 (bìxū) or  一定要 (yīdìng yào). It often implies that something is absolutely essential or crucial, and failure to do it would have serious consequences.  It is often used in formal settings or for giving serious instructions.

~
酗酒
酗酒 (xùjiǔ) specifically refers to habitual heavy drinking or alcoholism, not just a single instance of getting drunk.

~
尚且
Be aware of the double negative structure with 尚且 (shàngqiě), where it often appears with 不 (bù) or 没 (méi) to create the meaning of "not even." For example: 他连饭都吃不饱，尚且没钱买衣服 (tā lián fàn dōu chī bù bǎo, shàngqiě méi qián mǎi yīfu) - He can't even eat his fill, let alone have money to buy clothes.

~
甭
甭 (béng) is a colloquial contraction of 不用 (bùyòng), meaning "need not" or "don't." It is mostly used in northern dialects and might sound out of place in other regions.

~
钩子
In addition to the literal meaning "hook," 钩子 (gōuzi) can be used figuratively to refer to something tricky or deceitful, a "catch," similar to how "hook" can be used in English.

~
骨干
The figurative meaning of 骨干 (gǔgàn) - "backbone," "core," or "mainstay" - is very common and refers to the key members of a group or organization.

~
方位
方位 (fāngwèi) is a more formal and technical term than 方向 (fāngxiàng) for "direction." It often implies a precise location or bearing, especially in navigation or geography.

~
发育
When referring to sexual maturity, 发育 (fāyù) is a more clinical and less direct way to say it than other terms.

~
涂抹
涂抹 (túmǒ) implies a messy or careless application of something, not a precise or artistic one.  It can also mean to cover something up, often in a deceitful way.

~
海拔
海拔 (hǎibá) is specifically height above sea level, not just altitude or elevation in general.

~
奔驰
奔驰 (bēnchí) is also the Chinese name for Mercedes-Benz.

~
捎
捎 (shāo) implies bringing something along with you on an already planned trip, not making a special trip for the sole purpose of delivering the item.

~
微观
微观 (wēiguān) relates to things too small to be seen with the naked eye, not just small in a general sense.

~
大肆
大肆 (dàsì) is almost always used in a negative context to describe actions done excessively or recklessly, such as spreading rumors, criticizing, or squandering money.

~
连同
连同 (liántóng) means "together with," but it emphasizes inclusiveness, suggesting everything mentioned is treated as a single unit.

~
部署
部署 (bùshǔ) usually refers to the strategic arrangement of troops or resources, not just any arrangement of things.

~
粒
粒 (lì) is specifically for small, granular objects.  Using it for larger objects would be incorrect.

~
调和
调和 (tiáohé) often refers to mediating a conflict or finding a compromise, in addition to mixing or blending.

~
知觉
知觉 (zhījué) is both the physical senses and the awareness of them, a broader concept than just the individual senses.

~
钻石
钻石 (zuànshí) is the specific word for "diamond."  宝石 (bǎoshí) is the general word for "gem" or "precious stone."

~
鸽子
鸽子 (gēzi) can be used figuratively to refer to a messenger or carrier, especially of secret information.

~
开采
开采 (kāicǎi) is primarily used for extracting natural resources, not other types of materials.

~
生理
生理 (shēnglǐ) is primarily used to discuss bodily functions, often related to reproduction or menstruation, and sometimes has a slightly taboo connotation.

~
沸腾
The figurative use of 沸腾 (fèiténg), "to boil over," is common to describe strong emotions or excitement.

~
威望
威望 (wēiwàng) implies respect earned through authority and accomplishment, not just popularity.

~
迹象
迹象 (jīxiàng) refers to subtle or indirect signs, often suggesting something is about to happen or is hidden.

~
武装
武装 (wǔzhuāng) can function as a noun ("arms," "equipment") a verb ("to arm"), and an adjective ("armed").

~
习俗
习俗 (xísú) refers to established customs and traditions, often passed down through generations.

~
周折
周折 (zhōuzhé) implies unexpected difficulties or complications that require effort to overcome.

~
僵硬
僵硬 (jiāngyìng) can describe physical stiffness or a rigid, inflexible attitude.

~
呈现
呈现 (chéngxiàn) implies a clear display or presentation of something, making it noticeable.

~
土壤
土壤 (tǔrǎng) can also refer to the environment or conditions for something to grow or develop, not just literal soil.

~
解散
解散 (jiěsàn) refers to formally breaking up a group or organization, not just people dispersing.

~
不妨
不妨 (bùfáng) is a polite way to suggest something, implying there is no harm in trying.

~
暧昧
暧昧 (àimèi) often has a romantic connotation, suggesting a vague or undefined relationship.

~
贪婪
贪婪 (tānlán) carries a strongly negative connotation, implying excessive greed and selfishness.

~
束缚
束缚 (shùfù)  can refer to physical restraints or limitations on freedom and development.

~
支柱
支柱 (zhīzhù) is used metaphorically to describe the key element or support of something.

~
外向
外向 (wàixiàng) describes a personality that is outgoing and sociable, as well as an economic policy focused on exports.

~
神气
神气 (shénqì) can have both positive and negative connotations. It can mean energetic and lively, but also arrogant or self-satisfied.

~
推测
Can be used as a noun or a verb.

~
淹没
This word can be used literally, as in "the flood submerged the village", or figuratively, as in "the truth was drowned out by lies".

~
敌视
This word is much stronger than "dislike". It implies deep-seated hatred and antagonism, often to the point of wanting to harm or destroy the other party.

~
领土
A related word is 领地 (lǐngdì). 领土 refers to territory belonging to a country, while 领地 can refer to the territory of any group, even a small, informal one, like a gang or a pack of animals. So you can use 领地 to talk about a dog's territory, but not 领土.

~
缴纳
This word is more formal than 付 (fù) or 交 (jiāo). It's often used for official payments, like taxes or fees.

~
频率
Note that 频率 is usually used for repeating events, whereas 速度 (sùdù) is used for things that move.

~
人质
There is no important difference between the use of 人质 in Chinese and hostage in English.

~
充实
As an adjective, 充实 means "full" or "substantial", and is often used to describe a feeling of fulfillment or satisfaction, e.g., after a busy but productive day. As a verb, it means "to enrich" or "to enhance", often by adding more content or substance.

~
密封
There is no important difference between the use of 密封 in Chinese and seal in English.

~
包袱
Aside from its literal meaning, 包袱 can also refer to a burden (both literal and figurative), a weight (both literal and figurative), or the punchline of a joke. 


~
忧郁
This word has stronger connotations of sadness and melancholy than 难过 (nánguò) or 伤心 (shāngxīn), which are more general terms for sadness or unhappiness.

~
勾结
This word carries strong negative connotations of conspiracy and underhanded dealings. It suggests a secret alliance for illicit purposes. 

~
熬
The character 熬 has two main meanings:

1. To cook on a slow fire: This usually refers to cooking something over a long period, often to extract flavors or nutrients, as in making soup or traditional Chinese medicine.

2. To endure: This refers to persevering through a difficult or unpleasant situation, often involving hardship or suffering.

~
肥沃
There is no important difference between the use of 肥沃 in Chinese and fertile in English.

~
茫茫
There is no important difference between the use of 茫茫 in Chinese and "vast and obscure" in English. However, note that the English expression is literary. The Chinese word is less so.

~
杂交
The usage of 杂交 is quite parallel with the English word "hybridize", but the meaning related to "promiscuity" is vulgar.

~
呵
There is no important difference between the use of 呵 in Chinese and the relevant English expressions.

~
格局
格局 can refer to the physical layout or arrangement of something, but it can also refer to a more abstract structure or pattern, such as the overall situation or the way things are organized. 

~
扩张
This word usually carries a neutral connotation of expansion or growth, but it can also imply an aggressive or uncontrolled expansion, especially in a political or military context.

~
冷落
冷落 can refer to a place being desolate or unfrequented, or it can describe the act of treating someone coldly or ignoring them. 

~
运算
This word specifically refers to mathematical calculations or operations. While 计算 (jìsuàn) can also mean "to calculate", 运算 is often used in more technical or scientific contexts.

~
潇洒
This word describes a carefree and unrestrained manner or style, often associated with elegance and confidence. It suggests a natural grace and ease of movement or behavior.

~
文物
There is no important difference between the use of 文物 in Chinese and "cultural relic" in English.

~
地质
There is no important difference between the use of 地质 in Chinese and "geology" in English.

~
埋伏
This word implies a hidden position or a state of concealment, often with the intention of surprising or attacking someone. 

~
赋予
This word implies granting something of value or importance, such as a right, responsibility, or quality. It emphasizes the act of giving or bestowing something.

~
还原
This word implies returning something to its original or previous state, whether it's a physical object, a situation, or a chemical compound. It emphasizes the process of reversing a change or transformation.

~
刑事
This word is used in legal contexts to describe matters related to crime and punishment. It distinguishes criminal cases from civil cases.

~
贩卖
This word usually implies selling illegal or illicit goods, such as drugs or weapons. It often carries a negative connotation of exploitation or profiteering.

~
气质
气质 is a more abstract concept than 性格 (xìnggé), which refers to personality. 气质 describes a person's overall demeanor, presence, and the impression they make on others.

~
公安局
There is no important difference between the use of 公安局 in Chinese and "public security bureau" in English.

~
融化
This word can be used both literally (e.g., ice melting) and figuratively (e.g., blending into a new culture).

~
慢性
This word describes something that develops or progresses slowly over time, often without obvious symptoms in the early stages.

~
尖端
尖端 can refer to the literal pointed end of something, or it can be used figuratively to describe the most advanced, sophisticated, or cutting-edge aspects of a field or technology.

~
安详
This word describes a peaceful and serene state, often associated with calmness, tranquility, and a sense of contentment. 

~
吹捧
This word has a negative connotation, suggesting excessive or insincere praise, often for personal gain or to manipulate someone. 

~
诬陷
This word implies a deliberate and malicious attempt to falsely accuse someone of a crime or wrongdoing, often with the intention of causing them harm or damage. 

~
窝
This word has many meanings, ranging from a physical nest or den to a place where illegal activities take place, to a verb meaning "to harbor" or "to bend."

~
眨
There is no important difference between the use of 眨 in Chinese and "blink" or "wink" in English.

~
流浪
This word describes a state of wandering or homelessness, often implying a lack of direction or purpose. 

~
魄力
