A related word is 气魄 (qìpò). 魄力 describes someone's inner motivation to achieve something great, including their courage and boldness. On the other hand, 气魄 refers to someone's imposing manner or impressive appearance, possibly resulting from their 魄力.

~
表彰
This is a formal word (书面语) used for official commendation.  A more colloquial way to say "praise" is 称赞 (chēngzàn) or 表扬 (biǎoyáng).

~
敏锐
Can be used to describe any of the five senses, but is most commonly used for eyesight and the sense of smell.

~
辉煌
Often collocates with 成就 (chéngjiù), 功绩 (gōngjì), 历史 (lìshǐ), etc.

~
秃
Note the pronunciation of this word (tū). The related word 秃子 (tūzi) refers to a bald-headed person.  Be careful when using this word as it can be considered offensive.

~
提拔
This word is more often used in the context of official promotions, within a company or other organization.

~
比喻
As a verb, 比喻 means "to use a metaphor". As a noun, 比喻 means "metaphor".

~
周密
Often collocates with 计划 (jìhuà), 安排 (ānpái), 部署 (bùshǔ), 考虑 (kǎolǜ), etc.

~
承包
The structure is usually:  A 承包 B 给 C. For example, 老板把工作承包给我 (lǎobǎn bǎ gōngzuò chéngbāo gěi wǒ).  The boss contracted the work out to me.

~
航行
Although this word can be used for airplanes, it is more common to use it for seafaring vessels. For planes, a more natural word would be 飞行 (fēixíng).

~
遗留
This word has a negative connotation, referring to problems or disadvantages left behind from previous actions or times.

~
排练
A similar word is 演练 (yǎnliàn), but this refers to practicing a plan or procedure, especially for emergencies.

~
瘫痪
Can be used figuratively, e.g. 交通瘫痪 (jiāotōng tānhuàn) traffic paralysis;  the transportation system is crippled.

~
颁布
Specifically refers to making something like a law, decree, or policy officially known to the public. It emphasizes the authoritative and formal nature of the announcement.  A more general word for "announce" is 公布 (gōngbù).

~
国务院
Refers to the State Council of the People's Republic of China, analogous to a cabinet or a council of ministers in other countries. It's the highest administrative authority in the PRC.

~
生育
Can also be used as a noun, to refer to childbirth, e.g. 生育率 (shēngyùlǜ) birth rate.

~
喇叭
The most common meaning now is "loudspeaker." It is also sometimes used in northern China to refer to a horn (of a vehicle).  The musical instrument meaning is less common.

~
疲惫
A more formal synonym is 疲乏 (pífá).

~
伯母
Can be used to address either your father's elder brother's wife, or out of courtesy, a woman around your mother's age whom you don't know how to address otherwise.

~
未免
Often appears at the beginning of a sentence and conveys a sense of disapproval or disagreement. The speaker feels that something is excessive or unreasonable.

~
不愧
Often followed by 是 (shì), 为 (wèi), or 于 (yú).

~
额外
Used to describe something beyond the normal or expected amount, often implying an additional burden, cost, or effort.

~
海滨
A related word is 海边 (hǎibiān). Both mean "seaside" or "coast", but 海滨 often refers to a developed coastal area with tourist attractions. 海边 is a more general term.

~
短促
Often used to describe breathing (e.g. 呼吸短促 hūxī duǎncù, short of breath) or sounds.

~
人性
Often used in philosophical discussions or when discussing the fundamental qualities of human beings.

~
丙
In everyday usage, 丙 is rarely used. Mostly appears in technical contexts (e.g. hepatitis B 丙型肝炎).  It is also common to use 甲乙丙丁 (jiǎ yǐ bǐng dīng) in legal or formal contexts as placeholders. For example, 甲方 (jiǎfāng) party A.

~
吼
Implies a loud, deep, and often prolonged sound, suggesting either aggression or distress.

~
拥护
Expresses strong support and often active defense of someone or something, often related to political ideologies, leaders, or policies.

~
珍稀
More emphatic than 稀有 (xīyǒu) or 罕见 (hǎnjiàn).

~
饱和
Can be used metaphorically, e.g. 市场饱和 (shìchǎng bǎohé).  The market is saturated.

~
寄托
The object of 寄托 is usually abstract, such as hopes, ideals, or emotions.  You place your hopes *in* something, not *on* something.

~
奴隶
Often used in historical or metaphorical contexts, referring to being controlled or exploited by someone or something.

~
枯燥
Describes something lacking in interest or stimulation, often referring to work, study, or daily routines.

~
擅自
Emphasizes acting without authorization, often with negative consequences.

~
性感
Be mindful of cultural context, as open discussions of sexuality can be less common in Chinese culture than in some Western cultures.

~
压抑
Refers to a feeling of being burdened or restricted, often by external forces or internal emotions. It suggests a state of being held back or suppressed.

~
就职
A formal term for taking up a position, often of importance or responsibility.

~
和睦
Often used to describe family relationships or the atmosphere within a community.
~
诧异
Expresses a higher degree of surprise than 惊讶 (jīngyà). It often implies being taken aback or speechless due to the unexpectedness of something.

~
娇气
This word has negative connotations, and means something closer to "spoiled" or "pampered."

~
嫌疑
This word is usually used in legal contexts.

~
转折
Specifically refers to a dramatic shift or turning point in a story or situation.  It's not just any change, but a significant one that alters the direction or outcome.

~
处置
The "punish" meaning is less common than the "handle" or "take care of" meaning.

~
迁就
Usually suggests compromising one's own needs or preferences to accommodate someone else, often implying a degree of reluctance or forbearance.

~
相差
When used with a quantity, 相差 (xiāngchà) indicates a difference or discrepancy between two values. It emphasizes the gap or disparity between them.  It's often followed by a numerical value to specify the extent of the difference.

~
交涉
Implies a more formal and serious discussion or negotiation, often involving some level of disagreement or conflict.  It can be used in diplomatic, business, or personal contexts where there's a need to resolve a dispute or reach a compromise.

~
查获
Specifically refers to the act of discovering and confiscating illegal or prohibited items or apprehending individuals involved in criminal activities. It's commonly used in law enforcement or customs contexts.

~
招收
Focuses on the process of actively seeking and enrolling individuals, often for employment, education, or membership. It implies a deliberate effort to attract and select suitable candidates.

~
斯文
This word can be used ironically or sarcastically to describe someone who appears polite and gentle on the surface, but is actually deceitful or malicious.

~
逼迫
This word has strong negative connotations and implies the use of force, pressure, or intimidation to compel someone to do something against their will.

~
旗帜
Can also be used metaphorically to represent a cause, ideology, or principle that a group or individual rallies behind.

~
依托
Highlights the reliance or dependence on something or someone for support, often in a more significant or structural way. It can refer to physical support, resources, or even abstract concepts like ideas or relationships.

~
勤劳
This word has strong positive connotations and is often used to praise someone's work ethic and dedication.

~
纯洁
Can also be used metaphorically to describe something untainted, innocent, or morally upright.

~
臂
This word can also be used metaphorically to represent support, assistance, or close relationships.

~
下属
Can also be used as a verb meaning "to be subordinate to."

~
缓和
Focuses on the lessening of intensity, severity, or tension in a situation or relationship. It implies a gradual easing or calming down of a difficult or strained atmosphere.

~
胸怀
This word can also be used figuratively to represent someone's capacity for tolerance, understanding, and forgiveness.

~
监狱
This word can also be used metaphorically to describe a restrictive or oppressive environment.

~
开阔
Can also be used figuratively to describe a broad or open-minded perspective.

~
泰斗
This word is used to describe individuals of the highest eminence and expertise in a particular field, often implying a level of respect and reverence.

~
株
The "to involve others (in shady business)" meaning is somewhat obscure.

~
数额
Specifically refers to a quantifiable amount or figure, typically used in financial or statistical contexts. It emphasizes the precise numerical value rather than a general quantity.

~
坚韧
This word often describes a person's character or spirit, suggesting an ability to persevere through challenges and hardships.

~
啃
This word implies a persistent and determined effort, often with some difficulty involved.

~
改良
Implies making incremental changes or adjustments to improve something's functionality, quality, or effectiveness. It suggests a process of refinement rather than a complete overhaul.

~
预料
Implies making a prediction or estimation about something that is expected to happen in the future. It can also refer to the expectation itself.

~
飘扬
Describes the graceful and fluid movement of something light and airy, such as a flag, hair, or a ribbon, as it is carried by the wind.

~
公证
Specifically refers to the legal process of verifying the authenticity and legality of a document or transaction. It involves an official certification by a notary public or other authorized authority.

~
规章
Refer to a set of established rules or procedures that govern conduct or behavior within a specific organization, context, or field.

~
伪造
Implies creating a fraudulent imitation of something with the intent to deceive or mislead. It can involve documents, signatures, artwork, or other items of value.

~
磅
The word 磅 (bàng) is most commonly used in the expression "磅礴" (páng bó), which describes something vast, majestic, or powerful.  On its own, it refers to a unit of weight or a printing measurement, but these uses are less frequent.

~
焦急
Describes a state of intense worry, nervousness, or impatience, often accompanied by physical symptoms like restlessness or fidgeting.

~
失踪
Implies that someone's whereabouts are unknown, and they cannot be located. It suggests a sudden or unexpected disappearance, often raising concerns about their safety.

~
屑
The meaning "bits/fragments/crumbs/filings" is most common.  The other meaning, "to condescend to," is very rare.

~
救济
Specifically refers to providing aid or assistance to people in need, typically in the form of financial support, food, shelter, or other essential resources.

~
爽快
The two seemingly different meanings of 爽快 (shuǎngkuài) – "refreshed/rejuvenated" and "frank and straightforward" – are actually connected. Both convey a sense of openness and ease.  The first meaning refers to a physical feeling of invigoration, while the second refers to a direct and unhesitating manner of speaking or acting.

~
棍棒
This word can also be used metaphorically to represent physical force or violence.

~
人为
Highlights the involvement of human actions or intentions in causing or influencing something, often in contrast to natural causes or random events. It can imply deliberate manipulation or unintended consequences of human activity.

~
角落
A related word is 角 (jiǎo). 角 refers to an external corner, whereas 角落 refers to an internal corner. So, the corner of a building would be a 角, but the corner of a room would be a 角落.

~
殖民地
There is no difference between the use of 殖民地 in Chinese and "colony" in English.

~
归还
This word emphasizes returning something to its rightful owner.  If you are simply giving something back, like a borrowed pen, a better word would be 还 (huán).

~
逢
When 逢 means "to fawn upon," it is usually used in the form 逢迎 (féngyíng).

~
喘气
The word 气喘 (qìchuǎn) means asthma.

~
魔术
变戏法 (biàn xìfǎ) is another word that means magic. 变戏法 emphasizes the act of performing magic, rather than the concept of magic as a whole.

~
口气
This can also refer to the taste left in one's mouth. Another meaning is "a puff of air; breath".

~
阵地
This word has meanings beyond its military context. Figuratively, it refers to any area being defended in some sort of conflict.  For example, defending your viewpoint in an argument.

~
布告
As a verb, it is pronounced bùgào, not bùgao.

~
敞开
This word implies opening something wide for a purpose, such as letting in fresh air or to welcome guests.  It implies an open, receptive attitude.

~
摧残
This implies an ongoing process of destruction.

~
贤惠
This is almost exclusively used to describe women (traditionally wives), specifically referring to managing a household and treating other family members well. It can be somewhat old-fashioned.

~
廉洁
This term is usually used to describe someone in a position of power, most commonly politicians or officials.

~
立方
When used as an abbreviation, 立方 (lìfāng) is pronounced with the fourth tone.  It is pronounced with the first tone when it means "cube" as in shape, or the third power of a number (e.g., x³).

~
演变
This word describes gradual change and development. The word 演化 (yǎnhuà) is a near synonym which focuses on the process of evolution, particularly in biology.

~
导向
导向 can act as a verb, but it is more commonly used as a noun.

~
可恶
This word is strong and expresses a high degree of disgust or hate.

~
冷酷
This word can imply a lack of compassion and empathy to the point of cruelty.

~
打量
When this means "to suppose" or "to reckon", it implies making a rough estimate or a guess based on observation.

~
谦逊
This word connotes sincerity and genuineness in one's humility.

~
指令
This is a more formal and technical term, often associated with computing, military commands, or official orders. 命令 (mìnglìng) is a more common and general term for "order" or "command."

~
布局
Beyond its concrete meanings, it can also metaphorically refer to strategic planning or arrangements in a broader context, such as business strategies or career paths.

~
考古
This word also refers to the academic discipline of archaeology.

~
独裁
This implies absolute power and often tyrannical rule.

~
磋商
This refers to formal discussions between parties, often involving negotiation and compromise. 

~
颈椎
Be careful not to confuse this with the word “颈部” (jǐngbù) which simply refers to the neck as a whole.

~
贝壳
This word usually refers specifically to seashells rather than the shells of other mollusks such as snails or land slugs.

~
嗅觉
There is no significant difference between the use of 嗅觉 in Chinese and "sense of smell" in English.

~
斑
The character itself can also mean spot, mark, speckle, etc. When used to refer to animal patterns, it can refer to the overall pattern of spots or stripes.

~
解剖
This term can be used metaphorically to mean analyzing a problem in detail.

~
偏偏
Note the difference between 偏偏 and 偏偏 is that 偏偏 emphasizes the unexpected and undesired nature of the situation, while 偏偏 emphasizes the deliberate and contrary action of the subject.

~
作弊
Cheating can also be expressed more colloquially as  cheating, such as on a test.

~
品德
This word encompasses both moral character and ethical behavior.

~
正负
This word can be used in broader contexts to represent opposites or contrasting forces.

~
思索
This word suggests a more profound and contemplative thought process than simply thinking.

~
拖延
 This implies putting things off intentionally, often out of procrastination or avoidance.

~
萌芽
Figuratively, this describes the beginning or early stages of something, like an idea, a trend, or a movement.

~
把手
把手 can also mean "to take charge of something" (掌管).

~
壮丽
This word evokes a sense of awe and grandeur.

~
逐年
This emphasizes a steady and consistent change over time.

~
口头
A related word is 当面 (dāngmiàn). Both words relate to something being said in person, but 口头 (kǒutóu) emphasizes that the communication is spoken rather than written, whereas 当面 emphasizes that the communication is taking place in the presence of the person being addressed. So 口头协议 (kǒutóu xiéyì) is an "oral agreement," while 当面道谢 (dāngmiàn dào xiè) is "thanking someone in person."

~
融洽
This word is typically used to describe interpersonal relationships. It is not really used in other contexts, such as to describe the taste of food.

~
间隔
This word relates to both time and space. Another similar word is 间隙 (jiànxì).  Both words mean "interval" or "gap."  间隔 is more general and can be used for both space and time.  间隙 usually refers to a small gap or interval and is more often used in the context of time.

~
劈
The word 劈 (pī) is often used in combination with other characters to create words with more specific meanings. For example, 劈柴 (pī chái) means "to chop firewood," 劈腿 (pītuǐ) means "to do the splits," and 劈啪 (pīpā) means "crackling" or "snapping" sound.

~
排斥
This is often used to describe immune reactions. It is less frequently used in social situations. In social situations, it often implies active discrimination rather than simple dislike.

~
暂且
暂且 (zànqiě) is used to indicate a temporary state of affairs. It often suggests that the current situation is not ideal or permanent and that a change is expected in the future. It's often used in conjunction with other words that reinforce this temporary nature, such as 先 (xiān, "first") or 等一下 (děng yīxià, "wait a moment").  For example, you could say "我们暂且在这里休息一下" (wǒmen zànqiě zài zhèlǐ xiūxí yīxià), which translates to "Let's rest here for a while."

~
庄严
This word is often collocated with other positive words such as 隆重 (lóngzhòng, grand) or 盛大 (shèngdà, magnificent) to emphasize the significance and solemnity of an occasion.

~
灵感
Aside from meaning inspiration, this word also can refer to a hunch.

~
当面
A similar word is 面对面 (miàn duì miàn).  This means "face to face" and emphasizes the directness of the interaction.

~
油腻
Note that the meanings "greasy food" and "vulgar" are completely unrelated. The second meaning is a slang usage.

~
迁徙
This word can describe the movement of either animals or people.

~
羞耻
羞耻 (xiūchǐ) is a more formal and literary term for shame than the more commonly used words like  不好意思 (bù hǎoyìsi) or  难为情 (nánwéiqíng).

~
物资
物资 (wùzī) refers to physical goods and supplies, typically necessities like food, clothing, and fuel. It is often used in contexts like disaster relief or military logistics. It emphasizes tangible items rather than abstract concepts or services.

~
饲养
This word can describe the raising of either livestock or pets.

~
会晤
会晤 (huìwù) is a formal term for a meeting, often implying a high-level encounter between officials or dignitaries.  It suggests a planned and significant meeting rather than a casual get-together.

~
踪迹
踪迹 (zōngjì) refers to the traces or tracks left by someone or something, often implying that they are being followed or searched for. It carries a sense of mystery and often appears in detective stories or tales of adventure.

~
索取
索取 (suǒqǔ) carries a negative connotation of demanding or extorting something, often aggressively or unfairly. It differs from simple requests and implies an entitlement or a lack of consideration for the giver.

~
悲哀
悲哀 (bēi'āi) conveys a deep sense of sorrow or grief, often associated with a significant loss or disappointment. It is more intense and profound than simple sadness and suggests a lasting emotional impact.

~
隔阂
隔阂 (géhé) refers to a barrier or estrangement in a relationship, often caused by misunderstanding or a lack of communication. It implies a distance and coolness between individuals or groups.

~
吃苦
吃苦 (chīkǔ) emphasizes the endurance of hardship and the development of resilience. It often carries a positive connotation of learning valuable lessons through difficult experiences.

~
标记
标记 (biāojì) can be both a noun and a verb, referring to a mark or sign used for identification or the act of making such a mark.  It can be used in various contexts, from labeling objects to marking locations on a map.

~
急躁
急躁 (jízào) describes impatience and irritability, often manifested as a quick temper and a tendency to rush things. It suggests a lack of calmness and composure.

~
监视
监视 (jiānshì) means to closely monitor or surveil someone or something, usually with a sense of control or suspicion.  It often carries a negative connotation, implying a lack of trust or the potential for intrusive observation.

~
巷
In mainland China, this word is generally used in the names of streets, e.g. 王府井大街 (Wángfǔjǐng Dàjiē) and 小吃胡同 (Xiǎochī Hútòng), where 大街 (Dàjiē) means "avenue" and 胡同 (Hútòng) means "alley" or "lane".  If you hear someone refer to simply to a "胡同" (Hútòng), they are likely talking about the specific place in Beijing.


~
急切
急切 (jíqiè) describes a strong sense of urgency and eagerness, often related to achieving a specific goal or obtaining something desired. It implies impatience and a desire for immediate action.

~
恭敬
恭敬 (gōngjìng) conveys a deep sense of respect and deference, often towards elders or superiors. It suggests a polite and humble attitude.

~
严寒
严寒 (yánhán) refers to extremely cold weather, often below freezing. It emphasizes the severity and harshness of the cold.

~
塑造
塑造 (sùzào) is often used in a figurative sense, referring to the creation or development of something intangible, like a character's personality or a company's image.

~
砍伐
砍伐 (kǎnfá) refers specifically to cutting down trees, often on a large scale.  It implies the removal of trees for purposes like logging or clearing land.

~
保重
保重 (bǎozhòng) is a common way to express care and concern for someone's well-being, often used in parting or during times of illness. It is a more formal and heartfelt way to say "take care."

~
忙碌
忙碌 (mánglù) describes a state of being busy and occupied, often with many tasks or responsibilities.  It suggests a high level of activity and a demanding schedule.

~
绅士
绅士 (shēnshì) refers to a gentleman, often implying good manners, courtesy, and refined behavior. It suggests a person of high social standing and impeccable character.

~
挥霍
挥霍 (huīhuò) means to squander or waste resources, often money or time, in a reckless or extravagant manner. It implies a lack of responsibility and careful planning.

~
奢侈
奢侈 (shēchǐ) describes something luxurious and extravagant, often beyond what is necessary or affordable. It suggests indulgence and a focus on material pleasures.

~
耍
The word 耍 (shuǎ) has many meanings depending on context and collocations.  For instance, 耍朋友 (shuǎ péngyou) means to date or to be in a romantic relationship with someone. 耍脾气 (shuǎ píqi) means to throw a tantrum or to lose one's temper. 耍花招 (shuǎ huāzhāo) means to play tricks.


~
美妙
美妙 (měimiào) describes something beautiful, wonderful, and delightful, often referring to experiences or sensations.  It suggests a sense of pleasure and enjoyment.

~
做主
The phrase 做主 (zuòzhǔ) means "to make a decision" or "to take charge".  It emphasizes the authority and responsibility of the decision-maker.

~
体系
体系 (tǐxì) refers to a system or framework, often complex and organized, composed of interconnected parts. It suggests a structured and coherent whole.

~
高超
高超 (gāochāo) describes a high level of skill, expertise, or ability.  It implies exceptional proficiency and mastery in a particular area.

~
留神
留神 (liúshén) means to pay attention or be careful, often used as a warning to avoid danger or mistakes. It emphasizes vigilance and caution.

~
呻吟
Can be used figuratively to describe the creaking or groaning of objects, like trees in the wind or old machinery.

~
分歧
Often used in formal contexts, like political discussions or academic debates, to describe disagreements or differences in opinion.  A more colloquial equivalent might be 不同意 (bù tóngyì) or 有分歧 (yǒu fēnqí).

~
序言
Sometimes used metaphorically to refer to the beginning of something, not just a book, like the 序言 of a new era or project.

~
沮丧
Often collocates with words like “感到” (gǎndào, to feel) or “显得” (xiǎnde, to appear).  For example, 他感到很沮丧 (tā gǎndào hěn jǔsàng, he felt very dejected).

~
验收
Often used in a technical or official context, such as construction projects or product delivery.

~
荣誉
Can be used both as a noun and an adjective. As an adjective, it precedes a noun to describe something honorable, like 荣誉称号 (róngyù chēnghào - honorary title).

~
惋惜
Often followed by the particle “地” (de) before a verb or adjective, e.g., 他惋惜地说 (tā wǎnxī de shuō - He said regretfully).

~
上进
Usually used to describe young people who are ambitious and strive to improve. It can also be used with “心” (xīn, heart) to form the noun “上进心” (shàngjìnxīn), meaning ambition or the desire to improve.

~
空白
Can also refer to a gap in knowledge or memory, like a mental blank.

~
陶醉
Often followed by the preposition “于” (yú) or “在” (zài), indicating the source of enchantment or infatuation.  For example, 她陶醉于音乐中 (tā táozuì yú yīnyuè zhōng - She was intoxicated by the music).

~
畔
Usually used in fixed expressions, such as 河畔 (hé pàn - riverbank) or 湖畔 (hú pàn - lakeside).  It's less commonly used on its own.

~
弊端
Usually refers to a flaw or defect inherent within a system or institution, rather than a one-time error or mistake.

~
干旱
Can be used metaphorically to describe something lacking vitality or excitement.

~
话筒
In modern usage, mainly refers to a microphone.  Using it to mean a telephone receiver might sound outdated.

~
大不了
Has a casual, even dismissive, tone and is often used to downplay the seriousness of a situation.

~
处境
Usually describes a difficult or unfavorable situation.

~
非法
Often used in legal or official contexts.  A more colloquial equivalent is 不合法 (bù héfǎ).

~
反常
Often used in scientific or technical contexts to describe something deviating from the norm.

~
刊物
A relatively formal word for publications, often used for academic journals or official bulletins.

~
雌雄
Can be used metaphorically to describe the outcome of a competition or battle, with the winner being the 雄 (xióng - male) and the loser being the 雌 (cí - female).

~
偿还
Usually refers to repaying debts or loans, rather than returning borrowed items.

~
方圆
Typically used for distances, such as 方圆十里 (fāngyuán shí lǐ - within a radius of ten miles).

~
并列
Often used to describe items of equal importance or status.

~
言论
Can sometimes carry a negative connotation, suggesting controversial or irresponsible speech.

~
秤
In modern usage, more often refers to a small scale used in kitchens or markets.  A larger platform scale would be called a 地秤 (dìchèng).

~
缺席
Often collocates with meetings, classes, or other organized events.

~
化妆
Can also refer to camouflage or disguise.

~
摸索
Implies a lack of clear direction or understanding, often in a new or unfamiliar situation.

~
捣乱
Often used to describe children's mischievous behavior.

~
舒畅
Often used to describe a feeling of physical or emotional well-being.

~
通缉
A formal legal term.

~
颇
Functions as an adverb, modifying adjectives or verbs.

~
谴责
A strong word, implying official or public disapproval.

~
花瓣
The character “瓣” (bàn) also appears in words like “蒜瓣” (suànbàn, clove of garlic) or “桔瓣” (júbàn, segment of an orange).

~
亏待
Usually implies unintentional neglect or unfair treatment, rather than deliberate malice.

~
恳切
Implies a deep and sincere desire for something.

~
磁带
Outdated in most contexts.

~
开拓
Often used metaphorically to describe expanding one's knowledge or skills.

~
司法
A formal term often used in legal or political discussions.

~
志气
This word is more about having the "spirit" to accomplish something difficult, rather than simply having a goal.  It's about having backbone and drive.  It can be translated as "resolve" or "guts."

~
报复
A more formal synonym is 报仇 (bàochóu).

~
清除
This word emphasizes completely eliminating something, often something undesirable or harmful.

~
变质
For food, this means "to spoil" or "go bad".  For abstract things, this means to degenerate morally or ethically.  It does *not* mean simply to change in nature (变化).

~
平行
This word can also mean "of equal rank" in a hierarchy, or simultaneous events which do not intersect.

~
椭圆
Although 椭圆 can mean "oval", it's usually used to describe a precise mathematical ellipse, whereas 卵形 (luǎnxíng) is used for general oval shapes.

~
才干
This word implies not just ability, but also talent and potential. It's often used to describe someone's leadership qualities or capability in a particular field.

~
反面
When referring to the "other side of a problem", 反面 highlights the negative or opposing aspects.

~
财务
This word specifically refers to the management of finances, often in a business or organizational context.  It's not simply "money".

~
响亮
Besides meaning "loud and clear", 响亮 can also describe a name or slogan that is memorable and impactful.

~
胡乱
This word describes actions done carelessly or without thought, potentially leading to negative consequences.

~
刹那
This word emphasizes the extreme brevity of a moment, often a fleeting or ephemeral experience.

~
敏捷
This word describes both physical quickness and mental agility or sharpness.

~
功劳
This word highlights contributions that have brought significant positive results or achievements.

~
牢固
This word emphasizes something being firmly fixed or deeply ingrained, implying stability and resistance to change.

~
粉碎
This word suggests complete destruction, often violently, leaving something in pieces or fragments.

~
刊登
This word specifically refers to publishing in print media like newspapers or magazines, not just any form of publication.

~
尸体
Remember the measure word for 尸体 is 具 (jù).

~
借助
This emphasizes utilizing something as a tool or support to achieve a goal.

~
歹徒
This term strongly implies criminal intent and harmful actions, not just someone who is bad or unpleasant.

~
履行
This word highlights the responsible and dutiful execution of a commitment, often formal or legal.

~
蚂蚁
The measure word for 蚂蚁 is 只 (zhī).  Also note that a colony of ants is called an ant "nest" (蚁巢 - yǐcháo)

~
勤俭
This word emphasizes the combination of hard work and thriftiness, often seen as virtues.

~
思念
This word describes a deep emotional longing or missing someone or something.

~
气势
This word refers to an aura of power, grandeur, or imposing presence, often associated with natural landscapes or influential figures.

~
对策
This word emphasizes a strategic response to a specific problem or challenge.

~
后代
This word can refer to both direct descendants and future generations in a broader sense.

~
掩饰
This word implies an intention to deceive or hide the truth.

~
胸膛
This word refers specifically to the chest area, often associated with emotions or vulnerability.

~
领事馆
This refers specifically to a consulate, a diplomatic mission smaller than an embassy.

~
喜悦
This word expresses a feeling of deep joy and happiness.

~
空隙
This word can refer to both physical gaps and intervals in time.

~
洽谈
This word suggests formal discussions, often for business or diplomatic purposes.

~
资深
This word emphasizes extensive experience and a high level of expertise in a particular field.

~
陈列
This word implies a deliberate arrangement of items for display, often in a museum or exhibition.

~
大臣
This word can refer to high-ranking officials in both historical and contemporary contexts.

~
搓
This word describes a specific rubbing motion, often involving rolling something between the fingers.

~
充当
This word highlights taking on a role or function, often temporarily or in a specific situation.

~
请示
This word implies requesting guidance or approval from a higher authority.

~
书记
This word can refer to both administrative secretaries and party officials in a communist context.

~
和解
This word is more formal (书面) than other ways of saying "reconcile," such as 重归于好 (chóngguīyúhǎo).

~
豪迈
This word is usually used to describe a person's personality. It is not usually used to describe physical size.

~
东道主
Can be used metaphorically, e.g.  在人工智能领域，中国正逐渐成为东道主 (In the field of artificial intelligence, China is gradually becoming the host/leader).

~
将就
Often used with the word "凑合" (còuhe), which has a similar meaning. 将就 is slightly more formal.

~
推论
More formal than other ways of saying "infer," such as "猜" (cāi).

~
咋
This word is dialectal and rarely used in writing. In most contexts, 怎么 (zěnme) is preferred.

~
流露
This word suggests something being revealed unintentionally or subtly.

~
拄
Specifically describes leaning on something long and thin, such as a cane or crutch.  It would not be used for leaning against a wall.  For that, you'd use "靠" (kào).

~
准则
More formal than other words for "standard," such as 标准 (biāozhǔn). Often used for moral or ethical principles.

~
勘探
Specifically refers to searching for natural resources.

~
告诫
More formal and serious than other ways of saying "warn," such as 提醒 (tíxǐng).

~
活该
Very informal and can be quite rude.  Use with caution.

~
审理
This specifically refers to the legal process of examining and judging a case.

~
振奋
Often used in a patriotic or inspirational context.

~
反馈
Can be used as both a noun and a verb.

~
垂直
A more scientific/technical term than other ways of saying "vertical," such as 竖直 (shùzhí).

~
戒备
Often used in military or emergency contexts.

~
耐用
Similar to "durable," but it also carries a slight connotation of being able to withstand difficult situations.

~
稿件
This word refers to any written material submitted for publication, such as articles, manuscripts, etc.

~
蔚蓝
Specifically refers to the deep blue color of the sky or sea. It doesn't refer to other shades of blue.

~
边界
More formal than other words for "boundary," such as 边 (biān). Often used in political or geographical contexts.

~
灿烂
Can be used metaphorically to describe a bright future or brilliant achievements.

~
荒唐
Implies not only absurdity, but also a sense of moral disapproval.

~
火焰
Refers to the actual visible part of a fire.  "火" (huǒ) is the more general word for "fire."

~
风趣
Implies a refined and elegant sense of humor.

~
敷衍
When meaning "perfunctory," it can be written as 敷衍了事 (fūyǎnliǎoshì).

~
气味
Can be either pleasant or unpleasant.  For a specifically pleasant smell, use "香味" (xiāngwèi); for an unpleasant smell, use "臭味" (chòuwèi).

~
凹凸
Describes a surface that is not smooth.

~
丰盛
Often used to describe meals, banquets, etc.

~
罪犯
More formal than other words for "criminal," such as 坏人 (huàirén).

~
作风
Often used to describe the way someone works or behaves, especially in a professional setting.

~
颤抖
Implies a more intense shaking than other words for "shake," such as 抖 (dǒu).

~
坚实
Describes something that is both firm and solid.

~
盯
Implies a fixed and intense gaze.

~
牢骚
Often used in a negative context, suggesting petty complaints.

~
应酬
Refers specifically to social obligations, often related to business or work.

~
领悟
Implies a deeper understanding achieved through reflection or insight.

~
拜托
Used when asking a favor, and can be translated as "please" in English.

~
纯粹
Can be used to emphasize the absolute nature of something.

~
辽阔
Used to describe vast expanses of land or sea.

~
心眼儿
This word has several meanings. It can mean "thought," "mind," or "intention." It can also refer to a "willingness to accept new ideas" or "baseless suspicions." Note the "儿" (er) suffix, which makes this word colloquial.  Without the 儿, 心眼 (xīnyǎn) is more literary and refers to someone's tolerance, or capacity for forgiveness.

~
慎重
This word emphasizes careful consideration and prudence, often in making important decisions. It implies a sense of gravity and responsibility.

~
炉灶
While 炉灶 generally refers to a stove, it can also be used metaphorically to represent a system, framework, or approach, especially in political or economic contexts.  For example, "经济炉灶" (jīngjì lú zào) - economic framework.

~
适宜
适宜 suggests something is suitable and fitting for a particular purpose, occasion, or person. It often implies a sense of harmony and appropriateness.

~
投掷
This verb emphasizes the action of throwing with force and aiming for a specific target.  It is more formal than 扔 (rēng).

~
永恒
永恒 describes something that is timeless and unending. It carries a sense of grandness and permanence.

~
支流
支流 specifically refers to a smaller river or stream that flows into a larger one.  It does not refer to other types of tributaries.

~
构思
构思 refers to the mental process of conceiving, designing, or planning something, especially a creative work like a novel or a painting. It emphasizes the intellectual and imaginative aspects of creation.

~
事态
事态 refers to the state of affairs or the development of a situation, often implying a dynamic and potentially changing context.

~
温带
温带 refers specifically to the temperate zone between the tropics and the polar circles.

~
驱逐
驱逐 describes the act of forcing someone to leave a place, often implying a sense of authority or power.

~
唠叨
唠叨 describes repetitive and often tedious talking, often complaining or nagging.

~
盛情
盛情 refers to exceptional kindness, hospitality, or enthusiasm, often exceeding normal expectations.

~
表态
表态 describes the act of expressing one's stance or opinion publicly, often in a formal or official setting.

~
即便
即便 introduces a hypothetical situation, equivalent to "even if" or "even though." It can also mean "right away" or "immediately," but this usage is less common.

~
船舶
船舶 is a collective term for ships and boats, often used in formal or technical contexts.

~
制止
制止 describes the act of stopping or preventing something from happening, often forcefully or decisively.

~
传授
传授 emphasizes the passing down of knowledge, skills, or traditions from one person to another.

~
侮辱
侮辱 refers to the act of insulting or humiliating someone, causing them to lose face or dignity.

~
澄清
澄清 has two main meanings: (1) to become clear or to clarify, often referring to liquids or situations; (2) to clear up a misunderstanding or misconception.

~
心得
心得 refers to insights, understanding, or lessons learned from experience, reading, or reflection. It often implies a personal and profound understanding.

~
钞票
钞票 specifically refers to paper money or banknotes, as opposed to coins.

~
气概
气概 describes a person's spirit, mettle, or lofty quality, often implying courage, determination, and an impressive demeanor.

~
惊动
惊动 means to disturb, alarm, or startle someone.

~
辩护
辩护 refers to speaking in defense of someone or something, often in a legal or formal context.

~
发扬
发扬 describes the act of developing, promoting, or carrying forward something positive, such as a tradition or a good quality.

~
立交桥
立交桥 refers to an overpass or flyover, a bridge that carries one road over another.

~
古怪
古怪 describes something strange, eccentric, or unusual.

~
翼
翼 has multiple meanings, including wing (of a bird or airplane), flank (of an army), and a supporting role.  It also has a rare astronomical meaning.

~
垫
垫 can be a noun meaning a pad, cushion, or mat or a verb meaning to pad, cushion, or advance money.

~
落成
落成 is specifically used for the completion of a construction project, typically a large building or monument.

~
拘束
拘束 describes feeling constrained, awkward, or ill at ease, often due to social conventions or unfamiliar surroundings.

~
锋利
锋利 means sharp, often referring to blades or cutting tools.  It can also be used figuratively to describe incisive or to-the-point language.

~
挖掘
挖掘 describes the act of digging or excavating, often to uncover something hidden or valuable.  It can also be used metaphorically to describe exploring or uncovering information.

~
闪烁
闪烁 describes a flickering or twinkling light. It can also refer to evasive or vague speech.

~
诚挚
诚挚 emphasizes sincerity and cordiality, often in expressing feelings or intentions.

~
简陋
简陋 describes something simple, crude, or lacking in amenities.

~
泄气
泄气 can mean to leak gas, but more commonly it means to be discouraged, disheartened, or to lose enthusiasm.

~
吝啬
吝啬 means stingy or miserly, unwilling to spend or share money.
~
验证
验证 refers to the process of verifying or confirming something, often through experimentation or evidence.

~
力争
Often used in official contexts, similar to the English "strive to".

~
行政
行政 often refers to general administration or the executive branch, as opposed to legislation or the judiciary.

~
宏伟
宏伟 describes something grand and magnificent in scale, often used for buildings, plans, or natural landscapes.  It implies an impressive scope and stature.

~
师范
师范 specifically relates to teacher training. A 师范大学 is a normal university.

~
哄
哄 has many meanings, so pay attention to context. When it means "to deceive," it carries a negative connotation.

~
经纬
经纬 can be used metaphorically to refer to the main points or gist of something.

~
丁
丁 has many meanings. It can be a surname, a classifier for male adults, a stem in the Chinese sexagenary cycle, and even a chemical term.

~
跟踪
跟踪 implies a covert or stealthy form of following.

~
疙瘩
疙瘩 can refer to a physical lump or knot, but also to a metaphorical "knot" in one's heart, representing a worry or problem.

~
动荡
动荡 describes instability and turbulence, often in a social or political context.

~
晋升
晋升 specifically refers to promotion to a higher position or rank, often in a professional setting.

~
愈
愈 intensifies the adjective or adverb it precedes, meaning "the more... the more..."  For example, 愈多愈好 (yuè duō yuè hǎo) means "the more, the better."

~
苦涩
苦涩 can describe a literal bitter and astringent taste, but also a metaphorical feeling of pain or bitterness, often related to emotional experiences.

~
识别
识别 emphasizes the ability to differentiate and recognize specific features or characteristics.

~
检讨
检讨 carries a connotation of serious reflection and self-criticism, often in the context of admitting mistakes and taking responsibility.

~
压缩
压缩 implies reducing the size or volume of something, often by applying pressure or force.

~
枕头
In China, pillows have traditionally been hard, unlike the softer pillows commonly used in the West.

~
气色
气色 refers to the overall appearance of one's face, reflecting their health and well-being.

~
投机
投机 can have a negative connotation when referring to speculation or profiteering, suggesting opportunistic behavior.

~
神仙
神仙 are often depicted in Chinese mythology and folklore, possessing supernatural powers and immortality.

~
宰
宰 is a versatile character with several meanings. In colloquial contexts, it can mean to rip someone off.

~
探望
探望 usually involves visiting someone out of concern or care, especially when they are sick or in a difficult situation.

~
督促
督促 implies urging someone to complete a task, often with a sense of oversight and encouragement.

~
无耻
无耻 is a strong term to describe someone shameless and lacking in moral integrity.

~
招标
招标 is a formal process of soliciting bids for a project or contract.

~
样品
样品 is a representative example of a product used for demonstration or testing.

~
繁华
繁华 describes a bustling and prosperous urban scene, often characterized by vibrant commercial activity.

~
势必
势必 indicates something that is certain or inevitable.

~
朝代
朝代 refers to a specific period of rule by a particular dynasty in Chinese history.

~
喉咙
Be mindful of the tones.

~
音响
音响 can refer to sound in general, but it's also commonly used to denote audio equipment like a stereo system.

~
勉强
勉强 can describe doing something with difficulty or reluctantly, or something that is barely sufficient.

~
精简
精简 emphasizes efficiency and streamlining, often involving reducing complexity or redundancy.

~
朴素
朴素 describes a simple and unadorned style, often associated with humility and frugality.

~
抚摸
抚摸 implies a gentle and caring touch, often used to comfort or express affection.

~
省会
省会 is the administrative center of a province.

~
固体
固体 is a scientific term for a substance in its solid state.

~
皇后
皇后 specifically refers to the empress, the wife of the emperor.

~
牵扯
牵扯 can mean to implicate someone in a matter or to describe the interconnectedness of things.

~
遗失
遗失 implies losing something unintentionally or accidentally.

~
内涵
This word has two main meanings. It can refer to "meaningful content" such as the meaning of a piece of art or literature. It can also refer to a person's "inner qualities". Note that these inner qualities are usually positive qualities.

~
往常
This word is similar to 平常 (píngcháng), but perhaps a little more formal.

~
隐瞒
This word is usually used in negative contexts, when someone is concealing the truth about something bad.

~
屡次
This word means "repeatedly", but with a connotation of "too many times". Usually whatever is being repeated is undesirable.

~
涮火锅
The character 涮 is pronounced shuàn in this context, but it's often mispronounced as shuān, because that pronunciation is used in another context: 涮羊肉 (shuān yángròu).

~
备忘录
Like the English word "memorandum", this word is usually abbreviated to 备忘 (bèiwàng).

~
复兴
Note that this word can also refer to Fuxing District of Handan city or Fuxing township of north Taiwan.

~
无辜
Aside from its meaning of "innocent", this word also carries a connotation of "undeserving of something bad that happened".

~
委员
Can mean member of any committee. Note that the word 委员会 (wěiyuánhuì) means "committee".

~
慷慨
The pronunciations are kāngkǎi when it means generous and kàngkǎi when it means vehement. However, the meaning of vehement is very rare.

~
蔑视
This word often collocates with the word 不屑 (búxiè).

~
渔民
The traditional character is 漁民.

~
争端
Usually used for international disputes.

~
昏迷
This word can be used as either a verb or a noun.

~
纽扣儿
The 儿 (er) is frequently dropped in spoken language.

~
粉色
Has two common uses: 1) to describe a colour between white and red; and 2) to describe content that has erotic or sexual undertones.

~
哼
Can be pronounced hēng (to groan), hng (humph!), or hng (to hum).

~
开朗
Can be used to describe both a physical space and someone's character. When used to describe a physical space, it means spacious and well-lit, and when used to describe a character, it implies an optimistic, happy and carefree attitude.

~
节制
This word is often used to mean "to show restraint"

~
譬如
More formal than 例如 (lìrú) or 比方说 (bǐfāngshuō).

~
丢人
This is always undesirable.

~
以致
This is usually used to describe something with a negative effect, e.g. 他喝多了酒，以致开车出了车祸 (tā hē duō le jiǔ, yǐzhì kāichē chū le chēhuò).

~
麻木
Unlike the English word numb, this word can be used in a metaphorical sense. For example, one might say a person is emotionally numb.

~
损坏
This can refer to either physical objects or abstract things, such as reputation.

~
巡逻
The traditional character form is 巡邏.

~
神圣
This word often collocates with 不可侵犯 (bùkě qīnfàn), to mean "sacrosanct".

~
噪音
This can either refer to unpleasant noise of any kind, or more specifically to static on a phone line etc.

~
携带
In Taiwan, this word can also be pronounced [xī dài].

~
惊奇
A book called "Hatchet" was translated as "惊奇之旅". The word can be used as a verb, adjective or noun.

~
衰退
More commonly refers to an economic recession.

~
坚硬
Usually used for solids.

~
瘸
This word is a little impolite. A more polite word is 跛 (bǒ).

~
边疆
A poetic way of saying 边境 (biānjìng).

~
清澈
This implies both clear and clean.

~
学说
More grand than 理论 (lǐlùn), and usually implies a long and complex idea with historical implications.

~
追悼
The traditional characters are 追悼.

~
推翻
Can either mean "to overthrow" or "to overturn" (e.g. an earlier decision).

~
欣慰
This word implies a sense of relief.

~
沼泽
The traditional character is 澤.



~
私自
私自 (sīzì) emphasizes doing something without permission, often secretly or covertly.  It carries a negative connotation, suggesting a violation of rules or trust.  A close synonym is 擅自 (shànzì), but 私自 carries a stronger implication of personal gain or hiding the action.

~
反感
The definition of 反感 (fǎngǎn) as "to be disgusted with" is slightly misleading. A better translation might be "to have a strong aversion to" or "to be strongly repelled by." While disgust can be involved, 反感 is broader and can describe a strong dislike for something that isn't necessarily disgusting, such as a particular personality trait or style of music.

~
崭新
崭新 (zhǎnxīn) is a stronger term than just "new." It implies a pristine, completely unused condition, as if just taken out of the box.

~
疲倦
疲倦 (píjuàn) is more formal than 累 (lèi) and implies more mental and emotional exhaustion in addition to physical tiredness.

~
奔波
奔波 (bēnbō) describes continuous and exhausting travel or activity, often for work or a specific purpose. It emphasizes the tiring and relentless nature of the movement rather than the speed or distance covered.

~
气功
Be mindful of the tones: 气功 (qìgōng).  It might be helpful to know that the first character, 气 (qì), refers to "vital energy," while the second, 功 (gōng), means "skill" or "practice."

~
恐吓
恐吓 (kǒnghè) suggests a serious threat, often involving violence or other harmful actions.  It's stronger than a simple warning.

~
丑恶
丑恶 (chǒu'è) refers to something morally repulsive or despicable, not just physically unattractive. It describes evil or wickedness.

~
引擎
引擎 (yǐnqíng) is indeed a loanword.  While 台 (tái) is a common measure word for engines, 部 (bù) can also be used.

~
阵容
阵容 (zhènróng) can also describe a powerful or impressive group of people assembled for a particular purpose, such as a team of experts.

~
后勤
后勤 (hòuqín) encompasses all support activities that ensure the smooth operation of an organization or military force, not just supplies and transportation.

~
真挚
真挚 (zhēnzhì) describes feelings that are deeply felt and genuine, not just superficially polite or friendly.

~
开明
开明 (kāimíng) suggests a willingness to consider new ideas and adapt to changing circumstances, often in contrast to traditional or conservative views.

~
榜样
榜样 (bǎngyàng) is a role model, someone worthy of emulation.

~
开除
开除 (kāichú) is a formal term for expulsion or dismissal, often from a job or organization.

~
沉淀
In its figurative sense, 沉淀 (chéndiàn) often refers to the accumulation of experience or knowledge over time.

~
教养
教养 (jiàoyǎng) refers to good manners, upbringing, and refinement. It suggests not just education, but also the cultivation of proper social behavior.

~
嚷
嚷 (rǎng) implies loud and often insistent shouting or yelling, often in a complaining or demanding manner.

~
仁慈
仁慈 (réncí) is a more profound and encompassing form of kindness than just being nice or polite. It suggests compassion, empathy, and a deep concern for the well-being of others.

~
毅然
毅然 (yìrán) emphasizes the decisiveness and unwavering resolve of an action taken, often despite difficulties or opposition.

~
揍
揍 (zòu) is a colloquial and somewhat forceful term for hitting or beating someone.

~
正气
正气 (zhèngqì) refers to a righteous or morally upright spirit, often in the face of adversity. It suggests integrity and courage.

~
确信
确信 (quèxìn) implies a strong and unwavering belief, based on solid evidence or reasoning.

~
自卑
自卑 (zìbēi) describes a lack of confidence and self-worth, often accompanied by feelings of inadequacy or inferiority.

~
章程
章程 (zhāngchéng) are the formal written rules or regulations that govern an organization or activity.

~
警惕
警惕 (jǐngtì) implies being watchful and cautious, anticipating potential danger or problems.

~
防御
防御 (fángyù) focuses on protective measures taken to prevent or mitigate harm, either physical or otherwise.

~
不像话
不像话 (bù xiàng huà) is a strong expression of disapproval, suggesting that something is unacceptable or absurd.

~
过问
过问 (guòwèn) can also imply interfering in something that is not one's business.

~
笨拙
笨拙 (bènzhuō) describes physical clumsiness or awkwardness, as well as a lack of social grace or tact.

~
智商
智商 (zhìshāng) is an abbreviation of 智力商数 (zhìlì shāngshù).

~
传单
传单 (chuándān) are typically used for advertising or disseminating information to the public.

~
赤字
赤字 (chìzì) literally means "red figures," referring to the traditional practice of writing debts or losses in red ink.

~
触犯
触犯 (chùfàn) means to violate a law or rule, often a serious one.

~
踊跃
踊跃 (yǒngyuè) describes enthusiastic and active participation, often in a positive or constructive activity.

~
嘲笑
嘲笑 (cháoxiào) suggests mockery or ridicule with the intent to belittle or humiliate.

~
堵塞
堵塞 (dǔsè) can be used figuratively to describe anything that obstructs or hinders progress, such as a traffic jam or a bureaucratic process.

~
沐浴
沐浴 (mùyù) can also be used metaphorically to mean being immersed in something, such as sunlight or love.

~
凝固
In its figurative sense, 凝固 (nínggù) often describes a moment frozen in time or a feeling of intense focus or concentration.

~
畅销
畅销 (chàngxiāo) describes goods that are selling very well and are in high demand.

~
妄想
The word 妄想 has two main usages.  When it acts as a verb, it means "to vainly attempt".  When it acts as a noun, it means "delusion".  Be careful not to confuse these two meanings.

~
压榨
压榨 is more often used figuratively than literally. It often describes exploitation, oppression, or squeezing someone dry (financially or emotionally). For example, you might see it used in discussions of labor rights or unfair business practices.

~
巴结
This word has a negative connotation. It describes insincere flattery or fawning behavior for personal gain.  It implies a lower status person trying to gain favor with a higher status person through excessive flattery.

~
起哄
起哄 carries a connotation of a group of people joining in on boisterous teasing, jeering, or creating a disturbance. It implies a playful or mischievous, though sometimes malicious, intent.  It can sometimes imply "egging someone on".

~
跳跃
While 跳跃 can refer to various types of jumping, it often emphasizes a more energetic or lively jump, like skipping or bounding.  It can also be used figuratively to describe rapid changes or fluctuations, e.g., prices or emotions.

~
挽救
挽救 implies rescuing something from a dangerous or critical situation, often involving loss or damage. It has a more serious tone than just "saving" and suggests a greater effort to prevent a negative outcome.

~
砸
The meaning "to fail" or "to muck up" is usually used in the colloquial expression 砸锅 (záguō), which literally translates to "smash the pot" but idiomatically means "to screw up; to mess up; to botch; to fail."

~
捞
捞 can also mean to gain illicitly or through underhanded means, especially money or benefits.  For example, 捞油水 (lāo yóushui) means "to seek personal gain; to line one's pockets."

~
堤坝
堤 (dī) and 坝 (bà) are often used together, but they're not interchangeable. 堤 refers to a dike or embankment built along a river, while 坝 refers to a dam or barrier used to control or contain water.

~
特长
特长 specifically refers to a special skill or talent, something one excels at.  It is not just a general strength but a particular area of expertise or ability.

~
简化
While 简化 means to simplify, it's often used in the context of simplifying complex processes, systems, or written characters.  It can also imply reducing something to its essential elements.

~
文凭
文凭 is a more formal and official term for a diploma or certificate.  It carries more weight and prestige than just a general certificate of completion.

~
得罪
得罪 carries a stronger connotation of causing offense than simply making a mistake. It suggests causing displeasure or resentment, possibly damaging a relationship.  The polite use (excuse me!) is rare in modern Mandarin.  Most learners will only encounter the "to offend" meaning.

~
内幕
内幕 implies secrets or confidential information, often related to a scandal, conspiracy, or something not generally known to the public.

~
结算
结算 specifically refers to settling accounts or bills, often in a financial or business context.  It implies a final calculation and payment.

~
引用
Be aware of the different meanings of 引用.  In academic contexts, it means "to cite" or "to quote." In other contexts, it can mean "to recommend" or "to appoint" someone to a position.

~
责怪
责怪 suggests assigning blame or finding fault, often with a critical or disapproving tone.

~
剪彩
剪彩 is specifically used for the ceremonial ribbon-cutting at an opening or launching ceremony. It's a formal and celebratory act.

~
高明
高明 describes someone who is highly skilled, insightful, or wise, particularly in a specific area or field. It implies a level of mastery or expertise.

~
精华
精华 refers to the most refined, valuable, or essential part of something.  It can be used for physical substances or abstract concepts.

~
嘴唇
Be mindful of the measure word for 嘴唇, which is 片 (piàn).

~
果断
果断 describes decisiveness and firmness in making decisions or taking action. It implies acting quickly and confidently.

~
元宵节
The Lantern Festival is celebrated on the 15th day of the first lunar month, marking the end of the Spring Festival celebrations.

~
租赁
租赁 is a more formal term for renting or leasing, often used in legal or business contexts. It implies a contractual agreement.

~
捆绑
捆绑 often describes tying something tightly or restricting movement, sometimes with a negative connotation of being bound or constrained.

~
局限
局限 often implies being limited or confined, often by circumstances, conditions, or one's own perspective.

~
愚蠢
愚蠢 is a strong word for stupid or foolish, carrying a more negative and critical connotation.

~
波涛
波涛 describes large, rolling waves or billows, often used in poetic or literary contexts.

~
分红
分红 specifically refers to distributing profits or dividends, often in a business or investment context.

~
俘虏
俘虏 refers to a captive taken during wartime or conflict.

~
精心
精心 describes doing something with great care, attention to detail, and meticulous effort.

~
惩罚
惩罚 refers to punishment or penalty for wrongdoing, often implying a formal or official sanction.

~
丘陵
丘陵 refers to a landscape of rolling hills, typically smaller and less steep than mountains.

~
片刻
片刻 emphasizes a very short period of time, a brief moment or instant.

~
震撼
震撼 describes a strong emotional or physical shock or impact, often leaving one stunned or shaken.

~
窍门
窍门 refers to a clever trick, shortcut, or ingenious method for doing something, often implying specialized knowledge or skill.

~
不惜
不惜 is used before a verb or phrase to indicate a willingness to do or sacrifice something, regardless of the cost or consequences.

~
动脉
动脉 refers specifically to arteries, blood vessels that carry oxygenated blood away from the heart.

~
雕刻
雕刻 can refer to carving or engraving in various materials, often implying artistic skill and precision.

~
疏远
疏远 describes a gradual drifting apart or estrangement in a relationship, often due to lack of contact or communication.

~
黎明
A more poetic way to say 黎明 is 拂晓 (fúxiǎo).

~
管辖
The difference between 管辖 (guǎnxiá) and 管理 (guǎnlǐ) is subtle. 管辖 is more about official jurisdiction or legal authority, while 管理 is more about practical administration. For example, the police have 管辖权 (jurisdiction) over a certain area, but the local government 管理s (administers) the area.

~
卓越
This is a formal word.

~
狼狈
The two meanings of this word are related. The original meaning is "wolves paired with狽s" (a mythical wolf-like creature with short front legs). Because of their physical limitations, they had to cooperate to survive. Later, it came to mean a difficult situation. The slang meaning is derived from the difficult situation the wolves faced, which led to a sorry figure.

~
油漆
Be careful not to confuse this word with "oil" (油 - yóu). When talking about cooking or lubricating oils, that is usually just 油.

~
衷心
This word is almost always used as an adverb.  It is commonly paired with 祝愿 (zhùyuàn - to wish).  For example, 衷心祝愿你一切顺利 (zhōngxīn zhùyuàn nǐ yīqiè shùnlì - I sincerely wish you all the best).

~
拧
This word can also mean "to twist." The difference in meaning is given by the object of the verb. For example, 拧毛巾 (nǐng máojīn - wring a towel) means "to wring" while 拧螺丝 (nǐng luósī - twist a screw) means "to twist." Note also that while the character can have a fourth tone (as in stubborn) it is also very common for the character to be pronounced in the third tone (as in twist/wring). The character for "stubborn" can also be written as 拧巴.

~
琢磨
There is no difference between the use of 琢磨 in Chinese and "to ponder" or "to mull over" in English. Note that while the word can be pronounced zhuómó, the pronunciation zuómo is more common.

~
崇敬
This is a formal word, more common in written than spoken Chinese.

~
蹬
The Taiwan pronunciation is more common in general. The slang meaning, "to dump someone", is more common in Taiwan.

~
解雇
This word is formal.  A more informal word is 炒鱿鱼 (chǎoyóuyú - to fire).

~
打仗
Be careful not to confuse this with 打架 (dǎjià), which means "to fight" as in to engage in a physical fight.

~
恐怖
恐怖 (kǒngbù) primarily refers to psychological fear or terror.  A similar word, 可怕 (kěpà), primarily refers to something physically dangerous or harmful, rather than the psychological feeling of fear. For example, a scary movie is 恐怖, but a dangerous animal is 可怕.

~
岩石
This word is interchangeable with 石头 (shítou), but 岩石 (yánshí) is a more formal or technical term.

~
散发
散发 (sànfā) emphasizes distribution over a wide area or to a large number of people, typically something non-physical like an odor, information or emotion.  A related word, 分发 (fēnfā), implies the orderly or systematic distribution of materials or resources to a specific group of people.

~
声誉
This is quite a formal word. A more colloquial way to say this is 名声 (míngshēng).

~
加剧
This word is rather formal and generally refers to something negative or undesirable that becomes worse.

~
美观
A related word is 好看 (hǎokàn). The difference is that 美观 (měiguān) emphasizes elegance or refinement in aesthetic appearance, often related to design or artistry, while 好看 is a more general term for something visually appealing.

~
误差
There is no difference between the use of 误差 in Chinese and "error" or "inaccuracy" in English.

~
着想
This word is usually used in the form "为…着想" (wèi... zhuóxiǎng). It emphasizes consideration for another person’s needs or well-being, placing their interests before one's own.  A related word, 考虑 (kǎolǜ), means to consider all factors, not necessarily prioritizing the other person.

~
旷课
Similar to 逃学 (táoxué) and 逃课 (táokè). These are all colloquial terms for "skip class" or "play truant", but 旷课 (kuàngkè) is slightly more formal.

~
精密
This emphasizes both complexity and accuracy. For example, a 精密 (jīngmì) instrument could be both complex and highly accurate, while a simple ruler is just accurate.

~
衣裳
This word has an old-fashioned feel and is rarely used now.  Use 衣服 (yīfu) instead.

~
级别
Be careful not to confuse this with 水平 (shuǐpíng), which refers to skill, proficiency, or standard.  级别 (jíbié) refers specifically to position in a hierarchy, especially in official contexts like government, the military, or an organization.

~
伺候
This word originally meant "to serve" as in an emperor or high-ranking official, and carries connotations of servitude that might be inappropriate in modern usage. For ordinary service, like a waiter in a restaurant, use 服务 (fúwù).  When used in a more family context, it can often take on the connotation of looking after someone who is sick or frail.

~
高涨
高涨 (gāozhǎng) describes a rapid, powerful swelling, often of things not physically tangible.  A related word, 上涨 (shàngzhǎng), simply means to go up or rise, such as with prices or water levels.

~
书籍
This is a more formal and literary way to say "books". More common words are 书 (shū) and 本书 (běnshū).

~
世代
世代 (shìdài) carries a more historical or traditional connotation, suggesting continuity of families or traditions over a long period of time.  A similar word, 一代 (yīdài), simply refers to a generation as a unit of time, approximately 20-30 years.

~
元首
元首 (yuánshǒu) is specifically used for the head of state of a country, generally at the presidential or royal level. Other titles like 总理 (zǒnglǐ), 首相 (shǒuxiàng) or 国王 (guówáng) are used for head of government, prime minister, or king respectively.

~
关照
This phrase has two separate meanings: (1) keep an eye on (someone), take care of (someone); and (2) to give preferential treatment, similar to 走后门 (zǒuhòumén). Context is key to understanding which meaning is being used.

~
扛
There is no difference between 扛 (káng) and 扛 (gāng). Just use 扛 (káng).

~
铜
Be careful not to confuse this with 筒 (tǒng) or 同 (tóng).  铜 (tóng) is copper.

~
腹泻
腹泻 (fùxiè) is the more formal medical term.  拉肚子 (lādùzi) is more colloquial.

~
标本
There is no difference between the use of 标本 in Chinese and "specimen" in English.

~
水利
There is no difference between the use of 水利 in Chinese and "water conservancy" in English.

~
偏见
There is no difference between the use of 偏见 in Chinese and "prejudice" in English.

~
摇滚
This is specifically "rock and roll". Use this word only for the music genre.

~
日益
日益 (rìyì) is more formal and literary.  越来越 (yuè lái yuè) is more common in spoken Chinese.

~
启蒙
启蒙 (qǐméng) is more formal and literary.

~
发财
This word is usually used with the character 了.  For example, 发财了 (fācái le). It can also be used as a congratulatory remark during the Lunar New Year period.

~
视力
A related word is 眼力 (yǎnlì). 眼力 is more about one's ability to perceive, judge, or appreciate something, rather than just physical vision. For example, it can refer to one's ability to spot a good business opportunity or to judge a person's character.  In contrast, 视力 simply refers to the physical capacity of one's eyes to see.

~
功效
This is a somewhat formal word (书面语).  More colloquial equivalents include 作用 (zuòyòng) and 效果 (xiàoguǒ).

~
容纳
The "tolerate (different opinions)" meaning is much less common than the physical meanings.

~
猛烈
A related word is 激烈 (jīliè).  Both words describe intense actions or feelings. 猛烈 emphasizes the sheer force or power involved, often implying a sudden and violent impact. 激烈, on the other hand, focuses on the intensity or fervor of something, suggesting a high degree of excitement or agitation.  For example, 猛烈的风暴 (měngliè de fēngbào) "fierce storm" highlights the destructive power of the storm, while 激烈的辩论 (jīliè de biànlùn) "heated debate" emphasizes the passionate exchange of arguments.

~
遮挡
There is no significant difference between 遮挡 and 遮蔽 (zhēbì), though 遮蔽 is slightly more formal.

~
雷达
This is pronounced léidá.

~
趣味
More colloquial words for "interest" are  兴趣 (xìngqù) and 爱好 (àihào).

~
气压
Relatively formal (书面).  A more colloquial synonym is 气压 (qìyā).

~
耀眼
A related word is 灿烂 (cànlàn), which also describes brilliant light.  耀眼 (yàoyǎn) specifically emphasizes a brightness that is so intense it's almost blinding. 灿烂 (cànlàn) suggests a more expansive and glorious radiance, often associated with beauty or happiness. Think of the sun's glare (耀眼) versus a beautiful sunset (灿烂).

~
向来
This implies that something has *always* been true up until *now*, but might not be true any more.

~
姑且
This implies a temporary, provisional solution or acceptance of something, often because there's no better alternative at the moment or more information is needed.

~
瓦解
Although it can refer to physical objects collapsing, it is more commonly used for organizations or groups falling apart.

~
呼吁
This is formal (书面).

~
偏僻
More colloquial equivalents include 荒凉 (huāngliáng) which emphasizes emptiness and desolation, and 偏远 (piānyuǎn) emphasizes distance but not necessarily desolation.

~
鼻涕
Colloquial. The more formal (and medical) term is 鼻粘液 (bí niányè).

~
血压
The same as in English.


~
迈
Can also just mean "to step" without emphasis on largeness of step.

~
从容
Relatively formal (书面).  More colloquial words include  轻松 (qīngsōng) and 悠闲 (yōuxián).


~
馋
Relatively colloquial.

~
次品
More colloquial than 劣质品 (lièzhìpǐn).


~
淋
For the meaning of "to pour liquid (on something)," the characters are 淋 (lin2), not 淋 (lin1).  For the other meanings listed above, the characters are 淋 (lin1).

~
贪污
This word implies abuse of public funds, not private funds (such as stealing from your boss).  For stealing from a private individual or company, the word is 盗窃 (dàoqiè).

~
文雅
Relatively formal (书面).  More colloquial equivalents include  优雅 (yōuyǎ) and 斯文 (sīwén).

~
心血
This word evokes a strong sense of dedication, effort, and personal investment.  It implies that something is the result of long and painstaking labor.

~
辫子
"A mistake or shortcoming that may be exploited by an opponent" is a more specialized, figurative meaning.

~
失事
To lose something (e.g., a wallet) the words are 丢失 (diūshī) or 失去 (shīqù).

~
平庸
More formal than its near-synonyms  普通 (pǔtōng) and 一般 (yībān). 平庸 carries a negative connotation, suggesting a lack of distinction or excellence.

~
奖赏
More formal than 奖励 (jiǎnglì).  奖赏 often implies a more significant or official recognition, whereas 奖励 is more general.

~
容器
Relatively formal. More colloquial is  盒子 (hézi) if it's a box-like container or 瓶子 (píngzi) if it's bottle-shaped.


~
敬礼
This is mainly used in the military, and not commonly used otherwise.

~
犹如
More formal and literary than  像 (xiàng) or  好像 (hǎoxiàng).

~
奠定
More formal than 建立 (jiànlì). 奠定 emphasizes the act of establishing a firm foundation for something, often abstract, such as a theory or a relationship.

~
压制
Implies force in preventing something from happening. More colloquial is  控制 (kòngzhì).

~
列举
More formal (书面).  A common synonym is  举例 (jǔlì).

~
辐射
The same as in English.

~
惦记
More colloquial than  想念 (xiǎngniàn) or  挂念 (guàniàn).  惦记 implies a constant, somewhat anxious concern for someone or something.

~
起草
More formal (书面) and usually refers to official or legal documents. For less formal drafting, use  写草稿 (xiě cǎogǎo).

~
眯
This can also mean "to be sleepy," or "sleepy-eyed," or "to be nearly asleep."

~
范畴
Formal (书面).  More colloquial words include  范围 (fànwéi) and  领域 (lǐngyù).


~
逮捕
Formal.  More colloquial is 抓 (zhuā).

~
分明
This can also mean "obviously". Note that it's usually used in negative sentences such as 看不清，字迹不分明 (The handwriting is not clear; I cannot see it clearly).

~
简要
A synonym is 简洁 (jiǎnjié).

~
指南针
A more colloquial word is 指南车 (zhǐnánchē), which is usually used metaphorically.

~
寓言
The measure word 则 (zé) is only used for written works. When talking about fables in general, no measure word is needed.

~
释放
For prisoners, the more common word is now usually 释放, not other synonyms like 开释 (kāishì).

~
本钱
For the capital of a company, this word is usually now replaced by 资本 (zīběn).

~
宽容
As a verb, its usage is slightly different to the English word "to forgive". 宽容 means more like "to tolerate" or "to be lenient", while 原谅 (yuánliàng) has the same meaning as "to forgive".

~
缠绕
For the meanings "to pester" or "to bother", a synonym is 纠缠 (jiūchán).

~
颠倒
For the meanings "confused", "deranged" or "crazy", a synonym is 神志不清 (shénzhì bù qīng).

~
把关
This word is often used in a political sense, where somebody is responsible for scrutinizing or approving something, e.g., 把好意识形态关 (bǎ hǎo yìshí xíngtài guān) means maintaining strict control over the public's views, attitudes and beliefs.

~
熨
For the meaning "reconciled; smooth", this is pronounced "yù". For "an iron" or "to iron", this is pronounced "yùn". Note that 熨 is usually only used for smoothing clothes with heat. If you want to smooth something else, use 弄平 (nòng píng).

~
视野
This can also be used in the sense of "one's experiences".

~
封锁
This word usually refers to the blockade of information, communications, etc., or of a port. For a blockade by military force, use 包围 (bāowéi).

~
捍卫
This is usually used in the context of defending rights, causes or beliefs. It can thus sound quite formal.

~
梢
This can also refer to the top of a mast on a ship.

~
利害
For the meaning "pros and cons; advantages and disadvantages", this is pronounced lì hài. For the other meanings, this is pronounced lì hai.

~
固然
This word is used in the following structure:

固然…, 可是 / 但是…

What comes after 固然 is a statement that one acknowledges to be true, but then the 可是/但是 clause indicates that one is about to make a counterpoint, which weakens the significance of the point in the 固然 clause. The closest equivalent in English is "admittedly".

~
片断
A related word is 碎片 (suìpiàn), but 片断 implies that the original piece was complete, while 碎片 means the original piece itself was broken, e.g. broken glass or china.

~
向往
Similar words include 渴望 (kěwàng) and 憧憬 (chōngjǐng). The difference is that 向往 emphasizes an ideal state or type of existence, while 渴望 emphasizes an intense desire to get something missing from one's life, and 憧憬 emphasizes hope and a beautiful future vision.

~
桨
A similar word is 橹 (lǔ), but 桨 is held in the hands and moves back and forth in the water, while 橹 is attached to the side or back of the boat and moves side to side.

~
指望
The structure is 指望 + sb. + do sth.

~
力求
It is only used to emphasize that every effort is being made to *do something*. It is not used for achieving a general state, e.g. one says 力求完美 (lìqiú wánměi) "strive for perfection" and 力求创新 (lìqiú chuàngxīn) "strive for innovation", but not 力求漂亮 (lìqiú piàoliang) "strive for beauty" or 力求开心 (lìqiú kāixīn) "strive to be happy".

~
信誉
This word is used in contexts of public reputation, reliability or financial creditworthiness, and not in the sense of "prestige".

~
掩盖
This is often used in combination with an abstract noun as the object, e.g. 掩盖事实 (yǎngài shìshí) to cover up the truth.

~
和气
This is an adjective. There is no verb form.

~
遭殃
遭殃 means to suffer misfortune *as a result of some disaster*. It is different to 受苦 (shòukǔ), which means to endure hardship in general.

~
打猎
The measure word for the animal being hunted is 只 (zhī), e.g., 打了两只兔子 (dǎ le liǎng zhī tùzi) means "hunted two rabbits".

~
磨合
This can be used for two people getting along better after a period of conflict.

~
大意
For the meaning "careless", there are two related words: 粗心 (cūxīn) and 马虎 (mǎhu). 粗心 means carelessness in general, while 马虎 specifically emphasizes carelessness in speech or actions, and also means "sloppy" and "perfunctory". 大意 implies carelessness because of arrogance or overconfidence.

~
砖
Specifically, this word is used to refer to a rectangular block of fired clay used for building. Do not use this word to refer to paving slabs or concrete blocks, which are called 板砖 (bǎnzhuān).

~
否决
This word is quite formal and is usually used in the context of official pronouncements.

~
容貌
Although 容貌 has a similar meaning to 长相, there is a subtle difference. 容貌 is more objective, referring to a person's general physical characteristics (e.g., facial features, figure, complexion, etc.).  长相, on the other hand, carries a subjective evaluation of these features, implying whether someone is considered good-looking or not.

~
纳闷儿
This word is mostly used in spoken language. It expresses a mild sense of bewilderment, puzzle, or curiosity, whereas other words like "困惑" (kùn huò) often imply a greater level of confusion or perplexity.

~
荒谬
荒谬 (huāngmiù) describes something illogical or nonsensical, often implying a level of absurdity that is laughable or preposterous. It carries a stronger connotation than other words like "不合理" (bù hélǐ - unreasonable) or "没道理" (méi dàolǐ - illogical), suggesting not just a lack of logic, but also a departure from common sense or accepted norms.

~
不堪
不堪 (bùkān) is often used as part of a two-character compound word, where it modifies the second character to indicate an extreme degree of the quality described by the second character. For example, 不堪设想 (bùkān shèxiǎng) - unimaginable, too dreadful to contemplate; 不堪重负 (bùkān zhòngfù) - unable to bear a heavy load/burden; 不堪入目 (bùkān rùmù) - unsightly; an eyesore. It's usually used in more formal contexts.

~
港湾
Aside from its literal meaning of a harbor, 港湾 can also metaphorically refer to a place of shelter, comfort, or refuge, often used in a more poetic or literary context.

~
公关
公关 (gōngguān) is commonly used as an abbreviation for 公共关系 (gōnggòng guānxì), meaning "public relations." In China, the term can also carry the connotation of crisis management and even some forms of lobbying or backdoor dealing. It sometimes has a slightly negative connotation.

~
窜
This word has many different meanings. The usage notes provided cover most of its meanings. However, none of the meanings in the definitions have the meaning of "to scurry" which can be used to describe the fast movement of rats, mice, etc.

~
穿越
穿越 can also refer to the genre of fictional stories about "time travel". It is often used as a verb, but can also be a noun.

~
航天
航天 (hángtiān) specifically refers to space flight or aerospace technology. It's distinct from 航空 (hángkōng) which refers to aviation, or flight within the Earth's atmosphere.  航天 emphasizes travel beyond Earth's atmosphere, while 航空 is limited to air travel within the atmosphere.

~
慈善
慈善 (císhàn) has a strong association with Buddhism and Confucianism, both of which emphasize kindness, compassion, and altruism. It encompasses both the act of giving and the benevolent motivation behind it.  In modern usage, it often refers to philanthropy and charitable activities organized by institutions or individuals.

~
据悉
据悉 (jùxī) indicates that the information comes from an unspecified but generally reliable source. It is a journalistic term commonly used in news reports to cite information without naming the specific source.

~
倔强
倔强 (juéjiàng) carries a slightly more positive connotation than other words for "stubborn" like 固执 (gùzhí), suggesting persistence and determination rather than simply being unreasonable.

~
歌颂
歌颂 (gēsòng) implies enthusiastic and often public praise, often used in a formal or official context, especially to praise the ruling party, great leaders, or heroic deeds.  It carries a stronger sense of celebration than other words like 赞扬 (zānyáng) or 表扬 (biǎoyáng).

~
保管
When 保管 is used in the sense of "to guarantee," it's usually followed by a clause. E.g. 我保管他会来 (Wǒ bǎoguǎn tā huì lái) = I guarantee he will come.

~
和蔼
和蔼 (hé'ǎi) is usually used to describe older people who are gentle, kind, and approachable.

~
坦白
坦白 (tǎnbái) often implies admitting to something wrong or previously hidden. It's stronger than simply being "honest" and carries a sense of confession or revelation. It's also used in political and criminal justice contexts.

~
庄重
庄重 (zhuāngzhòng) implies a formal and dignified seriousness, often associated with ceremonies, rituals, or solemn occasions.  It suggests a sense of respect and decorum.

~
诈骗
诈骗 (zhàpiàn) emphasizes the use of deception or trickery to gain something illegally, while other words like 欺骗 (qīpiàn) have a broader meaning of deception and may not necessarily involve illegal activities.

~
合算
合算 (hésuàn) means worthwhile or cost-effective, focusing on whether something is a good deal or a wise investment.  It implies a consideration of cost and benefit.

~
轮胎
轮胎 is usually used to mean tires of vehicles such as cars, buses, and trucks. The term for bicycle or motorcycle tires is 车胎.

~
点缀
This word is often used in a slightly negative way, to refer to something that is added merely for superficial decoration rather than actual function.

~
反思
反思 (fānsī) carries a stronger connotation than just simple reflection. It suggests critical self-examination, often in response to a mistake, failure, or negative experience. It emphasizes identifying the root causes of a problem and learning from it.

~
冰雹
冰雹 (bīngbáo) usually occurs together with thunderstorms.

~
文献
