文献 (wénxiàn) usually refers to formal, written materials, such as academic papers, historical records, or official documents, that are considered valuable resources for research or study.  It's not typically used for everyday written materials like letters or notes.

~
灌溉
灌溉 (guàngài) refers specifically to the artificial watering of crops or land, unlike other words like 浇水 (jiāoshuǐ) which have a broader meaning of watering anything.

~
自发
自发 (zìfā) emphasizes the absence of external prompting or organization.  It suggests that something arose naturally from the will or initiative of the people involved.

~
激发
激发 (jīfā) suggests stimulating something into action or bringing out a hidden potential.  It emphasizes the act of "triggering" or "sparking" a reaction or response.

~
调剂
调剂 (tiáojì) has multiple meanings. Be careful not to confuse it with 调节 (tiáotié) which also means "to adjust," but is used in the context of machinery or systems, whereas 调剂 carries the connotation of mitigating or balancing.

~
悬念
悬念 (xuánniàn) indicates a state of uncertainty or anticipation, often used in the context of storytelling or dramatic situations to keep the audience engaged.

~
预算
预算 (yùsuàn) often refers to a detailed plan for spending money, typically within a specific timeframe, unlike other words like 开支 (kāizhī) which generally refer to expenses.

~
无比
无比 (wúbǐ) is a relatively strong term emphasizing the lack of any comparison or equal.

~
请柬
请柬 (qǐngjiǎn) is more formal than other words for invitation like 邀请 (yāoqǐng) and is typically used for significant events like weddings or formal ceremonies.

~
筛选
筛选 (shāixuǎn) involves a process of carefully selecting the desired elements while discarding the unwanted ones, often implying a more meticulous or systematic approach than other words like 选择 (xuǎnzé).

~
曲折
曲折 (qūzhé) can be used literally to describe a winding path or road, and figuratively to describe a complex or convoluted situation or story.

~
寒暄
寒暄 (hánxuān) refers specifically to exchanging polite, superficial greetings or small talk, often as a social convention rather than a genuine expression of interest.

~
嘈杂
嘈杂 (cáozá) describes a loud and chaotic mixture of sounds that are often unpleasant or irritating, unlike other words like 吵闹 (chǎonào) which can also refer to lively or cheerful noise.

~
割
割 (gē) implies cutting with a sharp blade or instrument, often involving a slicing or severing action.

~
锤
锤 (chuí) can act as both a noun (hammer) and a verb (to hammer).

~
削弱
削弱 (xuēruò) suggests a gradual or progressive weakening, often implying a deliberate effort to diminish someone's power or influence.

~
通俗
A related word is 俗气 (súqi). 通俗 means easy to understand, while 俗气 means vulgar or tacky.


~
宗旨
Can be confused with 主题 (zhǔtí, theme or topic). 宗旨 is more about a long-term goal or ultimate purpose, while 主题 is more about the specific subject matter being discussed.


~
批发
There is no major difference in usage compared to "wholesale" in English. Note that sometimes you can see the abbreviated pīfā.


~
福气
This has a similar meaning to "blessing". It can be used more generally though, referring to happiness and prosperity which comes from luck.


~
折腾
This word is difficult to translate. It can refer to physical tossing and turning, but is often used figuratively. It carries a connotation of restlessness and futility.


~
浑身
Similar to "all over" in English. However, it is more literary and vivid, often implying a strong physical sensation or feeling.


~
杜绝
This word implies complete eradication, stronger than just "preventing".


~
笼罩
This evokes an image of being covered completely. It often refers to abstract things like fear or fog.


~
欲望
No significant usage notes. Similar to English words such as desire, craving, or longing.


~
派别
Refers to groups with differing opinions or approaches, often within a larger organization or field.


~
馅儿
No significant usage notes, simply the "erhua" form of 馅.


~
拼搏
This implies great effort and struggle, often against significant challenges.


~
结晶
Figuratively, this refers to the valuable outcome of hard work.


~
感染
Figuratively, this refers to inspiring or influencing, often with positive emotions.


~
妥当
Implies suitability and safety, often in relation to arrangements or plans.


~
酒精
No significant usage notes. Same meaning as "alcohol" in English.


~
服气
Implies genuine acknowledgment of someone's superiority.


~
坑
As a verb, this has the colloquial meaning of "to cheat" or "to rip off".


~
命名
No significant usage notes. Similar to "to name" in English.


~
容忍
Implies enduring something unpleasant or unwelcome, often out of necessity.


~
股份
No significant usage notes. Refers to shares in a company, like the English word "stock".


~
英明
This word is highly complimentary, often used to praise leaders or decisions.


~
姿态
Can refer to both physical posture and a more abstract attitude or stance.


~
纵横
Often used to describe someone who is highly skilled and influential in a particular field.


~
俗话
Refers to common sayings or proverbs, similar to "folk wisdom".


~
蔓延
Implies gradual but relentless spread, often of something negative.


~
不得已
Emphasizes the lack of choice or the involuntary nature of an action.


~
授予
Often used in formal contexts, such as awarding honors or degrees.


~
铸造
Refers specifically to casting metal, and can also be used metaphorically to refer to shaping or creating.


~
坠
Often used to describe things falling from a height.


~
皱纹
No significant usage notes. Refers to wrinkles.


~
固执
Can be negative, implying stubbornness, but can also be positive, implying persistence.


~
憋
Can refer to various forms of holding back, including breath, emotions, and urine.


~
零星
Implies a small, scattered, and insignificant quantity.


~
黄昏
Refers to the time of dusk or twilight.


~
盆地
A geographical term referring to a basin or depression.


~
撤退
Implies a strategic withdrawal, often in a military context.


~
参谋
Can be both a noun (staff officer) and a verb (to advise).


~
陡峭
Describes steep slopes or cliffs.


~
终究
Emphasizes the inevitability of a final outcome.

~
脉搏
Figuratively, 脉搏 (màibó) is often used in a societal context, referring to the "pulse" of a city, a group, or a trend.  It represents the rhythm, vitality, or underlying sentiment.  For the medical sense, the word is identical to the English.

~
麻痹 (má bì)
While this word can mean "paralysis" in a medical sense, it's more commonly used figuratively to describe a state of mental numbness, apathy, or negligence.  Think of it as being "paralyzed" into inaction or indifference due to complacency or a lack of concern.  For example, you might say someone is 麻痹大意 (mábì dàyì) - paralyzed by carelessness.

~
一度 (yīdù)
一度 can mean "once" or "at one time," indicating something that happened in the past but is no longer the case. It can also denote a period of time or a degree/extent.  The key is to pay attention to the context to discern the specific meaning.

~
信赖 (xìnlài)
信赖 carries a stronger sense of reliance and dependence than simply "trusting" someone. It suggests a deep-seated confidence and belief in someone's reliability and competence.

~
人道 (réndào)
The most common modern meaning of 人道 is related to humanitarianism and compassion. The other meanings are archaic and rarely used.  Be aware of the context to avoid misinterpretations.

~
讥笑 (jīxiào)
讥笑 implies a mocking or derisive laugh, often with a hint of scorn or contempt.  It's stronger than just a simple chuckle or giggle, and is often used to express disapproval or belittlement.

~
埋葬 (máizàng)
While primarily meaning "to bury," 埋葬 can also be used figuratively to describe the act of putting an end to something, such as a dream, hope, or relationship.

~
赤道 (chìdào)
赤道 refers specifically to the Earth's equator unless otherwise specified.  If referring to the celestial equator, it would typically be paired with 天 (tiān) – 天赤道 (tiān chìdào).

~
恶化 (èhuà)
恶化 implies a significant and often rapid deterioration of a situation.  It suggests a worsening beyond a simple decline and often carries a negative connotation.

~
掠夺 (lüèduó)
掠夺 suggests a violent or forceful taking, often involving theft or exploitation.  It's a stronger term than simply "taking" or "grabbing."

~
覆盖 (fùgài)
覆盖 implies a complete covering, often like a blanket or a layer.  Think of it as "enveloping" or "blanketing" something.

~
赞叹 (zàntàn)
赞叹 expresses strong admiration and praise, often with a sense of awe or wonder.  It's a more enthusiastic expression than simply saying "good job."

~
昼夜 (zhòuyè)
When used to mean "continuously," 昼夜 emphasizes the relentless nature of the action, often suggesting it goes on around the clock without pause.

~
冻结 (dòngjié)
In a figurative sense, 冻结 can refer to halting or suspending a process, project, or relationship.  Think of it as "freezing" something in place.

~
华丽 (huálì)
华丽 suggests a flamboyant and extravagant type of gorgeousness, often involving elaborate decorations and rich colors.

~
弊病 (bìbìng)
弊病 refers to inherent flaws or weaknesses within a system, practice, or institution.  It points to a persistent problem rather than a one-time error.

~
泄露 (xièlù)
泄露 suggests an unintentional or careless disclosure of information, often confidential or sensitive.  It carries a negative connotation, implying a breach of trust or security.

~
攒 (zǎn)
攒 implies saving diligently over time, often for a specific purpose.  It's more focused and intentional than simply "saving."

~
是非 (shìfēi)
是非 can refer to both a dispute or argument, as well as the broader concepts of right and wrong.  Pay attention to the context to determine the specific meaning.

~
要命 (yàomìng)
要命 is used colloquially to emphasize the severity or annoyance of something. It can range from expressing a life-threatening situation to simply complaining about something extremely bothersome.

~
畏惧 (wèijù)
畏惧 describes a deep-seated fear or dread, often accompanied by feelings of helplessness or anxiety.  It's a stronger emotion than simple fear.

~
遏制 (èzhì)
遏制 implies suppressing or restraining something by force or authority.  It suggests a deliberate effort to prevent something from happening or developing.

~
蹦 (bèng)
蹦 suggests a light and quick jump, often with a sense of energy or excitement.

~
草案 (cǎo'àn)
草案 specifically refers to a preliminary or provisional version of a document, subject to revision and approval.

~
动身 (dòngshēn)
动身 emphasizes the act of beginning a journey, the actual setting off, rather than just the intention to travel.

~
悬挂 (xuánguà)
悬挂 implies hanging something from above, typically suspended in the air.  It suggests a state of being dangling or hanging freely.

~
变故 (biàngù)
变故 usually refers to an unexpected and often negative turn of events.  It often implies a sudden change that disrupts the normal course of things.

~
轮廓 (lúnkuò)
轮廓 refers to the outer boundary or shape of something, often a silhouette or a rough outline.

~
歪曲 (wāiqū)
歪曲 implies a deliberate and often malicious misrepresentation of facts or information.  It suggests a conscious effort to distort the truth.

~
饥饿 (jī'è)
饥饿 refers to the physical sensation and discomfort of lacking food. It describes the feeling of being hungry.

~
诞辰 (dànchén)
诞辰 is a more formal and respectful term for "birthday," often used in formal contexts or for respected figures.

~
昔日 (xīrì)
昔日 evokes a sense of nostalgia and often implies a contrast between the past and the present.

~
团圆 (tuányuán)
团圆 specifically refers to a family reunion, often during holidays or special occasions. It emphasizes togetherness and harmony.

~
夹杂 (jiāzá)
夹杂 implies a mixture of different and often unrelated elements, sometimes creating a sense of disorder or complexity.

~
体面 (tǐmiàn)
体面 emphasizes respectability and social appropriateness, often concerning appearance, behavior, or social standing. It suggests meeting social expectations and maintaining a good image.

~
生疏 (shēngshū)
生疏 describes a lack of familiarity or practice, leading to awkwardness or incompetence. It can refer to skills, relationships, or knowledge.

~
颁发 (bānfā)
颁发 implies an official and authoritative act of issuing or bestowing something, such as a certificate, award, or law.

~
干劲 (gànjìng)
干劲 describes enthusiasm and motivation specifically for work or tasks.  It's a drive to achieve something, a zest for getting things done.

~
更正 (gēngzhèng)
更正 implies making a formal correction to an error or mistake, often in a written or official context.  It suggests a deliberate effort to rectify inaccurate information.

~
沉着 (chénzhuó)
沉着 describes a calm and composed demeanor, especially in the face of pressure or difficulty.  It suggests a level-headedness and ability to remain steady under stress.

~
收缩
A relatively formal (书面) word. More colloquial words are  缩小 (suōxiǎo) and 缩短 (suōduǎn).

~
捕捉
Can be used figuratively, to mean to capture the essence of something.

~
排放
Has a negative connotation when it comes to the environment, implying excessive or irresponsible discharge of pollutants.

~
临床
临床试验 (línchuáng shìyàn) means "clinical trial".

~
侦探
A 侦探小说 (zhēntàn xiǎoshuō) is a "detective novel".

~
过滤
Can be used figuratively to mean filter (out) information.

~
历来
Similar meaning to 一向 (yīxiàng) and 从来 (cónglái).  It is more formal than those two words, and is almost exclusively used in writing.

~
响应
响应号召 (xiǎngyìng hàozhào) means "to respond to a call" or "to answer a summons."

~
孤立
Be careful not to confuse this word with 鼓励 (gǔlì, to encourage).

~
枯萎
Has a stronger connotation of complete and irreversible withering than the word 干枯 (gānkū).

~
愣
The different meanings of this word are all related by an idea of mental emptiness and lack of focus.

~
淡季
The opposite of 淡季 is 旺季 (wàngjì), which means peak season or busy season.

~
阐述
Often used with abstract topics such as theories, ideas, or viewpoints. It implies a more systematic and in-depth explanation compared to other words like 解释 (jiěshì) or 说明 (shuōmíng).

~
四肢
Specifically refers to the arms and legs.

~
逆行
Can also be used metaphorically to describe going against the trend or the norm.

~
外行
The opposite of 外行 (wàiháng) is 内行 (nèiháng), meaning expert or professional.

~
熄灭
Figuratively refers to the extinguishing of hope, passion, or other abstract concepts.

~
主权
主权国家 (zhǔquán guójiā) means "sovereign state".

~
传记
Usually used to refer to biographies of famous or influential people.

~
顽固
Can be used to describe both people and things (e.g., a stubborn stain, a persistent problem). It has a more negative connotation than 坚持 (jiānchí).

~
叮嘱
Implies a sense of care or concern from the person giving the warning.

~
颠簸
Figuratively refers to experiencing instability or hardship in life.

~
签署
More formal than 签 (qiān), and usually used for official documents or agreements.

~
条款
Often used in legal or contractual contexts.

~
走漏
The meanings of this word seem unrelated, but share the common thread of "something getting out that shouldn't".

~
须知
Often used in announcements or instructions to highlight essential information.

~
外表
Can also refer to one's outward behavior or demeanor.

~
停泊
Can be used figuratively to suggest seeking temporary respite or rest.

~
滋味
More profound and nuanced than simply taste, implying a complex emotional experience.

~
轰动
The caused sensation is usually positive.

~
壮烈
Often used in the context of heroic sacrifices or deeds.

~
疑惑
Can be used as a noun or a verb.

~
行列
Used to denote membership in a specific group or profession.

~
法人
法人代表 (fǎrén dàibiǎo) is a "legal representative".

~
巴不得
Often used to express a strong desire for something to happen, especially something negative to someone else.

~
探测
Often used in scientific or technical contexts, and implies a systematic investigation.

~
瞬间
Emphasizes the extreme brevity of the moment.

~
款式
This word is often confused with other near synonyms. 款式 (kuǎnshì) refers to the overall design and shape of clothing or accessories. 式样 (shìyàng) refers to a pattern, style, or fashion.

~
瞪
Often implies anger or disapproval.

~
熏陶
Implies a subtle, gradual, and often positive influence.

~
贯彻
Often used with abstract nouns such as 精神 (jīngshén, spirit), 指示 (zhǐshì, instructions), or 政策 (zhèngcè, policy).  It implies a thorough and complete implementation.

~
规格
规格 is more about the technical specifications or standards, while 标准 (biāozhǔn) is more general and can refer to quality, level, or criteria. For example, you might talk about the 规格 of a phone (screen size, processor, etc.), but the 标准 of customer service.

~
配偶
This is a formal word for "spouse." More colloquial equivalents include 老公 (lǎogong, husband), 老婆 (lǎopo, wife), or simply 爱人 (àiren, loved one).

~
公道
While it can mean "fair," it's more commonly used in the sense of "justice" or "righteousness."  The word for a public highway is 公路 (gōnglù).

~
家常
家常 can also be used as an adjective, meaning "home-style" or "everyday," as in 家常菜 (jiāchángcài, home-style cooking).

~
无偿
Can be used with other nouns too, such as 无偿献血 (wúcháng xiànxuè) "to donate blood" and 无偿劳动 (wúcháng láodòng) "unpaid labor/volunteer work".

~
纲领
This refers to a more fundamental and overarching program, often with political or ideological connotations.  A more general word for "program" or "plan" is 计划 (jìhuà).

~
冒犯
This word is quite formal and implies a serious offense.  A more colloquial way to say "offend" is 得罪 (dézuì).

~
绑架
This word also encompasses metaphorical kidnapping, such as emotional or intellectual kidnapping.

~
任性
This carries a negative connotation, suggesting childish or selfish behavior.

~
嘿
This is a versatile interjection that can express surprise, disagreement, or a call for attention.

~
贬低
This implies an intentional and often unfair lowering of someone's status or value.

~
可口
More colloquial and often used to describe food.  美味 (měiwèi) is a more formal synonym.

~
纤维
Remember the measure word is 种 (zhǒng).

~
答辩
Note the different meanings depending on context. For dissertations, it specifically refers to the oral defense.

~
过失
This emphasizes unintentional mistakes due to negligence, rather than deliberate wrongdoing.

~
过奖
This is a common polite response to a compliment.

~
摘要
This is a concise summary of a longer work, highlighting the key points.

~
液体
Remember the measure word is 杯 (bēi) for cupfuls and 瓶 (píng) for bottles.

~
诽谤
This is a legal term referring to the act of making false statements to damage someone's reputation.

~
不由得
This indicates an involuntary reaction or feeling.

~
共鸣
The figurative meaning of "sympathetic response" is commonly used.

~
理睬
This implies ignoring someone deliberately.

~
泛滥
This can also be used metaphorically to describe something negative spreading unchecked, like rumors or fake news.

~
乞丐
Considered somewhat impolite;  a more respectful term is 流浪者 (liúlàngzhě).

~
提议
More formal than 建议 (jiànyì, suggestion) and often used in official settings.

~
圈套
This implies a carefully planned trap designed to deceive.

~
镇静
This emphasizes inner calmness in the face of pressure or danger.

~
倡议
This implies taking the initiative to propose an idea or action.

~
储备
Often used in economic or military contexts, implying storing resources for future use.

~
贵族
This refers to the social class, while a specific member of the nobility would be called a 贵族成员 (guìzú chéngyuán) or simply 贵族 (guìzú).

~
宁肯
This expresses a strong preference for one option, even if it involves sacrifice.  It is often followed by 也 (yě, also) or 都 (dōu, all).

~
晾
The figurative meaning "to cold-shoulder" is increasingly common.

~
生效
Often used for laws, contracts, or agreements.

~
掐
The slang meaning of "to fight" is quite informal and regional.

~
扰乱
This implies disrupting order or peace.

~
辩证
The philosophical meaning "dialectical" is important for understanding Marxist thought.

~
参照
This implies using something as a guide or model.

~
哭泣
More literary and formal than 哭 (kū).

~
倘若
More formal than 如果 (rúguǒ) or 假如 (jiǎrú).

~
使命
使命 (shǐmìng) is a weighty word, referring to a grand or noble mission, a calling, a vocation, etc., often with a long-term commitment and significant impact.  It's not used for everyday tasks or errands.  Think of "saving the world," "advancing scientific knowledge," "promoting peace." It would sound odd to use 使命 for picking up groceries.

~
连年
连年 (liánnián) refers to something happening for several consecutive years.  It emphasizes the unbroken continuity of the occurrence.  It doesn't simply mean "many years."

~
增添
增添 (zēngtiān) implies adding something new to something already existing, thus enhancing or enriching it.  It's not the same as simply increasing a number.  Think of adding new features to a product or new books to a collection.

~
迫害
迫害 (pòhài) carries a strong connotation of systematic and prolonged mistreatment, often involving oppression or persecution. It's a serious word and not used for minor annoyances or disagreements. Think of religious persecution or political oppression.

~
周转
周转 (zhōuzhuǎn) primarily refers to the circulation of funds or resources, often in a business context. It implies a cycle of use and reuse, ensuring smooth operation. While it can relate to physical objects, the financial aspect is usually more prominent.

~
神态
神态 (shéntài) describes a person's overall demeanor, expression, and posture, often reflecting their inner thoughts or feelings.  It is more than just facial expression.  It encompasses the entire bearing of a person.

~
论坛
论坛 (lùntán) specifically refers to a platform or forum for discussion, often public and organized.  It's not simply any chat or conversation. Think of online forums, academic conferences, or public debates.

~
飞翔
飞翔 (fēixiáng) describes a graceful and sustained flight, often soaring or gliding. It's more elegant than just "flying," suggesting skillful movement through the air.  Think of eagles soaring or birds gliding on air currents.

~
固有
固有 (gùyǒu) highlights something inherent, intrinsic, or deeply ingrained.  It's more permanent than simply "existing" or "having."  Think of inherent rights, intrinsic properties, or deeply ingrained habits.

~
兴隆
兴隆 (xīnglóng) describes a state of prosperity, particularly in business or commerce.  It suggests flourishing activity and increasing success.  Think of a thriving business or a booming market.

~
情理
情理 (qínglǐ) refers to reason and logic combined with human emotion and empathy. It often involves considering the circumstances and feelings of others when making judgments.  It's about what's fair and reasonable given the human element.

~
哆嗦
哆嗦 (duōsuo) emphasizes involuntary trembling, often due to cold or fear. It's more intense than just a slight shiver.

~
呼唤
呼唤 (hūhuàn) implies calling out loudly, often with urgency or emotion.  It can be a cry for help, a summons, or an expression of strong feeling. Think of calling out for help in an emergency, or summoning someone from a distance.

~
启示
启示 (qǐshì) suggests a sudden realization or understanding, often profound or enlightening. It's more than just a hint or a clue; it's a moment of clarity or revelation.  Think of a sudden insight, a flash of inspiration, or a religious epiphany.

~
强制
强制 (qiángzhì) denotes the use of force or coercion to compel someone to do something against their will. It carries a negative connotation, implying a lack of choice or freedom. Think of mandatory evacuations, forced confessions, or coercive policies.

~
挎
挎 (kuà) specifically describes carrying something slung over the arm, shoulder, or side, often a bag or basket. It's different from carrying something in your hand or on your back.

~
宏观
宏观 (hóngguān) describes a broad, overarching perspective, often dealing with large-scale systems or phenomena.  It contrasts with 微观 (wēiguān - microscopic), which focuses on small details.

~
伤脑筋
伤脑筋 (shāng nǎojīn) means "to rack one's brains" or "to be a headache." It's used to express frustration or annoyance at something difficult or troublesome.

~
紧迫
紧迫 (jǐnpò) emphasizes urgency and the need for immediate action.  It suggests a pressing deadline or a critical situation.  Think of a tight deadline, an impending crisis, or an urgent need.

~
步伐
步伐 (bùfá) refers to the pace, rhythm, and manner of walking or marching.  It can be used literally or figuratively to describe progress or development.

~
平面
平面 (píngmiàn) can refer to a flat surface in geometry or print media as opposed to broadcast media. The context will usually make the meaning clear.

~
眼色
眼色 (yǎnsè) refers to non-verbal communication using glances or eye movements, often subtle and meaningful. It's about conveying messages or cues without speaking.

~
制服
制服 (zhìfú) has two main meanings:  a uniform and to subdue or control. The context will clarify which meaning is intended.

~
任命
任命 (rènmìng) is a formal word for appointment to a position, usually of authority.  It's not used for casual jobs or assignments. Think of appointing a CEO, a government official, or a military commander.

~
朴实
朴实 (púshí) describes someone simple, honest, and down-to-earth, without pretense or affectation.  It implies a sincerity and lack of artificiality.

~
掀起
掀起 (xiānqǐ) literally means "to lift up" or "to raise."  Figuratively, it means to initiate or start something significant, often a movement, trend, or wave of activity.

~
威力
威力 (wēilì) refers to great power or force, often destructive or impactful.  Think of the power of a weapon, the force of nature, or the influence of a powerful person.

~
玩意儿
玩意儿 (wányìr) can be a diminutive and affectionate term for "thing," but it can also refer to toys or gadgets. It can also carry a slightly negative connotation, implying something frivolous or insignificant. The tone and context are key to understanding the intended meaning.

~
蕴藏
蕴藏 (yùncáng) implies hidden potential or untapped resources. It suggests something valuable waiting to be discovered or utilized.

~
正月
正月 (zhēngyuè) refers specifically to the first month of the lunar calendar, a time of significant cultural and traditional importance.

~
败坏
败坏 (bàihuài) describes the act of corrupting, ruining, or spoiling something, often referring to morals, reputation, or a system.

~
汹涌
汹涌 (xiōngyǒng) describes a turbulent, surging flow, often of water, but can also describe crowds or emotions.

~
主义
主义 (zhǔyì) refers to a doctrine, ideology, or principle, often forming the basis of a political or social system.  It's usually used as a suffix, like communism (共产主义 - gòngchǎnzhǔyì) or capitalism (资本主义 - zīběnzhǔyì).


~
问世
问世 (wènshì) refers to something new being introduced to the world, often a book, invention, or product.  It's similar to "coming out" or "being published."

~
挪
挪 (nuó) means to shift or move something, usually with some effort or difficulty.  It implies a deliberate and often slow relocation.

~
摇摆
摇摆 (yáobǎi) describes a back-and-forth or swaying motion, either physically or metaphorically, often indicating indecision or wavering.

~
悔恨
悔恨 (huǐhèn) expresses deep regret or remorse, often for past actions or mistakes. It's a stronger feeling than simple regret.

~
联欢
联欢 (liánhuān) refers to a social gathering or celebration, often involving entertainment and festive activities.

~
以至
以至 (yǐzhì) and 以至于 (yǐ zhìyú) are conjunctions meaning "to the extent that" or "so that."  以至于 is slightly more emphatic. They introduce a result or consequence.
~
留念
留念 (liúniàn) has two main meanings: to keep a souvenir as a memento, and to cherish the memory of something. The context will determine the specific meaning.

~
筹备
筹备 is more formal than 准备.

~
庄稼
庄稼 is more formal than 农作物.


~
工艺品
Remember the measure word for 工艺品 is 件 (jiàn).

~
筐
The most common measure word for 筐 is 个 (gè). 只 (zhī) is also sometimes used, but less often.

~
涌现
涌现 is typically used for positive things, like the emergence of talent or new technologies. It carries a sense of profusion or abundance.

~
剥削
剥削 is a politically charged word, primarily used within Marxist discourse to describe the exploitation of labor by capital. While it can technically translate to "exploit," it carries heavy ideological baggage.

~
总和
总和 is more formal than 总数.


~
盲目
Use this word cautiously, as it can be a strong criticism in some contexts.

~
空洞
空洞 is more figurative than "empty." Instead of referring to a physical space being void, it can describe words, theories, or ideas as lacking substance or meaning.


~
机动
When 机动 means "adaptable" or "flexible," it is most commonly used in combination with other words, such as 机动时间 (jīdòng shíjiān) for flexible hours.


~
腐蚀
腐蚀 is not only applicable to material objects rusting or decaying but also has a metaphorical sense of corruption, such as the corrosive effects of greed or power.


~
扭转
扭转 implies a significant shift or change from a negative situation, similar to "turn around" but often in the context of reversing a decline or loss.


~
解体
解体 describes the dismantling or breaking up of something complex, such as a political system or organization, as well as the physical disintegration of a material object.


~
实质
实质 emphasizes the true nature or core of something beneath superficial appearances or misleading representations.


~
盛产
盛产 is used when a region is known for its abundant production of a specific resource or product, often natural resources or agricultural goods.


~
火药
火药 can also refer to an explosive temperament or a volatile situation, meaning "touchy" or "sensitive," as in 一触即发的火药味 (yīchùjífā de huǒyàowèi) - "an explosive atmosphere."


~
起源
起源 is used for the earliest beginning of something, often historical or scientific, and less commonly for tracing personal origins or ancestry.


~
毅力
毅力 highlights determination and resolve in the face of adversity, suggesting a persistent and unyielding effort.


~
书面
书面 is typically used in phrases like 书面语 (shūmiànyǔ) - written language, or 书面通知 (shūmiàn tōngzhī) - written notice.


~
大体
Although 大体 can refer to a cadaver, this usage is extremely specialized and should not be your primary understanding of the word. The more common meanings of "generally" or "on the whole" are more relevant for everyday conversation.


~
情报
情报 refers to specific, often secret, information related to a particular subject or event, usually in a military, political, or business context.


~
挣扎
挣扎 conveys a desperate and strenuous effort to escape a difficult situation, often involving physical exertion or emotional turmoil.


~
重叠
重叠 can also describe the overlapping of schedules or time periods, in addition to its literal meaning of physical objects lying on top of each other.


~
呼啸
呼啸 is often used to describe the sound of wind or a fast-moving object whooshing by, as well as the howling of a siren or loud shouts.


~
充沛
充沛 is used to describe things that are full of energy, vitality, or resources, such as 充沛的精力 (chōngpèi de jīnglì) - abundant energy.


~
蜡烛
The measure word 根 (gēn) for 蜡烛 emphasizes the cylindrical shape, while 支 (zhī) treats it as a more generic object.


~
摊
摊 can also refer to the act of setting up a street vendor's stall, such as 摊位 (tānwèi) - a stall or booth.


~
含糊
含糊 not only describes language that is unclear but also actions or attitudes that are evasive, noncommittal, or wishy-washy.


~
妥善
妥善 suggests handling something carefully and appropriately to achieve a satisfactory resolution or avoid problems.


~
惯例
惯例 emphasizes established practices or customs within a specific group or organization, rather than universal or legal norms.


~
哨
哨 is most commonly used in military contexts to refer to a sentry post or guard duty.


~
胡须
The measure word 根 (gēn) for 胡须 emphasizes the individual hairs, while 绺 (liǔ) refers to a bunch or lock of beard hair.


~
背叛
背叛 is a strong word that implies a betrayal of trust or loyalty, often causing serious consequences.


~
残留
残留 describes something left behind after a larger part has been removed or destroyed, often implying an undesirable or unwelcome remnant.


~
庸俗
庸俗 carries a strong negative connotation, describing behavior, attitudes, or tastes considered vulgar, tasteless, or lowbrow.


~
虚荣
虚荣 emphasizes excessive pride in one's appearance, accomplishments, or possessions, often driven by a desire for social status or admiration.


~
沉闷
沉闷 can describe an atmosphere or mood that is heavy, oppressive, and joyless, as well as sounds that are dull or muffled.


~
野心
野心 can have both positive and negative connotations. It can mean ambition in a neutral sense but often suggests a ruthless or unchecked desire for power.


~
以免
以免 introduces an action or precaution taken to prevent a negative consequence, similar to "so as to avoid" or "lest."


~
机智
机智 implies quick thinking and resourcefulness in finding clever solutions to problems, often in unexpected or challenging situations.

~
耗费
Can be used as a verb or a noun.  Similar to 花费 (huāfèi), but implies a degree of wastefulness or excessive spending.  It's often used for time, money, or resources.

~
操练
Implies repetitive practice, often in a military or disciplined context, to achieve proficiency.

~
纺织
This word encompasses both spinning and weaving, and is often used in the context of the textile industry.

~
溶解
Specifically refers to the process of a solid dissolving in a liquid.

~
若干
Indicates an unspecified but limited quantity or number. It suggests that the amount is not precisely known but is within a certain range.

~
导航
Commonly used in the context of GPS and map apps.  Can also refer to guidance in general.

~
框架
Can refer to a physical frame or a conceptual framework, such as the framework of an agreement.

~
预言
Implies a prediction about the future, often with a sense of foreboding or mystery.

~
凑合
As an adjective, it means "passable" or "making do". As a verb, it means "to make do with what one has" or "to put up with a less-than-ideal situation".  It often carries a sense of compromise or settling for less.

~
缺口
Can refer to a physical gap or a figurative shortfall, such as a budget shortfall.

~
犬
While it means "dog", it's more formal and less common than 狗 (gǒu). Often used in scientific or technical contexts, or in compound words like 犬齿 (canine teeth).

~
肿瘤
A medical term for tumor.

~
毫无
Used to emphasize complete absence or lack of something.  Often followed by a two-syllable noun.

~
捧
When used in the sense of "to sing the praises of", it often implies excessive or insincere flattery.

~
污蔑
Implies a malicious and deliberate attempt to damage someone's reputation through false accusations.

~
崇高
Describes something noble, lofty, or of high moral value.

~
专程
Emphasizes that a trip or action was taken solely for a specific purpose.

~
根源
Refers to the fundamental origin or root cause of something.

~
递增
Indicates a gradual and continuous increase, often in a numerical or quantitative sense.

~
媳妇
Traditionally refers to a daughter-in-law, but can also be used affectionately by a husband to refer to his wife.  This usage is more common in northern China.

~
提炼
Implies a process of extraction and purification, often used in the context of refining raw materials.

~
领会
Suggests a deeper level of understanding than simply knowing or comprehending.  Implies grasping the essence or underlying meaning of something.

~
柔和
Describes something gentle, soft, and pleasant, often in relation to light, sound, or texture.

~
地势
Refers to the physical features and layout of the land.

~
别扭
Describes a feeling of awkwardness, discomfort, or unease, often due to social or interpersonal situations.  Can also refer to something that is difficult to handle or manage.

~
浓厚
Describes something dense, thick, or intense, often in relation to color, flavor, or atmosphere.  Can also refer to a strong interest or enthusiasm.

~
辜负
Implies failing to live up to expectations or betraying someone's trust.  Often expresses a sense of disappointment or regret.

~
岔
The word itself often implies an unexpected or unintended deviation.

~
皆
A more formal and literary way of saying "all".

~
权威
Refers to recognized expertise or power in a particular field.

~
坟墓
A more formal and literary term for grave or tomb.

~
座右铭
A personal motto or guiding principle.

~
鞭策
Implies encouragement through urging or prodding, often with a sense of pushing oneself or others to achieve more.

~
奥秘
Refers to something mysterious, secret, or difficult to understand.

~
玩弄
Implies manipulating or toying with something or someone in a careless or disrespectful way.

~
嫉妒
A feeling of resentment or envy towards someone's success or possessions.

~
过瘾
Expresses a feeling of great satisfaction or enjoyment, often after satisfying a craving or experiencing something exciting.

~
欺骗
A general term for deceiving or cheating.

~
在意
Means to care about or be concerned with something. The negative form 不在意 is often used to express "not minding" or "not caring".

~
制裁
Refers to official punishments or sanctions imposed for wrongdoing, often in a legal or political context.

~
驻扎
驻扎 is typically used to describe the stationing of troops or military personnel in a particular location. It has a more formal and military connotation compared to other words like  停留 (tíngliú - to stay) or  居住 (jūzhù - to reside).

~
体裁
体裁 encompasses a broader range of creative works than just writing. It can also refer to genres in music, film, and other art forms.

~
光彩
光彩 refers to a more brilliant and dazzling kind of shine, often associated with something precious or glorious.  It differs from  光亮 (guāngliàng - bright), which describes a more general brightness.

~
贫乏
贫乏 implies a severe lack or deficiency of something, often resources or knowledge. It is stronger than  缺乏 (quēfá - to lack), which describes a more general absence.

~
分量
分量 can refer to weight, quantity, or the importance or influence of something.  It is distinct from  重量 (zhòngliàng - weight), which specifically refers to physical weight.

~
寂静
寂静 emphasizes the absence of sound, implying a deep stillness and quiet. It is more intense than  安静 (ānjìng - quiet), which can describe a general state of calmness.

~
生物
While 生物 includes all living organisms,  动物 (dòngwù) refers specifically to animals, and  植物 (zhíwù) refers to plants.

~
混淆
混淆 highlights the act of mixing things up, making them difficult to distinguish. It differs from  混乱 (hùnluàn - chaos), which describes a state of disorder.

~
乐谱
乐谱 is a general term for musical scores.  It can be further specified as  钢琴谱 (gāngqínpǔ - piano score) or  吉他谱 (jítāpǔ - guitar score) for specific instruments.

~
示意
示意 implies a subtle or indirect way of communicating an idea. It is different from  指示 (zhǐshì - to instruct), which is more direct and explicit.

~
宣誓
宣誓 carries a formal and solemn tone, often associated with official ceremonies or legal proceedings.  It is more serious than  发誓 (fāshì - to swear), which can be used in everyday situations.

~
派遣
派遣 suggests sending someone on a specific mission or assignment. It is more formal than  送 (sòng - to send) or  派 (pài - to dispatch).

~
炎热
炎热 describes extremely hot weather, typically associated with summer. It is stronger than  热 (rè - hot).

~
国防
国防 refers specifically to national defense matters.  It is different from  安全 (ānquán - safety) or  保护 (bǎohù - protection), which have broader meanings.

~
无非
无非 emphasizes that there are no other possibilities or explanations. It is similar to  只不过 (zhǐbuguò - only; nothing more than).

~
对联
对联 are specific to Chinese culture and tradition. They are often used during festivals and special occasions.

~
销毁
销毁 refers to the complete destruction of something, often by burning or melting. It is more thorough than  破坏 (pòhuài - to destroy), which can imply partial damage.

~
折磨
折磨 describes the infliction of physical or mental suffering. It is more intense than  困扰 (kùnrǎo - to trouble) or  烦恼 (fánnǎo - to worry).

~
滞留
滞留 implies being forced to stay somewhere due to unforeseen circumstances. It is different from  停留 (tíngliú - to stay), which is more voluntary.

~
性命
性命 emphasizes the preciousness of life, often in situations of danger. It is more serious than  生命 (shēngmìng - life).

~
登陆
Be mindful of the common error of writing 登陆 (dēnglù - to land) when intending to write 登录 (dēnglù - to log in).

~
化验
化验 refers specifically to laboratory tests, often medical or scientific.  It is different from  检查 (jiǎnchá - to inspect) or  测试 (cèshì - to test).

~
婴儿
Be aware of the dual meaning of 婴儿 as both "infant" and the element "lead" (Pb), particularly in scientific contexts.

~
计较
计较 can have both positive and negative connotations.  Positively, it can mean to plan or strategize.  Negatively, it means to be overly concerned with minor details or to haggle.

~
吹牛
吹牛 is generally used in a lighthearted way, but it can also be considered rude if done excessively.

~
亦
亦 is a more formal and literary alternative to  也 (yě - also).

~
意图
意图 emphasizes the intended purpose or aim behind an action. It is more deliberate than  想法 (xiǎngfǎ - thought) or  主意 (zhǔyi - idea).

~
案件
案件 refers specifically to legal cases or incidents.  It is different from  事件 (shìjiàn - event) or  事情 (shìqíng - matter).

~
盛
盛 has multiple meanings, including "flourishing," "vigorous," and "to contain." Pay attention to the context to determine the correct meaning.

~
施加
施加 highlights the act of applying pressure or influence on someone or something. It is more forceful than  给予 (jǐyǔ - to give) or  提供 (tígōng - to provide).

~
家伙
家伙 can refer to tools, utensils, or even people in a casual context. Be mindful of the potentially informal and even slightly derogatory connotation when referring to people.

~
渺小
渺小 emphasizes the insignificance or tininess of something. It is stronger than  小 (xiǎo - small).

~
致力
致力 highlights dedication and commitment towards a specific goal. It is more active than  努力 (nǔlì - to work hard).

~
蛋白质
蛋白质 is a specific term for "protein."  It is different from  营养 (yíngyǎng - nutrition) which encompasses a broader range of nutrients.

~
精确
精确 emphasizes a high degree of accuracy and precision. It is stronger than  准确 (zhǔnquè - accurate).

~
蒸发
蒸发 describes the physical process of turning liquid into vapor.  It is different from  消失 (xiāoshī - to disappear) which can be due to other reasons.

~
恼火
恼火 describes a state of annoyance or frustration. It is stronger than  生气 (shēngqì - to be angry).

~
手势
手势 refers to gestures made with hands and fingers for communication. It is different from  动作 (dòngzuò - movement) which encompasses all body movements.

~
立足
立足 emphasizes establishing a stable position or foundation.  It is different from  站立 (zhànlì - to stand) which simply means being upright.


~
贼
贼 can be used as an intensifier, similar to "very" or "extremely," usually in a negative context.  For example, 贼贵 (zéi guì) means "extremely expensive."

~
啥
This word is the dialectal equivalent of 什么 (shénme). Note, however, that it is only used in informal settings.

~
见解
A more formal way of saying 见解 is 看法.

~
亲热
When used to describe the relationship between two people, 亲热 (qīn rè) suggests a deep bond of affection and intimacy, often involving physical closeness. It is typically used to describe familial relationships or very close friendships, and can sometimes even have romantic connotations depending on the context.

~
树立
This word carries a connotation of establishing something positive, substantial, or praiseworthy.  It often implies building something enduring or influential, such as a model example, a strong image, or a positive mindset.  Common collocations include 树立榜样 (shùlì bǎngyàng - to set up a role model), 树立形象 (shùlì xíngxiàng - to establish an image), and 树立信心 (shùlì xìnxīn - to build confidence). It is rarely used for concrete objects.

~
免疫
Be careful not to confuse this with 免疫力 (miǎnyìlì) which is the word for the immune system.

~
背诵
This word implies reciting something from memory with a degree of fluency and accuracy, often suggesting a formal or educational context such as reciting a poem, a passage from a text, or lines from a play.

~
柴油
Be careful not to confuse this word with 汽油 (qìyóu), which means gasoline.

~
炊烟
This word evokes a sense of nostalgia and traditional rural life, often used in literature or poetic descriptions. It often symbolizes home, warmth, and the simple pleasures of life.

~
侧面
When referring to an aspect or perspective, 侧面 (cèmiàn) suggests an indirect or secondary viewpoint, often providing additional information or insights that may not be apparent from the main or frontal perspective.  It can also imply a more subtle or implicit understanding of something.

~
尖锐
The term 尖锐 (jiānruì) carries a connotation of sharpness, intensity, and sometimes even hostility or conflict when used figuratively.  It often describes situations or opinions that are highly critical, confrontational, or divisive.  For example, 尖锐的批评 (jiānruì de pīpíng - sharp criticism) or 尖锐的矛盾 (jiānruì de máodùn - acute contradiction).

~
拜年
This refers to a traditional Chinese New Year custom of visiting relatives and friends to extend New Year greetings and wishes.  It typically involves exchanging gifts, sharing festive meals, and engaging in celebratory activities.

~
激励
激励 (jīlì) emphasizes inspiring and motivating someone to achieve something positive or overcome challenges.  It implies a boost in morale, energy, and determination.

~
严峻
严峻 (yánjùn) implies a seriousness and gravity that often foreshadows potential difficulties or hardship.  It suggests a situation requiring careful attention and resolute action.

~
可观
可观 (kěguān) emphasizes the considerable or impressive nature of something, often in terms of size, quantity, or impact.  It implies a level of significance worth noting or paying attention to.

~
幼稚
幼稚 (yòuzhì) carries a negative connotation, often suggesting a lack of maturity, experience, or sound judgment.  It can be used to describe childish behavior, naive thinking, or simplistic ideas.

~
叼
The verb 叼 (diāo) is specifically used for holding something long and relatively thin with the mouth, such as a cigarette, a pipe, a blade of grass, or a small stick.

~
同志
While the traditional meaning of 同志 (tóngzhì) remains in use, particularly in formal contexts or official settings, be aware of its slang usage within the LGBTQ+ community in China, where it refers to a homosexual person, especially a gay man. This slang usage is widely understood in contemporary Chinese society.

~
贬义
贬义 (biǎnyì) refers to the negative connotations or unfavorable implications associated with a word or expression.  It indicates that the term carries a derogatory or pejorative sense, often used to express disapproval or criticism.

~
华侨
This term specifically refers to overseas Chinese who retain their Chinese citizenship.  It distinguishes them from 外籍华人 (wàijí huárén), which refers to ethnic Chinese who have adopted foreign citizenship.

~
君子
君子 (jūnzǐ) represents an idealized Confucian concept of a virtuous and noble person, embodying qualities such as integrity, benevolence, wisdom, and courage.  It emphasizes moral excellence and ethical conduct.

~
严禁
严禁 (yánjìn) denotes an absolute and uncompromising prohibition, often backed by legal or regulatory authority.  It emphasizes the seriousness of the prohibition and the potential consequences of violation.

~
衔接
衔接 (xiánjiē) focuses on the smooth and seamless connection between two or more things, ensuring continuity and coherence.  It implies a precise and well- coordinated joining or linking process.

~
孕育
When used figuratively, 孕育 (yùnyù) often describes the gradual development or gestation of something abstract, such as an idea, a trend, or a cultural movement.  It suggests a process of nurturing and maturation before something comes into full fruition.

~
搏斗
搏斗 (bódòu) implies a physical struggle or combat involving intense effort and often violence.  It suggests a fight for survival, dominance, or a specific objective.

~
瞄准
瞄准 (miáozhǔn) implies careful aiming and precision, often in the context of shooting a weapon or directing something with accuracy.  It suggests a focused and deliberate effort to hit a target.

~
袭击
袭击 (xíjī) suggests a sudden, unexpected, and often violent attack, usually intended to cause harm or damage.  It implies an element of surprise and aggression.

~
专长
专长 (zhuāncháng) highlights a specific area of expertise or a particular skill in which someone excels.  It suggests a high level of proficiency and mastery in a particular field or domain.

~
嫂子
嫂子 (sǎozi) is generally used to address the wife of one's older brother. However, it can also be used as a polite form of address for a married woman who is slightly older than oneself, even if there's no actual familial relation. It conveys respect and friendliness.

~
峡谷
峡谷 (xiágǔ) describes a deep, narrow valley with steep sides, often carved by a river. It is usually larger and more dramatic than a ravine or gully.

~
揭露
揭露 (jiēlù) implies uncovering something hidden, often something negative or scandalous, such as a crime, a conspiracy, or a misdeed. It suggests bringing something to light that was previously concealed or obscured.

~
季军
季军 (jìjūn) specifically refers to the competitor or team that finishes in third place in a competition. It is commonly used in sports contexts.

~
剧烈
剧烈 (jùliè) emphasizes the intensity and forcefulness of something, often describing physical sensations or changes. It suggests a high degree of activity, movement, or impact.

~
攻克
攻克 (gōngkè) implies overcoming a significant obstacle or challenge, often through persistent effort and determination. It suggests a victory or breakthrough achieved through focused and sustained action.

~
周边
周边 (zhōubiān) refers to the surrounding area or vicinity of a particular location. It can encompass the physical surroundings as well as related or auxiliary aspects, such as peripheral products or supplementary materials.

~
手艺
手艺 (shǒuyì) emphasizes skills acquired through practice and experience, often involving manual dexterity and creativity. It often refers to traditional crafts or artisanal skills.

~
谋求
谋求 (móuqiú) implies seeking something through careful planning and strategic effort. It suggests a deliberate and purposeful pursuit of a specific goal or objective.

~
极限
极限 (jíxiàn) refers to the utmost point or boundary of something, often relating to physical capacity, endurance, or performance. It suggests pushing something to its absolute limits or reaching a point beyond which it cannot go.

~
抢劫
抢劫 (qiǎngjié) involves the use of force or threat of force to steal something from someone. It implies a direct and confrontational act of theft.

~
佳肴
佳肴 (jiāyáo) emphasizes the high quality and deliciousness of food, often referring to elaborate or exquisite dishes. It suggests a culinary experience that is both enjoyable and memorable.

~
伴随
伴随 (bànsuí) indicates something that occurs or exists alongside something else, often in a close or connected manner. It suggests a simultaneous or concurrent relationship between two or more things.

~
克制
克制 is more formal than 控制 (kòngzhì).  It usually refers to controlling one's emotions or desires, often with difficulty.  控制, on the other hand, can refer to controlling anything, including physical objects or situations.

~
罐
When referring to a can of soda, 罐 is typically used with a measure word, such as a can of coke: 一罐可乐 (yī guàn kělè).

~
荤
In modern usage, 荤 (hūn) primarily refers to non-vegetarian food, especially meat.  The meaning of "strong-smelling vegetable" is archaic and rarely used.  Be careful not to confuse it with 腥 (xīng), which refers to a fishy or raw meat smell.  When Buddhists talk about abstaining from 荤, they mean not eating meat, not pungent vegetables.

~
惹祸
惹祸 emphasizes the act of causing trouble or inviting disaster.  It suggests that the trouble is a result of one's own actions.

~
废除
废除 is a formal term often used for laws, regulations, systems, or customs. It implies a complete and official annulment.

~
荣幸
It is typically used in formal settings, such as speeches or official letters. A common phrase is "很荣幸..." (hěn róngxìng...), meaning "It's an honor to...".

~
抵制
抵制 suggests a conscious and deliberate act of resistance, often against something considered harmful or undesirable. It often implies collective action.

~
迎面
迎面 can be used as an adverb, meaning "head-on" or "face-to-face," or as an adjective, meaning "approaching."  For example, 迎面而来 (yíngmiàn ér lái) means "coming head-on."

~
沾光
沾光 often implies a sense of humility and acknowledges that the benefit received is due to someone else's favor or influence.

~
霞
While 霞 (xiá) can refer to the rosy hues at both sunrise and sunset, it is more commonly associated with sunset.  朝霞 (zhāoxiá) specifically refers to the rosy clouds at sunrise.

~
出卖
When referring to betrayal, 出卖 implies a breach of trust or loyalty, often for personal gain.

~
苏醒
苏醒 implies a gradual return to consciousness, often from a state of unconsciousness or a deep sleep.

~
明智
明智 is often used to describe decisions, choices, or actions.  It suggests wisdom and foresight.

~
旗袍
旗袍 is almost always transliterated to Cheongsam or Qipao. The translations of "Chinese-style dress" although literal, does not immediately give the user a sense of what type of dress it is.

~
镇定
镇定 describes a calm and composed demeanor, especially in the face of pressure or difficulty.

~
毁灭
毁灭 implies complete and utter destruction, often beyond repair.

~
磕
This word has many meanings, and the pronunciation can change depending on usage and context. When it means "to knock," the pronunciation is "kē." When it means "to kowtow" it is pronounced "kē." When used in the internet slang 嗑CP, it is pronounced "kè."

~
凄凉
凄凉 evokes a sense of sadness, loneliness, and desolation, often in relation to a place or situation.

~
陈旧
陈旧 describes something that is outdated, old-fashioned, or no longer relevant.

~
宫殿
The measure word for 宫殿 is 座 (zuò).

~
现成
现成 implies that something is already prepared and readily available, saving time and effort.

~
湖泊
湖泊 is a more formal term than just 湖 (hú - lake). It often refers to larger lakes or is used in geographical contexts.

~
宪法
The measure word for 宪法 (xiànfǎ) is 部 (bù).

~
挺拔
挺拔 describes something tall and straight, often in reference to trees, posture, or buildings.  It conveys a sense of strength and uprightness.

~
阻挠
阻挠 implies deliberate and often underhanded attempts to obstruct or hinder progress.

~
论证
论证 involves presenting evidence and reasoning to support a claim or argument.  It is a more formal and structured process than simply stating an opinion.

~
着手
着手 emphasizes the beginning of a task or process. It suggests taking concrete action.

~
视线
视线 refers to the direction of one's gaze or the range of what can be seen.

~
疤
疤 (bā) specifically refers to a scar, while 痂 (jiā) refers to a scab.

~
而已
而已 (éryǐ) is a literary expression used to downplay or diminish the significance of something. It often follows a statement and means "that's all" or "nothing more."

~
伶俐
伶俐 describes someone who is quick-witted, clever, and agile, both mentally and physically.

~
破例
破例 emphasizes the act of making an exception to a rule or established practice.

~
分寸
分寸 refers to a sense of propriety and appropriateness in behavior, speech, and action. It implies knowing the boundaries and acting accordingly.

~
栋
栋 (dòng) is the measure word for buildings.

~
上任
上任 (shàngrèn) refers specifically to taking up a new position or office.

~
屈服
屈服 implies giving in to pressure, force, or authority, often against one's will.

~
里程碑
里程碑 (lǐchéngbēi) refers to a significant event or achievement that marks a turning point or stage of development.

~
保障
保障 implies taking measures to ensure or safeguard something, often related to rights, safety, or well-being.

~
拳头
拳头 (quántou), aside from its literal meaning "fist," can also colloquially refer to a competitive product or service.  For example, 拳头产品 (quántou chǎnpǐn) means "flagship product" or "core product."  The measure word for 拳头 is 个 (gè).

~
成心
成心 (chéngxīn) emphasizes intentionality and deliberation. It suggests that an action was done on purpose, often with a negative connotation.

~
停滞
A similar word is 迟缓 (chíhuǎn), but 迟缓 simply means slow, whereas 停滞 means to come to a standstill.

~
索性
This word is used when someone decides to do something out of desperation, or because they think there are no better options.  It implies a giving up on a previous plan. It often carries the connotation of "in that case..." or "might as well...".

~
迟缓
A similar word is 停滞 (tíngzhì), but 迟缓 simply means slow, whereas 停滞 means to come to a standstill.

~
废墟
Can be combined with other words, such as:

* 战争废墟 (zhànzhēng fèixū): war ruins
* 城市废墟 (chéngshì fèixū): city ruins
* 核战争废墟 (hé zhànzhēng fèixū) ruins of a nuclear war
* 变成一片废墟 (biàn chéng yīpiàn fèixū): reduced to ruins


~
效益
效益 is more abstract than simply profit. It considers the overall effectiveness and societal benefit in addition to monetary gains.

~
媒介
媒介 (méijiè) can refer to both intermediary and media.  When referring to news sources, 媒体 (méitǐ) is more common.

~
掰
掰 (bāi) is often used in the context of breaking something brittle or crisp, like a cracker, vegetable or twig, using one's hands. It's not typically used for softer items.

~
淘汰
This is not just about washing or culling. It includes any process of eliminating something considered inferior or obsolete. It can be used both literally and figuratively.

~
财政
财政 (cáizhèng) specifically refers to government revenue, expenditure, and management of public funds.

~
让步
除了表示妥协或放弃外，“让步”也可以表示一种谈判策略，为了获得更大的利益而暂时放弃一些小的利益。

~
征收
征收 (zhēngshōu) implies compulsory acquisition, often by the government. It often involves taxes, land, or other resources.

~
罕见
The word 罕见 (hǎnjiàn) emphasizes the rarity or infrequency of something. It often carries a sense of unusualness or peculiarity.

~
空虚
This word describes an inner feeling of emptiness, often related to a lack of purpose or meaning in life. It’s more profound than simply being bored.

~
眼神
眼神 (yǎnshén) refers more to the expression or emotion conveyed by someone's eyes, rather than simply their eyesight. It's about what the eyes communicate.

~
谢绝
谢绝 (xièjué) is a polite way of declining something. It's more formal than simply saying "no."

~
雄厚
雄厚 (xiónghòu) describes something substantial, robust, and powerful, often in terms of resources, strength, or foundation.  It can refer to economic, military, or even intellectual power.

~
腐朽
This describes more than just physical decay; it can refer to moral or ideological decline, as in a corrupt system or outdated belief.

~
懒惰
This is a stronger term than just being occasionally lazy. It implies a habitual aversion to work or effort.

~
勇于
This word is not only about courage, but also about having the initiative and taking the necessary risks to do something challenging or unconventional.  It implies a conscious decision to face difficulty.

~
留恋
This describes a feeling of attachment and reluctance to leave a person, place, or experience.  It often evokes a sense of nostalgia or fondness for the past.

~
挫折
This encompasses more than just a minor setback.  It implies a significant obstacle or defeat that can be disheartening and discouraging.

~
拐杖
While 拐杖 (guǎizhàng) can refer to crutches in general, it often specifically means a single walking stick or cane used for support.

~
优异
优异 (yōuyì) indicates exceptional quality or performance, surpassing ordinary standards. It suggests a high level of excellence.

~
意向
意向 (yìxiàng) often refers to a preliminary intention or inclination, not yet a firm decision. It suggests a potential course of action.

~
胆怯
This refers to a personality trait of being easily frightened or intimidated. It's deeper than just being momentarily scared.

~
公然
公然 (gōngrán) implies a deliberate and defiant act done in public, often in violation of norms or rules.

~
靠拢
This describes a gradual process of drawing closer, either physically or ideologically, often to align with a group or principle.

~
草率
草率 (cǎoshuài) implies a lack of thoroughness and consideration, leading to hasty and often flawed actions.

~
示威
示威 (shìwēi) typically refers to a public display of protest or dissent, often involving a group of people expressing their opposition to something.

~
告辞
告辞 (gàocí) is a formal and polite way of saying goodbye. It's more appropriate for formal occasions or when leaving someone's home.

~
漂浮
Besides its literal meaning, 漂浮 (piāofú) can also figuratively describe something lacking substance or depth, like superficial ideas or a wandering lifestyle.

~
揉
揉 (róu) is typically a gentle and repetitive action, often with the purpose of softening, shaping, or soothing something.

~
嗨
Be mindful of the different meanings and contexts for 嗨 (hāi), including an exclamation of surprise, a greeting, or referring to a state of excitement or intoxication.

~
弹性
弹性 (tánxìng) refers to the ability to adapt, change, or recover from difficult situations. It implies resilience and flexibility.

~
应邀
应邀 (yìngyāo) specifically indicates that someone is participating in something because they were invited. It emphasizes the role of the invitation.

~
动力
动力 (dònglì) can refer to both physical force that drives something and the motivational force that drives someone's actions.

~
候选
候选 (hòuxuǎn) specifically refers to being a candidate for something, typically an election or a position. It's an attributive adjective.

~
自满
自满 (zìmǎn) implies excessive satisfaction with one's accomplishments, often leading to complacency and a lack of further effort.

~
乌黑
乌黑 (wūhēi) describes a deep, glossy black color, often used for hair, eyes, or other dark objects.

~
丛
The measure word for 丛 is 丛 (cóng).

~
隐患
There is no difference between the use of 隐患 in Chinese and "hidden danger" in English.

~
牲畜
There is no difference between the use of 牲畜 in Chinese and "livestock" in English.

~
酝酿
For the meaning of "to mull over", there is another similar word, which is 琢磨 (zuómo). The difference is that 酝酿 suggests that an idea is still in its early stages of development and has not yet taken a clear shape. It emphasizes the process of gradual formation and refinement. On the other hand, 琢磨 suggests that the speaker is actively considering and evaluating different options or aspects of an idea. It emphasizes the process of careful thought and analysis.

~
鞠躬
There is no difference between the use of 鞠躬 in Chinese and "to bow" in English.

~
拽
This word is primarily used in northern dialects.  In standard Mandarin, the more common word is 拉 (lā).

~
记性
This word has a neutral connotation, and can be used to describe good memory as well as bad memory. If you want to praise somebody's good memory, you might want to use the word "记忆力" (jìyìlì).

~
钻研
There is no difference between the use of 钻研 in Chinese and "to delve into" in English.

~
竞选
There is no difference between the use of 竞选 in Chinese and "to run for office" in English.

~
出息
For the meaning "future prospects", this word usually carries negative connotation. It is usually used in sentences like "这孩子真没出息 (zhè háizi zhēn méi chūxi)", which means "This child is hopeless".

~
顿时
There is no difference between the use of 顿时 in Chinese and "suddenly" in English.

~
往事
There is no difference between the use of 往事 in Chinese and "past events" in English.

~
攀登
There is no difference between the use of 攀登 in Chinese and "to climb" in English.

~
弥漫
There is no difference between the use of 弥漫 in Chinese and "to pervade" in English.

~
报仇
There is no difference between the use of 报仇 in Chinese and "to take revenge" in English.

~
隧道
There is no difference between the use of 隧道 in Chinese and "tunnel" in English.

~
端正
This word can be used to describe a person's appearance (e.g. facial features), but it can also be used to describe a person's behavior or attitude. E.g. "态度端正 (tàidù duānzhèng)" means "to have a correct attitude".

~
鼓动
For the meaning of "to urge", 鼓动 carries a negative connotation, and it means to incite somebody to do something harmful, rebellious or dangerous. For urging somebody to do something beneficial, one might use the word 鼓励 (gǔlì).

~
风味
There is no difference between the use of 风味 in Chinese and "distinctive flavor" in English.

~
辛勤
There is no difference between the use of 辛勤 in Chinese and "hardworking" in English.

~
起初
There is no difference between the use of 起初 in Chinese and "originally" or "at first".

~
礼节
There is no difference between the use of 礼节 in Chinese and "etiquette" in English.

~
陷阱
There is no difference between the use of 陷阱 in Chinese and "trap" in English.

~
名次
There is no difference between the use of 名次 in Chinese and "rank" in English.

~
公务
There is no difference between the use of 公务 in Chinese and "official business" in English.

~
枚
There is no difference between the use of 枚 as a measure word in Chinese and the use of measure words for similar objects in English.

~
完毕
This word is somewhat formal (书面). A more colloquial way to say "to finish" is "完成" (wánchéng).

~
垄断
There is no difference between the use of 垄断 in Chinese and "to monopolize" in English.

~
埋怨
There is no difference between the use of 埋怨 in Chinese and "to complain" in English.

~
开辟
There is no difference between the use of 开辟 in Chinese and "to open up" in English.

~
宣扬
This word carries a negative connotation, and suggests that what is being advertised is false or harmful information. For neutral publicity, one might want to use the word 宣传 (xuānchuán).

~
田野
There is no difference between the use of 田野 in Chinese and "field" in English.

~
况且
There is no difference between the use of 况且 in Chinese and "moreover" in English.

~
拿手
There is no difference between the use of 拿手 in Chinese and "good at" in English.

~
茎
There is no difference between the use of 茎 in Chinese and "stem" in English.

~
渣
When referring to a person, 渣 (zhā) is slang and can be translated as “scumbag”, usually referring to a man who mistreats women.  When referring to the remnants of something, it can be translated as “dregs”, “residue”, or “leftovers.”

~
卑鄙
There is no difference between the use of 卑鄙 in Chinese and "despicable" in English.

~
耕地
There is no difference between the use of 耕地 in Chinese and "to plow land" or "arable land" in English.


~
抱负
There is no difference between the use of 抱负 in Chinese and "ambition" in English.

~
哦
Note that there are several different characters for the sound "ó". When it is an interjection, it can mean "oh, I see", to show understanding or acknowledgement.
~
见闻
A more common synonym is 阅历 (yuèlì).

~
雕塑
When used as a verb, 雕塑 is usually paired with a direct object. For example, 雕塑一座佛像 (diāosù yīzuò fóxiàng) - to sculpt a Buddhist statue.  It can also be used as a noun to refer to a sculpture.

~
威信
Note the pronunciation: wēixìn. This is different than the popular app 微信 (Wēixìn - WeChat), despite the similar characters.

~
次序
次序 (cìxù) is a more formal way of saying 顺序 (shùnxù).

~
致使
This is a formal word, often used in writing. More colloquial alternatives include 导致 (dǎozhì) and 使 (shǐ).

~
杂技
The measure word is 场 (chǎng), not (chang3).

~
忌讳
This can function as a noun or a verb.

~
生锈
A more colloquial synonym is 生锈了.


~
源泉
This is a somewhat literary (书面) word.  A more common way to say "source" is 来源 (láiyuán).

~
濒临
This is often used with negative contexts, such as danger or extinction.

~
遥控
Can be used as a verb or an adjective. For example, 遥控汽车 (yáokòng qìchē) means "remote control car."

~
副
Knowing the correct measure word for 副 is important, as it's used for things that come in pairs.

~
吩咐
This implies a superior giving instructions to a subordinate.  A more general word for "instruct" is 指示 (zhǐshì).  A more colloquial way to say "tell" is  跟…说 (gēn...shuō).

~
重心
This can refer to a literal center of gravity, or, figuratively, to the main focus or priority.

~
种子
Note the different measure words: 颗 (kē) is generally for smaller seeds, while 粒 (lì) is used for larger seeds or grains.

~
畜牧
Can be a noun or a verb.

~
声势
Often used in a negative context, such as 声势浩大 (shēngshì hàodà), which might be translated as a "huge uproar" or "major commotion."

~
屏障
Can be literal (e.g., a physical barrier) or metaphorical (e.g., a language barrier).

~
界限
Refers to a boundary or limit.  Can be concrete or abstract.

~
兜
The primary meaning learners should focus on now is "pocket". Less common meanings can be learned later.

~
夕阳
Poetic and evocative. Often used in a nostalgic or melancholic context.


~
着重
More formal than 强调 (qiángdiào).

~
鉴于
Formal and often used in official documents or announcements. Similar to "in light of" or "considering."

~
反射
The meaning depends on the context. Can be physical reflection (like light off a mirror) or a reflexive action.

~
扩充
Means to expand or enlarge something that already exists, as opposed to creating something entirely new.

~
滋润
Can be used literally (moist) or figuratively (comfortable and well-off).  The figurative meaning is common. For example,  生活滋润 (shēnghuó zīrùn) - "to live a comfortable life."

~
拼命
Implies a desperate or all-out effort, sometimes with the risk of harm to oneself.

~
生机
Often used in situations where life or hope is threatened.

~
迟疑
Implies hesitation due to uncertainty or fear.  A more neutral word for "hesitate" is 犹豫 (yóuyù).

~
境界
Can be literal or figurative. The figurative meaning implies a high level of achievement or a profound state of mind.

~
导弹
Measure word is 枚 (méi).

~
鉴别
Implies careful examination to determine authenticity or quality.


~
展望
Relatively formal. Often used when discussing the future.


~
灵敏
Can describe physical or mental quickness and sensitivity.


~
感慨
Implies deep emotion, often tinged with sadness or regret.

~
隐蔽
Emphasizes the act of hiding or concealing, often with a strategic or military connotation.


~
扒
Many meanings.  When giving a command, it means "peel."

~
翘
The most common meaning for learners is "to stick up" or "to tilt upwards."

~
隆重
Usually describes ceremonies or events.

~
繁忙
More formal than 忙 (máng).

~
仓促
This word has a negative connotation, implying a lack of preparedness or planning. It suggests that something was done hastily or without sufficient time or consideration.  It doesn't necessarily mean "all of a sudden" in the sense of unexpectedly.

~
争气
Can also mean to bring honor to one's family. For example, if a child does well in school, a parent might say "你真争气!"

~
新颖
More accurately, it suggests something that is both new and original.

~
耸
This can be used in the more literal sense of something rising up high (e.g., mountains, shoulders).  The figurative sense of something exciting is less common.

~
茂盛
Specifically refers to the lushness of vegetation, not other things that can be abundant.

~
严密
Often used to describe security, surveillance, or logic.

~
振兴
While it can mean "to revive," it usually carries the specific connotation of restoring something to its former glory or prosperity, often in a national or economic context.

~
开支
Be careful to use the correct measure word. Use 笔 (bǐ) for individual expenses, and 项 (xiàng) for categories of expenses.

~
美满
Specifically refers to happiness and completeness in family life or relationships, not general happiness.

~
渗透
The meaning of "infiltrate" specifically implies that something harmful is seeping in, often in a military or political context.

~
瞻仰
This word carries a sense of deep respect and reverence, often used for important figures, monuments, or sacred places. It is not a casual synonym for "admire."

~
包庇
Implies actively concealing someone's wrongdoing, often involving criminal activity or serious misconduct.  Carries a strongly negative connotation.

~
反驳
Indicates a strong, direct rebuttal or refutation, often in a formal or argumentative context. It's not simply disagreeing, but actively countering an argument.

~
庞大
Emphasizes sheer size and scale, often implying complexity or unwieldiness. It is not simply a synonym for "big" or "large."

~
任意
When used to mean "any", it is usually followed by a measure word. 

~
盖章
Can be both literal (to stamp) and figurative (to finalize or approve).  In the figurative sense, it can imply bureaucratic processes.

~
完备
Suggests completeness in every detail, leaving nothing lacking. It emphasizes thoroughness and perfection.

~
凝视
Indicates a long, intense gaze, often conveying deep thought, fascination, or other strong emotions.

~
盗窃
Specifically refers to the act of stealing, while "偷" (tōu) can have a broader range of meanings, including "to steal" but also "to pilfer," "to snatch," or even "to do something secretly."

~
发誓
Implies a serious and solemn vow, often with consequences attached if broken.

~
溪
Specifically refers to a small stream or brook, smaller than a river (河 hé).

~
孔
As a classifier, 个 is the usual measure word, but you might use 口 (kǒu) when referring to the opening of a well or a container.

~
狠心
As an adjective, describes someone cruel and unfeeling.  As a verb phrase (下狠心), it means to make a difficult, often painful decision.

~
挑拨
Carries a strong negative connotation, suggesting malicious intent to create conflict or disharmony.

~
进而
Implies a progression or advancement to a further stage or level. It signals a deepening or intensification of something.

~
搁
The meaning "to bear/to stand/to endure" is only in specific dialects.

~
统统
Emphasizes completeness and inclusivity, leaving nothing out.  It's more emphatic than simply saying "all."

~
挑剔
Implies excessive criticism and fault-finding, often about minor details.

~
晃
When describing light, think "glare" or "dazzling" rather than simple "flashing." For movement, think "swaying" or "oscillating."

~
迷惑
Implies a state of being perplexed or disoriented, often unable to distinguish between right and wrong or truth and falsehood.

~
演绎
In a logical context, refers to deductive reasoning.  In other contexts, it suggests a process of unfolding or developing, often creatively.

~
顾虑
Implies worry and concern, often about potential negative consequences.  Carries a more hesitant or cautious tone than simply "worrying."

~
本能
Highlights an innate, unlearned response or behavior, often driven by survival instincts.

~
无赖
Describes someone who is dishonest, shameless, and often exploits others. Carries a strong negative connotation.

~
凶恶
Emphasizes fierceness and malicious intent, often associated with violent or criminal behavior.

~
革命
In modern Chinese, this word usually refers to a political or social revolution, often involving radical change.

~
较量
Implies a direct competition or contest, often involving skill, strength, or strategy.  It's not simply a casual comparison.

~
麻醉
Figuratively, it suggests a numbing or desensitizing effect, often used in the context of escaping reality or difficult emotions.

~
嘱咐
Implies earnest and detailed instructions or advice, often given by someone in authority or with experience.

~
出身
Refers to one's family background, social class, and origins.  Often carries implications about social status and opportunities.

~
预先
A related word is 事先 (shìxiān). Both mean to do something in advance, but 预先 emphasizes preparation and planning for a future event. 事先, on the other hand, emphasizes doing something before another action or event takes place.  预先 often involves more elaborate arrangements, while 事先 may simply refer to doing something earlier in time.

~
权衡
This is more formal than simpler words like 考虑 (kǎolǜ). It specifically means to carefully consider by weighing up the pros and cons of different factors or options. It highlights the act of balancing and evaluating competing considerations before making a decision.

~
丰满
When not referring to a place name, it's best translated as "full-figured" when referring to people.  When referring to other things, like fruit, it means plump or well-developed.

~
茫然
This word captures the feeling of being utterly bewildered and lost, often to the point of being unable to think or react.  It doesn't necessarily carry the sense of staring blankly, it is possible to feel 茫然 whilst engaging in normal activities.

~
挑衅
This describes the act of deliberately provoking someone, often with the intent of starting a conflict or eliciting a reaction. It emphasizes an open, direct, and often aggressive form of provocation, distinct from simply annoying or irritating someone.

~
埋没
This refers to the potential or talent of something being overlooked, neglected, or ultimately forgotten or wasted.  It can also mean to literally bury.

~
安宁
This refers to a sense of peace, tranquility, or calmness, often associated with quiet and stability.  It suggests a more profound sense of inner peace than simply being quiet.

~
裁缝
This can also refer to the act of tailoring or dressmaking.  So, apart from being a noun, it can also be a verb.

~
封建
In modern Chinese, this word often has a negative connotation, associated with outdated social structures and oppressive hierarchies.

~
诱惑
This describes the act of attracting someone to do something, often something considered wrong or unwise, by promising pleasure or gain.  It implies a sense of allurement and enticement that can lead someone astray.

~
良心
This refers to a person's moral sense of right and wrong, the inner voice that guides their actions and decisions.

~
局势
This refers to a general state of affairs or situation, often in a political or social context.  It often refers to matters with a widespread or significant impact.

~
呕吐
There is no difference between the use of 呕吐 in Chinese and "vomit" in English.

~
表决
This refers to the formal process of making a decision by voting, usually in a group or assembly setting.

~
棉花
There is no difference between the use of 棉花 in Chinese and "cotton" in English.

~
急剧
This describes a sudden, sharp, and rapid change or increase, often with a dramatic or intense quality.

~
儒家
There is no difference between the use of 儒家 in Chinese and "Confucianism" in English.

~
弱点
This describes a point of vulnerability, either in a person's character or in a system or structure.

~
档次
This describes a level or grade of quality, usually in reference to consumer goods or services.

~
编织
When not referring to literally weaving something, this word describes the figurative act of creating something complex or intricate, often a story, lie, or excuse.

~
意料
This refers to what one anticipates or expects to happen, often based on prior knowledge or assumptions.  It can also refer to the verb "to anticipate".

~
唾弃
This describes the act of expressing strong contempt or disgust for someone or something, often accompanied by a feeling of moral outrage.

~
拘留
This refers to the act of detaining someone in custody, often by law enforcement authorities.

~
压岁钱
Traditionally, this money was given in red envelopes (红包 - hóngbāo).

~
捏
This describes the act of holding something between the thumb and fingers, often with a gentle or delicate touch.  It also has the additional nuance of implying a careful manipulation or shaping of the object being held.

~
墨水儿
This is simply the 儿化 of 墨水. It retains the original meaning but adds a touch of colloquial informality.  The 儿化 is common in northern dialects.

~
宁愿
