This is typically used to express a preference for one option over another, especially when the preferred option involves some kind of sacrifice or compromise.  It emphasizes the willingness to accept the less desirable aspects of the preferred choice to avoid the alternative.

~
当事人
This refers to the people directly involved or affected by a particular situation or event, especially in legal or formal contexts.

~
断定
This describes the act of making a firm and definite judgment or conclusion about something, often based on evidence or reasoning.  It implies a sense of certainty and conviction.

~
确切
This describes something that is precise, exact, and accurate, leaving no room for doubt or ambiguity.  It can refer to information, data, measurements, or descriptions.

~
偏差
This describes the difference between an observed value and a true or expected value, a variation from the norm or standard.

~
艘
There is no difference between the use of 艘 in Chinese and its English translation.

~
并非
This is a more emphatic way of saying "not" or "is not." It often highlights a contrast or correction of a misconception.

~
附和
This describes the act of expressing agreement with someone, often in a way that suggests insincerity or a lack of independent thought.  It implies going along with others without genuinely sharing their views.

~
脂肪
There is no difference between the use of 脂肪 in Chinese and "fat" in English.

~
狭隘
This describes something narrow or limited in scope, either physically or metaphorically. It can refer to physical spaces, viewpoints, or experiences.  When referring to a person, it means "narrow-minded".

~
稻谷
There is no difference between the use of 稻谷 in Chinese and its English translation.

~
算数
Besides meaning "to count," this also means "to count for something" or "to be valid." It implies that something is taken seriously and has an actual impact.

~
成天
This means to do something all day long.  It is more colloquial than 整天.  It often carries a slightly negative connotation, suggesting excessive or unproductive activity.

~
城堡
Besides meaning "castle", this word can also mean "rook" in the context of the game of chess.

~
历代
Can be translated as "past dynasties," "successive generations," or "successive dynasties." The best translation depends on context. When referring to rulers, translate as "past dynasties" or "successive dynasties." When referring to people or families, translate as "successive generations."


~
事迹
Refers to noteworthy deeds or accomplishments, often with a historical or biographical significance. It's not just any event, but something remarkable or praiseworthy.  A better translation than "important event of the past" might be "remarkable deeds."


~
恩怨
Encompasses both positive (gratitude, kindness) and negative (resentment, grievance) feelings stemming from past interactions. It's often used to describe complex or tangled relationships.


~
敬业
Emphasizes a strong sense of dedication and professionalism in one's work, going beyond simply fulfilling duties. It implies diligence, responsibility, and a commitment to excellence.


~
附属
Indicates a subordinate or secondary relationship, often implying dependence or attachment to something larger or more important.  It can be translated as "subsidiary," "auxiliary," "attached," or "affiliated," depending on the specific context.


~
悬殊
Highlights a significant difference or disparity between two things, often to the point of being extreme or striking.  "Vastly different" or "poles apart" are suitable translations.


~
拟定
Refers to the process of drafting or formulating a plan, document, or agreement. It implies careful consideration and preparation before finalization.


~
抹杀
Means to completely erase or obliterate something, often figuratively, such as suppressing the truth or denying someone's contributions. It carries a stronger connotation than simply "to erase" and often implies a deliberate act of concealment or destruction.


~
精通
Indicates a high level of proficiency or mastery in a particular skill, subject, or language. It suggests not only knowledge but also expertise and fluency.


~
舟
A more literary or poetic term for "boat," often used in classical Chinese or formal contexts.  In modern everyday conversation, 船 (chuán) is more common.


~
武侠
Refers to a specific genre in Chinese literature, film, and television that features martial arts heroes who often uphold justice and fight against oppression. It combines elements of martial arts, chivalry, and fantasy.


~
啰唆 / 啰嗦
Both are correct. 啰嗦 is the simplified form and the more commonly used one.


~
宇宙
Refers to the entire universe or cosmos, encompassing all matter, energy, and space.


~
冤枉
Has multiple meanings: 1) to wrongly accuse someone of something they didn't do, 2) to treat someone unfairly or unjustly, 3) to feel that something is not worthwhile or a waste of effort.  The appropriate translation depends on the context.


~
动静
Can refer to any detectable movement or activity, even subtle ones, suggesting a sense of alertness or awareness. It can also refer to the combination of movement and stillness, often in a philosophical or artistic context, representing the interplay of opposing forces.


~
盈利
Specifically refers to financial profit or gain, often used in a business context.


~
及早
Emphasizes the importance of acting promptly or without delay, as early as possible, often to prevent negative consequences or seize an opportunity.


~
就近
Means to choose the nearest or most convenient option, emphasizing proximity and efficiency.


~
直径
A mathematical term specifically referring to the length of a straight line passing through the center of a circle or sphere and connecting two points on the circumference or surface.


~
预兆
Refers to an omen, sign, or indication of something that is likely to happen in the future, often carrying a sense of foreboding or anticipation.


~
慈祥
Describes a kind, benevolent, and gentle demeanor, often associated with older people. It suggests warmth, compassion, and a nurturing quality.


~
放射
Can refer to the emission of radiation, as in radioactive materials, or the spreading out of something from a central point, like rays of light.  Be mindful of the context to determine the correct meaning.


~
镶嵌
Refers to the process of inlaying, embedding, or setting something, such as a jewel in a ring or tiles in a mosaic. It implies a precise and decorative arrangement.


~
阻拦
Means to obstruct or prevent someone or something from progressing or proceeding. It implies a deliberate act of interference.


~
执着
Describes a strong attachment, dedication, or persistence towards something, often to the point of obsession. In Buddhism, it refers to clinging to worldly desires and attachments, which is seen as a source of suffering.


~
卡通
A loanword specifically referring to cartoons or animated media.


~
倾斜
Describes a slanted, sloping, or tilted position or movement. It can be used literally or figuratively to describe imbalances or biases.


~
雇佣
Means to employ or hire someone for work, often in exchange for wages or salary.


~
拣
Means to choose, pick, or sort out items, often implying selectivity or careful consideration. It can also mean to pick something up from the ground.


~
舆论
Refers to public opinion or the prevailing sentiment on a particular issue, often influencing social or political discourse.


~
狭窄
Means narrow or constricted, referring to physical spaces or, figuratively, to limited perspectives or viewpoints.


~
衰老
Refers to the process of aging and the accompanying physical and mental decline. It emphasizes deterioration and weakening associated with old age.


~
威风
Describes an awe-inspiring, impressive, or imposing presence, often associated with power, authority, or prestige.


~
绣
Refers to the art of embroidery, creating decorative designs using needle and thread.


~
皮革
Refers to leather, a material made from animal hides or skins.


~
中立
Means neutral or impartial, not taking sides in a conflict or dispute.


~
阶层
Refers to a social class or stratum, a group of people sharing a similar economic, social, or cultural status.


~
陶瓷
Refers to ceramics, including pottery and porcelain, made from clay and hardened by heat.


~
报酬
Refers to a reward, payment, or remuneration received in exchange for work or services.


~
牵制
Means to control, restrict, or impede someone or something, often by diverting attention or resources.  It can also refer to pinning down enemy troops in military strategy.

~
斟酌
Can also mean "to fill a cup to the brim", although this usage is less common. Note also that the pronunciation is zhēnzhuó.

~
债券
There is no difference between the use of 债券 in Chinese and "bond" or "debenture" in English.

~
停顿
There is no difference between the use of 停顿 in Chinese and "pause", "halt", or "break off" in English.

~
品尝
There is no difference between the use of 品尝 in Chinese and "to taste" or "to sample" in English.

~
厌恶
There is no difference between the use of 厌恶 in Chinese and "to loathe" or "to hate" in English.


~
溜 (liū)
This word has several meanings and pronunciations. As a verb, when pronounced liū, it can mean "to slip away; to escape stealthily."  When pronounced liù, it can mean "to skate," as in 滑冰 (huábīng - to ice skate).  It's also used in the word 冰溜 (bīngliù), meaning "icicle."

~
杠杆
There is no difference between the use of 杠杆 in Chinese and "lever, pry bar, crowbar" or "financial leverage" in English.

~
寻觅
There is no difference between the use of 寻觅 in Chinese and "to look for" or "to seek" in English.  It is slightly more formal and poetic than 找 (zhǎo).

~
聋哑
There is no difference between the use of 聋哑 in Chinese and "deaf and mute/nonverbal" in English. Note that the word "dumb" is now considered offensive in English when referring to people who can't speak and "mute" or "nonverbal" is preferred.

~
擅长
There is no difference between the use of 擅长 in Chinese and "to be good at" or "to excel at/in" in English. It's usually followed by a noun or verb phrase indicating the area of expertise.

~
人格
There is no difference between the use of 人格 in Chinese and "personality", "integrity" or "dignity" in English. Note that the meanings of "integrity" and "dignity" are sometimes combined to form a single concept in Chinese.

~
糟蹋
Be mindful of the potential double pronunciation (zāota and zāota).  While both are acceptable, zāota is more common.  The word carries a strong sense of not just wasting something material, but also of squandering something valuable or treating it disrespectfully.

~
兑现
There is no difference between the use of 兑现 in Chinese and "to cash (a check)" or "to honor (a commitment)" in English. The latter meaning implies fulfilling a promise or obligation.

~
光芒
There is no difference between the use of 光芒 in Chinese and "rays of light", "brilliant rays", or "radiance" in English.  It often implies a brilliant or dazzling light.

~
野蛮
There is no difference between the use of 野蛮 in Chinese and "barbarous" or "uncivilized" in English.  It can refer to both behavior and people.

~
冷却
There is no difference between the use of 冷却 in Chinese and "to cool" in English, in both literal and figurative senses.  The figurative sense can refer to a cooling of emotions or enthusiasm.

~
抛弃
There is no difference between the use of 抛弃 in Chinese and "to abandon", "to discard", "to renounce", or "to dump" in English.  It implies a deliberate and often heartless act of leaving something or someone behind.

~
隐约
There is no difference between the use of 隐约 in Chinese and "vague", "faint", or "indistinct" in English. It suggests something is difficult to perceive clearly.

~
掩护
There is no difference between the use of 掩护 in Chinese and "to screen", "to shield", "to cover", or "protection/cover" in English.  It often has a military connotation, suggesting protecting someone or something from attack.

~
起伏
There is no difference between the use of 起伏 in Chinese and "to move up and down", "to undulate", or "ups and downs" in English. It can describe both physical terrain and abstract concepts like emotions or fortunes.

~
战役
There is no difference between the use of 战役 in Chinese and "military campaign" or "(military) battle" in English. It usually refers to a large-scale military operation.

~
董事长
There is no difference between the use of 董事长 in Chinese and "chairman of the board" or "chairperson of the board" in English.

~
曲子
There is no difference between the use of 曲子 in Chinese and "tune", "song", or "music" in English.  Remember the measure word is 支 (zhī).

~
装卸
There is no difference between the use of 装卸 in Chinese and "to load and unload", "to load or unload", or "to handle cargo" in English.  It can also refer to assembling and disassembling something.

~
持久
There is no difference between the use of 持久 in Chinese and "lasting", "enduring", "persistent", "long-lasting" in English.  It emphasizes duration and resistance to change.

~
随即
There is no difference between the use of 随即 in Chinese and "immediately", "at once", "thereupon" or "following which" in English.  It emphasizes the immediacy of an action following a previous one.


~
亭子
There is no difference between the use of 亭子 in Chinese and "pavilion" or "gazebo" in English.

~
尊严
There is no difference between the use of 尊严 in Chinese and "dignity", "honor", "self-respect" or "majesty" in English.

~
贿赂
There is no difference between the use of 贿赂 in Chinese and "bribe" or "to bribe" in English.

~
全局
There is no difference between the use of 全局 in Chinese and "overall situation", "the big picture", or "the whole picture" in English.  It emphasizes a comprehensive perspective.

~
流氓
There is no difference between the use of 流氓 in Chinese and "rogue", "hoodlum", "gangster", "thug", or "ruffian" in English.  It can also refer to immoral or hooligan behavior.

~
塌
塌 (tā) can mean to collapse, sink, or cave in, especially for something like a roof or a building. It can also mean "drooping" or "sagging."  It can also mean "to settle down" (dust, etc.)

~
变迁
There is no difference between the use of 变迁 in Chinese and "changes", "vicissitudes", "transformations" or "transitions" in English.  It often implies significant changes over time.

~
机灵
There is no difference between the use of 机灵 in Chinese and "clever", "smart", "quick-witted", "sharp", "ingenious", or "bright" in English.  It often suggests alertness and resourcefulness.

~
乐意
There is no difference between the use of 乐意 in Chinese and "to be willing to", "to be happy to", "to be glad to" in English.

~
结局
There is no difference between the use of 结局 in Chinese and "ending", "conclusion", "outcome" or "denouement" in English.

勉励
There is no difference between the use of 勉励 in Chinese and "to encourage", "to urge", "to exhort" in English.  It implies inspiring someone to do better.

喧哗
There is no difference between the use of 喧哗 in Chinese and "noise", "clamor", "hubbub", "to make noise", "to make a racket" in English.

~
扩散
There is no difference between the use of 扩散 in Chinese and "to spread", "to diffuse", "to proliferate" or "to disseminate" in English.  It often refers to the spreading of information, influence, or a substance.

~
对照
There is no difference between the use of 对照 in Chinese and "to compare", "to contrast", "to check", or "to refer to" in English. It often involves placing two things side-by-side to highlight similarities or differences.

~
稠密
A related word is 茂密 (màomì), which also means dense, but is usually used to describe forests, vegetation, or hair.  稠密, on the other hand, is more general and can be used for things like population, fog, or a schedule.  Think of 稠 as referring to thickness or viscosity, and 密 as referring to closeness or compactness.

~
忍耐
Can also mean "patience" or "endurance" as a noun.

~
转达
This is often used in formal settings like passing on messages from superiors or conveying condolences.  For casual everyday communication between friends,  telling someone something is more naturally expressed with other verbs like  告诉 (gàosu) or  说 (shuō).

~
陈述
This implies a formal, reasoned statement of facts or opinions.  It's not used for casual conversation.  It’s more like presenting an argument or giving testimony.

~
生态
While 生态 literally translates to "ecology," it can also be used more broadly in Chinese to talk about the "ecosystem" of a particular industry, field, or environment.  For example, you might see the phrase  互联网生态 (hùliánwǎng shēngtài) meaning "internet ecosystem."

~
橙
The color 橙色 (chéngsè) is closer to dark yellow or gold than the typical English "orange."

~
格式
This can also refer to social conventions or established forms of behavior, beyond just document formatting.

~
灭亡
This term is typically used for civilizations, nations, or species, signifying complete destruction or extinction. It carries a stronger sense of finality than just death or destruction of an individual.

~
施展
This often implies utilizing one’s talents, abilities, or influence fully and effectively, not just simply using something.

~
飞跃
This word can also be used figuratively to represent a significant advancement or breakthrough, not just a literal leap.

~
乡镇
Although both mean "small administrative unit," 乡 is usually smaller and more rural than 镇.

~
作息
This refers to a regular schedule of work and rest, implying a healthy and balanced lifestyle.

致辞
This implies a formal speech, often given at a ceremony or important occasion, not just any casual remarks.

~
幢
As a classifier, 幢 is specifically for buildings, especially large or imposing ones.

~
忠诚
This is a strong word implying unwavering loyalty and devotion, often in a political or military context.  It can sometimes carry connotations of blind obedience.

This implies taking corrective action after a mistake or failure has already occurred.

This usually describes rooms or spaces, emphasizing their spaciousness and airiness.

This suggests following rules, principles, or traditions closely and respectfully.  It implies conscious and deliberate compliance.

合伙
This carries the connotation of joining together for a specific purpose, often business-related, implying shared responsibility and profit/loss.

隔离
This can imply forced separation due to safety or health concerns, as in quarantine.

之际
This is a formal written term often used to mark a specific point in time or during the occurrence of an event.

~
局部
This can also be used figuratively to mean a limited aspect or part of a larger whole.

This emphasizes the element of coincidence or luck.

This carries a more literal meaning of sowing seeds, not just planting in general. It can also be used metaphorically for laying the groundwork for something.

This implies enduring hardship or suffering, often physical or emotional.

栽培
This often implies careful nurturing and development of someone's talent or potential, not just simple training.

~
潜水
Online, 潜水 (qiánshuǐ) refers to lurking.  It means browsing a forum or online community without actively participating, just reading posts and threads.

地步
This word often describes a negative or undesirable state of affairs that has been reached.

爱戴
This describes a deep respect and affection felt by people towards a leader or respected figure.

The figurative meaning, "to expose a scandal," is becoming increasingly common.

This suggests a detailed and vivid description, often visual, as if painting a picture with words.

This refers to cruel and inhumane treatment, often involving physical or emotional harm.

This carries a negative connotation, implying unrealistic and impractical ideas or fantasies.

This word has strong religious connotations and implies granting forgiveness for a serious offense.

The figurative meaning, "to think over," suggests careful consideration and reflection on something.

Be careful. This term can imply gossip or idle chatter, which may be considered negative.

削
The Taiwanese pronunciation of 削 is [xue4]. Aside from that, there is nothing special about this word.

~
正经
This word has two main uses.  The first is as an adjective, meaning decent, honorable, proper, or serious. The second is as an adverb, meaning "actually" or "really", often with a sarcastic or ironic tone. For example, "你正经点儿！" (Nǐ zhèngjǐng diǎnr!) means "Be serious!" or "Get real!".

~
搂
This character has a few different meanings and usages. When used to describe a physical action, it can mean "to hug," "to embrace," or "to hold in one's arms." It can also mean "to draw towards oneself," "to gather," or "to gather up."  In some contexts, it can even mean "to grab" (especially money) or "to extort."  The specific meaning will depend on the context.
